The Living World Test-01  (id 3338) [FREE]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > The Living World
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. Taxon is a:
    (A) Group of related species
    (B) Group of related families
    (C) Group of living organisms
    (D) Ranking   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Each category in the taxonomic hierarchy represents the rank and is commonly termed as a taxon. Hence, the correct option is Ranking.

Q2. The expansion of ICBN is:
    (A) International Class of Botanical Nomenclature
    (B) Indian Class of Botanical Nomenclature
    (C) Indian Code of Botanical Nomenclature
    (D) International Code of Botanical Nomenclature   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The scientific names are based on agreed principles and criteria, which are provided in the International Code for Botanical Nomenclature (ICBN). Hence, the correct option is the International code of botanical nomenclature.

Q3. The expansion of ICZN is:
    (A) International class of zoological nomenclature
    (B) Indian class of zoological nomenclature
    (C) Indian code of zoological nomenclature
    (D) International code of zoological nomenclature   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Animal taxonomists have evolved the International Code of Zoological Nomenclature (ICZN). Hence, the correct option is the International code of zoological nomenclature.

Q4. A binomial nomenclature has ________ words.
    (A) Three
    (B) One
    (C) Five
    (D) Two   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The first word in a biological name represents the genus while the second component denotes the specific epithet. Hence, the correct option is Two.

Q5. In Magnifera indica Linn, Linn denotes:
    (A) The name of the author who first described the formation
    (B) The name of the author who first described the species.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) The name of the author who first described the genus.
    (D) The name of the author who first described the subspecies.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In Mangifera indica Linn, the word ‘Linn’ indicates that this species was first described by Linnaeus. Hence, the correct option is the name of the author who first described the species.

Q6. The scientific name of organisms should be written as:
    (A) Subspecies species
    (B) Species subspecies
    (C) Genus species   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Species genus
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Mangifera Indica. Here, Mangifera is a generic name while Indica is a specific name. Hence, the correct option is the Genus species.

Q7. International Code of Biological Nomenclature is applied to_______.
    (A) Virus
    (B) Plants
    (C) Both Plants and Animals   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Animals
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Since biology deals with both plants and animals, the international code of biological nomenclature is applied to both plants and animals. Hence, the correct option is Both plant and animals.

Q8. The first step in taxonomy is ______.
    (A) Classification
    (B) Naming
    (C) Identification   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Description
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The basics of taxonomy are the identification, naming, and classification of organisms are universally evolved under international codes. Hence, the correct option is Identification.

Q9. Which one is the exclusive characteristic of a living organism?
    (A) Isolated metabolic reaction occuring in vitro.
    (B) Perception of events happening in the environment and their memory   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Increase in mass both from outside and inside
    (D) Increase in mass from inside
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The most obvious and technically complicated feature of all living organisms is this ability to sense their surroundings or environment and respond to these environmental stimuli which could be physical, chemical or biological. We sense our environment through our sense organs. Plants respond to external factors like light, water, temperature, other organisms, pollutants, etc. All organisms, from the prokaryotes to the most complex eukaryotes can sense and respond to environmental cues. Hence, the correct option is the Perception of events happening in the environment and their memory.

Q10. Living things differ from non-living things in a manner that:
    (A) Living things respond to the physical level
    (B) Living things have a different level of organisation   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Living things are more in member than non-living
    (D) Living things perform various functions
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The cellular level organisation of the body is the defining feature of life forms or living things. Hence, the correct option is Living things have a different level of organisation.

Q11. Sometimes different authors give different names to one and the same species. In such a situation:
 The name under which the species was first described is a valid name.
 The latest name under which the species was described is valid.
 People can use any one of the names for the species.
 All known names are discarded and a new name is given to the species.
    (A) (A)   <-- CORRECT
    (B) (C)
    (C) (D)
    (D) (B)
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In Mangifera indica Linn, the word ‘Linn’ indicates that this species was first described by Linnaeus. Hence, the correct option is The name under which the species was first described is the valid name.

Q12. Hierarchical classification refers:
    (A) To divide orders into families
    (B) To divide division into classes
    (C) To divide classes into orders
    (D) To rank one above the other   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Classification is not a single step process but involves a hierarchy of steps in which each step represents a rank or category. Hence, the correct option is To rank one above the other.

Q13. Which of the following statement is correct with respect to nomenclature?
 The scientific name when typed or handwritten should be underlined.
 Generic names always begin with capital letters whereas specific names begin with small letters.
 Scientific names should be printed in italics.
    (A) (C)
    (B) All of these   <-- CORRECT
    (C) (B)
    (D) (A)
    Answer: B
    Explanation: All of these are the universal rules of binomial nomenclature. Hence, the correct option is All of these.

Q14. In a scientific name, the name of the author is printed in ________.
    (A) Abbreviated   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Capital letters
    (C) Italics
    (D) Bold
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The name of the author appears after the specific epithet, i.e., at the end of the biological name and is written in an abbreviated form, e.g., Mangifera indica Linn. It indicates that this species was first described by Linnaeus. Hence, the correct option is Abbreviated.

Q15. Which are the terms interchangeable?
    (A) Genes and species
    (B) Species and subspecies
    (C) Kingdom and phylum
    (D) Taxonomy and systematics   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The characterization, identification, classification, and nomenclature are the processes that are basic to taxonomy as well as systematics. Hence, the correct option is Taxonomy and systematics.

The Living World Test-02  (id 3339) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > The Living World

Q1. Which is not the universal rule of nomenclature?
 Biological names are generally in Greek.
 The biological names are printed in italics.
 Genus name starts with a capital letter while the species name starts with small letters.
 The first word represents the genus and the second word represents species.
    (A) (C)
    (B) (A)   <-- CORRECT
    (C) (D)
    (D) (B)
    Answer: B
    Explanation: According to the universal rule of nomenclature, the biological names are generally in Latin and written in italics. Hence, the correct option is Biological names are generally in Greek.

Q2. The number of species that are known and described is:
    (A) 1.7 - 1.8 million   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 5 - 30 million
    (C) 5,000 - 10,000
    (D) 2 - 4 million
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Each different kind of plant, animal, or organism represents a species. The number of species known and described ranges between 1.7-1.8 million. This refers to biodiversity or the number and types of organisms present on earth. Hence, the correct option is 1.7 - 1.8 million.

Q3. The Darwin of the 20th century is:
    (A) Ernst Mayr   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Aristotle
    (C) Carolus Linnaeus
    (D) Theophrastus
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Born on 5 July 1904, in Kempten, Germany, ERNST MAYR, the Harvard University evolutionary biologist who has been called ‘The Darwin of the 20th century’, was one of the 100 greatest scientists of all time.

Q4. A virus differ from a bacterium as it contains:
    (A) DNA as genetic material
    (B) Cytosol
    (C) A cell wall
    (D) DNA or RNA as genetic material with no ribosome   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Virus differs from bacteria in terms of having DNA or RNA as genetic material with no ribosomes. The virus can replicate inside the host cell but become inactive outside the host cell.

Q5. Wildlife is destroyed most when:
    (A) There is lack of proper care
    (B) Natural habitat is destroyed   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Natural calamity
    (D) Mass scale hunting
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Wildlife is destroyed most when natural habitat is destroyed. The organisms survive and reproduce only in the natural habitat. The loss of habitat of wild animals is the main reason behind the extinction of organisms.

Q6. Animals that have become extinct in India is _____.
    (A) Cheetah   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Wolf
    (C) Snow Leopard
    (D) Hippopotamus
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The animals that were present earlier but now not available are called extinct animals. In India, a number of animals have become extinct such as Cheetah.

Q7. In which organism protoplasm and cellular structure is absent ______.
    (A) Algae
    (B) Bacteria
    (C) Fungi
    (D) Virus   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The protoplasm and cellular structure are absent in Virus. A virus consists of genetic material (DNA or RNA) along with a capsule of protein without any cellular structure.

Q8. Living organisms show internal growth due to the addition of materials and formation of cells inside the body. Such a method is called _______.
    (A) Intussusception   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Accretion
    (C) Degrwoth
    (D) Totipotancy
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The method in which living organism show internal growth due to the addition of materials fand formation of cells inside the body is called intussusception.

Q9. Example of interspecific hybrid is:
    (A) Cat and lion
    (B) Liger and dog
    (C) Tigon and liger   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Tigon and tiger
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Tigon and liger are produced by hybridization of tow interspecific species. Although hybridization generally takes place between the same species.

Q10. A living organism is unexceptionally differentiated from a non-living structure on the basis of
    (A) growth and movement.
    (B) reproduction.
    (C) interaction with environment.
    (D) responsiveness.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: All organisms, from primitive prokaryotes to most advanced and complex eukaryotes, are able to sense and respond to environmental factors. The stimuli are perceived by sense organs in higher animals through sensory receptors e.g., eyes, ears, nose. Plants do not possess such sense organs. However, they do respond to external factors such as light, water, temperature, pollutants, other organisms, etc. Human beings have an additional facility of self-consciousness (awareness of self). Consciousness and response to stimuli are said to be the defining properties of living organisms.

Q11. The number of categories in the hierarchical classification is ______.
    (A) 5
    (B) 6
    (C) 7   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 8
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Taxonomical studies of all known organisms have led to the development of common categories such as kingdom, phylum (for animals) or division (for plants), class, order, family, genus, and species. Hence, the correct option is 7.

Q12. In a taxonomic hierarchy, the various categories are arranged in:
    (A) Vertical order
    (B) Ascending order
    (C) Descending order   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Horizontal order
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Kingdom $\rightarrow$ Phylum/Division $\rightarrow$ Class $\rightarrow$ Order $\rightarrow$ Family $\rightarrow$ Genus $\rightarrow$ Species.
Hence, the correct option is Descending order.

Q13. Choose the correct sequence of taxonomic categories in descending order:
    (A) Division - Order - Family - Class - Genus - Species
    (B) Division - Class - Order - Family - Genus - Species   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Division - Family - Class - Order - Genus - Species
    (D) Division - Class - Order - Genus - Family - Species
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The correct sequence of taxonomic categories form higher to lower are Division - Class - Order - Family - Genus - Species.

Q14. A group of closely related families is called ______.
    (A) Order   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Class
    (C) Species
    (D) Genus
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Class includes a group of related orders, Genus comprises a group of related species, species is a basic unit of classification. Hence, the correct option is Order.

Q15. The highest categories of classification is ________.
    (A) Kingdom   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Family
    (C) Class
    (D) Order
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The taxonomic hierarchy Kingdom $\rightarrow$ Phylum/Division $\rightarrow$ Class $\rightarrow$ Order $\rightarrow$ Family $\rightarrow$ Genus $\rightarrow$ Species.
Hence, the correct option is the Kingdom.

The Living World Test-03  (id 3340) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > The Living World
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. A group of closely related classes is called _______.
    (A) Order
    (B) Phylum   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Family
    (D) Genus
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Genus comprises a group of related species, Family has a group of related genera, the order has a group of related family. Hence, the correct option is Phylum.

Q2. The basic unit of classification is ______.
    (A) Genus
    (B) Family
    (C) Phylum
    (D) Species   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The basic unit of classification is species. Species are the population of organisms that can interbreed among themselves to produce new organisms.

Q3. Related genera belong to the same ________.
    (A) Variety
    (B) Species
    (C) Family   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Breed
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A family is a group of genera having some common properties. So, related genera belong to the same family.

Q4. A fundamental category of classification ranking below a genus is_______.
    (A) Order
    (B) Species   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Kingdom
    (D) Family
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The taxonomic hierarchy Kingdom $\rightarrow$ Phylum/Division $\rightarrow$ Class $\rightarrow$ Order $\rightarrow$ Family $\rightarrow$ Genus $\rightarrow$ Species. Hence, the correct option is Species.

Q5. In a hierarchical system of classification of plants, which of the following taxonomic rank ends in ceae?
    (A) Genus
    (B) Family   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Class
    (D) Order
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Plant families like Convolvulaceae, Solanaceae are included in the order Polymoniales mainly based on the floral characters. Hence, the correct option is Family.

Q6. Triticum aestivum belong to the family _______.
    (A) Hominidae
    (B) Muscidae
    (C) Anacardiaceae
    (D) Poaceae   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Triticum aestivum, common or bread wheat, is an annual grass in the Poaceae (grass family) native to the Mediterranean region and southwest Asia.

Q7. A group of plants with similar traits of any rank is _______.
    (A) Order
    (B) Taxon   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Genus
    (D) Species
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Each category in the taxonomic hierarchy represents the rank and is commonly termed as a taxon. Hence, the correct option is Taxon.

Q8. Identify the correct binomial nomenclature of Mango:
    (A) Mangifera indica lin
    (B) Mangifera India lin
    (C) Mangifera Indica Linn   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Mangifera Indiaca linn
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The biological name of an organism consists of the genus name and species name. the correct biological nomenclature of Mango is Mangifer indica Linn.

Q9. What is the difference between the taxonomic categories of division and phylum?
    (A) The phylum is a more inclusive category
    (B) Division refers to plants whereas phylum refers to animals   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Division is a more inclusive category
    (D) Phylum is more exclusive than division
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In the case of plants, classes with a few similar characters are assigned to a higher category called division, whereas phylum was used to refer to animals. Hence, the correct option is Division refers to plants whereas phylum refers to animals.

Q10. The housefly belongs to order ______.
    (A) Primata
    (B) Sapindales
    (C) Poales
    (D) Diptera   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Houseflies are insects of the order Diptera, the name is derived from the Greek di = two, and ptera = wings

Q11. Which is the incorrect statement from the following?
 Lion, tiger, leopard, and cat belong to the same genus.
 A family is a group of related genera with still less number of similarities as compared to genus and species.
 Taxonomic aids are the prime source of taxonomy, systematics, and future studies.
 Systematics takes into account the evolutionary relationship between organisms.
    (A) (A)   <-- CORRECT
    (B) (D)
    (C) (C)
    (D) (B)
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Lion (Panthera leo), leopard (P. pardus), and tiger (P. Tigris) with several common features are all species of the genus Panthera. The genus Felisincludes cats. Hence, the correct option is Lion, tiger, leopard and cat belong to the same genus.

Q12. What is the scientific name of wheat?
    (A) Musca domestica
    (B) Triticum aestivum   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Mangifera indica
    (D) Homo sapiens
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Wheat is a grass widely cultivated for its seed, a cereal grain which is a worldwide staple food. There are many species of wheat which together make up the genus Triticum; the most widely grown is common wheat (T. aestivum).

Q13. A true species consist of a population:
    (A) Interbreeding   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Sharing same niche
    (C) Reproductively isolated
    (D) Feeding over the same food
    Answer: A
    Explanation: As per the definition given by Ernst Mayr in 1964: "A species is a group of actually or potentially inbreeding populations that are reproductively isolated from other such groups."
A species may have subgroups, called subspecies or varieties, showing certain distinct features of their own.

Q14. Systema Naturae is a book written by:
    (A) Bentham and Hooker
    (B) John Ray
    (C) Linneaus   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Lamarck
    Answer: C
    Explanation: ‘Systema Naturae’ is a book written by Carolus Linneaus. This book gives in-depth details of the classification system and binomial nomenclature of organisms.

Q15. The scientific study of the diversity of organism and their evolutionary relationship is called:
    (A) Morphology
    (B) Taxonomy
    (C) Systematics   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Anatomy
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Systematics is the scientific study of the diversity of organisms and their evolutionary relationship. Systematics is also known as taxonomy. It includes identification, nomenclature, and classification.

The Living World Test-04  (id 3341) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > The Living World

Q1. Full form of ICBN is:
    (A) Indian code for botanical nomenclature
    (B) International class for botanical nomenclature
    (C) International code of biological nomenclature
    (D) International code of botanical nomenclature   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: ICBN stands for the International code of botanical nomenclature that frames rules for the nomenclature of plants applicable all over the world.

Q2. Which one is less general in characteristic as compared to the genus?
    (A) Class
    (B) Family
    (C) Species   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Division
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Species is the lowest rank in the hierarchy. It means species contain the least general characters as compared to other categories.

Q3. Identify from the following, category which has real existence.
    (A) Phylum
    (B) Kingdom
    (C) Species   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Genus
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Species

Q4. Classification based on the evolutionary and genetic relationship is called:
    (A) Phylogenetic classification   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Natural classification
    (C) Genetic classification
    (D) Numerical classification
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The classification of organisms on the basis of the evolutionary and genetic relationship is called a phylogenetic system of classification. The organisms are arranged according to their evolution on earth.

Q5. The branch of study that deals with identification, nomenclature, and classification is called _______.
    (A) Grouping
    (B) Taxonomy   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Phylactery
    (D) Genetics
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Taxonomy is the branch of biological science that deals with identification, nomenclature, and classification of organisms according to certain sets of rules.

Q6. Which genus has a large number of closely related species?
    (A) Falidae
    (B) Solanum   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Fabacea
    (D) Convolvulaceae
    Answer: B
    Explanation: A genus consists of a large number of closed related species. Genus Solanum consist of larger common species that include potato, tomato, brinjal, etc.

Q7. Living organisms are classified because of:
    (A) All of these   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Easy study and to keep records
    (C) To bring out similarities and to know habitat
    (D) Easy identification and study
    Answer: A
    Explanation: All of these

Q8. Carolus Linnaeus is associated with:
    (A) Inheritance of acquired character
    (B) Origin of species
    (C) Binomial nomenclature   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Law of limiting factor
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Carolus Linnaeus is associated with Binomial nomenclature in which the name of the organism consists of the genus name and species name.

Q9. Which one is an obligate category of classification?
    (A) Tribe
    (B) Family   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Sub phylum
    (D) Variety
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Family is the obligate category of classification as it forms the basic functional unit of classification. The family includes all the related species having similar characters.

Q10. Plant and animal specimens may also be preserved as dry specimens in________.
    (A) Herbarium
    (B) Zoo
    (C) Museum   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Park
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Plant and animal specimens may also be preserved as dry specimens in museums. Hence, the correct option is the Museum.

Q11. Which serve as quick referral systems in taxonomical studies?
    (A) Museum
    (B) Manuals
    (C) Monographs
    (D) Herbarium   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Museums have collections of preserved plant and animal specimens for study and reference. Manuals are useful in providing information for the identification of names of species found in an area. Monographs contain information on anyone's taxon. Hence, the correct option is Herbarium.

Q12. Specimens are preserved in the containers or jars in preservative solutions in ______.
    (A) park
    (B) zoo
    (C) museum   <-- CORRECT
    (D) herbarium
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Specimens are preserved in the containers or jars in preservative solutions in the museum.

Q13. The existence of a wide range of different types of organisms in a given place at a given time is_______.
    (A) Museum
    (B) Park
    (C) Zoo
    (D) Biodiversity   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The parks and zoo are the places where wild animals are kept in protected environments under human care. Museums have collections of preserved plant and animal specimens for study and reference. Hence, the correct option is Biodiversity.

Q14. Larger animals like birds and mammals are usually stuffed and preserved in ______.
    (A) Park
    (B) Herbarium
    (C) Zoo
    (D) Museum   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Larger animals like birds and mammals are usually stuffed and preserved in the museum. Hence, the correct choice is the Museum.

Q15. The famous botanical garden, Kew is located in ______.
    (A) USA
    (B) England   <-- CORRECT
    (C) France
    (D) Germany
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Kew Gardens is a botanical garden in southwest London that houses the "largest and most diverse botanical and mycological collections in the world".

The Living World Test-05  (id 3342) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > The Living World
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. Herbarium is:
    (A) Chemical to kill plants
    (B) Collection of living plants for reference
    (C) Collection of dried plant specimens   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Collection of preserved plant and animal specimen
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The herbarium is a storehouse of collected plant specimens that are dried, pressed and preserved on sheets. Hence, the correct option is Collection of dried plant specimens.

Q2. National Botanical Research Institute is situated at ______.
    (A) Howrah
    (B) Chennai
    (C) Dehradun
    (D) Lucknow   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The famous botanical gardens are at Kew (England), Indian Botanical Garden, Howrah (India) and at National Botanical Research Institute, Lucknow (India). Hence, the correct choice is Lucknow.

Q3. It is a handy book containing instructions of occurrence, collection, and identification of species found in a particular area that is known as ________.
    (A) Monograph
    (B) Flora
    (C) Manual   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Key
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Flora, manuals, monographs and catalogues are different means of recording descriptions. Manuals are useful in providing information for identification of names of species found in an area. Hence, the correct option is Manual.

Q4. The taxonomical aid used for identification of plants and animals based on the similarities and dissimilarities is _______.
    (A) Zoo
    (B) Key   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Museum
    (D) Park
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Zoo and parks are the places where wild animals are kept in protected environments under human care. Museums have collections of preserved plant and animal specimens for study and reference. Hence, the correct option is Key.

Q5. Each statement in the key is called ______.
    (A) Couplet
    (B) Monographs
    (C) Manuals
    (D) Lead   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The keys are based on the contrasting characters generally in a pair called a couplet. Manuals are useful in providing information for identification of names of species found in an area. Monographs contain information on anyone taxon. Hence, the correct option is Lead.

Q6. What contains the actual account of habitat and distribution of plants of a given area?
    (A) Catalogues
    (B) Manuals
    (C) Flora   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Monographs
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Manuals are useful in providing information for the identification of names of species found in an area. Monographs contain information on anyone taxon. Catalogue is also another means of recording descriptions which helps incorrect identification. Hence, the correct option is Flora.

Q7. National Botanical Institute is located in ________.
    (A) Kolkata
    (B) Delhi
    (C) Lucknow   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Chennai
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The national botanical research institute is located in Lucknow (UP). This is one of the largest botanical research institutes in the world housing thousands of plants.

Q8. Rajaji national park is in ______.
    (A) Karnataka
    (B) Uttrakhand   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Assam
    (D) Tamil nadu
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Rajaji national park is an Indian national park and tiger reserve that encompasses the Shivaliks, near the foothill of the Himalayas in Uttrakhand.

Q9. Lions are found in:
    (A) Gir forest   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Corbett national park
    (C) Madhya Pradesh
    (D) Western Ghat
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In India, lions are found in Gir forests located in the state of Gujarat, India. It is the sole home of the Asiatic lions and is considered to be one of the most important protected areas in Asia.

Q10. Largest Botanical Garden in the world is:
    (A) Indian Botanical Garden, Kolkata
    (B) Royal Botanical Garden, Kew   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Main Botanical Garden. Moscow
    (D) Bundes Garden, Vienna
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The Royal Botanical Garden, Kew (located in London, United Kingdom) is the largest and most renowned botanical garden in the world. It covers approximately 330 acres and houses one of the most extensive and diverse collections of living plants and preserved plant specimens. Kew Gardens is also a leading center for botanical research and conservation.
It is also a UNESCO World Heritage Site and a leading center for botanical research and conservation.

Q11. List of alternate characters arranged in such a manner that by selection and elimination an organism can easily be identified is______.
    (A) Key   <-- CORRECT
    (B) All of these
    (C) Herbarium
    (D) Lock
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Key is the list of alternate characters arranged in such a manner that by selection and elimination an organism can easily be identified. It is an important tool for the classification of the organism.

Q12. The first Biosphere Reserve established in India is:
    (A) Manas Biosphere Reserve
    (B) Sunderbans Biosphere Reserve
    (C) Nanda Devi Biosphere Reserve
    (D) Nilgiri Biosphere Reserve   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The Nilgiri Biosphere reserve is the first biosphere reserve established in India. Biosphere reserves are set to protect the flora and fauna of a particular area that houses a large number of wild animals.

Q13. A specified area in which multiple uses of the land is permitted by dividing into zones, each for a particular activity is called ________.
    (A) Wildlife reserves
    (B) Zoological park
    (C) Biosphere reserve   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Museums
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A biosphere reserve is divided into a number of zones, where different kinds of activities are allowed. In the outer zone, agriculture and other activities are allowed but in the central or core zone, no human activities are allowed.

Q14. Preservative liquid used for storing fleshy organs is
    (A) Acetic acid
    (B) Ethyl alcohol
    (C) Butanol
    (D) Formalin   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In a biological laboratory, formalin is used as a preservative liquid used for storing fleshy organs.

Q15. It is a handy book containing instructions as to the occurrence, collection, and identification of species found in a particular area.
    (A) Key
    (B) Manual   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Flora
    (D) Monograph
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Manual is a handy book containing instructions as to the occurrence, collection, and identification of species found in a particular area. It serves as an important tool for the classification of organisms.

Biological Classification Test-01  (id 3343) [FREE]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Biological Classification
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. The five kingdom classification was proposed by
    (A) Hutchinson
    (B) Whittaker   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Engler and Prantl
    (D) Bentham and Hooker
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Five kingdom classification was proposed by R.H. Whittaker in 1969. The kingdoms identified by him were Monera, Protista,Fungi, Plantae and Animalia.

Q2. Which among the five-kingdom system of classification do not possess nuclear membrane?
    (A) Kingdom Fungi
    (B) Kingdom Monera   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Kingdom Plantae
    (D) Kingdom Protista
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Kingdom Protista, kingdom Fungi, kingdom Plantae possess the nuclear membrane while the kingdom Monera does not possess a nuclear membrane.

Q3. In five kingdom of classification, Whittaker assigned eukaryotes to how many kingdoms?
    (A) Only three of five kingdoms
    (B) Only two of five kingdoms
    (C) Only four of five kingdoms   <-- CORRECT
    (D) All five kingdoms
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In Whittaker’s five kingdoms of classification, kingdom Protista, kingdom fungi, kingdom Plantae and kingdom Animalia are eukaryotic organisms. The kingdom monera includes prokaryotic organisms. Hence, four kingdoms out of five are eukayotes.

Q4. In five kingdom of classification, prokaryotic, non-nucleated and unicellular organisms are included under:
    (A) Kingdom Monera   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Kingdom Animalia
    (C) Kingdom Protista
    (D) Kingdom Plantae
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The fifth kingdom, Monera, contains all the single-celled organisms that do not possess a true nucleus. Members of the kingdom Monera are commonly referred to as bacteria.

Q5. Which kingdom brought Chlorella and Chlamydomonas with Paramoecium and Amoeba?
    (A) Kingdom Fungi
    (B) Kingdom Monera
    (C) Kingdom Plantae
    (D) Kingdom Protista   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Kingdom Protista has brought together Chlamydomonas, Chlorella which were earlier placed in Algae within Plants and (both having cell walls) with Paramoecium and Amoeba which was earlier placed in the animal kingdom which lacks it.

Q6. In five kingdom of classification, the kingdom Plantae are autotrophic, eukaryotic and_______.
    (A) Motile
    (B) Possess sexual reproduction
    (C) All of these
    (D) Tissue level   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The Kingdom Plantae includes all types of eukaryotic, multicellular, photosynthetic plants found in this biosphere. Most of the organism in this kingdom are autotrophs, which synthesis their own food with the help of solar energy.

Q7. Who was the earliest to attempt a more scientific basis for classification?
    (A) Pasteur
    (B) Aristotle   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Whittaker
    (D) Linnaeus
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Aristotle was the earliest to attempt a more scientific basis for classification. He used simple morphological characters to classify plants into trees, shrubs, and herbs.

Q8. Who divided animals into two groups based on the presence and absence of red blood cells?
    (A) Aristotle   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Linnaeus
    (C) Pasteur
    (D) Whittaker
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Aristotle used simple morphological characters to classify plants into trees, shrubs, and herbs. He also divided animals into two groups, those which had red blood and those that did not.

Q9. Which system of classification was developed during Linnaeus's time?
    (A) Five kingdom of classification
    (B) Three kingdom of classification
    (C) Four kingdom of classificaition
    (D) Two kingdom of classification   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In Linnaeus' time, a two Kingdom system of classification with Plantae and Animalia kingdoms was developed that included all plants and animals respectively. This system was used until very recently.

Q10. Which of the following organisms were placed together under algae?
    (A) All of these   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Spirogyra
    (C) Chlorella
    (D) Chlamydomonas
    Answer: A
    Explanation: As spirogyra, chlorella and chlamydomonas have same characterstics which are perfectly suitable for the 'algae', they all are placed together in algae.

Q11. Who is called as Father of taxonomy?
    (A) Theophrastus
    (B) Linnaeus   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Aristotle
    (D) Hooker
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Carl Linnaeus, also known as Carl von Linné or Carolus Linnaeus, is often called the Father of Taxonomy. His system for naming, ranking, and classifying organisms is still in wide use today with many changes.

Q12. Which of the following type of classification based on a few morphological characters?
    (A) Phylogenetic
    (B) Artificial   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Natural
    (D) Morphological
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Artificial classification is based on a few morphological characters of organisms like flower shape, the stem type and types of seeds.

Q13. The first phylogenetic system of classification was given by:
    (A) Whittaker
    (B) John Ray
    (C) Engler and Prantl   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Bantham and Hooker
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The first phylogenetic system of classification was given by Engler and Prantl which was based on the evolutionary relationship of the organisms. Those evolved earlier are classified first and newly evolved later on.

Q14. Classification and studies based on chemical constituents of an organism are called _______.
    (A) Phytotaxonomy
    (B) Chemotaxonomy   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Cytotaxonomy
    (D) Karytaxonomy
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Chemotaxonomy as the method of biological classification based on similarities in the structure of certain compounds among the organisms being classified. Two organisms morphologically similar to each other are classified on the basis of chemotaxonomy.

Q15. Which one is not a characteristic feature of prokaryotes?
    (A) Sexual reproduction   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Absence of spindle apparatus
    (C) Genetic material not organized in nucleus
    (D) Single envelop organization
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Prokaryotic organisms generally do not reproduce by sexual reproduction. However, they reproduce by asexual methods in favorable conditions.

Biological Classification Test-02  (id 3344) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Biological Classification
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. Arranging organism on the basis of their shared similar or derived characters that differ from ancestral character is called _________.
    (A) Cladogram   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Homogram
    (C) Histogram
    (D) Monogram
    Answer: A
    Explanation: A cladogram is arranging organisms on the basis of their shared similar or derived characters that differ from ancestral character. It is an important tool for taxonomical studies.

Q2. Unicellular algae and fungi are separated from other organisms on the basis of:
    (A) Presence of chlorophyll
    (B) Lack of tissue differentiation   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Absence of cilia
    (D) Absence of cell wall
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Unicellular organisms are made of only one cell and there is an absence of tissue differentiation. All unicellular algae and fungi are separated from other organisms on this basis.

Q3. Prokaryotes differ from Eukaryotes in the absence of:
    (A) Nuclear membrane and membrane bounded organelles   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Mitosis cell division and ribosome
    (C) All of these
    (D) Cell membrane and cytoplasm
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Prokaryotes differ from Eukaryotes in absence of nuclear membrane and membrane-bound organelles like mitochondria, Golgi bodies, etc.

Q4. Classification based on comparative cytological studies, the number of chromosome and behaviour of chromosome is called _______.
    (A) Chemotaxonomy
    (B) Cytotaxonomy   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Artificial taxonomy
    (D) Numerical taxonomy
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Cytotaxonomy is the branch of biology dealing with the relationships and classification of organisms using comparative studies of chromosomes.

Q5. Plant cells differ from animal cells in:
    (A) Having cell membrane and Golgi bodies
    (B) Having chloroplast and Golgi bodies
    (C) Having cell wall and Chloroplast   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Having chloroplast and Mitochondria
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Plant cells have a cell wall made up of cellulose and chloroplast that contain chlorophyll for photosynthesis. Animal cell lacks both cell wall and chloroplast.

Q6. A distinction between unicellular and multicellular is not possible in case of
    (A) Plantae
    (B) Animalia
    (C) Protozoa
    (D) Algae   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Algae may be unicellular as well as multicellular, primitive algae are unicellular, and red and green algae are multicellular having a length of several meters. It is not possible to distinguish unicellular and multicellular algae because of this that unicellular green algae have not been included in kingdom Protista by Whittaker.

Q7. Which of the following archaebacteria is present in the guts of ruminant animals such as cows and buffaloes?
    (A) Speculums
    (B) Holophiles
    (C) Heterogens
    (D) Methanogens   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Methanogens bacteria are present in the guts of ruminant animals such as cows and buffaloes. The characteristic smell of cow dungs is due to methane gas produced by this bacteria.

Q8. A peculiar odour found in marshy areas and cow sheds is of gas produced by________.
    (A) Cyanobacteria
    (B) Mycoplasm
    (C) Slime molds
    (D) Archaebacteria   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The peculiar odour found in marshy areas and cow sheds is methane gas produced by methanogens bacteria that belong to class Archaebacteria.

Q9. The unicellular eukaryotes belong to the kingdom______.
    (A) Mycota
    (B) Plantae
    (C) Protista   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Monera
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Unicellular Eukaryotes were included in the kingdom Protista while unicellular Prokaryotes were included in the kingdom Monera.

Q10. A kingdom common to unicellular plants and animals is_______.
    (A) Protista   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Monera
    (C) Fungi
    (D) Algae
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Protista includes all unicellular prokaryotic organisms that include both plants and animals. So, Protista is common to unicellular plants and animals.

Q11. The infectious spore-like stage is seen in_______.
    (A) Flagellated protozoans
    (B) Sporozoans   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Amoeboid protozoans
    (D) Ciliated protozoans
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Sporozoans include diverse organisms that have an infectious spore-like stage in their life cycle.

Q12. In which group of kingdom Protista, plasmodium is formed?
    (A) Euglenoids
    (B) Dinoflagellates
    (C) Slime moulds   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Chrysophytes
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Slime moulds are saprophytic protists. The body moves along decaying twigs and leaves engulfing organic material. Under suitable conditions, they form an aggregation called plasmodium which may grow and spread over several feet. During unfavourable conditions, the plasmodium differentiates and forms fruiting bodies bearing spores at their tips.

Q13. Which criterion made Fungi to be placed in separate groups?
    (A) Cell wall   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Mode of nutrition
    (C) Nuclear membrane
    (D) Cell type
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The cell wall of fungi is made up of chitin while the green plants had a cellulosic cell wall. Due to this, fungi were placed in a separate kingdom – Kingdom Fungi.

Q14. How bacteria reproduce during unfavourable conditions?
    (A) By DNA transfer
    (B) By fission
    (C) By producing spores   <-- CORRECT
    (D) All of these
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Bacteria reproduce mainly by fission. Sometimes, under unfavourable conditions, they produce spores. They also reproduce by a sort of sexual reproduction by adopting a primitive type of DNA transfer from one bacterium to the other.

Q15. The filamentous body of the fungus is called _________.
    (A) Filament
    (B) Stipe
    (C) Hyphae
    (D) Mycelium   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Mycelium is the vegetative part of a fungus or fungus-like bacterial colony, consisting of a mass of branching, thread-like hyphae.

Biological Classification Test-03  (id 3345) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Biological Classification
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. All prokaryotic, unicellular organisms are included under the kingdom:
    (A) Monera   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Protista
    (C) Animalia
    (D) Fungi
    Answer: A
    Explanation: All prokaryotic, unicellular organisms are included in the kingdom Monera. The Eukaryotic unicellular organisms are placed in the Protista kingdom.

Q2. The cell wall of fungi consists of _______.
    (A) Starch
    (B) Glycopeptides
    (C) Cellulose
    (D) Chitin   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The cell wall of fungi consists of special sugar molecules called chitin. The cell wall of plants is made up of cellulose.

Q3. Which among the following is photosynthetic as well as saprophytic?
    (A) Mushroom
    (B) Euglena   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Paramoecium
    (D) Amoeba
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Euglena is photosynthetic in presence of sunlight and is saprophytic in absence of sunlight.

Q4. Which bacteria help in oxidising inorganic substances?
    (A) Autotrophic bacteria
    (B) Chemosynthetic autotrophic bacteria   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Cyanobacteria
    (D) Heterotrophic bacteria
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Chemosynthetic autotrophic bacteria oxidize various inorganic substances such as nitrates, nitrites, and ammonia and use the released energy for their ATP production. They play a great role in recycling nutrients like nitrogen, phosphorous, iron, and sulphur.

Q5. The asexual reproduction in fungi takes place by
    (A) Ascospores
    (B) Basidiospores
    (C) OOspores
    (D) Zoospores   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In fungi, the asexual reproduction takes place by spores called conidia or sporangiospores or zoospores, and sexual reproduction is by oospores, ascospores and basidiospores.

Q6. A distinction between unicellular and multicellular is not possible in________.
    (A) Plantae
    (B) Algae   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Animalia
    (D) Protozoa
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Algae grouped together the unicellular organisms and the multicellular ones.

Q7. Which among the following is not included in the three domains system?
    (A) Viral Domain   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Bacteria Domain
    (C) Eukara Domain
    (D) Archaea Domain
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The three-domain system includes Archaebacteria, Eubacteria, and Bacteria domain.

Q8. Which archaebacteria is present in guts of ruminant animals such as cows and buffaloes?
    (A) Methanogens   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Heterogens
    (C) Thermoacidophiles
    (D) Holophiles
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Methanogens are present in the guts of several ruminant animals such as cows and buffaloes and they are responsible for the production of methane (biogas) from the dung of these animals.

Q9. The blue-green algae are also referred to as________.
    (A) Heterotrophic bacteria
    (B) Archaebacteria
    (C) Eubacteria
    (D) Cyanobacteria   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Blue-green algae are also called cyanobacteria. They are considered as the most primitive organism that still survives. It includes different forms of unicellular and multicellular organisms.

Q10. The organism that completely lacks a cell wall and is the smallest living cell known that can highly pleomorphic is _________.
    (A) Bacteriophages
    (B) Yeast
    (C) Virus
    (D) Mycoplasma   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Mycoplasma is a genus of bacteria that lack a cell wall around their cell membrane. Without a cell wall, they are unaffected by many common antibiotics such as penicillin or other beta-lactam antibiotics that target cell wall synthesis.
Mycoplasma species are the smallest bacterial cells yet discovered, can survive without oxygen, and come in various shapes. For example, M. genitalium is flask-shaped.

Q11. Which one is not a member of the kingdom Protista?
    (A) Slime molds
    (B) Protozoa
    (C) Phycomycetes   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Euglenoids
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Phycomycetes is a subdivision of fungus which are multicellular. Protozoa, slime moulds and euglenoids are part of the kingdom Protista which are unicellular and eukaryotic organisms.

Q12. The class of fungi in which mushroom is included is________.
    (A) Ascomycetes
    (B) Deuteromycetes
    (C) Basidiomycetes   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Phycomycetes
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Commonly known forms of basidiomycetes are mushrooms, bracket fungi, or puffballs.

Q13. Diatoms do not decay easily because:
    (A) They have siliceous walls   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Their body is impervious to water
    (C) They are chitinous
    (D) They are abundant in saline water
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The walls of the diatoms are embedded with silica and thus the walls are indestructible.

Q14. In fungi like ascomycetes and basidiomycetes, an intervening dikaryotic stage occurs. Such condition is called
    (A) Mycorrhizae
    (B) Karyogamy
    (C) Plasmogamy
    (D) Dikaryon   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In fungi like ascomycetes and basidiomycetes, an intervening dikaryotic stage (n + n i.e. two nuclei per cell) occurs; such a condition is called a dikaryon and the phase is called dikaryon phase of fungus.

Q15. The body of the fungus is filamentous and it is called _______.
    (A) Hyphae
    (B) Filament
    (C) Mycelium   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Steepened
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The body of the filamentous fungus is known as mycelium, which is a thread-like structure. Mycelium produces hyphae and sporogenous cells to produce spores.

Biological Classification Test-04  (id 3346) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Biological Classification
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. Cellular genes which are known to take part in producing cancer are termed as
    (A) Viral oncogens
    (B) Proto-oncogenes   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Inactive oncogens
    (D) Cellular oncogens
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Proto-oncogenes are a group of genes that cause normal cells to become cancerous when they are mutated.

Q2. Which one is important in nutrient to recycle and act as decomposer and mineralizes of the biosphere ______.
    (A) Protozoa
    (B) Amphibians
    (C) Algae
    (D) Fungi   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Fungi is important in the nutrient cycle and acts as decomposer along with bacteria and mineralizers of the biosphere to regular recycling of nutrients in the biosphere.

Q3. In fungus, food reserves are:
    (A) Phosphoglceride
    (B) Glycogen and fat   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Lipid
    (D) Glucose and fat
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Different fungi contain different kinds of reserve food materials depending upon the habitat and body structure of the fungus. In some fungi, the food reserves are glycogen and fat.

Q4. In which class of fungi the mushroom belongs to:
    (A) Ascomycetes
    (B) Phycomycetes
    (C) Basidiomycetes   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Deuteromycetes
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The mushroom belongs to class Basidiomycetes to kingdom fungi. Basidiomycetes produce basidiospores as reproductive units. The member of this group grows on dead and decaying matters.

Q5. Which is the possible region of respiration in bacteria?
    (A) Cell wall
    (B) Mesosome   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Mitochondria
    (D) Nucleoid
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Bacteria belong to the kingdom Monera in which organisms are unicellular and prokaryotic. Prokaryotic organisms lack membrane-bounded organelles like mitochondria where respiration occurs. In bacteria, respiration occurs in the mesosome.

Q6. A bacterium capable of tolerating extreme heat, dryness, and toxic chemicals is probably having_____.
    (A) Endotoxins
    (B) Thick wall
    (C) Endospore   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Endogenous buds
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A bacterium capable of tolerating extreme heat, dryness, and toxic chemicals have the ability to produce endospores inside the body that help them to tide over unfavorable conditions.

Q7. When a freshwater protozoan is placed in marine water:
    (A) Number of contractile vacuole increases
    (B) The contractile vacuole increase in size
    (C) The contractile vacuole remain same
    (D) The contractile vacuole disappear   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: When freshwater protozoan is placed in marine water, the contractile vacuole disappears because the function of the vacuole is to expel out excess water but in the case of marine water, the water should be retained instead of getting expelled. If the contractile vacuole will not disappear the cell will get dehydrated.

Q8. The plant cells differ from animal cells in:
    (A) Having cell wall and chloroplast   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Having chloroplast and mitochondria
    (C) Having chloroplast and golgibodies
    (D) Having cell membrane and golgibodies
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The plant cells have a eukaryotic structure with prominent chloroplasts and cell walls mainly made of cellulose.

Q9. Plants complete their life cycle in two phase, sporophytic and gametophytic which occurs alternately called
    (A) Alternation of diploid and haploid
    (B) Change in phases
    (C) Alternation of generation   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Change in structure
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The fluctuation between these diploid and haploid stages that occurs in plants is called the alternation of generations. The multicellular haploid plant structure is called the gametophyte, which is formed from the spore and gives rise to the haploid gametes.

Q10. Sexual reproduction is by the population of male and female followed by embryological development is a characteristic feature of_______.
    (A) Fungi
    (B) Animalia   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Plantae
    (D) Mucor
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The sexual reproduction in the kingdom Animalia is by the population of males and female followed by embryological development.

Q11. A plant that is partially heterotrophic is______.
    (A) Guava
    (B) Utricularias
    (C) Drosera   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Orange
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Drosera plant is partially heterotrophic. These plants capture insects to fulfil its protein requirement although it performs photosynthesis also.

Q12. Who demonstrated that the extract of the infected plants of tobacco could cause infection in healthy plants?
    (A) D.J.Ivanowsky
    (B) W.M.Stanley
    (C) M. W. Beijerinck   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Pasteur
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Beijerinck is considered one of the founders of virology. In 1898, he published results on the filtration experiments demonstrating that tobacco mosaic disease is caused by an infectious agent smaller than a bacterium and called the fluid as Contagiumvivum fluidum (infectious living fluid).

Q13. The outer protein covering of virus is_______.
    (A) Virion
    (B) Coat
    (C) Viroid
    (D) Capsid   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: A capsid is the protein shell of a virus. It consists of several oligomeric structural subunits made of a protein called protomers. The capsid encloses the genetic material of the virus.

Q14. The genetic material of a virus is:
    (A) Only DNA
    (B) Only RNA
    (C) Both DNA and RNA
    (D) Either DNA or RNA   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Most viruses have either RNA or DNA as their genetic material. The nucleic acid may be single- or double-stranded. The entire infectious virus particle, called a virion, consists of the nucleic acid and an outer shell of protein.

Q15. Diener discovered_____.
    (A) Mycoplasm
    (B) Lichens
    (C) Viroids   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Virus
    Answer: C
    Explanation: T.O. Diener discovered a new infectious agent that was smaller than viruses and caused potato spindle tuber disease. It was found to be a free RNA. It lacked the protein coat that is found in viruses, hence the name viroid.

Biological Classification Test-05  (id 3347) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Biological Classification
Questions: 14 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. A peculiar group of the dual organism which is formed by an association between algae and a fungus.
    (A) Yeast
    (B) Mushroom
    (C) Lichens   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Mucor
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A lichen is a composite organism that arises from algae or cyanobacteria living among filaments of multiple fungi in a symbiotic relationship. The combined lichen has properties different from those of its component organisms.

Q2. A virus that infects and replicates within a bacterium is called
    (A) Fungi
    (B) Bacteriophage   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Diatom
    (D) Bacterium
    Answer: B
    Explanation: A bacteriophage is a virus that infects and replicates within a bacterium.

Q3. Which is NOT the characteristic of viroids?
    (A) The RNA of the viroid has low molecular weight
    (B) It has a protein coat   <-- CORRECT
    (C) It is smaller than virus
    (D) It caused potato spindle tuber disease
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Viroids are smaller than viruses and caused potato spindle tuber disease. It was found to be a free RNA; it lacked the protein coat that is found in viruses, hence the name viroid. The RNA of the viroid was of low molecular weight.

Q4. The name virus was first given by_______.
    (A) D.J.Ivanowsky
    (B) Pasteur
    (C) Beijerinck   <-- CORRECT
    (D) W.M.Stanley
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The name virus was first given by Beijerinck, in 1898.

Q5. Identify the virus in figure given below
    (A) Bacteriophage   <-- CORRECT
    (B) TMV
    (C) HIV
    (D) Retrovirus
    Answer: A
    Explanation: A bacteriophage is a virus that infects and replicates within a bacterium.Bacteriophages are composed of proteins that encapsulate a DNA or RNA genome, and may have relatively simple or elaborate structures.

Q6. The genetic material for retrovirus is_________.
    (A) Both DNA and RNA
    (B) Nucleoprotein complex
    (C) DNA
    (D) RNA   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The virus in which genetic material is RNA is called a retrovirus. In this virus reverse transcription takes place to form DNA that synthesis proteins.

Q7. The three domains system do not include:
    (A) Archaea Domain
    (B) Eukara Domain
    (C) Bacteria Domain
    (D) Viral Domain   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Three kingdoms or domain system of classification does not include the viral domain. The virus was discovered after the invention of the electron microscope so, they were not part of the living world.

Q8. Identify the cuboidal virus from the following:
    (A) Foot and mouth virus
    (B) T2
    (C) TMV virus
    (D) Polymyelitis virus   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: A virus consists of genetic material (DNA or RNA) surrounded by protein capsules. They are of different shapes and sizes. The poliomyelitis virus is cubical in shape.

Q9. The organism that completely lacks a cell wall and is the smallest living cell know can survive without oxygen is_______.
    (A) Mycoplasmas   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Bacteriophages
    (C) Virus
    (D) Yeast
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Mycoplasmas are a group of organisms that lack a cell wall and are the smallest living organisms. They can survive without oxygen. Mycoplasmas are also called as PPLO (pleuro pneumonia-like organism).

Q10. Which one can be photosynthetic as well as saprophytic?
    (A) Mushroom
    (B) Amoeba
    (C) Euglena   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Paramecium
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Euglena is a photosynthetic as well as a saprophytic organism. It contains chlorophyll for photosynthesis and can absorb food from dead and decaying materials.

Q11. Select the incorrect pair:
    (A) Bacterial Virus - Bacteriophages
    (B) Algal Virus - Mycophages   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Animal Virus - Zoophagineae
    (D) Plant Virus - Phytophagineae
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Mycophages are not a group of bacteria. They are a group of organisms that use algae as food. The animal virus is called Zoophagineae, plant virus phytophagineae, and the bacterial virus is called bacteriophages.

Q12. Two categories of animals on the basis of red blood are:
    (A) Animate and inanimate
    (B) Enaima and Anaima   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Erythrocytes and Thrombocytes
    (D) Leucocytes and erythrocytes
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Haemoglobin in RBCs imparts red colour to it. The organisms whose blood contains haemoglobin are called enaima and those without it are called anaima.

Q13. The fusion of protoplasm between to motile or non-motile gamete is called ________.
    (A) Plasmogamy   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Karyogamy
    (C) Homogamy
    (D) Heterogamy
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Plasmogamy is the fusion of protoplasm of two cells which may be motile or non- motile. Plasmogamy occurs during sexual reproduction to form a diploid organism.

Q14. Plant disease in which pathogen is seen as cottony growth on the surface of the host is:
    (A) Smut
    (B) Downy mildew   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Powdery mildew
    (D) Rust
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Downy mildew disease is caused due to fungus that forms cottony growth on the surface of the host. The leaves' surface gets reduced that alters the photosynthesis rate.

Plant Kingdom Test-01  (id 3348) [FREE]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Plant Kingdom

Q1. In Phaeophyceae, the food stored in the form of:
    (A) Protein
    (B) Mannitol, laminarin   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Oil droplets
    (D) Starch
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In Phaeophyceae, food is stored as complex carbohydrates which may be in the form of laminarin or mannitol.

Q2. Kelps are ________.
    (A) Fresh water algae
    (B) Marine algae   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Terrestrial plant
    (D) Amphibious plant
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Kelps are marine algae of class Phaeophyceae or brown algae. The body of kelp may reach up to 100 meters long. They vary in colour from olive green to various shades of brown depending upon xanthophyll pigments, fucoxanthin present in them.

Q3. An algae having ribbon-shaped chloroplast is_______.
    (A) Kelps
    (B) Chara
    (C) Ulothrix
    (D) Spirogyra   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The shape of a chloroplast varies from species to species. It may be cup-shaped (e.g., Chlamydomonas), (e.g., Vaucheria), Girdle (e.g., Ulothrix), Stellate or Star-shaped (e.g., Zygnema), Reticulate or net-like (e.g., Cladophora, Oedogonium), Spiral or ribbon or scalariform (e.g., Spirogyra), ovoid or disc or spheroid in higher plants.

Q4. Laminaria and Fucus belong to:
    (A) Brown algae   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Golden brown algae
    (C) Green algae
    (D) Red algae
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The common forms of Brown algae or Phaeophyceae are Ectocarpus, Dictyota, Laminaria, Sargassum and Fucus.

Q5. Angiosperm: roots :: Phaeophyceae:
    (A) Holdfast   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Root hair
    (C) Prop root
    (D) Substratum
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The plant body of Phaeophyceae is usually attached to the substratum by a holdfast whereas the angiosperms attach to the substratum with the help of roots.

Q6. Half of the total carbon dioxide fixation on earth is carried out by algae through ________.
    (A) Absorption
    (B) Transportation
    (C) Respiration
    (D) Photosynthesis   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Being photosynthetic, algae increase the level of dissolved oxygen in their immediate environment.

Q7. In Ulothrix or Spirogyra, reduction division (meiosis) occurs at the time of:
    (A) Gamete formation
    (B) Vegetative reproduction
    (C) Zygospore germination   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Zoospore formation
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In Ulothrix/Spirogyra reduction division (meiosis) occurs at the time of zygospore germination. The plant body of Ulothrix and Spirogyra is gametophytic (haploid), they produce zoogametes (n) which fuses to form zygospores (2n) diploid, which is a resting spore. The onset of favourable condition zygospore undergoes reductional division, or meiosis to produce zoo- meiospores.

Q8. The cell wall of green algae is made up of _______.
    (A) Glycoproteins
    (B) Hemicellulose
    (C) Cellulose   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Proteins
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Green algae usually have a rigid cell wall made of an inner layer of cellulose and an outer layer of pectose.

Q9. Which classes of algae possess chlorophyll a, chlorophyll b, carotenoids and xanthophylls?
    (A) Chlorophyceae   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Phaeophyceae
    (C) Rhodophyceae
    (D) All of the these
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The class Chlorophyceae (Green Algae) contains chlorophyll a, chlorophyll b, carotenoids, and xanthophylls as their primary pigments. These pigments give them a distinct green color and help in photosynthesis.

Q10. The process of fusion between one large and non-motile female gamete with smaller, motile male gamete is termed as________.
    (A) Oogmous   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Homogamous
    (C) Isogamous
    (D) Anisogamous
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The fusion between one large, non-motile female gamete and a smaller, motile male gamete is termed as oogamous e.g., Volvox, Fucus.

Q11. Rhodophyta is commonly called red algae because of the predominance of pigment________.
    (A) Fucoxanthin
    (B) Chlorophyll b
    (C) r-Phycoerythrin   <-- CORRECT
    (D) p-Phycoerytrhin
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The algal class Rhodophyta are commonly called red algae because it contains a red pigment, r-phycoerythrin along with chlorophyll a and d.

Q12. Agar is obtained from_______.
    (A) Ectocarpus
    (B) Ficus
    (C) Gelidium   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Polysiphonia
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Agar, one of the commercial products obtained from Gelidium are used to grow microbes and in preparations of ice-creams and jellies.

Q13. The largest unicellular organism is_________.
    (A) Planaria
    (B) Acetabularia   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Yeast
    (D) Volvox
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Acetabularia is a genus of green algae, especially of the Polyphyaceae family. It is the largest unicellular organism.

Q14. Pond scum is________.
    (A) Ulothrix
    (B) Oedogonium
    (C) Nostoc
    (D) Spirogyra   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The green patchy structure that develops around the surface of stagnant water bodies having thread-like mass is called pond scum. They are actually a species of green algae, Spirogyra.

Q15. Algae with ribbon-shaped chloroplast _______.
    (A) Spirogyra   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Chara
    (C) Kelps
    (D) Ulothrix
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Spirogyra is an alga that has a long thread-like structure having a ribbon-shaped chloroplast. Spirogyra is found in stagnant water forming a green layer around the surface called pond scum.

Plant Kingdom Test-02  (id 3349) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Plant Kingdom
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. The algae that secrete and deposit calcium carbonate over their walls to contribute to producing coral reefs is______.
    (A) All of these
    (B) Red algae   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Brown algae
    (D) Green algae
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Red algae in the order Corallinales, characterized by a thallus that is hard because of calcareous deposits which contribute to producing coral reefs in seawater.

Q2. Identify the algae present in the figure
    (A) Spirogyra
    (B) Volvox
    (C) Chara
    (D) Chlamydomonas   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The algae present in the figure is Chlamydomonas which is a unicellular algae present in fresh water. Two flagella is attached to it that helps in the movement in water.

Q3. Which of the following is responsible for peat formation ?
    (A) Marchantia
    (B) Riccia
    (C) Funaria
    (D) Sphagnum   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Sphagnum mosses not only dominate large areas of the boreal peatlands, but they have also formed these habitats by their growth and production of decay-resistant litter. As they invade, they can quickly transform a high-pH fen with little peat accumulation to a bog where large amounts of carbon are stored. They are also responsible for the many types of surface patterns observed in peatlands. Their ability to shape and transform mires can to a large extent be understood from the peculiar anatomy and biochemistry, a fact which makes the links between species’ traits and ecosystem functions in peatlands very strong.

Q4. Which of the following is produced by moss spore on germination?
    (A) Protonema   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Annulus
    (C) Theca
    (D) Peristome
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The spore of moss germinate to produce a protonema, which is a green, branched, and frequently filamentous stage and develops a lateral bud which is called secondary protonema or a leafy stage. Secondary protonema also gives rise to gametophore initials. Secondary protonema can undergo both sexual and asexual modes of reproduction. It reproduces asexually by the processes of budding and fragmentation. Sexual reproduction is the process that occurs in the leafy stage.

Q5. Asexual reproduction in liverworts takes place by specialised structures, commonly known as:
    (A) Fragmentation
    (B) Budding
    (C) Gemmae cups   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Spores
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Asexual reproduction in liverworts takes place by the formation of specialized structures called gemmae (sing. gemma). Gemmae are green, multicellular, asexual buds, which develop in small receptacles called gemma cups located on the thalli. The gemmae become detached from the parent body and germinate to form new individuals.

Q6. A plant producing seeds but lacking flowers is:
    (A) Bryophyte
    (B) Pteridophyta
    (C) Angiosperms
    (D) Gymnosperms   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Gymnosperms produce seeds without the formation of flowers. The gymnosperms (Gymnos: naked, Sperma: seeds) are planted in which the ovules are not enclosed by any ovary wall and remain exposed, both before and after fertilization. The seeds that develop post-fertilization, are not covered, i.e., are naked.

Q7. A moss plant used as a fuel is __________.
    (A) Sphagnum   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Polytrichum
    (C) Marchantia
    (D) Funaria
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Species of Sphagnum, a moss, provide peat that has long been used as fuel.

Q8. Which of the following is also called 'amphibians of plant kingdom'?
    (A) Gymnosperms
    (B) Bryophytes   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Angiosperms
    (D) Thallophyta
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Bryophytes are also called amphibians of the plant kingdom because these plants can live in soil but are dependent on water for sexual reproduction as they release antherozoids into the water where they come in contact with archegonium to produce a zygote.

Q9. Bryophytes flourish is moist and shady environments because:
    (A) They cannot grow in land
    (B) Their gametes fuse in water   <-- CORRECT
    (C) They lack roots and stomata
    (D) They lack vascular tissues
    Answer: B
    Explanation: These plants can live in soil but are dependent on water for sexual reproduction as they release antherozoids into the water where they come in contact with archegonium to produce a zygote. They usually occur in damp, humid, and shaded localities.

Q10. Archegoniophore is found in ________.
    (A) Marchantia   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Adiantum
    (C) Funaria
    (D) Sphagnum
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Archegoniophore (female gametophytes ) develop on the thallus of Marchantia. Each archegonium produces a single egg cell which helps in sexual reproduction.

Q11. The root-like structure which helps in anchorage and absorption of water in Bryophytes is called ________.
    (A) Rhizoids   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Fibrous root
    (C) Tap root
    (D) Tubers
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Rhizoids are the root-like structures present in Bryophytes that help in anchorage and absorption of water. They are thin hair-like structures generally present at the ventral surface of Bryophytes.

Q12. Which of the following functions is carried out by Moss peristome?
    (A) Spore dispersal   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Absorption of water and minerals
    (C) Nutrition
    (D) Protection
    Answer: A
    Explanation: All moss capsules have an operculum and peristome. During spore dispersal, peristome teeth bend outwards and spores fall out of the capsule and are carried by air currents.

Q13. Thallus of Riccia is _________.
    (A) Haploid   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Tetraploid
    (C) Triploid
    (D) Diploid
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Riccia is a genus of liverworts in the order Marchantiales. In bryophytes, the plant body is generally haploid (n) that alternate with a diploid form for shorter period. The thallus of Riccia is Haploid.

Q14. Which one is peat moss?
    (A) Sphagnum   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Chara
    (C) Equisetum
    (D) Marchantia
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Sphagnum is also known as peat moss as it provides peat that has long been used as fuel.

Q15. Both Pteridophytes and Gymnosperms possesses_________.
    (A) Archegonia   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Seeds
    (C) Ovules
    (D) Independent gametophyte
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Pteridophytes and Gymnosperms belong to a different division of plant kingdom but both of them possess Archegonia as female sex organ which produces female gamete for sexual reproduction.
