Plant Kingdom Test-03  (id 3350) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Plant Kingdom
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. Cycas is a gymnosperm as it has:
    (A) Naked seeds   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Sieve tubes
    (C) Living fossil status
    (D) Vessels
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The gymnosperms (Gymnos: naked, Sperma: seeds) are plants in which the ovules are not enclosed by any ovary wall and remain exposed, both before and after fertilization. The seeds that develop post-fertilization, are not covered, i.e., are naked. Since Cycas has naked seeds, it belongs to gymnosperms.

Q2. In which pteridophytes, heterosporous is produced?
    (A) Psilotum
    (B) Equisetum
    (C) Adiantum
    (D) Salvinia   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Genera like Selaginella and Salvinia which produce two kinds of spores, macro (large) and micro (small) spores are known as heterosporous.

Q3. Choose the odd one out among the following: Dryopteris, Pteris, Adiantum, Selaginella.
    (A) Selaginella   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Dryopteris
    (C) Adiantum
    (D) Pteris
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Selaginella belongs to class Lycopsida and other plants (Dryopteris, Pteris, Adiantum) belong to class Pteropsida of Pteridophytes.

Q4. The giant redwood tree is ________.
    (A) Sequoia   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Pinus
    (C) Cedrus
    (D) Cycas
    Answer: A
    Explanation: One of the gymnosperms, Giant sequoias are the world's largest single tree with an average height of 50 - 85 m (164 - 279 ft) and 6 - 8 m (20 - 26 ft) in diameter.

Q5. Which among the following belong to Sphenopsida?
    (A) Equisetum   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Psilotum
    (C) Lycopodium
    (D) Pteris
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Equisetum of Pteridophyta belongs to class Sphenopsida.

Q6. Identify the plant shown in the figure given below.
    (A) Cycas   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Pinus
    (C) Coconut
    (D) Ginkgo
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The plant shown in the figure is cycas that belongs to division Cycadophyta and family Cycadaceae. It is dioecious and Cycas circinalis species is endemic to India.

Q7. Male and female gametophytes do not have a free independent existence in_____.
    (A) Pteris
    (B) Polytrichum
    (C) Funaria
    (D) Cedrus   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Unlike bryophytes and pteridophytes, in gymnosperms (Cedrus) the male and the female gametophytes do not have an independent free-living existence.

Q8. The structure formed by germinated fern spore is:
    (A) Embryo
    (B) Thallus
    (C) Germpore
    (D) Prothallus   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Fern spores germinate to give rise to inconspicuous, small but multicellular, free-living, mostly photosynthetic thalloid gametophytes called prothallus. The gametophytes bear male and female sex organs called antheridia and archegonia.

Q9. The megasporangium of naked seed plants are called
    (A) Thalamus
    (B) Ovary
    (C) Anther
    (D) Ovule   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The cones bearing megasporophylls with ovules or megasporangia are called macrosporangiate or female strobili.

Q10. The cone of Gymnosperms represent the:
    (A) Vegetative organs
    (B) Formative organs
    (C) Reproductive organs   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Buds
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In gymnosperms, male and female cones are formed that produce male and female gametes. The strobilus bearing microsporophylls and microsporangia are called microsporangia or male strobilus. The cones bearing megasporophylls with ovules or megasporangia are called microsporangia or female strobilus. So, the cone of gymnosperms represents the reproductive organs.

Q11. The main plant body of the bryophyte is _______.
    (A) Diplo-haplontic
    (B) Diploid
    (C) Haploid   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Haplo-diplontic
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The main plant body of the bryophyte is haploid. It produces gametes, hence is called a gametophyte.

Q12. Which plant has a fungal association in the form of mycorrhiza?
    (A) Sequoia
    (B) Pinus   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Cycas
    (D) Cedrus
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Roots in some genera of gymnosperms have a fungal association in the form of mycorrhizal (Pinus).

Q13. The sporophytes bearing sporangia having leaf-like appendages are called ________.
    (A) Microsporophyll
    (B) Megasporophyll
    (C) Sporophylls   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Saprophytes
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The sporophytes bear sporangia that are subtended by leaf-like appendages called sporophylls.

Q14. The phenomenon of having two types of spores by the same plant is called ________.
    (A) Heterogamy
    (B) Megaspory
    (C) Heterospory   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Bispory
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The phenomenon of having two types of spores by the same plant is called heterospory. Male spores are small (micro) and female spores are comparatively larger (macro) than males like Selaginella and Salvinia are heterosporous.

Q15. In mosses, the sex organs arise from:
    (A) Leaf apex   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Capsule
    (C) Foot
    (D) Setae
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In sexual reproduction, the sex organs antheridia and archegonia are produced at the apex of the leafy shoots.

Plant Kingdom Test-04  (id 3351) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Plant Kingdom
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. Liverworts are closely related to______.
    (A) Fungi
    (B) Mosses   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Algae
    (D) Lichen
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The bryophytes are divided into liverworts and mosses so they are closely related to each other.

Q2. Apophysis of moss is:
    (A) Terminal part of capsule
    (B) Sterile filaments in male receptacle
    (C) Lower part of capsule   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Part of peristome
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The sporophyte of moss is differentiated into three parts - foot, seta, and capsule. The capsule, in turn, is differentiated into 3 regions.
 Apophysis - the sterile basal portion of the capsule, it is in continuity with seta
 Theca or body of capsule, which is the fertile region, and
 Operculum the apical region of capsule.
Apophysis is rich in chloroplast and thus the photosynthetic region of moss, it also provides nutrition to the developing sporangium.

Q3. On germination, moss spore produce _________.
    (A) Protonema   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Annulus
    (C) Theca
    (D) Peristome
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The spore of moss germinates to produce protonema. It is a creeping, green, branched, and frequently filamentous stage, which develops into secondary protonema as a lateral bud. This stage bears sex organs.

Q4. Which one of the following is a vascular cryptogam?
    (A) Marchantia
    (B) Equisetum   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Cedrus
    (D) Ginkgo
    Answer: B
    Explanation: A Cryptogam is a plant that reproduces by spores without flowers or seeds. Most of the cryptogamous plants lack vascular bundles i.e xylem and phloem but some member of pteridophytes like Equisetum contain vascular bundle.

Q5. Which one is living fossil _______.
    (A) Metasequoia
    (B) Seleginella
    (C) Pinus
    (D) Ginkgo   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Ginkgo is a living fossil. This plant belongs to the gymnosperms division. It is considered as one of the oldest plants known and still surviving in some parts of the world.

Q6. Which plant division is known as amphibians _________.
    (A) Thallophyta
    (B) Angiosperms
    (C) Gymnosperms
    (D) Bryophytes   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Bryophytes are called amphibians of the plant kingdom as they can grow in both land and water. Water is essential for the completion of the life cycle as they release antherozoids into the water where they come in contact with archegonium to produce a zygote.

Q7. The yellow or brown spots which have sporangia in fern are called ______.
    (A) Arthropodia
    (B) Capsule
    (C) Archegonia
    (D) Sori   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The yellow or brown spots which have sporangia in fern are called sori. Spores are produced inside these sporangia to produce haploid gametophyte.

Q8. In gymnosperms, cross-pollination is accompanied by-
    (A) Insects
    (B) Water
    (C) Wind   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Bats
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In Gymnosperms, cross-pollination is mainly accompanied by wind. The pollen grains are produced in large quantities and generally lighter.

Q9. Greatest extent of adaptation to various environments is found in_______.
    (A) Ferns
    (B) Gymnosperms
    (C) Bryophytes
    (D) Angiosperms   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Adaptation is essential for the survival of the living organism. The greatest extent of adaption in various environmental conditions is found in Angiosperms. Angiosperms are found in all kinds of environments and altitudes.

Q10. Primary endosperm nucleus is formed by ________.
    (A) Fusion of central nucleus
    (B) Triple fusion   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Syngamy
    (D) Egg synergid
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The pollen tubes enter the embryo-sac where two male gametes are discharged. One of the male gametes fuses with the egg cell to form a zygote (syngamy). The other male gamete fuses with the diploid secondary nucleus to produce the triploid primary endosperm nucleus (PEN). Because of the involvement of two fusions, this event is termed as double fertilization.

Q11. In dicots, each embryo-sac consist of:
    (A) Egg apparatus, polar nuclei and endosperm
    (B) Egg, antipodal cell and funicle
    (C) Synergids, egg and antipodal cells
    (D) Egg apparatus, antipodal cells and polar nuclei   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In dicots, each embryo-sac consists of egg apparatus (ovum and two synergids) located at micropylar end, three antipodal cells located at the chalazal end and two polar nuclei at the centre.

Q12. A plant that forms seeds but no fruits are ______.
    (A) Radish
    (B) Mustard
    (C) Potato
    (D) Pinus   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Pinus belongs to division gymnosperms. In gymnosperms, seeds are formed but not inside the fruit. They are also called as plants with naked seeds.

Q13. A plant that forms fruits but not seeds are ______.
    (A) Radish
    (B) Banana   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Potato
    (D) Sweet potato
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Generally, seeds are formed inside the fruits. But in banana viable seeds are not present. It is a parthenocarpic fruit.

Q14. Select one of the following pairs of important features distinguishing Gnetum from Cycas and Pinus and showing affinities with angiosperms.
    (A) Absence of rasin duct and leaf venation
    (B) Presence of vessels elements and the absence of archegonia   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Perianth and two integuments
    (D) Embryo development and apical meristem
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Gnetum belongs to order Gnetales. In gymnosperms except Gnetales xylem consists of xylem parenchyma and tracheids with bordered pits but lacks vessels. This shows that Gnetales are the most advanced among gymnosperms. They lack archegonia in female gametophytes thus showing similarity with angiosperms and acts as a connecting link between the gymnosperms and angiosperms.

Q15. Top shaped multinucleate male gametes and mature seeds with one embryo having two cotyledons are characteristic features of_______.
    (A) Gametopetalous angiosperms
    (B) Conifers
    (C) Polypetalous angiosperms
    (D) Cycas   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Cycas produces top-shaped multinucleate male gametes and mature seeds with one embryo having two cotyledons. Although, male and female gametes are generally uninucleate in gymnosperms.

Plant Kingdom Test-05  (id 3352) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Plant Kingdom
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. All seed bearing plant, alternation of generation is ________.
    (A) Diplontic   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Monoplontic
    (C) Haplontic
    (D) Haplo-diplontic
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In diplontic life cycle, diploid sporophyte is the dominant, photosynthetic, independent phase of the plant. The gametophytic phase is represented by the single to few-celled haploid gametophyte .All seed bearing plants i.e., gymnosperms and angiosperms exhibits diplontic life cycle.

Q2. The sperms of ________ are largest in the biological world.
    (A) Ginkgo
    (B) Mango
    (C) Pinus
    (D) Cycas   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The sperms of male gamete of Cycas are the largest in the biological world. It is top-shaped. In Cycas revoluta the size of the sperm ranges between 180 to 210 μm and they are clearly visible to the naked eye.

Q3. Haplontic life cycle is seen in_______.
    (A) Volvox   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Cycas
    (C) Marchantia
    (D) Sphagnum
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In the haplontic life cycle, the dominant, photosynthetic phase is the free-living gametophyte which is seen in Volvox, Spirogyra, and Chlamydomonas.

Q4. Thallus of Riccia is ________.
    (A) Haploid   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Diploid
    (C) Triploid
    (D) Tetraploid
    Answer: A
    Explanation: A dominant, independent, photosynthetic, thalloid, or erect phase of Bryophytes and pteridophytes is represented by a haploid gametophyte.

Q5. Pteridophytes differ from mosses in having:
    (A) Independent gametophyte
    (B) Independent and dominant sporophyte   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Dependent gametophyte
    (D) Flagellate antheriozoids
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In bryophytes, the dominant phase in the life cycle is the gametophytic plant body. However, in pteridophytes, the main plant body is a sporophyte which is differentiated into true root, stem and leaves.

Q6. All seed-bearing plant, alternation of generation is_________.
    (A) Haplo-diplontic
    (B) Monoplontic
    (C) Haplontic
    (D) Diplontic   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: All seed-bearing plants i.e., gymnosperms and angiosperms follow diplontic alternation of a generation where the diploid sporophyte is the dominant, photosynthetic, independent phase of the plant. The gametophytic phase is represented by the single to the few-celled haploid gametophyte.

Q7. Megasporangium of seed plants are called:
    (A) Ovary
    (B) Anther
    (C) Thalamus
    (D) Ovule   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Megasporangium of seed plants is called an ovule. The ovule is present inside the ovary which becomes seed on maturation after fertilization. It produces megasporocytes or Megaspore mother cells that yield megaspores.

Q8. Angiosperm: roots :: Rhodophyta :?
    (A) Holdfast   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Root hair
    (C) Prop root
    (D) Substratum
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Angiosperms plants have roots to hold the soil and remain erect. Similarly, Rhodophytes have holdfast by which they remain attached with substratum to absorb water and minerals.

Q9. Primary endosperm nucleus is formed by _____________.
    (A) Egg synergids
    (B) Fusion of central nucleus
    (C) Triple fusion   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Syngamy
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The fusion of two polar nuclei with one male gamete is called triple fusion. The primary endosperm nucleus is formed by triple fusion and divide mitotically to form endosperm.

Q10. The phloem of angiosperms differ from that of other vascular plants by the presence of:
    (A) Vessels
    (B) Trachieds
    (C) Companion cells   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Albuminous cells
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Gymnosperms and lower vascular plants have sieve cells as their sieve elements, while sieve tubes and companion cells are characteristic of flowering plants (angiosperms). Phloem transports food from leaves to all other parts of plants.

Q11. Some plants are dependent on the larger plant for space only. Such plants are called as ________.
    (A) Halophytes
    (B) Mesophytes
    (C) Epiphytes   <-- CORRECT
    (D) bryophyte
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Epiphytes are dependent on other large plants for space or physical support. It remains to attach with other plants but does not obtain food or another nutrient from it so they are not parasitic on the supporting plants.

Q12. Which of the following includes a diploid structure?
    (A) Gametophyte and spore mass
    (B) Gametophyte and Capsule   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Gametophyte and oospores
    (D) Gametophyte and antheridia
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Gametophytes and capsule are diploid structure and alternate with a haploid structure called spores by reduction division.

Q13. Non-flowering plants belong to:
    (A) Monocots
    (B) Phanerogams
    (C) Cryptogams   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Dicots
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The cryptogams are flowerless and seedless plants. They are simple plants like algae, mosses, and ferns which do not produce flowers, fruits, and seeds. Cryptogams are considered as lower plants.

Q14. In which one of the following, male and female gametophytes do not have free living independent existence?
    (A) Pteris
    (B) Cedrus   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Funaria
    (D) Polytrichum
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In Cedrus plants, male and female gametophytes do not have a free independent existence. They remain attached to sporophytic forms to obtain nutrients.

Q15. Fusion between one large and non-motile female gamete with smaller, motile male gamete is termed as______.
    (A) Homogamous
    (B) Oogamous   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Isogamous
    (D) Anisogamous
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Oogamy is a form of anisogamy (heterogamy) in which the female gamete (e.g. egg cell) is significantly larger than the male gamete and is non-motile.

Animal Kingdom Test-01  (id 3353) [FREE]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Animal Kingdom
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. Which phylum contains coelomic and triploblastic animals?
    (A) Phylum Platyhelminthes   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Phylum Porifera
    (C) Phylum Ctenophora
    (D) Phylum Coelenterata
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Those animals in which the developing embryo has a three germinal layer, mesoderm in between the ectoderm and endoderm, are called triploblastic animals, and the absence of an internal body cavity is called coelomic.

Q2. Choose the odd one out based on coelom: Annelids, Molluscs, Platyhelminthes, Arthropods.
    (A) Platyhelminthes   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Molluscs
    (C) Annelids
    (D) Arthopods
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Animals possessing coelom are called coelomates such as annelids, molluscs, arthropods, echinoderms, hemichordates and chordates. In Platyhelmites coelom is absent.

Q3. In Coelenterates, the cell shows:
    (A) Organ system level of organisation
    (B) Organ level of organisation
    (C) Tissue level of organisation   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Cellular level of organisation
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In coelenterates, the arrangement of cells is more complex. Here, the cells performing the same function are arranged into tissues, hence is called tissue level of organization.

Q4. The cross-section of the body of an invertebrate is given below. Identify the animal which has this body plan:-
    (A) Cockroach
    (B) Earthworm
    (C) Round worm   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Planaria
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In some animals, the body cavity is not lined by mesoderm, instead, the mesoderm is present as scattered pouches in between the ectoderm and endoderm. Such a body cavity is called pseudocoelom and the animals possessing them are called pseudocoelomates, e.g.,aschelminthes such as round worm.

Q5. The largest phylum of kingdom animalia is ________.
    (A) Nematode
    (B) Arthropoda   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Chordate
    (D) Annelida
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Arthropoda is the largest phylum of kingdom Animalia. It includes all insects, arachnids, myriapods, and crustaceans. They are characterized by jointed limbs and cuticles.

Q6. Egg of reptiles and birds are:
    (A) Mesolecithal
    (B) Alecithal
    (C) Polylecithal   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Isolecithal
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The eggs of reptiles and birds are polyecithal because they contain a large amount of yolk inside the egg.

Q7. Animals of class Mammalia have:
    (A) Fourteen cervical vertebrae
    (B) Seven cranial nerve
    (C) Seven cervical vertebra   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Three chambered heart
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The animals of class Mammalia have seven cervical vertebrae and a four-chambered heart. Mammalian is characterized by the presence of mammary glands to feed their young ones.

Q8. The alimentary canal is absent in:
    (A) Ancylostoma
    (B) Taenia Solium   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Fasciola hepatica
    (D) Ascaris suum
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The alimentary canal is absent in Taenia Solium. Taenia Solium is an obligate parasite and obtains digested food from the small intestine of the human being as well as pigs. Pick the animals with true placenta.

Q9. Pick the animals with true placenta__________.
    (A) Kangaroo
    (B) Platypus
    (C) Echidna
    (D) Mongoose   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The true placenta is present in Mongoose. Placenta help in the transfer of nutrients and respiratory gases from the mother to the growing foetus.

Q10. The air bladder is present in_______.
    (A) Star fish
    (B) Actinopterygii   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Flying fishes
    (D) Chondricthyes
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The air bladder is present in Actinopterygii. It is also known as ray-finned fish due to the presence of fin rays.

Q11. Book lungs are respiratory organ of______.
    (A) Earthworm
    (B) Arachnida   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Mullusca
    (D) Mammals
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Book lung is a type of respiratory organ used for atmospheric gas exchange that is found in Arachnida such as scorpions and spiders.

Q12. Which of the following have notochord throughout life?
    (A) Fish
    (B) Buds
    (C) Amphioxus   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Snake
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Amphioxus or lancelets are fish-like marine chordates found in shallow temperate and tropical seas. They have notochord throughout their life.

Q13. The aquatic organisms that can actively swim at will against the water current are:
    (A) Benthos
    (B) Neuston
    (C) Necton   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Plankton
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Necton is an aquatic organism that can actively swim at will against the water current. Benthos and planktons float with the water current and not against the water current.

Q14. Haemocoel is found in:
    (A) Earthworm
    (B) Hydra
    (C) Snake
    (D) Pila   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Haemocoel is the main body cavity of invertebrates such as insects. It is also found in Pila which do not contain the blood circulating system.

Q15. An egg-laying animal grouped under mammals is:
    (A) Fluke
    (B) Kangaroo
    (C) Duck-billed Platypus   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Horn-bill
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Most of the animals belonging to class Mammalia are viviparous, produces young ones. But, Duck-billed platypus belongs to mammalian class but lay eggs.

Animal Kingdom Test-02  (id 3354) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Animal Kingdom
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. When the coelomic fluid serves as a skeleton it is known as__________.
    (A) Cartilaginous skeleton
    (B) Hydrostatic skeleton   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Exoskeleton
    (D) Endoskeleton
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Coelomic fluids serve as a skeleton in some insects called as a hydrostatic skeleton that helps in maintaining shape and size of the body of organisms in the absence of bone or cartilage.

Q2. Which one of the following group of animals is correctly matched with its characteristics without any exception?
    (A) Mammalia give birth to young ones
    (B) Reptilia possess a 3-chambered heart with incompletely divided ventricle
    (C) Chordates possess a mouth with an upper and lower jaw
    (D) Chondrichthyes possess a cartilaginous endoskeleton   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: All cartilaginous fish or Chondrichthyes possess a cartilaginous endoskeleton. But some reptiles have a four-chambered heart. Chordates may be jawless and some mammals lay eggs also.

Q3. Animals which possess cleidoic egg exhibit:
    (A) Internal fertilisation and external development   <-- CORRECT
    (B) External fertilisation and internal development
    (C) External fertilisation and external development
    (D) Internal fertilisation and internal development
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The cleidoic egg is the type of egg that reptiles and birds lay. These eggs exhibit internal fertilization and external development.

Q4. Which of these is a freshwater sponge?
    (A) Euplectella
    (B) Leucosolenia
    (C) Sycon
    (D) Spongilla   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Spongilla is a genus of freshwater sponges in the family Spongillidae found in lakes and slow streams. Sponges of the genus Spongilla attach themselves to rocks and logs and filter the water for various small aquatic organisms such as protozoans, bacteria, and other free-floating pond life. Unlike marine sponges, freshwater sponges are exposed to far more adverse and variable environmental conditions, so they have developed gemmules as a means of dormancy.

Q5. Which one of the following is a living fossil?
    (A) Bombyx
    (B) Locusta
    (C) Laccifer
    (D) Limulus   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Limulus (the king crab or horse-shoe crab) continues to remain unchanged for the past 190 million years. It is, therefore, also called living fossil. Excretion occurs through four pairs of coxal glands. Respiration occurs through book gills.

Q6. Which of the following is the largest phylum of kingdom Animalia?
    (A) Platyhelminthes
    (B) Annelida
    (C) Arthropoda   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Echinodermata
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Arthropoda is the largest phylum of Animalia which includes insects.

Q7. Petromyzon is included under_______.
    (A) Agnatha   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Cephalochordata
    (C) Tetrapoda
    (D) Pisces
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Petromyzon is a jawless vertebrate and hence included under Agnatha.

Q8. Which phylum has a water vascular system as a characteristic feature?
    (A) Phylum Ctenophora
    (B) Phylum Porifera
    (C) Phylum Coelenterata
    (D) Phylum Echinodermata   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The most distinctive feature of Echinodermata is the presence of the water vascular system.

Q9. What is common among Liver fluke, Planarians, and Tapeworms?
    (A) All of them are segmented
    (B) All of them are found in gut
    (C) All of them have flattened bodies   <-- CORRECT
    (D) All of them have a coelom
    Answer: C
    Explanation: All of them belong to Phylum Platyhelminthes and hence have dorsoventrally flattened bodies and so, are called flatworms.

Q10. Locomotory organ of Annelida is:
    (A) Sucker
    (B) Pseudopodia
    (C) Feet
    (D) Parapodia   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Locomotory organ of annelia is parapodia. Parapodium are in form of lateral fleshy protrusions on the body surface that help in movement and capturing food.

Q11. Which among the following is called Portuguese man-of-war?
    (A) Adamsia
    (B) Gorgonia
    (C) Physalia   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Meandrina
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The Portuguese man-of-war is a siphonophore, an animal that is made up of a colony of organisms working together. Physalia is called Portuguese man-of-war. It is also called a blue bottle or floating terror it is found floating on the water surface. "The name comes from the uppermost polyp, a gas-filled bladder, or pneumatophore, which sits above the water and somewhat looks like an old warship at full sail. They are also, known as bluebottles for the purple-blue colour of their pneumatophores" (A Portuguese man of war). The tentacles can extend to 165 feet, although, the average length is 30 feet (Portuguese Man-of-War Physalia physalis).

Q12. Which phylum has bioluminescence as its well-marked feature?
    (A) Phylum Porifera
    (B) Phylum Coelenterata
    (C) Phylum Ctenophora   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Phylum Echinodermata
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The property of a living organism to emit light is known as bioluminescence and is well-marked in ctenophores.

Q13. Choose the odd one out: Roundworm, Hookworm, Filaria worm, Earthworm.
    (A) Earthworm   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Round worm
    (C) Hook worm
    (D) Filaria worm
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Earthworm belongs to phylum Annelida whereas all other worms belong to phylum Aschelminthes.

Q14. A marine cartilaginous fish that can produce electric current is:
    (A) Trygon
    (B) Torpedo   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Scoliodon
    (D) Pristis
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Torpedo is a genus of rays, commonly known as electric rays, torpedo rays, or torpedoes. They are slow-moving bottom-dwellers capable of generating electricity as a defence and feeding mechanism.

Q15. Which phylum has balance organs?
    (A) Phylum Annelida
    (B) Phylum Arthropoda   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Phylum Aschelminthes
    (D) Phylum Platyhelminthes
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Sensory organs like antennae, eyes (compound and simple), statocysts, or balance organs are present in phylum Arthropoda.

Animal Kingdom Test-03  (id 3355) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Animal Kingdom
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. The limbless amphibian is:
    (A) Rana
    (B) Hyla
    (C) Ichthyophis   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Bufo
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Ichthyophis is an amphibian which is limbless. Sometimes called as Asian caecilians. They are found in southeast Asia and the southern Philippines.

Q2. The air bladder is absent in:
    (A) Trygon   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Exocoetus
    (C) Labeo
    (D) Clarias
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The air bladder is absent in Chondrichthyes that help in floating in the water.

Q3. The phylum in which adults exhibit radial symmetry and larva exhibit bilateral symmetry is:
    (A) Phylum Arthropoda
    (B) Phylum Echinodermata   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Phylum Aschelminthes
    (D) Phylum Annelida
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The animals of Phylum - Echinodermata have an endoskeleton of calcareous ossicles and, hence, the name Echinodermata. All are marine with the organ-system level of organization. The adult echinoderms are radially symmetrical but larvae are bilaterally symmetrical.
They are triploblastic and coelomate animals. The digestive system is complete with a mouth on the lower (ventral) side and anus on the upper (dorsal) side.

Q4. Which group of chordates possesses sucking and circular mouth without jaws?
    (A) Class Osteichthyes
    (B) Class Cyclostomata   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Both (b) and (c)
    (D) Class Chondrichthyes
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The organism beloging to class Cyclostomes have a sucking and circular mouth without jaws.They are primitive vertebrates. The cyclostomes are marine or fresh-water vertebrates.

Q5. Which among the following is oviparous?
    (A) Common dolphin
    (B) Platypus   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Flying fox (Bat)
    (D) Elephant
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Platypus is the oviparous that lays eggs.

Q6. Which phylum has comb plates for locomotion as their distinctive feature?
    (A) Phylum Echinodermata
    (B) Phylum Ctenophora   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Phylum Porifera
    (D) Phylum Coelenterata
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The body of phylum Ctenophora bears eight external rows of ciliated comb plates, which help in locomotion.

Q7. A fish that has an electric organ is:
    (A) Common carp
    (B) Katla
    (C) Pomfret
    (D) Torpedo   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Torpedo fish has electric organ. They are known for being capable of producing an electric discharge ranging from 8 to 220 volts depending on species.

Q8. In which of the organism, internal fertilization is seen?
    (A) Fish
    (B) Roundworm
    (C) Liver fluke   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Earthworm
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Most of the animals are not able to fertilize their own egg by sperms but in liver fluke, self-fertilization takes place. Earthworm also possesses both male and female reproductive organs in the same individual but not able to fertilize its own egg.

Q9. The endoskeleton is fully ossified and the long bones are pneumatic in:
    (A) Class Mammalia
    (B) Class Amphibia
    (C) Class Aves   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Class Reptilia
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The endoskeleton is fully ossified (bony) and the long bones are hollow with air cavities (pneumatic) in class aves.

Q10. The presence of milk-producing glands is a unique characteristic feature of the class:
    (A) Aves
    (B) Reptilia
    (C) Mammalia   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Amphibia
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Mammalia is found in a variety of habitats - polar ice caps, deserts, mountains, forests, grasslands, and dark caves. Some of them have adapted to fly or live in water. The most unique mammalian characteristic is the presence of milk-producing glands (mammary glands) by which the young ones are nourished. They have two pairs of limbs, adapted for walking, running, climbing, burrowing, swimming, or flying.

Q11. Which among the following is monoecious?
    (A) Only leeches
    (B) Only Earthworm
    (C) Earthworm and leeches   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Only Nereis
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Earthworms and leeches are monoecious, contain both male and female reproductive organs in the same individual.

Q12. Which phylum shows this type of germinal layers shown below?
    (A) Phylum Annelia
    (B) Phylum Pltyhelminthes
    (C) Phylum Arthropoda
    (D) Phylum Coelenterata   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The germinal layer shows diploblastic. Phylum Coelenterata shows this type of germinal layers.

Q13. Which phyla does not possess a coelom?
    (A) Echinodermata
    (B) Annelida
    (C) Mollusca
    (D) Platyhelminthes   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Phylum Platyhelminthes does not possess a coelom. The coelom is the body cavity in between organs. Animals with coelom are called coelomate and those without it are called acoelomate.

Q14. Bat and whales have ________ chambered heart.
    (A) 3
    (B) 5
    (C) 4   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 2
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Bat and whales have a four-chambered heart. Upper two chambers are called the atrium and lower two chambers are called the ventricle. All mammals have a four-chambered heart.

Q15. Which one of the following does not belonging to Urochordata?
    (A) Doliolum
    (B) Salpa
    (C) Lancelet   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Ascidia
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Lancelets are classified in the phylum Chordata, subphylum Cephalochordata. lancelet, the name for small, fishlike lower chordate also called amphioxus it shows many affinities with the vertebrates. There are about 30 lancelet species, most belonging to the genus Branchiostoma (formerly Amphioxus). Lancelets are usually about 1 in. (2.5 cm) long, with transparent bodies tapered at both ends. There is no distinct head and no paired fins.

Animal Kingdom Test-04  (id 3356) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Animal Kingdom
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. What is the main excretory organ in insects?
    (A) Proboscis gland
    (B) Gills
    (C) Malphighian tubules   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Excretory pore
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The insects belong to phylum Arthropoda and hence, the excretory organ is Malphighian tubules.

Q2. Which among the following is a gregarious pest?
    (A) Apis
    (B) Locusta   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Laccifer
    (D) Bombyx
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Locust (Locusta) is a gregarious pest belonging to phylum Arthropoda.

Q3. Identify the animal given below. Mention its phylum.
    (A) Spongilla and phylum Porifera
    (B) Ascidia and phylum Chordata
    (C) Aurelia and phylum Coelenterata
    (D) Euspongia and phylum Porifera   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The animal is identified as Euspongia which belong to phylum Porifera.

Q4. The excretory organ of Saccoglossus is:
    (A) Excretory pore
    (B) Gills
    (C) Proboscis gland   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Malphighian tubules
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Saccoglossus belong to phylum Hemichordata and hence the excretory organ is proboscis gland.

Q5. A reptile has a four-chambered heart is:
    (A) Salamander
    (B) Snake
    (C) Crocodile   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Alligator
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Reptiles generally possess three-chamber heart, two upper chamber and single lower chamber. But in crocodile, the heart is four-chambered having two atrium and two ventricles.

Q6. In Molluscs, the rasping feeding organ is:
    (A) Head
    (B) Radula   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Mantle
    (D) Visceral hump
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The mouth of molluscs contains a file-like rasping organ for feeding, called a radula.

Q7. Bony fishes have sac-like outgrowth, called air bladder arising from the dorsal wall of the oesophagus. It is used to:
    (A) All of these
    (B) Maintain buoyancy for swimming Swim constantly to avoid sinking
    (C) Changing direction for swimming
    (D) Maintain balance and to swim up and down Maintain buoyancy for swimming   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Air bladder is present in body fish that help them in maintaining balance and to swim up and down. Air bladder arises from the dorsal wall of the oesophagus.

Q8. Which is the second largest phylum?
    (A) Phylum Annelida
    (B) Phylum Echinodermata
    (C) Phylum Mollusca   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Phylum Arthropoda
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Phylum Mollusca is the second largest phylum after Arthropoda.

Q9. Which of the following is not a poisonous snake?
    (A) Testudo   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Bangarus
    (C) Naja
    (D) Vipera
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Examples of poisonous snakes are Naja(Cobra), Bangarus(Krait), Vipera(Viper). Testudo is a non-poisonous snake. It is found in Europe.

Q10. Which of the following does not have an excretory system?
    (A) Catla
    (B) Asterias   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Carcharodon
    (D) Myxine
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Asterias does not have an excretory system. Asterias includes starfish or sea star. They are exclusively marine.

Q11. Identify the animal in the figure given below and the phylum to which the animal belongs to?
    (A) Gorgonia and phylum Cnidaria
    (B) Pennatula and phylum Cnidaria
    (C) Octopus and phylum Mollusca   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Ctenoplana and phylum Ctenophora
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The animal is dentified as octopus which belongs to phylum Mollusca.

Q12. Choose the odd one out based on the levels of the organization: Annelids, Arthropods, Platyhelminthes, Molluscs.
    (A) Platyhelminthes   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Molluscs
    (C) Annelids
    (D) Arthropods
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The organ level is exhibited by members of Platyhelminthes and other higher phyla where tissues are grouped together to form organs, each specialized for a particular function. In animals like Annelids, Arthropods, Molluscs, organs have associated to form functional systems, each system concerned with a specific physiological function. This pattern is called an organ system level of organization.

Q13. Ancestors of mammals belongs to:
    (A) Chelonia
    (B) Therapsida   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Ornithischia
    (D) Silusoidea
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The ancestor of mammals belongs to class Therapsida. Therapsida is a group of synapsids that includes mammals and their ancestors.

Q14. Bat is member of the order ________.
    (A) Chiroptera   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Hymenoptera
    (C) Urodela
    (D) Lagomorpha
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Bat is a member of order Chiroptera of class Mammalia. Bats are only mammals to have achieved powered to flight in which forelimb is modified as wings.

Q15. Which one of the following has the highest number of species in nature?
    (A) Birds
    (B) Insects   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Mammals
    (D) Fungi
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Insects have the highest number of species in nature. Insect belongs to arthropods family of class Mammalia. They are characterized by jointed legs.

Q1. One animal that does not perform locomotion is______.
    (A) Sycon   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Euglena
    (C) Sepia
    (D) Nereis
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Sycon does not perform locomotion, although it is an animal. Sycon remains attached to the substratum and does not move from one place to another.

Q2. The larvae of urochordates is called:
    (A) Larvalone
    (B) Ammocoete
    (C) Tadpole   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Sticky rays
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The larvae of urochordates are called tadpole. Tadpole change into adults by the process of metamorphosis. The structure of tadpole is totally different from the adult ones.

Q3. Silk produced by Antheraeamylitta is called ________.
    (A) Muga silk
    (B) Mysore silk
    (C) Eri silk
    (D) Tasar silk   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The silk produced by Antheraeamylitta is called Tasar silk. This silk is considered as the most durable and best quality silk.

Q4. Species going to extinct due to low reproductive rate is ________.
    (A) Bald eagle
    (B) Giant panda   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Island spieces
    (D) Lion
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The giant panda is going to extinct due to low reproductive rate. They live in mountain ranges in central China. There reproductively rate is very less due to climatic conditions.

Q5. Which one is correct?
 Sea Lily is an echinoderm.
 Blue-green algae are a kind of fungus.
 Maidenhair tree is an angiosperm.
 Sea horse is related to dolphins.
    (A) (D)
    (B) (C)
    (C) (B)
    (D) (A)   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Sea Lily is an echinoderm having spine all over the body. Blue-green algae is a class of bacteria. Maidenhair tree is pteridophytes and the sea horse is not related to the dolphin.

Q6. Lac is produced by lac insect as:
    (A) Excretion from the body
    (B) Faecal matter
    (C) Excess food oozing out of the body
    (D) Secretion from the body   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Lac is obtained by lac insects as secretion from the body. This secretion is wounded around the cocoon of lac insects.

Q7. The life-span of honey bee drone is:
    (A) 3-4 months
    (B) 10-12 months
    (C) 1-2 months   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 6-7 months
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The life-span is the time period from birth to death of an organism. The life-span of honey bee drone is 1-2 months only. Queen has the longest life span in all three kinds of honey bees.

Q8. Largest mammal is ________.
    (A) Dolphin
    (B) Elephant
    (C) Blue whale   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Crocodile
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The blue whale is the largest mammals about 30 meter in length and 180 tons in weight.

Q9. What is the main excretory waste in insects?
    (A) Formic acid
    (B) Uric acid   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Ammonia
    (D) Urea
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The main nitrogenous excretory wastes of insects are uric acid. Uric acid is released in concentrated form. Other animals release nitrogenous wastes in form of ammonia and urea.

Q10. Salamander belongs to the class:
    (A) Pisces
    (B) Amphibian   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Aves
    (D) Reptiles
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Salamanders are a group of amphibians typically characterized by a lizard-like appearance, with slender bodies, blunt snouts, short limbs projecting at right angles to the body, and the presence of a tail in both larvae and adults.

Q11. Which two teeth are modified into tusk in elephants?
    (A) Two upper molar
    (B) Two upper incisors   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Two lower incisors
    (D) Two lower molar
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In elephants, two upper front teeth are modified into tusk of elephants. The continuous growth of tusk is enabled by formative tissues in the apical opening of the root of the teeth.

Q12. Which molluscs is without shell?
    (A) Snail
    (B) Star fish
    (C) Octopus   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Chiton
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Octopus belongs to molluscs but does not contain the shell. All other molluscs possess hard calcareous cells around their body to act as a protective covering.

Q13. Crocodile and penguin are similar to whale and dogfish in which one of the following features?
    (A) Have gill slit at some stage of life   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Lay eggs and guard them till they hatch
    (C) Possess bony skeleton
    (D) Possess single solid CNS
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Crocodile and penguins are similar to whale and dogfish in having gill slits at some stage of their life cycle which is used as respiratory organs.

Q14. The cross-section of body of an invertebrate is given below. Identify the animal which has this body plan:
    (A) Roundworm   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Earthworm
    (C) Planaria
    (D) Cockroach
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The given diagram is cross section of roundworm, an invertebrate that possesses coelom and centrally located alimentary canal.

Q15. Which of the following is most poisonous?
    (A) Heloderma   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Chameleon
    (C) Glass snake
    (D) Horn toad
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Heloderma is the most poisonous, which is a verminous lizard native to the southwestern united states and Mexico.

Morphology Of Flowering Plants Test-01  (id 3358) [FREE]

Q1. Monstera has:
    (A) Adventitious roots   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Tertiary root
    (C) Fibrous root system
    (D) Tap root system
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In some plants, like grass, Monstera, and the banyan tree, roots arise from parts of the plant other than the radicle and are called adventitious roots.

Q2. The root is covered at the apex by a thimble-like structure called:
    (A) Region of maturation
    (B) Region of meristematic activity
    (C) Root hair
    (D) Root cap   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The root is covered at the apex by a thimble-like structure called the root cap.

Q3. The part that develops from the plumule of the embryo of a germinating seed is:
    (A) Flower
    (B) Fruit
    (C) Stem   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Leaf
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The stem develops from the plumule of the embryo of a germinating seed.

Q4. Rhizophora possess________.
    (A) Modified root
    (B) Prop roots
    (C) Stilt root
    (D) Pneumatophores   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Rhizophora possess Pneumatophores

Q5. Roots developed from parts of the plant other than radicle are called
    (A) Nodular root
    (B) Adventitious roots   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Taproot
    (D) Fibrous root
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Roots developed from parts of the plant other than radicle are called adventitious roots.

Q6. The small lateral outgrowth of the leaf base which protects the young leaf and its axillary buds in the young stage is called _______.
    (A) Bracts
    (B) Stipules   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Petiolate
    (D) Pulvinus
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The leaf base bear two lateral small leaf like structures called stipules.

Q7. Potato is a modified______.
    (A) Root
    (B) Stem   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Node
    (D) Ovary
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Potato is a modified stem as it contains nodes in the form of eyes on potato tubers which germinate to produce new potato plants if placed in suitable conditions.

Q8. The type of aestivation shown by the diagram below is
    (A) Twisted
    (B) Vexillary   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Valvate
    (D) Imbricate
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The diagram shows which is vexillary aestivation.
Vexillary aestivation is a mode of aestivation in which one large upper petal folds over, and covers, the other smaller petals, as in most papilionaceous plants.

Q9. The axillary buds of stems may also get modified into woody, straight and pointed thorns in______.
    (A) Mint
    (B) Jasmine
    (C) Opuntia
    (D) Citrus   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The axillary buds of stems may also get modified into woody, straight, and pointed thorns in Citrus and Bougainvillea. They protect plants from browsing animals.

Q10. A lateral branch with short internodes and each node bearing a rosette of leaves and a tuft of roots are found in _____.
    (A) Strawberry
    (B) Pineapple
    (C) Chrysanthemum
    (D) Pistia   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: A lateral branch with short internodes and each node bearing a rosette of leaves and a tuft of roots are found in aquatic plants such as Pistia and Eicchornia.

Q11. Which part of the plant help to hold the blade to light?
    (A) Stipule
    (B) Lamina
    (C) Petiole   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Leaf base
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The petiole help hold the blade to light. Long thin flexible petioles allow leaf blades to flutter in wind, thereby cooling the leaf and bringing fresh air to the leaf surface.

Q12. Which part of the plant store food in garlic?
    (A) Fruit
    (B) Fleshy leaves   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Stem
    (D) Root
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The fleshy leaves of onion and garlic store food.

Q13. The correct arrangement of the zones as seen in the vertical section of root is
 Root hair zone
 Zone of meristem
 Root cap zone
 Zone of maturation
 Zone of elongation
    (A) A, B, C, D, E
    (B) D, E, A, C, B
    (C) E, D, C, B, A
    (D) C, B, E, A, D   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The correct arrangement of the zones as seen in the vertical section of root is root cap zone, region of meristematic activity, region of elongation, region of maturation and root hair region.

Q14. Phylloclade are:
    (A) Green succulent stems of indefinite growth   <-- CORRECT
    (B) One internodes long stem
    (C) Leaf modifications
    (D) Modified petiole
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Phylloclade are green succulent stems of indefinite growth that perform the function of photosynthesis due to the presence of chlorophyll.

Q15. Select the insectivorous plant from the following:
    (A) Cuscuta
    (B) Monotropa
    (C) Santlum
    (D) Drosera   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Those plants that eat insect to fulfil its protein requirement are called insectivorous plants. They have modified leaves to capture insects. Drosera is an insectivorous plant.

Morphology Of Flowering Plants Test-02  (id 3359) [PAID]

Q1. 120^o phyllotaxy occurs in _________.
    (A) Octastichous
    (B) Tristichous   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Distichous
    (D) Pentstichous
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Phyllotaxy is the arrangement of leaves on a plant stem. 120^o phyllotaxy occurs in a Tristichous arrangement in which three leaves are arranged at each node.

Q2. Parallel venation is present in _________.
    (A) Monocotyledons   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Dalbergia
    (C) polycotyledons
    (D) Dicotyledons
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Parallel venation is the characteristic features of monocots. Dicots possess reticulate venation. The arrangement of veins on the leaf is called venation.

Q3. Which is not a function of leaves?
    (A) Photosynthesis
    (B) Transpiration
    (C) Gaseous exchange
    (D) Formation of new buds   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Leaves perform the function of photosynthesis, exchange of gases, and transpiration to lose excess of water. The formation of new buds is not a function of leaves.

Q4. In Ocimum sanctum (tulsi), stem is_____.
    (A) Cylindrical
    (B) Triangular
    (C) Round
    (D) Quadrangular   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The stem of Ocimum sanctum or tulsi is quadrangular in shape. The stem is covered with hairy projection.

Q5. Bladders of Utricularia and Pitchers of Nepenthes are a modification of______.
    (A) Leaves   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Roots
    (C) Stems
    (D) Flowers
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Bladders of Utricularia and Pitcher of Nepenthes are a modification of leaves. They are modified to catch insects that are insectivorous plants.

Q6. A plant in which adventitious roots develop chlorophyll and perform photosynthesis is______.
    (A) Dischidia   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Tinospora
    (C) Doxantha
    (D) Argemone
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Dischidia

Q7. Inflorescence which shows indefinite growth and bears a number of flowers due to the active growing point is called ________.
    (A) Racemose   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Corymb
    (C) Spike
    (D) Cymose
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In racemose inflorescence indefinite growth occurs and bears a number of flowers due to the active growing point.

Q8. A scar on the seed coat through which the developing seeds were attached to the fruit is called _________.
    (A) Tegmen
    (B) Micropyle
    (C) Hilum   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Testa
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The hilum is a scar on the seed coat through which the developing seeds were attached to the fruit.

Q9. Name the type of thalamus in which the ovary is at top and stamens, petals and sepals are born below.
    (A) Semi-epigyny
    (B) Epigyny
    (C) Hypogyny   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Perigyny
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In hypergamous flowers, the ovary is at the tops and stamens, petals, and sepals are borne below on the thalamus. The ovary is called superior.

Q10. The fruit develops to form a whole inflorescence is called ________.
    (A) Aggregate fruits
    (B) Composite fruits   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Complex fruit
    (D) Simple fruit
    Answer: B
    Explanation: True fruit is the fruit that develops from ovary only. In composite fruits, the whole inflorescence develops into fruits as in case of jackfruit.

Q11. The cup-like structure formed by the adnation of sepals, petals, and stamens is ______.
    (A) Hypanthodium
    (B) Cyathium
    (C) Capitulum
    (D) Hypanthium   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In angiosperms, a hypanthium is a structure where basal portions of the calyx, the corolla, and the stamens form a cup-shaped tube.

Q12. Ancestors of mammals belong to________.
    (A) Ornithischia
    (B) Therapsida   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Silusoidea
    (D) Chelonia
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The ancestor of mammals belongs to class Therapsida. Therapsida is a group of synapsids that includes mammals and their ancestors.

Q13. Bat is member of an order________.
    (A) Lagomorpha
    (B) Urodela
    (C) Chiroptera   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Hymenoptera
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Bat is a member of the order Chiroptera of class Mammalia. Bats are only mammals to have achieved powered flight in which forelimb is modified as wings.

Q14. Which one of the following has the highest number of species in nature?
    (A) Fungi
    (B) Birds
    (C) Mammals
    (D) Insects   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Insects have the highest number of species in nature. Insect belongs to arthropods family of class Mammalia. They are characterized by jointed legs.

Q15. One animal that does not perform locomotion is ______.
    (A) Sycon   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Euglena
    (C) Sepia
    (D) Nereis
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Sycon does not perform locomotion, although it is an animal. Sycon remains attached to the substratum and does not move from one place to another.

Morphology Of Flowering Plants Test-03  (id 3360) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Morphology of Flowering Plants
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. The locomotory organ of Annelida is__________.
    (A) Pseudopodia
    (B) Feet
    (C) Sucker
    (D) Parapodia   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The locomotory organ of Annelida is parapodia. Parapodium is in the form of lateral fleshy protrusions on the body surface that help in movement and capturing food.

Q2. The larvae of urochordates are called:
    (A) Sticky rays
    (B) Tadpole   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Larvalone
    (D) Ammocoete
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The larvae of urochordates are called tadpole. Tadpole change into adults by the process of metamorphosis. The structure of tadpole is totally different from the adult ones.

Q3. Silk produced by Antheraea mylitta is called:
    (A) Eri silk
    (B) Tasar silk   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Mysore silk
    (D) Muga silk
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The silk produced by Antheraeamylitta is called Tasar silk. This silk is considered as the most durable and best quality silk.

Q4. The limbless amphibian is______.
    (A) Bufo
    (B) Hyla
    (C) Rana
    (D) Ichthyophis   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Ichthyophis is an amphibian which is limbless. Sometimes called as Asian caecilians. They are found in southeast Asia and the southern Philippines.

Q5. In an inflorescence where flowers are borne laterally in an acropetal succession, the position of the youngest floral bud in the floral axis shall be
    (A) Distal   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Intercalary
    (C) Proximal
    (D) Anywhere
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In the acropetal succession of an inflorescence, the youngest floral buds are found at the distal end and the oldest flowers are found at the proximal end.

Q6. In which type of placentation, the ovary is unilocular with a single ovule?
    (A) Basal placentation   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Marginal placentation
    (C) Free central placentation
    (D) Axile placentation
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In basal placentation, the placenta develops at the base of the ovary and a single ovule is attached to it.

Q7. The Aleurone layer of Maize grain is especially rich in_________.
    (A) Protein   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Starch
    (C) Auxine
    (D) Lipid
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Aleurone layer of maize grain is rich in proteins. It is the outermost layer of the endosperm followed by the inner starchy endosperm.

Q8. Individual component of the perianth are called:
    (A) Petals
    (B) Bracts
    (C) Tepals   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Sepals
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The flowers in which sepals and petals are not differentiated are called perianth. The individual component of the perianth is called Tepals.

Q9. The condensed part of the stem which is specialized to take part in sexual reproduction of angiosperm is called ________.
    (A) Buds
    (B) Pedicel
    (C) Peduncle
    (D) Flower   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The condensed part of the stem which is specialized to take part in sexual reproduction of angiosperms is called flower. Flower produce seeds and fruits for the propagation of species.

Q10. The wall of fruit is called ________.
    (A) Pericarp   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Endocarp
    (C) Epicarp
    (D) Mesocarp
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Fruits are the mature ovary or ovaries of one or more flowers. In fleshy fruits, the outer layer (which is often edible) is the pericarp, which is the tissue that develops from the ovary wall of the flower and surrounds the seeds.

Q11. The mature seeds of plants such as gram and peas, possess no endosperm, because
    (A) Endosperm gets used up by the developing embryo during seed development.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) The plants are not angiosperms.
    (C) Endosperm is not formed in them.
    (D) Double fertilization does not take place in the plants.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The mature seeds of plants do not possess endosperm because, it gets used up by the developing embryo during seed development.

Q12. The single cotyledon of cereal grain is_______.
    (A) Coleoptile
    (B) Tegmen
    (C) Scutellum   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Coleorhiza
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In monocotyledonous seeds, the single cotyledon is called as scutellum. It is found in cereal grains like rice, wheat, maize and other monocots.

Q13. Identify the correct one with respect to the symmetry of the flower.
    (A) Pea, Chilli and Bean,
    (B) Mustard, Datura and Chilli.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Mustard, Glumohur and Bean
    (D) Chilli, Pea and Datura
    Answer: B
    Explanation: When a flower is divided into two equal radial halves in any radial plane passing through the centre, it is said to be actinomorphic e.g., mustard, datura, chilli.

Q14. The ovary belonging to a single free carpel is called ________.
    (A) Polycarpous
    (B) Syncarpous
    (C) Megacarpous
    (D) Apocarpous   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: When more than one carpel is present, they may be free, it is called apocarpous.

Q15. Parenchymatous cushion present inside the ovary, where ovules are borne is called:
    (A) Placenta   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Funicle
    (C) Suture
    (D) Pistillode
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The placenta is the parenchymatous cushion present inside the ovary, ovules are borne. Ovules are attached with an ovary at the placenta to get nourishment.

Morphology Of Flowering Plants Test-04  (id 3361) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Morphology of Flowering Plants
Questions: 14 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. The parietal placentation is seen in:
    (A) Argemone   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Pea
    (C) Marigold
    (D) China rose
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In parietal placentation, the ovules develop on the inner wall of the ovary or on the peripheral part. The ovary is one-chambered but it becomes two-chambered due to the formation of the false septum, e.g., mustard and Argemone.

Q2. The form of the thalamus in which the ovary is at top and stamens, petals, and sepals are borne below is called ________.
    (A) Epigyny
    (B) Semi-epigyny
    (C) Hypogyny   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Perigyny
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In the hypogynous flower, the gynoecium occupies the highest position while the other parts are situated below it. The ovary in such flowers is said to be superior.

Q3. Which plant shows valvate aestivation?
    (A) China rose
    (B) Calotropis   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Gulmohur
    (D) Pea
    Answer: B
    Explanation: When sepals or petals in a whorl just touch one another at the margin, without overlapping, as in Calotropis, it is said to be valvate.

Q4. When the stamens in a flower remain free, it is said to be______.
    (A) Polyadelphous
    (B) Monoadelphous
    (C) Polyandrous   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Diadelphous
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The stamens in a flower may either remain free (polyandrous) or maybe united in varying degrees.

Q5. Mango is an example of_______.
    (A) Pepo
    (B) Pome
    (C) Berry
    (D) Drupe   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Drupe is an indehiscent fruit in which an outer fleshy part and surrounds a shell of hardened endocarp with a seed. Mango is an example of a drupe.

Q6. Edible part of Coconut is:
    (A) Mesocarp and Embryo
    (B) Epicarp and Mesocarp
    (C) Endosperm and Embryo   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Mesocarp and Endospem
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The edible part of Coconut is endosperm and embryo. The water inside the coconut is a cellular embryo and white kernel surrounding it is the main edible part that is the endosperm.

Q7. A seed is made up of
    (A) Only seed coat
    (B) Only embryo
    (C) Only cotyledons
    (D) A seed coat and an embryo   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: A seed is made up of a seed coat and an embryo.

Q8. If the margin of thalamus grows upward enclosing the ovary completely and getting fused with it, the other parts of flower arise above the ovary, the flower is said to be:
    (A) Hypergynous
    (B) Perigynous
    (C) Epigynous   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Hypogynous
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In epigynous flowers, the margin of the thalamus grows upward enclosing the ovary completely and getting fused with it, the other parts of the flower arise above the ovary.

Q9. The diagram below shows
    (A) Both are perigynous.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Hypogynous and Epigynous
    (C) Perigynous and Hypogynous
    (D) Epigynous and Hypogynous
    Answer: A
    Explanation: If gynoecium is situated in the centre and otherparts of the flower are located on the rim of the thalamus almost at thesame level, it is called perigynous. The ovary here is said to be half inferior.

Q10. When the ovules develop on the inner wall of the ovary, the placentation is______.
    (A) Apical
    (B) Axile
    (C) Marginal
    (D) Parietal   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In parietal placentation, the ovules develop on the inner wall of the ovary or on the peripheral part.

Q11. The aestivation seen in Solanaceae is_____.
    (A) Axile
    (B) Fabaceae
    (C) Basal
    (D) Valvate   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Valvate aestivation is seen in the family Solanaceae.

Q12. Dry indehiscent single-seeded fruit formed by bicarpellarysyncarpous inferior ovary is in the diagram given below, the parts A and B are respectively,
    (A) Hilum and Micropyle   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Plumule and Radicle
    (C) Radicle and Plumule
    (D) Micropyle and Hilum
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The part is identified as Hilum and Micropyle.

Q13. Which one is a monocarpic in nature?
    (A) Radish
    (B) Castor
    (C) Bamboo   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Cotton
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Monocarpic plants are those that flower, set seeds, and then die. Bamboo is monocarpic in nature that flowers once in a lifetime.

Q14. Which one of the following is a true nut?
    (A) Groundnut
    (B) Cashewnut
    (C) Coconut
    (D) Hazelnut   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: A true nut is a fruit composed of a hard shell and an edible seed. The shell does not open to release the seed (indehiscent), e.g., hazelnut, chestnuts.
Walnuts, almonds and pecans are drupes. The fruit of the coconut is a large, dry drupe. Cashew nuts are not true nuts. In the cashew nut, the ovary develops outside of the fruit (false fruit). The groundnut or peanut is not a true nut, but rather a legume. In groundnut, edible the cotyledons remain below ground and act as a storage organ.

Q1. Largest bud is found in______.
    (A) Sunflower
    (B) Wolffia
    (C) Cauliflower
    (D) Cabbage   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Cabbage is the bud of the cabbage plant. Cabbage bud is considered as largest bud present in angiosperms plants. A successive layer of leaves covers the buds to form the round structure on condensed stem.

Q2. The white, translucent, fleshy, and edible structure present between seed and pericarp is _____.
    (A) Aril   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Integument
    (C) Exocarp
    (D) Cupule
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The white translucent, fleshy and edible structure present between seed and pericarp is called an aril. It is found in a mace of the nutmeg seed.

Q3. Study of seed is called as______.
    (A) Fruit logy
    (B) Spermology   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Apology
    (D) Horticulture
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The study of seed is called Spermology. Study of seed includes shape, size, colour and viability.

Q4. The edible part of the apple is:
    (A) Endosperm and pericarp
    (B) Fleshy thalamus   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Pericarp and placenta
    (D) Fleshy ovary
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The edible part of the apple is fleshy thalamus. Apple is an example of false fruit as it contains thalamus along with ovary.

Q5. A chambered fruit formed from an inferior ovary and having succulent testa is_______.
    (A) Pomegranate   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Orange
    (C) Cucumber
    (D) Guava
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Pomegranate is the fruit which is formed from inferior ovary having succulent testa. Chambered compartment bears many seeds generally red in colour when ripened.

Q6. When the several pistils of the same flower are separate and the ovary belongs to a single free carpel, it is called _________.
    (A) Polycarpous
    (B) Megacarpous
    (C) Apocarpous   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Syncarpous
    Answer: C
    Explanation: When the several pistils of the same flower are separate and the ovary belongs to a single free carpel, it is called apocarpous.

Q7. When the several pistils of the same flower are separate and the ovary belongs to a single free carpel, it is called _________.
    (A) Syncarpous
    (B) Polycarpous
    (C) Megacarpous
    (D) Apocarpous   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: When the several pistils of the same flower are separate and the ovary belongs to a single free carpel, it is called apocarpous.

Q8. Sweet potato and potato are an example of:
    (A) Homologous structure
    (B) Oval structure
    (C) Vestigial structure
    (D) Analogous structure   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Sweet potato and potato are an example of analogous organs as they perform the same function that is storing food. But potato is a modified stem but sweet potato is modified root.

Q9. Many pulses of daily use belong to one of the families below (tick the correct answer)
    (A) Solanaceae
    (B) Fabaceae   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Liliaceae
    (D) Malvaceae
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Fabaceae are the sources of pulses such as gram, arhar, sem, moong, soybean.

Q10. The floral formula P_3+3 A_3+3 G_[3] belongs to
    (A) Fabaceae
    (B) Liliaceae   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Malvaceae
    (D) Solanaceae
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In Liliaceae, the flower is bisexual and actinomorphic. There are 6 (3+3) tepals and 6 (3+3) stamens with a superior ovary and trilocular with many ovules.

Q11. The dye plant belonging to family Fabaceae is______.
    (A) Indigofera   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Lupin
    (C) Sesbania
    (D) Trifolium
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Indigofera is a dye belonging to family Fabaceae.

Q12. Pentamerous, actinomorphic flower, bicarpellary ovary with oblique septum and berry or capsule fruit belong to the family______.
    (A) Asteraceae
    (B) Brassicaceae
    (C) Liliaceae
    (D) Solanaceae   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The members of family Solanaceae bears flower which is pentamerous, actinomorphic, bicarpellary, ovary with oblique septum and berry, or capsule fruit. It includes potato, brinjal, etc.

Q13. Hypanthodium is found in the genus is ________.
    (A) Cannabis
    (B) Ficus   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Euphorbia
    (D) Solanum
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Hypanthodium is a special type of inflorescence in which receptacle is fleshy and forms a hollow ball-like structure with an apical opening. This kind of inflorescence is found in genus ficus.

Q14. A plant having male, female and inter-sexual flowers is called ________.
    (A) Polyandrous
    (B) Polyploidy
    (C) Bisexual
    (D) Polygamous   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: A plant having male, female and inter-sexual flowers is called polygamous flower. The same plant bears all three kinds of flowers.

Q15. A flower which can be divided into two equal vertical halves by only one plane is called ________.
    (A) Zygomorphic   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Zoomorphic
    (C) Trimorphic
    (D) Actinomorphic
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The symmetry in which a flower can be divided into two equal vertical halves by only one plane is called zygomorphic flower as in pea.

Q1. What is samara?
    (A) Fruits having wings formed from other structure   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Fruits having many seeds
    (C) Fruit without seed
    (D) Fruit having single seed
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Samara is a winged achene, a type of fruit which a flattened wing of fibrous, papery tissue develops from the ovary wall.

Q2. Unipinnate compound leaves are present in:
    (A) Marigold
    (B) Moringa
    (C) Neem   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Palm
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A pinnately compound leaves are one which the midrib bears laterally a number of leaflets. Unipinnate compound leaves are present in neem plant.

Q3. Placentation in a syncarpous, unilocular ovary bearing two or more placentae longitudinally along the wall is called ________.
    (A) Parietal   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Axile
    (C) Apical
    (D) Marginal
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Placentation in a syncarpous, unilocular ovary bearing two or more placentae longitudinally along the wall is called parietal placentation.

Q4. Dry indehiscent single-seeded fruit formed by the bi-carpellary syncarpous inferior ovary is______.
    (A) Berry
    (B) Cypsela   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Cremocarp
    (D) Caryopsis
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Cypsela is a single-seeded dry indehiscent fruit that develops one form part of the inferior ovary which is bicarpellary and syncarpous.

Q5. The science that deals with the study of form, size, colour, structure, and relative position of various parts of an organism is called _________.
    (A) Histology
    (B) Cytology
    (C) Anatomy
    (D) Morphology   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Morphology is the branch of science in which we study about form, size, colour, structure and relative position of various parts of organisms.

Q6. Name the smallest angiosperm.
    (A) Wolffia   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Henbane
    (C) Arceuthobium
    (D) Lemna
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The smallest angiosperm plant is Wolffia. It is an aquatic plant, free-floating, green or yellow-green and without roots.

Q7. The small lateral outgrowth of the leaf base which protects the young leaf and its axillary buds in the young stage is called ________.
    (A) Petiolate
    (B) Stipules   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Bracts
    (D) Pulvinus
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Stipules are the small lateral outgrowth of the leaf base which protect the young leaf and its axillary buds in the young stage. It is a green leafy structure.

Q8. Which one is a marine angiosperm?
    (A) Monstera
    (B) Chara
    (C) Zostera   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Funaria
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Zostera is a marine angiosperms plant. The plants have broad leaves that help them in floating on the water surface, the root is poorly developed.

Q9. Among pea tendril, lemon thorn, and Opuntia spines, which one are homologous structures?
    (A) Opuntia and lemon thorn
    (B) Pea tendrils and Opuntia spines   <-- CORRECT
    (C) All of these
    (D) Pea tendrils and lemon thorn
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Homologous structures are those structures in which they have common origin and structure but perform different functions. Pea tendrils and Opuntia spines are homologous structures.

Q10. The main plant body of banana is:
    (A) Root
    (B) Leaflets
    (C) Aggregation of leaf base   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Stem
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The main plant body of banana is an aggregation of leaf base. The stem is highly reduced and rudimentary present at the base of the plant body.

Q11. Phylloclade are:
    (A) Green succulent stems of indefinite growth   <-- CORRECT
    (B) One internodes long stem
    (C) Modified petiole
    (D) Leaf modifications
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Phylloclade are green succulent stems of indefinite growth that perform the function of photosynthesis due to the presence of chlorophyll.

Q12. Which is not a function of leaves?
    (A) Photosynthesis
    (B) Gaseous exchange
    (C) Formation of new buds   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Transpiration
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Leaves perform the function of photosynthesis, exchange of gases, and transpiration to lose excess of water. The formation of new buds is not a function of leaves.

Q13. Silk produced by Antheraea mylitta is called:
    (A) Muga silk
    (B) Mysore silk
    (C) Eri silk
    (D) Tasar silk   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The silk produced by Antheraeamylitta is called Tasar silk. This silk is considered as the most durable and best quality silk.

Q14. Which plant shows valvate aestivation?
    (A) China rose
    (B) Pea
    (C) Gulmohur
    (D) Calotropis   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: When sepals or petals in a whorl just touch one another at the margin, without overlapping, as in Calotropis, it is said to be valvate.

Q15. A plant having male, female and inter-sexual flowers is called ________.
    (A) Bisexual
    (B) Polyploidy
    (C) Polygamous   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Polyandrous
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A plant having male, female and inter-sexual flowers is called polygamous flower. The same plant bears all three kinds of flowers.
