========================================================================
Anatomy Of Flowering Plants Test-01  (id 3364) [FREE]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Anatomy of Flowering Plants
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. The tissue present in all organs of plant is________.
    (A) Parenchyma   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Collenchyma
    (C) Chlorenchyma
    (D) Sclerenchyma
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Generally, all the organs of a plant are made up of parenchyma cells.

Q2. Which meristem contributes to the formation of the primary plant body?
    (A) Both lateral and apical meristem
    (B) Lateral meristem
    (C) Both apical and intercalary meristem   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Apical meristem
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Both apical meristems and intercalary meristems are primary meristems because they appear early in the life of a plant and contribute to the formation of the primary plant body.

Q3. Sclereids belongs to_______.
    (A) Collenchyma
    (B) Sclerenchyma   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Parenchyma
    (D) Fibres
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Sclereids belongs to sclerenchyma complex permanent tissue present in hard parts of plants. They are generally hard and founds in rough fruits and stem.

Q4. The parenchymatous cells which lie between the xylem and the phloem are called ________.
    (A) Conjunctive tissue   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Casparian strip
    (C) Endodermis
    (D) Pericycle
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Conjunctive tissue is a narrow strip of tissue (parenchyma or sclerenchyma) that lies between xylem and phloem bundles of the root.

Q5. A specialized parenchymatous cell, which is closely associated with sieve tube elements are:
    (A) Companion cells   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Phloem parenchyma
    (C) Xylem parenchyma
    (D) Phloem fibres
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The companion cells are specialised parenchymatous cells, which are closely associated with sieve tube elements. The sieve tube elements and companion cells are connected by pit fields present between their common longitudinal walls.

Q6. The meristems which occur at the tips of roots and shoots and produce primary tissues are called _________.
    (A) Apical meristem   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Intercalary meristem
    (C) Primary meristem
    (D) Lateral meristem
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Apical meristem is found at the apices, or tips of the plant, both the tip of the shoot and the root, and is a region of actively dividing cells. The definition is easy to remember when you break it down. An apex is a tip, the very end, of something.

Q7. A group of cells having a common origin and usually performing a common function is:
    (A) Tissues   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Cambium
    (C) Meristems
    (D) Protoderm
    Answer: A
    Explanation: A tissue is an ensemble of similar cells from the same origin that together carry out a specific function. Organs are then formed by the functional grouping together of multiple tissues.

Q8. Conjoint type of vascular bundles are common in:
    (A) Stems and leaves   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Leaves and roots
    (C) Stems, roots and leaves
    (D) Stems and roots
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In the conjoint type of vascular bundles, the xylem and phloem are situated at the same radius of vascular bundles. Such vascular bundles are common in stems and leaves. The conjoint vascular bundles usually have the phloem located only on the outer side of the xylem.

Q9. Which one is not a xylem cell?
    (A) Tracheids
    (B) Companion cells   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Xylem parenchyma
    (D) Vessels
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Xylem is a complex tissue, which consists of four kinds of cells. These cells are tracheid, vessels, xylem parenchyma and xylem fibres. Companion cell is part of phloem tissue.

Q10. Which is not the function of parenchymatous cells?
    (A) Secretion
    (B) Photosynthesis
    (C) Storage
    (D) Mechanical support   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The parenchyma performs various functions like photosynthesis, storage, secretion.

Q11. Which among the following are elongated or tube-like cells with thick and lignified walls and tapering ends?
    (A) Xylem fibres
    (B) Vessels
    (C) Xylem parenchyma
    (D) Tracheids   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Tracheids are elongated cells in the xylem of vascular plants that serve in the transport of water and mineral salts. Tracheids are one of two types of tracheary elements, vessel elements being the other.

Q12. The characteristic feature of which cells have lignified thickening at the corner?
    (A) Parenchyma
    (B) Sclerenchyma   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Chlorenchyma
    (D) Collechyma
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Sclerenchyma consists of long, narrow cells with thick and lignified cell walls having a few or numerous pits.

Q13. In monocotyledons, guard cell of stomata are The figure given below is the apical meristem in the root. Identify ‘A’ in the diagram.
    (A) Axillary bud
    (B) Procambium
    (C) Protoderm   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Cortex
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The part ‘A’ is protoderm in apical meristem of root.

Q14. Which is the function of companion cells?
    (A) Radial conduction of water.
    (B) To store food materials like resins, latex etc.
    (C) Controlling the functions of sieve tubes.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) To maintain the pressure gradient in the sieve tubes.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Controlling the functions of sieve tubes.

Q15. Tracheids differ from vessels in having:
    (A) Rounded structure
    (B) Pits in walls
    (C) Pointed tips   <-- CORRECT
    (D) All of these
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Tracheids and vessels are the main water and mineral conducting tissues of xylem. Tracheid has pointed tips but vessels have blunt ends.

Anatomy Of Flowering Plants Test-02  (id 3365) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Anatomy of Flowering Plants
Questions: 14 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. Epidermal appendages, unicellular or multicellular outgrowth strictly epidermal in origin is_________.
    (A) Prickles
    (B) Root hairs
    (C) Trichomes   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Scales
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Trichomes are epidermal appendages, unicellular or multicellular outgrowth strictly epidermal in origin present on the stem of plants.

Q2. In angiosperms, vascular tissue develops from:
    (A) Dematogen
    (B) Phelogen
    (C) Periblem
    (D) Plerome   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In angiosperms, vascular tissue develops from plerome. Plerome forms the central core of the primary meristem of a plant or plant part.

Q3. Which epidermis of the leaf contains more stomata?
    (A) Both adaxial and abaxial contain same
    (B) Lateral
    (C) Adaxial
    (D) Abaxial   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Stomata is present more on the lower surface of the leaf. The lower surface of the leaf is called abaxial part of the leaf that is away from direct sunlight to prevent an excess of water loss.

Q4. Jute fibres deteriorate because they have _______.
    (A) Low lignin
    (B) High cellulose
    (C) Low cellulose
    (D) High lignin   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Jute fibres are made of a high amount of lignin that deteriorates in the presence of high moisture and water.

Q5. In monocotyledons, guard cell of stomata are:
    (A) Bi-concave shaped
    (B) Biconvex shaped
    (C) Dumb-bell shaped   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Bean-shaped
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In monocotyledons, the guard cell of stomata is dumb-bell shaped, thicker on top and bottom and thinner in the middle.

Q6. Which one functions as a Biological check post?
    (A) Cuticle
    (B) Pericycle
    (C) Epidermis
    (D) Endodermis   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Endodermis forms the outermost layer of vascular bundles. Anything entering inside the plant body must cross the endodermis to be transported via xylem and phloem. So, endodermis is called a biological check post of the cell.

Q7. Which part of epidermis of the leaf contains fewer stomata?
    (A) Both adaxial and abaxial contain same
    (B) Lateral
    (C) Adaxial   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Abaxial
    Answer: C
    Explanation: There are a number of differences between abaxial and adaxial stomata. First, stomatal density is usually higher on the abaxial surface than it is on the adaxial surface of leaves.

Q8. The Casparian thickening occurs in the cells of:
    (A) Pericycle of root
    (B) Endodermis of root   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Endodermis of stem
    (D) Pericycle of stem
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The tangential, as well as radial walls of the endodermal cells, have a deposition of water-impermeable, waxy material-suberin-in the form of Casparian strips.

Q9. The vascular bundles are closed when they:
    (A) Have cambium
    (B) Lack pericycle
    (C) Lack cambium   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Have pericycle
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In the monocotyledons, the vascular bundles have no cambium present in them. Hence, since they do not form secondary tissues they are referred to as closed.

Q10. In leaves, the ground tissue consists of thin-walled chloroplast containing cells are called _________.
    (A) Parenchyma
    (B) Chlorenchyma
    (C) Mesophyll   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Sclerenchyma
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The tissues of a leaf that are located in between the layers of the epidermis and carry on photosynthesis, consisting of the palisade layer and the spongy parenchyma. Most mesophyll cells contain chloroplasts.

Q11. Which of the following do not undergo any secondary growth?
    (A) Dicotyledonous root
    (B) Dicotyledonous stem
    (C) Monocotyledonous stem
    (D) Monocotyledonous root   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Secondary growth in monocotyledonous roots is not observed as cambium is absent between xylem and phloem in a vascular bundle.

Q12. The shape of guard cells in grasses is:
    (A) Dumb-bell   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Elliptical
    (C) Round
    (D) Kidney
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Dumb-bell-shaped guard cells are found in grasses. Dumb-bell shaped guard cells are more advanced in evolutionary terms and more efﬁcient physiologically because guard cells of grasses require fewer solutes and less water to achieve a given unit increase in the aperture​.

Q13. Monocotyledonous leaves are_________.
    (A) Dorsiventral
    (B) Round
    (C) Pinnate
    (D) Isobilateral   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Monocotyledonous leaves are isobilateral as both the lower and upper sides of the leaves are the same.

Q14. The main seat of photosynthesis in the leaf is:
    (A) Abaxial epidermis
    (B) Spongy parenchyma
    (C) Cuticle
    (D) Palisade parenchyma   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The palisade parenchymatous cell in the mesophyll region has numerous chloroplasts. Hence, it is the main seat of photosynthesis in leaf.

Anatomy Of Flowering Plants Test-03  (id 3366) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Anatomy of Flowering Plants
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. Reticulate venation is characteristic in:
    (A) Dicotyledonous leaves   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Dorsiventral leaves
    (C) Monocotyledonous leaves
    (D) Isobilateral leaves
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Reticulate venation: In this type, the veins branch and unite forming a complicated network, All the veins are interconnected, like the strands of the net. Leaves of ‘Dicot plants’ generally have reticulate venation e.g., Hibiscus, Redgram.

Q2. Select the correct statement.
 Monocot roots do not undergo secondary growth.
 The hypodermis is a sclerenchymatous cell in dicot stems.
 Monocot roots undergo secondary growth.
 The hypodermis is collenchymatous cell in monocot stems.
    (A) (C)
    (B) (B)
    (C) (D)
    (D) (A)   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The roots of extant vascular cryptogams and most monocotyledons do not show any secondary growth; they remain entirely primary throughout their life.

Q3. Bulliform or motor cells are present in
    (A) Dorsiventral leaves of monocot
    (B) Isobilateral leaves of monocot   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Dorsiventral leaves of dicot
    (D) Unifacial leaves of monocot
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Bulliform cells or motor cells are large, bubble-shaped epidermal cells that occur in groups on the upper surface of the leaves of many monocots on the upper surface of the leaf.

Q4. In arborescent monocots stem, a secondary cambium grows in the following type of vascular bundle is seen in
    (A) Monocot stem
    (B) Monocot root   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Dicot root
    (D) Dicot stem
    Answer: B
    Explanation: It is the anatomy of monocotyledonous root.

Q5. Anatomy of stem differs from the root in:
    (A) Cutinized epidermal wall, conjoint vascular bundle, and narrow cortex   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Stem hairs, absence of chloroplast an broad cortex
    (C) Secondary vascular growth and presence of stomata
    (D) Xylem exarch, vascular bundle radial and narrow cortex
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The stem shows the epidermis covered with a thin layer of cuticle, narrow cuticle, and each vascular bundle is conjoint, open, and is endarch protoxylem.

Q6. The stem of grasses and related plants elongate by the activity of:
    (A) Lateral meristem
    (B) Both apical and intercalary meristem   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Apical meristem
    (D) Both lateral and apical meristem
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Grasses belong to monocotyledonous angiosperms in which secondary growth does not occur. Plants elongate by the activity of both apical and intercalary meristem.

Q7. Separate xylem and phloem bundles are known as_______.
    (A) Bicollateral
    (B) Radial   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Amphivessal
    (D) Collateral
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Separate xylem and phloem bundles are found in dicotyledonous roots. This kind of vascular bundle is called the radial vascular bundle.

Q8. The quiescent centre is found in the plant at:
    (A) Cambium
    (B) Shoot tips
    (C) Leaf tip
    (D) Root tips   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: A quiescent centre is a small group of cells with low mitotic activity. It is found at the tips of growing roots in the root meristem.

Q9. Ground tissue consists of:
    (A) All tissues except epidermis and vascular tissue   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Epidermis and cortex
    (C) All tissues internal to endodermis
    (D) All tissues external to endodermis
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The ground tissue of plants includes all tissues that are neither dermal nor vascular. It can be divided into three classes based on the nature of the cell walls.

Q10. Lacunate collenchyma occurs in stem of______.
    (A) Cucurbita   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Sunflower
    (C) Leucas
    (D) Sambucus
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Lacunate collenchyma is very much alike to angular collenchyma but the cells are regularly arranged. Thickening occurs at the inner and outer tangential wall. It is found in Cucurbita stem.

Q11. In Barley stem, vascular bundles are:
    (A) Closed and scattered   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Open and scattered
    (C) Open and in a ring
    (D) Closed and radial
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The vascular bundles in Hordeum vulgare (barley) plant are scattered in ground tissues, many in number, and vary in size-smaller towards the periphery and bigger towards the centre of the ground tissue, oval or rounded in outline, conjoint, collateral, and closed.

Q12. Guard cells of stomata are thicker:
    (A) In middle
    (B) Outer side
    (C) Both side
    (D) Inner side   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The cells surrounding the stomata are called guard cells. The guard cells of the inner side are thicker and that of outer side is comparatively thinner.

Q13. The function of the guard cell in stomata is to:
    (A) Maintain turgidity
    (B) Transpiration
    (C) Open and close stomatal pore   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Exchange of gases
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Opening and closing of stomatal pore of stomata is the function of guard cells. Change in osmotic potential cause the opening and closing of stomata.

Q14. Upper surface of leaf is:
    (A) Adaxial epidermis   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Palisade parenchyma
    (C) Mesophyll cell
    (D) Abaxial epidermis
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Epidermal cells are present on both sides of the leaves. The lower side contains more stomata. The upper surface of the leaf is called the adaxial epidermis.

Q15. Tyloses are balloon-like ingrowths in vessels developing from:
    (A) Fibres through the general surface of the vessel wall
    (B) Parenchyma through the pits of vessels wall   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Fibre through pits on vessels wall
    (D) Parenchyma through the general surface of the vessel wall
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Tyloses are balloon-like ingrowths in vessels developing from parenchyma cells through the pits of the vessel wall of the xylem of secondary heartwood.

Anatomy Of Flowering Plants Test-04  (id 3367) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Anatomy of Flowering Plants
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. Vascular bundles in which cambium is present between xylem and phloem is called as:
    (A) Amphivesal
    (B) Open   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Collateral
    (D) Closed
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Vascular bundles in which cambium is present between xylem and phloem are called open vascular bundles and those in which cambium is absent are called closed vascular bundles.

Q2. In angiosperms, the main water and mineral transporting elements are:
    (A) Tracheids and Vessels   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Xylem parenchyma
    (C) Xylem fibres
    (D) Primary xylem
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Tracheids and Vessels

Q3. Exarch xylem is present in______.
    (A) Both stem and roots
    (B) Roots   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Stem
    (D) Leaves
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The xylem in which protoxylem is outside and metaxylem is inside is called exarch xylem. This kind of xylem is found in the roots of dicots.

Q4. In arborescent monocots stem, a secondary cambium grows in:
    (A) Epidermal region
    (B) Hypodermal region   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Vascular region
    (D) Cuticular region
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In arborescent monocots stem, secondary cambium grows in the hypodermal region for secondary growth that increases the girth of the stem.

Q5. Which type of vascular bundle is shown in the figure below
    (A) Concentric
    (B) Amphicribal
    (C) Open
    (D) Closed   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The vascular bundle shown below is closed and conjoint as cambium is absent between xylem and phloem tissue.

Q6. In dicot stems, the cells of cambium present between the primary xylem and primary phloem are:
    (A) Vascular cambium
    (B) Medullary cells
    (C) Intrafascicular cambium   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Interfascicular cambium
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Intrafascicular Cambium is primary meristem. It develops from the procambium of the stem apex. It is located inside the open vascular bundles, between phloem and xylem patches.

Q7. The secondary growth of woody angiosperm stem occurs by:
    (A) Cork cambium and lateral meristem
    (B) Vascular cambium and apical meristem
    (C) Vascular cambium and cork cambium   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Cork cambium and apical meristem
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The tissues involved in secondary growth are the two lateral meristems namely, vascular cambium and cork cambium.

Q8. The wood is actually a:
    (A) Secondary xylem   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Primary xylem
    (C) Secondary phloem
    (D) Primary phloem
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Wood is a secondary xylem. It is secondary growth by cambium and constitutes the bulk of the plant body in dicot stems and dicot roots.

Q9. Interfascicular cambium arise from the cells of:
    (A) Protoxylem
    (B) Phellogen
    (C) Epidermal cells
    (D) Medullary rays   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: During secondary growth, cells of medullary rays, in a line with intrafascicular cambium, become meristematic and form interfascicular cambium.
Therefore, the intrafascicular and interfascicular cambia form a ring which separates the primary xylem and primary phloem and is known as cambium ring.

Q10. The region consisting of dead elements with highly lignified walls is called ________.
    (A) Heartwood   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Autumn wood
    (C) Sapwood
    (D) Springwood
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In old trees, the greater part of secondary xylem is dark brown due to deposition of organic compounds like tannins, resins, oils, gums, aromatic substances and essential oils in the central or innermost layers of the stem. These substances make it hard, durable and resistant to the attacks of microorganisms and insects. This region comprises dead elements with highly lignified walls and is called heartwood.

Q11. Cork cambium is also known as______.
    (A) Phelloderm
    (B) Complementary cells
    (C) Accessory cells
    (D) Phellogen   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: As the stem continues to increase in girth due to the activity of vascular cambium, the outer cortical and epidermis layers get broken and need to be replaced to provide new protective cell layers. Hence, another meristematic tissue called cork cambium or phellogen develops in the cortex region.

Q12. The cells of cambial ring cut off towards pith and mature into:
    (A) Primary xylem
    (B) Secondary xylem   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Secondary phloem
    (D) Secondary medullary rays
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The cambial ring becomes active and begins to cut off new cells, both towards the inner and the outer sides. The cells cut off towards pith, mature into secondary xylem.

Q13. The phelloderm is also called _______.
    (A) Cork cambium
    (B) Cork
    (C) Periderm
    (D) Secondary cortex   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The outer cells differentiate into cork or phellem while the inner cells differentiate into secondary cortex or phelloderm.

Q14. Aerating pores in the bark of plants is known as _______.
    (A) Lenticels   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Air pore
    (C) Respiration pores
    (D) Stomata
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Lenticels permit the exchange of gases between the outer atmosphere and the internal tissue of the stem. These occur in most woody trees.

Q15. Sclereids belongs to_______.
    (A) Fibres
    (B) Collenchyma
    (C) Parenchyma
    (D) Sclerenchyma   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Sclereids belongs to sclerenchyma complex permanent tissue present in hard parts of plants. They are generally hard and founds in rough fruits and stem.

# Structural Organisation in Animals  (6 tests)

Structural Organisation In Animals Test-01   (id 3368) [FREE]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Structural Organisation in Animals
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. Where is ciliated epithelium found in the human body?
    (A) Fallopian tubes   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Oesophagus
    (C) Stomach
    (D) Intestines
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The ciliated epithelium is mainly present in the inner surface of hollow organs like bronchioles and fallopian tubes.

Q2. The epithelium found in the lining of the stomach and intestine is ________.
    (A) Squamous epithelium
    (B) Columnar epithelium   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Ciliated columnar epithelium
    (D) Cuboidal epithelium
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The columnar epithelium is found in the lining of the stomach and intestine and help in secretion and absorption. It also provides a barrier against harmful microorganisms.

Q3. The epithelium involved in diffusion is:
    (A) Cuboidal epithelium
    (B) Columnar epithelium
    (C) Squamous epithelium   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Ciliated columnar epithelium
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The squamous epithelium is made of a single thin layer of flattened cells with irregular boundaries. They are found in the walls of blood vessels and air sacs of the lungs and are involved in functions like forming a diffusion boundary.

Q4. Collagen is:
    (A) Lipid
    (B) Carbohydrate
    (C) Fibres of structural proteins   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Globular protein
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In all connective tissues except blood, the cells secrete fibres of structural proteins called collagen or elastin.

Q5. Fibres and fibroblasts are compactly packed in:
    (A) Areolar tissues
    (B) Dense irregular connective tissues   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Dense regular connective tissues
    (D) Loose connective tissues
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Dense irregular connective tissue provides strength to body parts. Hence the cells and fibres are packed compactly.

Q6. Tendons connect:
    (A) Ligaments to muscles
    (B) Bones to bones
    (C) Ligaments to bones
    (D) Muscles to bones   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Tendons are dense connective tissue which provides strength and attach muscles to bones.

Q7. Which one of the following is not a connective tissue?
    (A) Bone
    (B) Nerve.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Blood
    (D) Lymph
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Blood, bone, lymph forms the connective tissue that connects the different parts of the body
Nerve cells are parts of neural system or nervous system that transmit information from one part of the body to others.

Q8. The epithelium found in proximal convoluted tubule (PCT) of the nephron in the kidney is_______.
    (A) Cuboidal epithelium   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Columnar epithelium
    (C) Ciliated epithelium
    (D) Squamous epithelium
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The cuboidal epithelium is composed of a single layer of cube-like cells found in ducts of glands and tubular parts of nephrons in kidneys and its main functions are secretion and absorption.

Q9. What makes up more than one-half the volume of neural tissue in our body?
    (A) Plasma membrane
    (B) Neuroglia   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Neuron
    (D) Adjacent neurons
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The neuroglial cells which constitute the rest of the neural system protect and support neurons. Neuroglia makes up more than one-half the volume of neural tissue in our body.

Q10. Intercalated discs occur in:
    (A) In striped muscles
    (B) At the junction of muscle and nerve cells
    (C) Between cardiac muscle fibres   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Between neurons
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In between cardiac muscle fibres, there are communication junctions which are made up of intercalated discs.

Q11. Fibroblasts, macrophages, and mast cells are present in ______.
    (A) Areolar tissue   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Adipose tissue
    (C) Cartilage tissue
    (D) Glandular tissue
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Apart from being connective tissue, Areolar tissue is also protective in nature. It has a large number of fibroblast cells that produce fibres. Mast cells, plasma cells, and macrophages help to protect against pathogens and aid in tissue repair.

Q12. The fibre that can't be made to contract merely by thinking about it, is the:
    (A) Cardiac muscle tissue
    (B) Neural tissue
    (C) Smooth muscle fibres   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Skeletal muscle fibres
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Smooth muscles are ‘involuntary’ muscles as they can't be directly controlled. We usually are not able to make it contract merely by thinking about it as we can do with skeletal muscles. Involuntary muscles are under the control of medulla oblongata and part of the cerebrum. Smooth muscles are spindle-shaped or fusiform, uninucleated, and unstriated fibres. The wall of internal organs such as the blood vessels, stomach, and intestine contains this type of muscle tissue.

Q13. Identify the figure given below:
    (A) Salivary gland.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Compound epithelium
    (C) Goblet cells of alimentary canal
    (D) Ciliated epithelium
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The figure is identified as salivary gland. It is multicellular and is lined with glandular epithelium cells. These types of cells are specialized in production and release of particular kind of digestive juices or sweat or oil. Salivary gland secretes alkaline fluid called saliva.

Q14. To which one of the following categories does adipose tissue belong?
    (A) Muscular
    (B) Connective   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Neural
    (D) Epithelial
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Adipose tissue is a type of connective tissue consisting mainly of adipose cells or adipocytes, specialized to synthesize and contain large globules of fat.

Q15. The junctions which help to stop substances from leaking across a tissue is:
    (A) Tight junctions   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Gap junctions
    (C) Adhering junctions
    (D) Specialized junctions
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Tight junctions hold cells together. They are narrow belts that circle around the upper part of lateral surfaces of the adjacent epithelial cells to create a fusion point. They stop substances from leaking across a tissue as they prevent the passage of molecules and ions through space between adjacent cells.

Structural Organisation In Animals Test-02  (id 3369) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Structural Organisation in Animals
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. The most abundant type of animal tissue in the complex animals is:
    (A) Epithelial tissue
    (B) Nervous tissue
    (C) Connective tissue   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Muscle tissue
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The most abundant type of animal tissue connective tissue as it forms a variety of tissues such as blood, bone, cartilage, adipose, lymph, tendon, and ligament. These connective tissue types perform a wide range of functions in the animal body such as giving support, packing, repairing, storing of fat, connecting different organs, etc.

Q2. The formation of erythrocytes in foetus takes place in:
    (A) Liver and Spleen   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Sarcoplasm
    (C) Blood plasma
    (D) Red bone marrow
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In the early fetus, erythropoiesis takes place in the mesodermal cells of the yolk sac. Later, the production of RBCs starts in the fetal liver and increases until the 2nd^ trimester. After this, the rate of synthesis begins to decline in the liver as erythropoiesis increases in the bone marrow. RBCs are still produced in the liver for approximately 1 week after birth.

Q3. Study of tissues is called:
    (A) Anatomy
    (B) Metrology
    (C) Histology   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Cytology
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Study of organisms at tissues level is called histology. It includes the study of tissue structure, origin, location and function.

Q4. The epithelium covering in the tongue is:
    (A) Simple cuboidal
    (B) Pseudostratified
    (C) Squamous non-keratinized   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Squamous keratinized
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The tongue is covered by non-keratinized squamous epithelial tissues having taste buds of different kinds in different regions of the tongue.

Q5. Two animal cells are interconnected by:
    (A) Cell wall
    (B) Desmosomes   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Plasma membrane
    (D) Plamodesmata
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Two animal cells are interconnected by desmosomes, through which the exchange of materials takes place between two cells. It is formed from protein plaques in the cell membranes linked by filaments.

Q6. Myelin sheath is derived from:
    (A) Nerve cells
    (B) Schwann cells   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Neuroglial cells
    (D) Myocytes
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The outer layer of the axon of nerve cells is called the myelin sheath. Myelin sheath is derived from Schwann cells.

Q7. Antibodies are formed by:
    (A) Histiocytes
    (B) WBC
    (C) Mast cells
    (D) Plasma cells   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Antibodies are formed against any foreign body entering the body. It is formed by plasma cells, globulins that develop resistance against a particular type of disease.

Q8. The cell lining the blood vessels are:
    (A) Smooth muscle tissue
    (B) Squamous epithelium   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Connective tissue
    (D) Columnar epithelium
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The endothelium is a type of epithelium that lines the interior surface of blood vessels and lymphatic vessels, forming an interface between circulating blood or lymph in the lumen and the rest of the vessel wall. It is a thin layer of simple squamous called endothelial cells.

Q9. Cardiac muscles are:
    (A) Smooth and voluntary
    (B) Striated and involuntary   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Smooth and involuntary
    (D) Unstriated and involuntary
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Cardiac muscle tissue is a contractile tissue present only in the heart. The cardiac muscle fibres are elongated, branched and uninucleate. They appear striated due to the presence of alternate light and dark band. Cardiac muscles are self-contracting and involuntary in nature. The contract in a rhythmic fashion and help the heart to pump the blood.

Q10. Which of the following structure is Ectodermal in origin?
    (A) Brain   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Notochord
    (C) Lungs
    (D) Kidney
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The ectoderm differentiates to form the nervous system (spine, peripheral nerves and brain), tooth enamel and the epidermis, the outer part of the integument. It also forms the lining of mouth, anus, nostrils, sweat glands, hair and nails.

Q11. A normal adult man and woman have ________ WBC per cubic millimetre.
    (A) 4.5 - 5 million   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 5.5 - 6 million
    (C) 1.5 – 3.5 million
    (D) 2.5 - 3 million
    Answer: A
    Explanation: A normal adult male and female have about 4.5 to 5 million of WBC per cubic millimetre of blood. The number of white blood cells increases during infection against pathogens.

Q12. The most active phagocytic white blood cells are:
    (A) Lymphocytes and macrophages
    (B) Eosinophils and neutrophils
    (C) Neutrophils and monocytes   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Neutrophils and eosinophils
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The most active phagocytic white blood cells are neutrophils and monocytes. These cells try to engulf the microbes that enter the blood to cause disease.

Q13. Nasal septum contains:
    (A) Elastic cartilage
    (B) Calcified cartilage
    (C) Fibrous cartilage
    (D) Hyaline cartilage   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The nasal septum of human beings consists of hyaline cartilage which is highly elastic having collagen. It contains no nerves or blood vessels and is pearly bluish in colour.

Q14. Lymph contains:
    (A) Serum and WBC   <-- CORRECT
    (B) WBC and RBC
    (C) Platelet and serum
    (D) Blood plasma
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Lymph contains serum and WBC. Lymph is called extracellular fluid that helps in the transport of fat and protein. It contains WBC, so also help in protection against the infection.

Q15. Intercalated discs occur:
    (A) In striped muscles
    (B) At the junction of muscle and nerve cells
    (C) Between neurons
    (D) Between cardiac muscle fibres   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Intercalated discs are microscopic identifying features of cardiac muscles fibres. Individual heart muscle cells are connected by intercalated discs to work as a single functional organ.

Structural Organisation In Animals Test-03  (id 3370) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Structural Organisation in Animals
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. Basophils help the body defence by:
    (A) Phagocytosis of pathogens
    (B) Inhibit allergic
    (C) Cell mediated and antibody immunity
    (D) Heparin formation for preventing thrombosis   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Basophils appear in many specific kinds of inflammatory reactions, particularly those that cause allergic symptoms. Basophils contain anticoagulant heparin, which prevents blood from clotting too quickly. (Thrombosisis the formation of a blood clot inside a blood vessel, obstructing the flow of blood through the circulatory system.) They also contain the vasodilator histamine, which promotes blood flow to tissues.

Q2. The life span of RBC and WBC are respectively:
    (A) 60 days and 90 days
    (B) 120 days and 90 days   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 90 days and 60 days
    (D) 90 days and 120 days
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Red blood cells (RBC) live for 120 days and white blood cells (WBC) live for 90 days. Afterwards, they are degraded in the spleen.

Q3. Nissl granules in a nerve cell are now identified as_______.
    (A) Ribosomes   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Cell metabolites
    (C) Fat granules
    (D) Mitochondria
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The Nissl granules in nerve cells are now identified as ribosomes after the discovery of an electron microscope that provides a highly magnified image for detailed study.

Q4. Which one of the following is the correct pairing of a body part and muscle fibre that moves it?
    (A) Heart wall - involuntary unstriated muscle
    (B) Biceps of upper arm - smooth muscle fibres
    (C) Iris - involuntary smooth muscle   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Abdominal wall - smooth muscle
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The iris contains involuntary smooth muscles. It encircles the pupil of the iris and helps to dilate the pupil when there is insufficient light for the normal function of the eye.

Q5. Which of the following leucocytes transforms into macrophages?
    (A) Basophils
    (B) Eosinophils
    (C) Monocytes   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Lymphocytes
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Monocytes are white blood cells or leucocytes that transform into macrophages to engulf the pathogen entering the body.

Q6. Intestinal mucosa has microvili to:
    (A) Supply blood
    (B) Easy movement of food
    (C) Absorption of blood
    (D) Increase the surface area   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The innermost layer of the intestinal wall is called the mucosa. Mucosa contains microvilli to increase the surface area for the absorption of digested food to transport into a different part of the body.

Q7. Which one is a heterocrine gland?
    (A) Salivary gland
    (B) Gastric glands
    (C) Pancreas   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Liver
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The pancreas is called heterocrine gland because it acts as both endocrine and exocrine gland to secrete hormone as well as digestive enzymes. Testis and Ovary are also heterocrine glands.

Q8. Blood plasma is pale yellow in colour due to:
    (A) WBC
    (B) Phospholipids
    (C) Platelets
    (D) Bilirubin   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Blood plasma is pale yellow in colour due to the presence of bilirubin pigment in it. Blood appears red due to the presence of haemoglobin in RBC.

Q9. Muscle forming cells are called:
    (A) Phycoblast
    (B) Monoblast
    (C) Chromocyte
    (D) Myoblasts   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The muscle forming cells are called myoblasts cells. Myoblast is a type of embryonic progenitor cell that differentiates to give rise to muscle cells.

Q10. Which layer produces a new cell by mitosis?
    (A) Stratum Malpighi   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Stratum granulosum
    (C) Stratum lucidum
    (D) Stratum corneum
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Stratum Malpighi is the basal layer of skin epidermis having basal layer and generative layer that produces new cells by mitosis.

Q11. A largest single mass of lymphatic tissue in the body is______.
    (A) Liver
    (B) Lung
    (C) Spleen   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Kidney
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Spleen is the largest single mass of lymphatic tissue in the body. Blood formation in the foetus and newly born child takes place in spleen.

Q12. Both WBC and RBC are formed in the:
    (A) Thymus
    (B) Adrenal
    (C) Bone marrow   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Thyroid
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In adults, both WBC and RBC are formed in the bone marrow that is located in long bones such as thighs.

Q13. Mature erythrocytes cannot utilise glucose because they lack_______.
    (A) Mitochondria   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Enzymes
    (C) Nucleus
    (D) Golgi complex
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Mature erythrocytes or red blood corpuscles cannot utilize glucose because these cells lack mitochondria as well as the nucleus. Though glycolysis or glucose breakdown occurs in the cytoplasm, the final breakdown of pyruvate takes place inside mitochondria. Also, the electron transport chain is located inside mitochondria. Hence, the presence of mitochondria is essential for a cell to utilize glucose and release energy.

Q14. The matrix of bone and cartilage can be distinguished by the presence of ________.
    (A) Adipose cells
    (B) Lacuna
    (C) Haversian canal   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Chromatophores
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The matrix of bone and cartilage differ by the presence of a Haversian canal that makes bone hard and stiff. On the other hand, cartilage is flexible.

Q15. The ciliated columnar epithelium cells in human are known to occur in:
    (A) Urethra and fallopian tube
    (B) Eustachian tube and stomach lining
    (C) Bronchioles and Fallopian tube   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Bile duct and oesophagus
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Ciliated columnar epithelium cells in humans occur in bronchioles and fallopian tube. They contain small hair-like cilia on the free surface. This helps to move egg into the fallopian tube. In bronchioles, it helps to move mucus or dust particles.

Structural Organisation In Animals Test-04  (id 3371) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Structural Organisation in Animals
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. Whales can live in cold water as they have thick coat of_________.
    (A) Blubber   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Striated skin
    (C) Proactive skin
    (D) Keratinized skin
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Whales can live in cold water as they have a thick coat of blubber. Blubber help in providing insulating coat beneath the skin that prevents loss of heat from the body.

Q2. Nerve fibres in the CNS can regenerate after injury due to the presence of________.
    (A) Schwann cells
    (B) Neurilemma   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Myelin sheath
    (D) Plasmolemma
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Nerve fibres in the CNS can regenerate after injury due to the presence of neurilemma. They are the outermost nucleated cytoplasmic layer of Schwann cells that surrounds the axon of the neuron.

Q3. Platelets are formed from the________.
    (A) Microkayocytes
    (B) Megakaryocytes   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Haemocytes
    (D) Thrombocytes
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Platelets are a little piece of blood cells that help wound healing and prevent bleeding by forming a blood clot. It is formed from the megakaryocytes.

Q4. Certain neutrophils in female mammals possess a small spherical lobe attached to their nucleus by a stalk. This lobe is called ________.
    (A) Barr body   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Leukopenia
    (C) Leucona
    (D) Golgi body
    Answer: A
    Explanation: A Barr body appears as a small drumstick-like projection on one of the lobes of some neutrophils in females. A Barr body is the inactive X chromosome in a female somatic cell.

Q5. The type of connective tissue that is associated with the umbilical cord is:
    (A) Adipose connective tissue
    (B) Reticular connective tissue
    (C) Jelly like connective tissue   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Areolar connective tissue
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Jelly like connective tissue is associated with the umbilical cord. It is a flexible cord-like structure containing blood vessels and attaching a human fetus to the placenta during gestation.

Q6. The haemoglobin content per 100 ml of blood of a normal healthy human adult is:
    (A) 5-11 g
    (B) 25-30 g
    (C) 12-16 g   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 17-20 g
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The haemoglobin content per 100 ml of blood of a normal healthy human adult is in the range of 12-16 g. Haemoglobin acts as a respiratory carrier. It is responsible for picking up oxygen from the lungs and transporting it to all parts of the body through blood. Maintaining a healthy level of haemoglobin in blood is essential for sufficient supply of oxygen to cells or tissues. Level of haemoglobin less than 12g/100ml leads to anaemia and weakness.

Q7. The type of muscles present in our:
    (A) the heart is involuntary and unstriated smooth muscle.
    (B) the upper arm is smooth muscle and fusiform in shape.
    (C) the intestine is striated and involuntary.
    (D) the thigh is striated and voluntary.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The muscle present in our thigh is striated and voluntary muscles. They are attached to the bone for movement and works according to our will.

Q8. Choose the odd pair out in the following:
    (A) Neuron - melanin   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Muscle fibre - actin
    (C) Epithelium - keratin
    (D) Areolar connective tissue - collagen
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Epithelium tissues contain keratin, muscles fibres contain actin and areolar connective tissue contain collagen but melanin is absent in neuron.

Q9. A close approximation of an axon of one neuron and a dendrite of the next is called ________.
    (A) Synapse   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Bridge
    (C) Joint
    (D) Junction
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The close connection between an axon and dendrite of the next neuron is called a synapse. Nerve impulses pass through it in the form of neurotransmitters due to the presence of synaptic fluid present in it.

Q10. The muscle which is immune to fatigue are:
    (A) Cardiac muscle   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Skeleton muscle
    (C) Unstriped muscle
    (D) Jaw muscle
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The muscles which are immune to fatigue are cardiac muscles present exclusively in the heart. They work from birth till death without getting fatigued.

Q11. The mammary gland is an example of:
    (A) Gastric glad
    (B) Merocrine gland
    (C) Holocrine gland
    (D) Apocrine gland   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Apocrine glands are a kind of exocrine gland found in the skin, breast, eyelids, and ears. Mammary glands are present in the breast that release milk in mammals.

Q12. In earthworm, two pairs of testes are present in:
    (A) 16th and 18th segment
    (B) 17th and 19th segment
    (C) 10th and 11th segment   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 12th and 13th segment
    Answer: C
    Explanation: There are two pairs of testes present in the 10th and 11th segments. Their vasa deferentia run-up to the 18th segment where they join the prostatic duct.

Q13. How many types of nephridia are seen in earthworm based on their location?
    (A) 5
    (B) 4
    (C) 3   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 2
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The excretory organs occur as segmentally arranged coiled tubules called nephridia.
They are of three types:
 septal nephridia
 integumentary nephridia
 pharyngeal nephridia.

Q14. The pharyngeal nephridia of earthworm occur in segments:
    (A) 4th, 5th and 6th   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 3rd, 4th and 5th
    (C) 14th, 15th and 16th
    (D) 5th, 6th and 7th
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The excretory system of earthworm contains a pair of nephridia in every segment, except for the first three and the last ones. Three types of nephridia are found in earthworm: integumentary, septal, and pharyngeal. The pharyngeal nephridia are present as three paired tufts in the 4th, 5th, and 6th segments.

Q15. Earthworms are known as Friends of farmers because:
    (A) Their burrow makes soil porous   <-- CORRECT
    (B) They are used as meal for farmers
    (C) Their burrow makes soil loose
    (D) They kill the birds
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Earthworms are known as ‘friends of farmers’ because they make burrows in the soil and make it porous which helps in respiration and penetration of the developing plant roots.

Structural Organisation In Animals Test-05  (id 3372) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Structural Organisation in Animals
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. In Pheretima, ovaries are present in:
    (A) 7th, 8th and 9th segments
    (B) 13th segments   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 14th, 15th and 16th segments
    (D) 5th, 6th and 7th segments
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In Pheretima a pair of whitish, small, lobulated ovaries are present on either side of the ventral nerve cord in 13th segments.

Q2. In earthworm, the stomach is present in:
    (A) 5 - 7 segments
    (B) 9 - 14 segments   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 8 - 10 segments
    (D) 15 - 26 segments
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The stomach of an earthworm is a long cylindrical structure and extends from 9-14 segments.

Q3. Which statement is wrong with respect to an earthworm?
 Muscular layer in the body wall of an earthworm is made up of circular muscles.
 Setae help in the locomotion.
 A single male genital pore is present.
 Typhlosole is the part of the intestine.
    (A) (D)
    (B) (C)
    (C) (A)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (B)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The body wall of the earthworm is covered externally by a thin non-cellular cuticle below which is the epidermis, two muscle layers namely, circular and longitudinal, and an innermost coelomic epithelium.

Q4. The clitellum in earthworm occur in:
    (A) 12 - 14 segments
    (B) 10 - 12 segments
    (C) 14 - 16 segments   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 13 - 15 segments
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In a mature worm, segments 14-16 are covered by a prominent dark band of glandular tissue called the clitellum.

Q5. Which of the following structure is Ectodermal in origin in the mouthparts of cockroach shown in the figure below?
    (A) Labrum
    (B) Mandible
    (C) Hypopharynx
    (D) Maxilla.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The maxilla is a paired structure present in the mouth part of cockroaches. It is derived from ectoderm and is used to hold and manipulate food.

Q6. How many pairs of spiracles are found in cockroach?
    (A) 10 pairs   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 7 pairs
    (C) 6 pairs
    (D) 8 pairs
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The respiratory system consists of a network of the trachea. This network opens through 10 pairs of small holes called spiracles present on the lateral side of the body.

Q7. Identify ‘A’ in the figure given below.
    (A) Ocellus   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Compound eye
    (C) Hypopharynx
    (D) Labrum
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The label ‘A’ is ocellus. It is a type of photoreceptor found in some animals like cockroaches.

Q8. In male cockroaches, genital pouch lies at the hind end of the abdomen bounded by:
    (A) Dorsally by 9th and 10th terga and ventrally by the 9th sternum   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Dorsally by 8th and 9th terga and ventrally by the 9th sternum
    (C) Dorsally by 8th and 9th terga and ventrally by the 8th sternum
    (D) Dorsally by 9th and 10th terga and ventrally by the 10th sternum
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In males, genital pouch or chamber lies at the hind end of abdomen bounded dorsally by 9th and 10th terga and ventrally by the 9th sternum. It contains dorsal anus, ventral male genital pore, and gonapophysis.

Q9. Which one of the following statements is true for cockroach?
    (A) The larval stage is called caterpillar
    (B) The number of ovarioles in each ovary are ten
    (C) They are ureotelic
    (D) Anal styles are absent in females   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Male cockroaches bear a pair of short, thread-like anal styles in the 9th segment which is absent in females.

Q10. The number of eggs contained in an ootheca of cockroach is:
    (A) 8 - 10
    (B) 10 -12
    (C) 9 - 11
    (D) 14 - 16   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: On average, females produce 9-10 oothecae. Each ootheca contains 14-16 eggs.

Q11. The number of ganglia in the nervous system of cockroach is:
    (A) 6 in thorax and 3 in the abdomen
    (B) 4 in thorax and 6 in the abdomen
    (C) 3 in thorax and 6 in the abdomen   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 4 in thorax and 3 in the abdomen
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The nervous system of cockroach consists of a series of fused, segmentally arranged ganglia. They are joined by paired longitudinal connectives on the ventral side. Three ganglia lie in the thorax, and six ganglia are found in the abdomen.

Q12. What type of metamorphosis occurs in cockroach?
    (A) Paurometabolous   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Holometabolous
    (C) Ametabolous
    (D) Hemimetabolous
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The development of cockroach is paurometabolous. This means a gradual development from the nymphal stage to the adult stage. Nymph represents a miniature adult and lives in the same habitat.

Q13. In cockroach, a mushroom-shaped gland is present in:
    (A) 2nd - 6th abdominal segments
    (B) 5th - 6th abdominal segments
    (C) 4th - 6th abdominal segments
    (D) 6th - 7th abdominal segments   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: A characteristic mushroom-shaped gland is present in the 6th-7th abdominal segments of the cockroach. This gland functions as an accessory reproductive gland.

Q14. Match the following and choose the correct answer with reference to cockroach:
 Column A
 Column B
 (i) Bundles of sperm
 (a) Ovarioles
 (ii) External genitalia
 (b) Gonopore
 (iii) Chain of developing ova
 (c) Phallomere
 (iv) Opening of ejaculatory duct
 (d) Spermatophore
    (A) (i) - (d), (ii) - (a), (iii) - (b), (iv) - (c)
    (B) (i) - (d), (ii) - (b), (iii) - (a), (iv) - (c)
    (C) (i) - (d), (ii) - (c), (iii) - (a), (iv) - (b)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (i) - (d), (ii) - (b), (iii) - (c), (iv) - (a)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The sperms are stored in the seminal vesicles and are glued together in the form of bundles called spermatophores which are discharged during copulation.
 The external genitalia is represented by chitinous asymmetrical structures surrounding the male gonopore is called male gonapophysis or phallomere.
 Each ovary is formed of a group of eight ovarian tubules or ovarioles, containing a chain of developing ova. 
 The ejaculatory duct opens into a male gonopore situated ventral to the anus.

Q15. The pericardial space in cockroach is regularly altered by the muscles:
    (A) Longitudinal
    (B) Ciliary
    (C) Circular
    (D) Alary   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Cockroaches have an open circulatory system. Their pericardial space is regularly altered by alary muscles.

Structural Organisation In Animals Test-06  (id 3373) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Structural Organisation in Animals
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. The mouth part of cockroach which is compared to the tongue is_______.
    (A) Hypopharynx   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Maxillae
    (C) Labium
    (D) Mandible
    Answer: A
    Explanation: A median flexible lobe called a hypopharynx act as the tongue. It lies within the cavity enclosed by the mouthparts.

Q2. How many times do nymphs moult to reach the adult form of a cockroach?
    (A) 12
    (B) 13   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 11
    (D) 10
    Answer: B
    Explanation: When the ootheca hatches, a tiny nymph comes out. It grows by undergoing molting about 13 times to reach the adult form.

Q3. Blood consists of:
    (A) Plasma, WBC and RBC
    (B) RBC, WBC and platelets
    (C) Plasma, WBC, RBC and platelets   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Plasma, WBC and platelets
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Blood is a fluid connective tissue containing plasma. It contains red blood cells (RBC), white blood cells (WBC), and platelets suspended in the plasma.

Q4. In frog, during aestivation and hibernation gaseous exchange takes place through
    (A) Heart
    (B) Lungs
    (C) Skin   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Buccal cavity
    Answer: C
    Explanation: As the frog becomes inactive during aestivation and hibernation, gaseous exchange does not take place through lungs. It takes place through skin.

Q5. The lymph in frog lacks:
    (A) RBCs and few proteins   <-- CORRECT
    (B) WBCs and few proteins
    (C) RBC and plasma
    (D) Plasma and WBCs
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The lymph is different from the blood. It is known as tissue fluid. Lymph is yellowish in colour as it lacks RBCs and few proteins.

Q6. The winter sleep in frog is called ________.
    (A) Camouflage
    (B) Aestivation
    (C) Mimicry
    (D) Hibernation   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: During extreme heat and cold periods, the frog takes shelter in deep burrows to protect them from extreme environmental conditions. This is called as summer sleep (aestivation) and winter sleep (hibernation).

Q7. The correct order of the digestive system of the frog is:
 Mouth, buccal cavity, oesophagus, stomach, intestine, rectum, cloaca, cloacal aperture
 Mouth, oesophagus, buccal cavity, stomach, intestine, rectum, cloacal aperture, cloaca
 Mouth, buccal cavity, oesophagus, intestine, stomach, rectum, cloacal aperture, cloaca
 Mouth, oesophagus, buccal cavity, stomach, rectum, intestine, cloaca, cloacal aperture, cloaca
    (A) (D)
    (B) (B)
    (C) (A)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (C)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The digestive system of a frog begins from the mouth which opens into the buccal cavity that leads to the esophagus through the pharynx. The esophagus is a short tube that opens into the stomach which in turn continues as the intestine and then rectum. The rectum finally opens outside by the cloaca through the cloacal aperture.

Q8. The special venous connection between liver and intestine as well as the kidney and lower parts of the body present in frogs is called ________.
    (A) Arterial system
    (B) Hepatic portal system
    (C) Vena cava
    (D) Renal portal system   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The renal portal system forms a special blood circulation system between liver and intestine. It also forms a special connection between the kidney and lower parts of the body present in frogs.

Q9. The number of nymphs produced from single ootheca of the frog is _______.
    (A) 15
    (B) 10
    (C) 16   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 12
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Young ones of frogs are called nymphs. When the ootheca ruptures, 16 nymphs come out.

Q10. Match the following with reference to the frog:
 Column A
 Column B
 (i) Medulla oblongata
 (a) Sensory papillae
 (ii) Smell
 (b) PNS
 (iii) Touch
 (c) Foramen magnum
 (iv) Cranial nerves
 (d) Nasal epithelium
    (A) (i) - (d), (ii) - (b), (iii) - (a), (iv) - (c)
    (B) (i) - (b), (ii) - (a), (iii) - (c), (iv) - (d)
    (C) (i) - (a), (ii) - (c), (iii) - (d), (iv) - (b)
    (D) (i) - (c), (ii) - (d), (iii) - (a), (iv) - (b)   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The medulla oblongata passes out through the foramen magnum and continues into the spinal cord, which is enclosed in the vertebral column.
 Frog has different types of sense organs. This includes organs of touch (sensory papillae) and smell (nasal epithelium).
 The nervous system is organized into a central nervous system including the brain and spinal cord and peripheral nervous system (PNS) including cranial and spinal nerves.

Q11. Blood plasma contains ________ % water.
    (A) 60
    (B) 98
    (C) 80
    (D) 90   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Blood consists of blood plasma formed cells ( RBC, WBC, Platelets) along with sugar, proteins, etc. Blood plasma contains about 90% water with a number of salts and few circulating hormones.

Q12. Myelin sheath is mainly made of______.
    (A) Protein
    (B) Fats
    (C) Carbohydrates
    (D) Phospholipids   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The myelin sheath is the outer layer of the axon of nerve cells. It is made up of phospholipids. It is mainly protective in nature, acts as an insulator, and helps in the transmission of impulses.

Q13. The formation of erythrocytes in foetus takes place in:
    (A) Blood plasma
    (B) Liver and Spleen   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Sarcoplasm
    (D) Red bone marrow
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In the early fetus, erythropoiesis takes place in the mesodermal cells of the yolk sac. Later, the production of RBCs starts in the fetal liver and increases until the 2nd^ trimester. After this, the rate of synthesis begins to decline in the liver as erythropoiesis increases in the bone marrow. RBCs are still produced in the liver for approximately 1 week after birth.

Q14. Nerve fibres in the CNS can regenerate after injury due to the presence of________.
    (A) Plasmolemma
    (B) Schwann cells
    (C) Neurilemma   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Myelin sheath
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Nerve fibres in the CNS can regenerate after injury due to the presence of neurilemma. They are the outermost nucleated cytoplasmic layer of Schwann cells that surrounds the axon of the neuron.

Q15. The most active phagocytic white blood cells are:
    (A) Neutrophils and eosinophils
    (B) Neutrophils and monocytes   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Lymphocytes and macrophages
    (D) Eosinophils and neutrophils
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The most active phagocytic white blood cells are neutrophils and monocytes. These cells try to engulf the microbes that enter the blood to cause disease.

# Cell The Unit of Life  (5 tests)

========================================================================
Cell The Unit Of Life Test-01   (id 3374) [FREE]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Cell The Unit of Life
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. New cells generate from:
    (A) Embryo
    (B) Abiotic materials
    (C) Regeneration of old cells
    (D) Pre-existing cells   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: All living organisms are composed of cells and products of cells.all cells arise from pre-existing cells.

Q2. Who first saw and described a live cell?
    (A) R. Virchow
    (B) T. Schwann
    (C) A.V. Leeuwenhoek   <-- CORRECT
    (D) M. Schleiden
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The first man to witness a live cell under a microscope was Anton van Leeuwenhoek, who in 1674 described the algae Spirogyra. Van Leeuwenhoek probably also saw bacteria.

Q3. Cytoskeleton is made of.
    (A) Calcium carbonate granules
    (B) Cellulose microfibrils
    (C) Protienaceous filaments   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Cellulose deposits
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Cytoskeleton is a series of intercellular proteins that help a cell with shape, support andmovement. So, cytoskeleton is made up of proteinaceous filaments.

Q4. Select the incorrect pairing:
    (A) Thylakoid - chloroplast
    (B) Digestive enzyme - Lysosome
    (C) Cristae - Mitochondria
    (D) Chromosome - RNA   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Mitochondria contain cristae, finger-like projection of inner layer, thylakoid is present in chloroplast and lysosome is a digestive enzyme but RNA is absent in Chromosome.

Q5. Which is common in plant and animal cells?
    (A) Plastids
    (B) Centrioles
    (C) Mitochondria   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Central vacuoles
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Mitochondria are present in both plants as well as animal cells. Plastids and central vacuoles are present in plant cells and centrioles are present in only animal cells.

Q6. Animal cell does not possess:
    (A) Plasmodesmata   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Ribosomes
    (C) Centriole
    (D) Plasmalemma
    Answer: A
    Explanation: An animal cell does not possess plasmodesmata but they contain ribosomes, centriole, and plasmalemma. Plasmodesmata are the connection between two plant cells.

Q7. The ability of a living somatic nucleated cell to form the complete organism is called:
    (A) Cellular totipotancy   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Regeneration
    (C) Morphogenesis
    (D) Cell differentiation
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Cellular Totipotency is the ability of a single cell to produce all cell types and to organize them into an entire organism when cultured in a suitable culture medium at the appropriate temperature and aeration conditions. Spores and Zygote are examples of totipotent cells.

Q8. The most recent and accepted model of the plasma membrane is:
    (A) Lamellar model
    (B) Fluid-Mosaic model   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Danielli and Davson model
    (D) Robertson model
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Fluid-Mosaic model is the most recent and accepted model of the plasma membrane. This model was proposed by Singer and Nicolson in 1972. The quasi-fluid nature of lipid enables the lateral movement of proteins within the overall bilayer.

Q9. Each centriole is surrounded by dense amorphous protoplasmic masses called:
    (A) Cytoplasmic particles
    (B) Massules   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Cell granules
    (D) Meta-molecule
    Answer: B
    Explanation: All animal cell has two small organelles called centrioles. Each centriole is surrounded by dense amorphous protoplasmic masses called Massules.

Q10. The photograph or diagram of metaphase chromosome arranged in homologous pair according to their length and thickness, the position of the centromere is called ________.
    (A) Idiogram   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Photogram
    (C) MRi
    (D) Chromogram
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Idiogram is a diagrammatic or systematized representation of the chromosome complement of an individual, species, or another group of organisms, indicating the number of chromosomes and their lengths, arm length ratio, centromere position, banding pattern.

Q11. The membrane complex formed in the folding of the plasma membrane in prokaryotic cells is called ________.
    (A) Vacuoles
    (B) Mesosome   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Mitochondria
    (D) Centrioles
    Answer: B
    Explanation: A special membranous structure is a mesosome which is formed by the extensions of the plasma membrane into the cell.

Q12. The smallest free-living organism is______.
    (A) Bacteria
    (B) Virus
    (C) Viroids
    (D) PPLOs   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: PPLO (Pleuro Pneumonia Like Organisms). They are generally smaller and multiply more rapidly than the eukaryotic cells.

Q13. In certain bacteria, the glycocalyx is formed into loose sheath layer is called as ________.
    (A) Cell membrane
    (B) Cell wall
    (C) Slime layer   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Capsule
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Glycocalyx differs in composition and thickness among different bacteria. It could be a loose sheath called the slime layer in some, while in others it may be thick and tough called the capsule. The cell wall determines the shape of the cell and provides strong structural support.

Q14. The bacterial flagellum consists of
    (A) Filament ,basal body, pili
    (B) Filament, hook and basal body   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Filament, hook, and fimbriae
    (D) Filament, pili, and basal body
    Answer: B
    Explanation: A bacterial flagellum has 3 basic parts: a filament, a hook, and a basal body.
The filament is the rigid, helical structure that extends from the cell surface.
The hook is a flexible coupling between the filament and the basal body.
The basal body consists of a rod and a series of rings that anchor the flagellum to the cell wall and the cytoplasmic membrane.

Q15. The rod-shaped bacteria is called as_______.
    (A) Spherical
    (B) Vibrio
    (C) Bacillus   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Spiral
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The shapes of bacteria are bacillus (rod-like), coccus (spherical), vibrio (comma-shaped) and spirillum (spiral).

Cell The Unit Of Life Test-02  (id 3375) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Cell The Unit of Life
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. The rod-shaped bacteria is called as_______.
    (A) Bacillus   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Spherical
    (C) Vibrio
    (D) Spiral
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The shapes of bacteria are bacillus (rod-like), coccus (spherical), vibrio (comma-shaped) and spirillum (spiral).

Q2. In prokaryotes, the reserved food material is stored in:
    (A) Vacuole
    (B) Cytoplasm   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Centrosome
    (D) Endoplasmic reticulum
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Reserve material in prokaryotic cells is stored in the cytoplasm in the form of inclusion bodies.

Q3. Tubulin occurs in:
    (A) All of these
    (B) Plasma membrane
    (C) Golgi bodies
    (D) Cilia and flagella   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Tubulin is a kind of protein that is present in the cilia and flagella of cells having it. It provides flexibility to the cilia and flagella.

Q4. Arrangement of ciliary microtubules is:
    (A) 9 + 4
    (B) 9 + 9
    (C) 9 + 2   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 9 + 3
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Cilia present in prokaryotic organisms consist of microtubules. These microtubules are arranged in 9+2 order in which 2 forms the centre and 9 are arranged at the periphery.

Q5. Which does not occur in cell membrane?
    (A) Phospholipids
    (B) Proline   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Glycolipids
    (D) Cholesterol
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The cell membrane is made up of lipid bilayer consisting of different components like phospholipids, glycolipids, and cholesterol. However, proline is an alpha-amino acid used in protein synthesis and is a major constituent of collagen.

Q6. Lipid molecules of plasma membrane occur
    (A) In series
    (B) Scattered
    (C) Parallel   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Alternately
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Phospholipids found in the plasma membrane is a lipid bilayer having a hydrophilic region called the head and a hydrophobic region called the tail. The hydrophilic region can interact with water due to the presence of a phosphate group which is polar, like water. The membrane is in contact with water on both the inner and outer sides. The hydrophilic heads arrange automatically on the outer side of the bilayer due to polarity and hydrophobic heads are facing each other between the bilayer, thus arranging all lipid molecules parallel to each other.

Q7. The plasma membrane consists mainly of:
    (A) Proteins embedded in a carbohydrate bilayer
    (B) Proteins embedded in a phospholipids bilayer   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Phospholipids embedded in protein bilayer
    (D) Proteins embedded in a polymer of glucose molecules
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The plasma membrane is composed of lipids that are arranged in a bilayer. Also, the lipids are arranged within the membrane with the polar head towards the outer sides and the hydrophobic tails towards the inner part. The membrane proteins can be classified as integral or peripheral. Peripheral proteins lie on the surface.

Q8. The nucleus was first described by:
    (A) Robert brown   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Schwann
    (C) Palade
    (D) Flemming
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Nucleus as a cell organelle was first described by Robert Brown as early as 1831.

Q9. Lysosomes are produced by:
    (A) Leucoplast
    (B) Mitochondria
    (C) Endoplasmic reticulum
    (D) Golgi bodies   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Lysosomes are manufactured and budded into the cytoplasm by the Golgi apparatus with enzymes inside. The enzymes that are within the lysosome are made in the rough endoplasmic reticulum, which is then delivered to the Golgi apparatus via transport vesicles.

Q10. The eukaryotic ribosomes are of_____.
    (A) 30S
    (B) 70S
    (C) 50S
    (D) 80S   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The eukaryotic ribosomes are the 80S while the prokaryotic ribosomes are 70S. Here ‘S’ stands for the sedimentation coefficient; it indirectly is a measure of density and size.

Q11. The vacuoles are bound by the single membrane is called as_________.
    (A) Cisternae
    (B) Food vacuole
    (C) Contractile vacuole
    (D) Tonoplast   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The vacuole is bound by a single membrane called tonoplast. In-plant cells the vacuoles can occupy up to 90% of the volume of the cell. In plants, the tonoplast facilitates the transport of a number of ions.

Q12. The chromosome having centromeres at one terminal end is called ________.
    (A) Submetacentric
    (B) Telocentric   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Acrocentric
    (D) Metacentric
    Answer: B
    Explanation: A telocentric chromosome's centromere is located at the terminal end of the chromosome. Telomeres may extend from both ends of the chromosome their shape is like I during anaphase. For example, the standard house mouse karyotype has only telocentric chromosomes. Humans do not possess telocentric chromosomes.

Q13. Nucleoplasm otherwise called as ______.
    (A) Nuclear matrix   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Nucleosome
    (C) Nuclear pores
    (D) Nucleolus
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The nuclear matrix or the nucleoplasm contains nucleolus and chromatin. The nucleoli are spherical structures present in the nucleoplasm.

Q14. Lysosomes are rich in hydrolytic enzymes such as:
    (A) Proteases and lipases
    (B) Hydrolyses and lipases
    (C) Hydrolyses and proteases
    (D) Hydrolyses, lipases, and proteases   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Lysosomes are found to be very rich in almost all types of hydrolytic enzymes (hydrolases - lipases, proteases, carbohydrases) optimally active at the acidic pH. These enzymes are capable of digesting carbohydrates, proteins, lipids, and nucleic acids.

Q15. Mitochondria is called Powerhouse of the cell because:
    (A) Presence of matrix
    (B) Formation of ATP   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Presence of DNA
    (D) 70S ribosomes
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Mitochondria are called as powerhouse of the cell because it contains an enzyme for cellular respiration in which energy is released in the form of ATP.
