Cell The Unit Of Life Test-03  (id 3376) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Cell The Unit of Life
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. The inner membrane of mitochondria thrown into folds to form finger-like structure is called ________.
    (A) Cristae   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Matrix
    (C) Amyloplast
    (D) Inter membrane space
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Mitochondria are double membranous structure. The inner membrane of mitochondria thrown into folds to form finger-like structure is called cristae.

Q2. The staining procedure is developed by:
    (A) Schwann
    (B) A.V.Leeuwenhoek
    (C) Schleiden
    (D) Hans Christian Gram   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The staining procedure developed by Gram viz., those that take up the gram stain are gram-positive and the others that do not are called gram-negative bacteria.

Q3. SER differ from RER in:
    (A) Absence of glucose molecule
    (B) Absence of granules on surface
    (C) Absence of ribosome on surface   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Presence of glucose molecules
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Smooth endoplasmic reticulum (SER) differs from the rough endoplasmic reticulum (RER) in absence of ribosome on the surface of the endoplasmic reticulum.

Q4. Golgi apparatus is the site for the formation of:
    (A) Glycolipids and glycoproteins   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Lipids
    (C) Carbohydrates
    (D) Enzymes
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Golgi apparatus is the important site of formation of glycoproteins and glycolipids.

Q5. Elaioplasts belongs to:
    (A) Chloroplast
    (B) Leucoplast   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Amyloplast
    (D) Chromoplast
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The leucoplasts are the colourless plastids of varied shapes and sizes with stored nutrients. Leucoplast includes:
 Amyloplasts storing carbohydrates.
 Elaioplasts storing oils and fats.
 Aleuroplasts storing proteins.

Q6. How much percent of vacuoles occupy the volume of the cell in plant cells?
    (A) 70%
    (B) 80%
    (C) 90%   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 50%
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In a mature cell, the vacuole may occupy as much as 90 percent of the cell volume, such that the rest of the cell contents are flattened against the cell membrane.

Q7. Chlorophyll is located inside_______.
    (A) Chromatophores
    (B) Thylakoids   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Stroma
    (D) Plasma lemma
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The chloroplast consists of a number of organized flattened membranous sacs called the thylakoids, Chlorophyll pigments are present in the thylakoids.

Q8. Which one is present nearest to plasmamembrane?
    (A) Middle lamella
    (B) Tonoplast
    (C) Secondary wall   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Primary wall
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The cell wall of a young plant cell, the primary walls capable of growth, which gradually diminishes as the cell matures and the secondary wall is formed on the inner (towards membrane) side of the cell.

Q9. The cytoskeleton is made of:
    (A) Proteinaceous filaments   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Phosphoglycerides
    (C) Hemicellulose
    (D) Micro tubules
    Answer: A
    Explanation: An elaborate network of filamentous proteinaceous structures present in the cytoplasm is collectively referred to as the cytoskeleton.

Q10. The movement of ions against the concentration gradient is
    (A) Diffusion
    (B) Osmosis
    (C) All of these.
    (D) Active transport   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Active transport is the movement of molecules across a cell membrane in the direction against their concentration gradient, i.e. moving from an area of lower concentration to an area of higher concentration.

Q11. The chromatin contains some basic proteins are called as ________.
    (A) Satellite
    (B) Non-histones
    (C) Kinetochores
    (D) Histones   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Histone proteins the basic packer and arranger of chromatin.

Q12. The centrioles are absent in______.
    (A) Animal cell
    (B) Human cell
    (C) Bacterial cell
    (D) Plant cell   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Animal cells have centrioles which are absent in almost all plant cells.

Q13. The ribosomes of a polysome translate:
    (A) mRNA to DNA
    (B) mRNA to Proteins   <-- CORRECT
    (C) DNA to DNA
    (D) Proteins to DNA
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Several ribosomes may attach to a single mRNA and form a chain called polyribosomes or polysome. The ribosomes of a polysome translate the mRNA into proteins.

Q14. Middle lamella is composed of:
    (A) Calcium pectate   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Phosphoglycerides
    (C) Mumramic acid
    (D) Hemicellulose
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The middle lamella is a layer mainly of calcium pectate which holds or glues the different neighbouring cells together.

Q15. Plasmodesmata take parts in:
    (A) Cytoplasmic streaming
    (B) Movement of substances between cells   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Locomotion in unicellular organism
    (D) Synchronize mitotic divisions
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The plasmodesmata consist of pores, or channels, lying between individual plant cells, and connect the symplastic space in the plant. They can also be termed as "bridges" between two plant cells. The plasmodesmata separate the outer cell membranes of the plant cells. A plasmodesma (plural plasmodesmata, singular plasmodesma) is a channel through the cell wall that allows molecules and substances to move back and forth as needed.

Cell The Unit Of Life Test-04  (id 3377) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Cell The Unit of Life
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. Who was the first to explain that cells divide?
    (A) Rudolf Virchow   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Robert Brown
    (C) Anton von LeeuwenHoek
    (D) Schwann
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The German doctor Rudolf Virchow proposed in 1855 that all cells result from the division of previously existing cells, and this idea became a key piece of modern cell theory.

Q2. Which of the following statements with reference to the cytoskeleton is not correct?
    (A) Cytoskeleton maintains the shape of the cell
    (B) Cytoskeleton helpful in production of ATP   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Cytoskeleton helpful in mechanical support
    (D) Cytoskeleton helps in motility
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The cytoskeleton in a cell is involved in functions like mechanical support, motility, maintenance of the shape of the cell.

Q3. The organelle involved in respiration is_______.
    (A) Mitochondria   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Golgi complex
    (C) Chloroplast
    (D) Endoplasmic reticulum
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Mitochondria are the sites of aerobic respiration. They produce cellular energy in the form of ATP.

Q4. Cell organelles with a single membrane are ________.
    (A) Lysosomes   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Mitochondria
    (C) Plastids
    (D) Chloroplast
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Lysosomes are single membrane structures containing enzymes for digestion of all types of macromolecules.

Q5. The site for the light reactions is ________.
    (A) Stroma
    (B) Cisternae
    (C) Grana   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Vacuoles
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In-plant cells, the chloroplasts are responsible for trapping light energy essential for photosynthesis. The grana, in the plastid, is the site of light reactions.

Q6. Select the incorrect matching.
    (A) Digestive enzyme-Lysosome
    (B) Thylakoid-Chloroplast
    (C) Chromosome-RNA   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Cristae-Mitochondria
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The nucleus contains the chromosomes which in turn contain the genetic material, DNA.

Q7. The stacks of closely packed thylakoids are called ________.
    (A) Stroma
    (B) Granum   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Matrix
    (D) Lumen
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Granum: A stacked membranous structure within the chloroplasts of plants and green algae that contains chlorophyll and is the site of the light reactions of photosynthesis. The saclike membranes that makeup grana are known as thylakoids.

Q8. Which one of the following is common between Prokaryotic and Eukaryotic cell?
    (A) Presence of cell wall   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Presence of membrane bounded organelles
    (C) Presence of nuclear membrane
    (D) Number of chromosomes
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Most prokaryotic cells, particularly the bacterial cells, have a chemically complex cell envelope. All eukaryotic cells are not identical. Plant and animal cells are different as the former possess cell walls.

Q9. The structure of the plasma membrane fluid mosaic model is proposed by:
    (A) Gram
    (B) Schwann and Schleiden
    (C) Singer and Nicolson   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Robert brown
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The fluid mosaic model explains various observations regarding the structure of functional cell membranes. The model, which was devised by SJ Singer and GL Nicolson in 1972, describes the cell membrane as a two-dimensional liquid that restricts the lateral diffusion of membrane components.

Q10. Proteins synthesized by ribosomes on the endoplasmic reticulum are modified in________.
    (A) Stroma
    (B) Cisternae   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Tubules
    (D) Vesicles
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The cisternae of the Golgi apparatus is responsible for transporting, modifying, and packaging proteins and lipids into vesicles for delivery to targeted destinations.

Q11. Subunits of 80S ribosome are:
    (A) 60 S
    (B) 60 S and 20 S
    (C) 40 S and 60 S   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 40 S
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Each ribosome consists of two subunits.
Eukaryotes have 80S ribosomes, each consisting of a small (40S) and large (60S) subunit.
Their 40S subunit has an 18S RNA (1900 nucleotides) and 33 proteins.
The large subunit is composed of a 5S RNA (120 nucleotides), 28S RNA (4700 nucleotides), a 5.8S RNA (160 nucleotides) subunits, and 46 proteins.

Q12. Cell drinking is another name of _______.
    (A) Phagocytosis
    (B) Pinocytosis   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Aquacytosis
    (D) transcytosis
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Cell drinking is another name of pinocytosis. Pinocytosis, a process by which liquid droplets are ingested by living cells. Pinocytosis is one type of endocytosis, the general process by which cells engulf external substances, gathering them into special membrane-bound vesicles contained within the cell.

Q13. Which one is not a part of the Golgi complex?
    (A) Glycosomes   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Tubules
    (C) Cisternae
    (D) Vesicles
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Golgi complex or Golgi body consists of cisternae, tubules and spherical vesicles. Glycosome is not present in the Golgi complex.

Q14. Lysosomes are called suicide bag because it contain:
    (A) Large number of toxic materials
    (B) Large amount of lipase
    (C) Large number of digestive enzyme   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Large amount of hormones
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Lysosome is called a suicide bag because it contain a large number of digestive enzyme that can digest the whole cell in case of rapture.

Q15. Which is not a function of the vacuole in a plant cell?
    (A) Waste disposal
    (B) Formation of H_2O_2   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Storage
    (D) Cell elongation
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Plant cell contains large central vacuole which helps in waste disposal, cell elongation and storage but not involved in the formation of H_2O_2.

Cell The Unit Of Life Test-05  (id 3378) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Cell The Unit of Life
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. The ribosome is granules formed of:
    (A) mRNA and protein
    (B) mRNA and rRNA
    (C) rRNA and protein   <-- CORRECT
    (D) rRNA and tRNA
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A ribosome is a small, dense granular particle comprising usually three or four ribosomal RNA molecules and more than 50 protein molecules, interconnected to form the site of protein synthesis.

Q2. A clear zone around Golgi apparatus is zone of _______.
    (A) Transition
    (B) Exclusion   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Inclusion
    (D) Separation
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The clear zone surrounding the Golgi apparatus is a zone of exclusion, where no other cellular activity takes place.

Q3. Largest organelles in the cell are:
    (A) Golgi bodies
    (B) Lysosomes
    (C) Mitochondria in animal cell and chloroplast in plant cell   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Centrioles in animals and plastids in plant cell
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Mitochondria is the largest cell organelles in animal cell and chloroplast is the largest cell organelles in a plant cell.

Q4. A cell membrane shows fluid behaviour due to:
    (A) Mosaic of lipid and proteins   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Sandwich of protein between lipids layer
    (C) Presence of fluid protein
    (D) Mosaic of fat and glucose
    Answer: A
    Explanation: A cell membrane shows fluid behaviour due to the mosaic of lipid and proteins. Fluid mosaic model of the plasma membrane is the most accepted and recent model.

Q5. The structural element of chromatin is _________.
    (A) Histone
    (B) Amino acids
    (C) Nuclear matrix
    (D) Nucleosome   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Chromatin is the thread-like structure present in the nucleus. Chromatin has beads like structure called nucleosome that contain histone protein and DNA.

Q6. Two cell organelles in plant cell having their own genetic material are called ________.
    (A) Mitochondria and Chloroplast   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Mitochondria and Golgi bodies
    (C) Golgi bodies and lysosomes
    (D) Chloroplast and Golgi bodies
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Genetic material is mainly present in the nucleus of the cell but these two cell organelles also contain their own genetic material.

Q7. Longest cell in human body is ________.
    (A) Mast cells
    (B) Muscle cell
    (C) Nerve cells   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Blood cells
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A nerve cell or neuron is the longest cell in the human body. They are responsible for the transfer of information from one part of the body to the other in form of nerve impulses.

Q8. Smallest free-living organism are:
    (A) Bacteria
    (B) Viroids
    (C) Virus
    (D) PPLOs   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Pleuro Pneumonia Like Organism (PPLO) or mycoplasma is considered as the smallest free-living organism.

Q9. The fluid-filled vacuoles or vesicles which are separated from the cytoplasm by a selectively permeable membrane called ________.
    (A) Hydroplast
    (B) Aquaplast
    (C) Tonoplast   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Symplast
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Tonoplasts are the fluid filled vacuoles or vesicles which are separated from cytoplasm by a selectively permeable membrane. It helps in maintaining turgidity of the cell.

Q10. Which one is present nearest to plasma membrane?
    (A) Primary wall
    (B) Middle lamella
    (C) Secondary wall   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Tonoplast
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Secondary wall is formed inside the primary wall. Secondary wall is present nearest to the plasma membrane of a plant cell.

Q11. Ions connected with forming cross-bridge is______.
    (A) K^+
    (B) Mg^2+
    (C) Ca^2+   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Na^+
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Ions connected with forming cross-bridge is calcium ions (Ca^2+) that help the impulse to cross the gaps at the synapse.

Q12. The joined area between adjacent cells are ________.
    (A) Inter digitations
    (B) Intercellular gap
    (C) Desmosome   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Gap junctions
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A desmosome is a cell structure specialised for the cell to cell adhesion. They are located on lateral sides of plasma membranes.

Q13. Which one is not a difference between Prokaryotic and Eukaryotic cells?
    (A) Presence of cell wall   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Presence of membrane-bounded organelle
    (C) Presence of nuclear membrane
    (D) Number of chromosomes
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Prokaryotic and Eukaryotic cells and differentiated on the basis of the number of chromosomes, presence or absence of nuclear membrane and presence and absence of membrane-bounded organelles. The cell wall is not a difference.

Q14. The inner membrane of mitochondria thrown into folds to form finger-like structure is called ________.
    (A) Matrix
    (B) Cristae   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Amyloplast
    (D) Inter membrane space
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Mitochondria are double membranous structure. The inner membrane of mitochondria thrown into folds to form finger-like structure is called cristae.

Q15. Who first saw and described a live cell?
    (A) R. Virchow
    (B) T. Schwann
    (C) A.V. Leeuwenhoek   <-- CORRECT
    (D) M. Schleiden
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The first man to witness a live cell under a microscope was Anton van Leeuwenhoek, who in 1674 described the algae Spirogyra. Van Leeuwenhoek probably also saw bacteria.

========================================================================
 Biomolecules Test-01  (id 3379) [FREE]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Biomolecules
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. The oils have:
    (A) No melting point
    (B) Optimum melting point
    (C) Low melting point   <-- CORRECT
    (D) High melting point
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Oils have a lower melting point (e.g., gingely oil) and hence remain as oil in winters.

Q2. The diagram represents
    (A) Nucleotide
    (B) Lipids
    (C) Nitrogen base   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Nucleoside
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The diagram shown is a uracil which is a pyramidine belonging to nitrogen bases.

Q3. Arachidonic acid has:
    (A) 20 carbon atoms   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 16 carbon atoms
    (C) 1 carbon atom
    (D) 19 carbon atoms
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Arachidonic acid has 20 carbon atoms including the carboxyl carbon. Molecular formula - C_20H_32O_2.

Q4. Which of the following are aromatic amino acids?
    (A) Lysine, valine
    (B) Alanine, glycine
    (C) Phenylalanine, tryptophan   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Serine, glutamic acid
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Based on the number of amino and carboxyl groups, there are acidic (e.g., glutamic acid), basic (lysine) and neutral (valine) amino acids. Similarly, there are aromatic amino acids (tyrosine, phenylalanine, tryptophan).

Q5. Which one is the neutral amino acid?
    (A) Tryptophan
    (B) Valine   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Lysine
    (D) Tyrosine
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Sidechains that have pure hydrocarbon alkyl groups (alkane branches) or aromatic (benzene rings) are non-polar. Examples include valine, alanine, leucine, isoleucine, phenylalanine.

Q6. Lipids that are found in the cell membrane are:
    (A) Diglycerides
    (B) Phospholipids   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Triglycerides
    (D) Simple lipids
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Some lipids have phosphorous and a phosphorylated organic compound in them. These are phospholipids. They are found in the cell membrane.

Q7. Chitin occurs in the cell wall of _______.
    (A) Yeast
    (B) Bacteria
    (C) Algae
    (D) Fungi   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The cell wall of fungi is made of chitin, complex sugar molecules. The cell wall of plants is made up of cellulose.

Q8. Which of the following is not obtained on hydrolysis of nucleic acid?
    (A) Phosphoric acid   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Purine
    (C) Pyrimidine
    (D) Pentose sugar
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Hydrolysis of nucleic acid (DNA and RNA) produces pentose sugar (ribose or deoxyribose) purine and pyrimidine. Phosphoric acid is not released on hydrolysis of DNA or RNA.

Q9. No cell could live without ______.
    (A) Chloroplast
    (B) Protein
    (C) Phytochrome
    (D) Enzyme   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Enzymes are bio-catalyst. All the metabolic biochemical reactions are carried out with the help of the enzyme. No cell could survive without enzyme.

Q10. The most abundant organic molecule present on earth is______.
    (A) Steroids
    (B) Lipid
    (C) Protein
    (D) Cellulose   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Cellulose is the most abundant organic molecule present on earth. Cellulose forms the cell wall of all plant cells. The cell wall is the outermost protective layer of the cell.

Q11. 98% of a living body is formed of six elements- C, H, N, O and ________.
    (A) Ca and P
    (B) S and Mg
    (C) Mg and Na
    (D) P and S   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Everything in the universe is made up of elements. The body of living organisms contains mainly six elements. These are carbon, hydrogen, oxygen phosphorous, and sulphur. In fact, 98% of the living body is formed on these six elements.

Q12. Element located in the centre of the porphyrin ring of chlorophyll is ______.
    (A) Mg   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Ca
    (C) Mn
    (D) K
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Chlorophyll molecule consists of a porphyrin ring and a long tail like a chain of carbon and hydrogen. The centre of the porphyrin ring is occupied by Mg ions.

Q13. What should be TDS of Ca^++ and Mg^++ in soft water?
    (A) Up to 800 ppm
    (B) Up to 120 ppm   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Up to 200 ppm
    (D) Up to 150 ppm
    Answer: B
    Explanation: TDS stands for total dissolved solids which are inorganic salts dissolved in water. The TDS of soft water should be up to 120 ppm.

Q14. Identify the incorrect pair in the following:
    (A) RNA - Protein synthesis
    (B) Steroids - Sex hormones
    (C) Haemoglobin - Transport of gases
    (D) Glucose - Storage product   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Haemoglobin present in blood transport gases, RNA (tRNA and mRNA) are involved in protein synthesis and steroids are used as sex stimulating chemicals but glucose is not a storage product.

Q15. Most abundant mineral in body fluids are:
    (A) Mg^2+ and I^-
    (B) Na^+ and Mg^2+
    (C) Na^+ and Cl^-   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Ca^2+ and O^2
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Most abundant mineral in body fluids is Na^+ and Cl^- ions. These ions are responsible for the generation of impulses and its transfer through neuron cells.

Biomolecules Test-02  (id 3380) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Biomolecules
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. Which of the following metabolites are incorrect pairs?
    (A) Drugs - Ricin   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Pigments - Carotenoids
    (C) Alkaloids - Morphine
    (D) Essential oils - Lemon grass oil
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Ricin and abrin are toxins.

Q2. Number of fatty acid residues found in one molecule of fat is_____.
    (A) 4
    (B) 1
    (C) 2
    (D) 3   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Fat consists of molecules of fatty acids and molecules of glycerine. Each molecule of fat contains three molecules of fatty acids and one molecule of glycerine.

Q3. In most fungi, the structural polysaccharide of the cell wall is ________.
    (A) Chitin   <-- CORRECT
    (B) All of the these
    (C) Cellulose
    (D) Steroids
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In most fungi the structural polysaccharide of the cell wall is chitin. In the plant cells, the cell wall is made up of cellulose.

Q4. Which of the following nitrogenous base produces nucleoside only with ribose sugar?
    (A) Guanine
    (B) Uracil   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Adenine
    (D) Thymine
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Uracil nitrogenous base is produced nucleoside only with ribose sugar. This nucleoside is present only inside the RNA and absent in DNA.

Q5. The plant cell wall is made up of_______.
    (A) Starch
    (B) Inulin
    (C) Cellulose   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Glycogen Bacteria
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Plant cell walls are made of cellulose. Paper made from plant pulp is cellulose.

Q6. The nucleotide chemical components are:
    (A) Sugar and Phosphate
    (B) Phosphate and heterocyclic compounds
    (C) Heterocyclic compounds, sugar, and phosphate   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Heterocyclic compounds and sugar
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The nucleotide has three chemically distinct components. One is a heterocyclic compound, the second is a monosaccharide and the third a phosphoric acid or phosphate.

Q7. Which of the following carries the hereditary information from parents to progeny?
    (A) Nucleoside
    (B) Proteins
    (C) Nucleic acids   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Nucleotides
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Nucleic acids carry hereditary information and are passed on from parental generation to progeny.

Q8. Identify the correct pairing between nitrogen bases in DNA.
    (A) G+C/A+T   <-- CORRECT
    (B) A+G/C+T
    (C) T+C/G+A
    (D) A+C/T+G
    Answer: A
    Explanation: There are two hydrogen bonds between A and T pairing. There are three hydrogen bonds between G and C pairing. Each strand appears like a helical staircase.

Q9. A polysaccharide present as a storehouse of the energy of plant tissues:
    (A) Chitin
    (B) Hemi cellulose
    (C) Starch   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Cellulose
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Starch is a variant of this but present as a storehouse of energy in plant tissues.

Q10. Which is the most abundant chemical for the living organisms?
    (A) Water   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Lipids
    (C) Ions
    (D) Proteins
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Water is the most abundant chemical for living organisms. In adult men, about 60% of their bodies are water.

Q11. Which of the following statements are not correct?
    (A) The purines and pyrimidines are paired with hydrogen bonds.
    (B) The nucleic acid consists of ribose.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) The backbone is formed by sugar-phosphate molecule.
    (D) In DNA two strands are run in the opposite direction.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: A nucleic acid containing deoxyribose is called deoxyribonucleic acid (DNA) while that which contains ribose is called ribonucleic acid (RNA).

Q12. The nucleic acids that behave like enzymes are called as:
    (A) Lysases
    (B) Ligases
    (C) Ribozymes   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Isomerases
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Almost all enzymes are proteins. There are some nucleic acids that behave like enzymes. These are called ribozymes.

Q13. Nucleic acids are serve as:
    (A) Building blocks of cell
    (B) Energy
    (C) Cellular functions
    (D) Genetic material   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Nucleic acids carry hereditary information and are passed on from parental generation to progeny.

Q14. The exoskeleton of arthropods have ______.
    (A) Fructose
    (B) Gluctose
    (C) Cellulose
    (D) Chitin   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Exoskeletons of arthropods have a complex polysaccharide called chitin. These complex polysaccharides are heteropolymers.

Q15. DNA differs from RNA in having:
    (A) Guanine
    (B) Thymine   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Uracil
    (D) Adenine
    Answer: B
    Explanation: DNA differs from RNA in having Thymine. Thymine is absent in RNA. RNA contains uracil in place of thymine.

Biomolecules Test-03  (id 3381) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Biomolecules
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. Double helix model of DNA was proposed by proposed by:
    (A) Holley and Nirenberg
    (B) Watson and Crick   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Kornberg
    (D) Nirenberg
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Double helix model of DNA was proposed by James Watson and Francis Crick in 1953 based on X-ray diffraction data produced by Maurice Wilkins and Rosalind Franklin.

Q2. Length of DNA with 23 base pairs is ________.
    (A) 74.8 A^o
    (B) 78.4 A^o
    (C) 78.2 A^o   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 78 A^o
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The distance between two base pairs in DNA is 3.4 A^o. The length of DNA with 23 base pairs is 23 $\times$ 3.4 = 78.2 A^o.

Q3. DNA and RNA resemble each other in possessing:
    (A) Similar pyrimidines bases
    (B) Ability to replicate
    (C) Similar sugar
    (D) Polymers of nucleotides   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Both DNA and RNA consists of polymers of nucleotides. RNA is single-stranded but DNA is double-stranded. DNA polynucleotide contains thymine but RNA polynucleotide contains uracil.

Q4. Base pairs found in 5 turns of DNA spirals are _______.
    (A) 100
    (B) 10
    (C) 50   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 20
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Each turn of DNA spirals contains 10 base pairs. So, in five turns of DNA total number of Base pair is 5 $\times$ 10 = 50 base pairs.

Q5. The molecular formula of haemoglobin is:
    (A) C_3032H_564O_542N_785S_8Fe_4
    (B) C_3242H_132O_943N_795S_6Fe_2
    (C) C_3032H_872O_872N_780S_8Fe_4   <-- CORRECT
    (D) C_3032H_168O_872N_745S_6Fe_2
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Haemoglobin is responsible for carrying oxygen. The molecular formula of haemoglobin is C_3032H_872O_872N_780S_8Fe_4.

Q6. Plants can synthesis all types of fatty acids but animals lack the machinery to synthesis three fatty acids called essential fatty acids. They are:
    (A) Linoleic, Tartaric, and Oleic acids
    (B) Linoleic, Linolenic, and Arachidonic acids   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Palmitic, Tartaric and Linoleic
    (D) Linolenic, Palmitic, and Arachidonic acids
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Plants can synthesis all types of fatty acids but animal cells lack the machinery to synthesis three fatty acids called essential fatty acids. These are Linoleic, Linolenic, and Arachidonic acids.

Q7. Proteins are polymerization product of:
    (A) Muramic acid
    (B) Monosaccharide
    (C) Amino acids   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Glucose
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The polymerisation is the chain of a large number of repeating units. Proteins are polymerization product of Amino acids combine together with peptide bonds.

Q8. Which one of the following is fibrous protein?
    (A) Hemicellulose
    (B) Collagen   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Ribozymes
    (D) Haemoglobin
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Collagen is a fibrous protein. It is the main structural protein in the extracellular space in the various connective tissues. It is the most abundant protein in mammals.

Q9. The number of amino acids found in proteins is _____.
    (A) 22
    (B) 18
    (C) 20   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 16
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Proteins are made up of amino acids, which are organic compounds that combine to form the building blocks of proteins. There are 20 standard amino acids that are encoded by the universal genetic code and found in proteins. These include essential amino acids that must be obtained through the diet and non-essential amino acids that can be synthesized by the body.
Although there are some other amino acids like selenocysteine (sometimes referred to as the 21st amino acid) and pyrrolysine, these are not universally found in all proteins and are encoded by specific rare genetic mechanisms.

Q10. Proteins are made up of___________.
    (A) Heteropolymers   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Nucleosides
    (C) Monomers
    (D) Homopolymers
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Proteins are made of building blocks which are different. Proteins are heteropolymers made of amino acids.

Q11. The most abundant protein present in the whole of the biosphere is:
    (A) RUBISCO   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Collagen
    (C) Fatty acid
    (D) Cellulose
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Ribulose bisphosphate Carboxylase-Oxygenase (RUBISCO) is the most abundant protein in the whole of the biosphere.

Q12. The long protein chain is folded upon itself like hollow woollen ball are called as:
    (A) Quaternary structure
    (B) Primary structure
    (C) Secondary structure
    (D) Tertiary structure   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Tertiary structure: Long protein chain is folded upon itself like a hollow woolen ball. Gives a 3-dimensional view of protein, e.g., myosin.

Q13. Dietary proteins are otherwise called as:
    (A) Non-essential aminoacids
    (B) Essential aminoacids   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Aromatic aminoacids
    (D) Alpha aminoacids
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Dietary proteins are the source of essential amino acids. Therefore, amino acids can be essential or non-essential. The latter are those which our body can make, while we get essential amino acids through our diet.

Q14. Proteins carry out many functions in living organisms such as:
    (A) Fight against infectious organisms   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Role in catalytic activity of the enzyme
    (C) Storehouse of energy
    (D) Genetic material
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Proteins are molecules made of amino acids. They also play a central role in biological processes. For example, transport molecules such as oxygen, keep us healthy as part of the immune system and transmit messages from cell to cell.

Q15. Which helps in transporting glucose into cells?
    (A) Trypsin
    (B) Insulin
    (C) Receptornucleicacids
    (D) GLUT-4   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Glut-4 enables glucose transport into cells.

Biomolecules Test-04  (id 3382) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Biomolecules
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. How many subunits are there in human adult haemoglobin?
    (A) 2
    (B) 3
    (C) 4   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 5
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Proteins human haemoglobin consists of 4 subunits. Two of these are identical to each other. Hence, two subunits of $\alpha $ type and two subunits of $\beta $ type together constitute the human haemoglobin (Hb).

Q2. The following ratio is generally constant for a given species:
    (A) A+C/T+G
    (B) A+G/C+T
    (C) G+C/A+T   <-- CORRECT
    (D) T+C/G+A
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The ratio of the sum of guanine and cytosine to the sum of adenine and thymine is always constant for a species. This is due to the formation of hydrogen bonds between purine and pyrimidine.

Q3. Which one is not a denaturing factor for protein?
    (A) High temperature
    (B) Drastic change in pH
    (C) High pressure   <-- CORRECT
    (D) High energy radiation
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Protein molecules get denatured due to high temperature, very high or low pH, and high energy radiation but there is no effect due to high pressure.

Q4. Which one is an initiation codon for protein synthesis?
    (A) AUG   <-- CORRECT
    (B) UGA
    (C) UAA
    (D) UAG
    Answer: A
    Explanation: AUG codon is an initiation codon for protein synthesis. This codon code for amino acids methionine.

Q5. One full turn of DNA strands involves:
    (A) Ten base pairs   <-- CORRECT
    (B) One base pair
    (C) Two base pairs
    (D) Three base pairs
    Answer: A
    Explanation: One full turn of the helical strand would involve ten steps or ten base pairs. The pitch would be 34$\mathop {\text{A}}\limits^{\text{o}} $.

Q6. The formation of both peptide and glycosidic bonds involves:
    (A) Hydration
    (B) Esterification
    (C) Dehydration   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Acidification
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In a polypeptide or a protein, amino acids are linked by a peptide bond which is formed when the carboxyl (-COOH) group of one amino acid reacts with the amino (-NH_2) group of the next amino acid with the elimination of a water moiety (the process is called dehydration). In polysaccharide, the individual monosaccharides are linked by a glycosidic bond. This bond is also formed by dehydration.

Q7. Secondary plant products are of great use in commerce in making:
    (A) colours and furniture
    (B) Poisons and furniture
    (C) Paints and colours
    (D) Drugs and perfumes   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Many secondary plant products are of great use in commerce in making drug and perfumes. The primary product of plants is carbohydrates synthesized during photosynthesis.

Q8. Fevicol is a synthetic sticky substance insoluble in water. It is a type of ______.
    (A) Polysaccharides
    (B) Steroids
    (C) Resins   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Cellulose
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Fevicol is a synthetic sticky substance insoluble in water and used for joining wood and paper is a type of resins.

Q9. The amino acids are linked together serially by:
    (A) Hydrogen bonds
    (B) Peptide bonds   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Ionic bonds
    (D) Covalent bonds
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The amino acids are linked together one after the other by peptide bonds. This bond is formed between NH_3 of one amino acid with a carboxyl end of another amino acid to release water.

Q10. The energy currency of the cell is______.
    (A) ADP
    (B) GDP
    (C) NAD
    (D) ATP   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The most important form of energy currency in living systems is the bond energy in a chemical called ATP.

Q11. Blood concentration of glucose in a normal healthy individual is:
    (A) 2 - 4.0 mM
    (B) 1 - 4.5 mM
    (C) 3 - 5.0 mM
    (D) 4.5 - 5.0 mM   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The blood concentration of glucose in a normal healthy individual is 4.5-5.0 mM.

Q12. The chemical compounds undergo changes in shape without the breakdown of bonds are called as:
    (A) Inorganic chemical process
    (B) Chemical process
    (C) Biological process
    (D) Physical process   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Chemical compounds undergo two types of changes. A physical change simply refers to a change in shape without breaking of bonds. This is a physical process.

Q13. ATP is______.
    (A) Nucleoside
    (B) Nuleosome
    (C) Purine base
    (D) Nucleotide   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Adenosine triphosphate (ATP) is a nucleotide. A nucleotide is formed by pentose sugar, nitrogenous base and phosphates. Many nucleotides join together to form polynucleotide.

Q14. What name is given to that part of the enzyme where catalytic work is carried out?
    (A) Pro-active site
    (B) Reactive site
    (C) Enzymatic site
    (D) Active site   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Enzymes are bio-catalyst that alter the rate of biochemical reactions in living organisms. The part of the enzyme where catalytic work is carried out is called the active site.

Q15. Given graph shows the effect of substrate concentration on the rate of reaction of enzyme phosphatase. What does given graph indicate?
    (A) Presence of an enzyme inhibitor   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Formation of E-S complex
    (C) At high substrate concentration pH changes
    (D) Rate is proportional to substrate concentration
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The graph showed above shows effects of substrate concentration on rate of reaction of enzyme phosphate. Usually rate of reaction increases with increase in concentration but presence of enzyme inhibitors decrease the velocity.

Biomolecules Test-05  (id 3383) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Biomolecules
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. The number of substrate molecules changed per minute by a molecule of the enzyme is called:
    (A) Final number
    (B) Formation number
    (C) Turn over number   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Enzyme reaction number
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The number of substrate molecules changed per minute by a molecule of the enzyme is called turn over number. Higher the turn over number more effective is the enzyme.

Q2. Monoterpene esters called pyrethroids found in flowers and leaves of chrysanthemum are used commercially for making ______.
    (A) Perfumes
    (B) Insecticides   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Drugs
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Monoterpene eaters called pyrethroids found in flowers and leaves of chrysanthemum are used commercially for making insecticides.

Q3. The inhibition of enzyme activity by the presence of a chemical that competes with the substrate for binding to the active site of the enzyme is called:
    (A) None-competitive inhibitor
    (B) Irreversible inhibition
    (C) Reversible inhibition
    (D) Substrate analogue   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The inhibition of enzyme activity by the presence of a chemical that competes with the substrate for binding to the active site of the enzyme is called substrate analogue.

Q4. Select the group of fat-soluble vitamins from the followings:
    (A) Vitamins B, C, D and K
    (B) Vitamins A, D, E, and K   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Vitamins B, C and E
    (D) Vitamins A, B, C and D
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Vitamins A, D, E, and K are fat-soluble but insoluble in water. Vitamin B and C are water-soluble vitamins.

Q5. Enzymes functional inside the living cells are called:
    (A) Coenzymes
    (B) Endoenzymes   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Holoezymes
    (D) Exoenzymes
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Enzymes functional inside the living cells are called endoenzyme or intracellular enzyme. It functions only inside the cell in which it was produced.

Q6. Polysaccharide does not metabolise in the human body and used for kidney function is________.
    (A) Inulin   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Chitin
    (C) Fructose
    (D) Gluctose
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Inulin is a starchy substance found in a wide variety of fruits, vegetables and other herbs. This polysaccharide is not metabolized in the human body and used for kidney function.

Q7. Metal ions required for the functioning of the enzyme is _______.
    (A) Holoenzyme
    (B) Co-enzyme
    (C) Co-factor   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Prosthetic group
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A number of enzymes require metal ions for their activity which form coordination bonds with side chains at the active site and at the same time form one or more coordination bonds with the substrate, e.g., zinc is a cofactor for the proteolytic enzyme carboxypeptidase.

Q8. Which one is the cofactor for the proteolytic enzyme carboxypeptidase?
    (A) Mercury
    (B) Magnesium
    (C) Copper
    (D) Zinc   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Zinc is a cofactor for the pro­teolytic enzyme carboxypeptidase and forms coordina­tion bonds with the side chains of two histidines and one glutamic acid residue at the active site. A fourth bond is formed between zinc and the a-carboxyl group of the substrate amino acids, and it is here that the cleavage of the peptide occurs.

Q9. The enzymes show high activity at:
    (A) Freezing temperature
    (B) High temperature
    (C) Low temperature
    (D) Optimum temperature   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Each enzyme shows its highest activity at a particular temperature and pH called the optimum temperature and optimum pH.

Q10. In yeast, during fermentation, the glycolysis pathway leads to:
    (A) Production of pyruvic acid
    (B) Production of oxygen
    (C) Production of glucose
    (D) Production of ethanol   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Yeast cells obtain energy under anaerobic conditions using a very similar process called alcoholic fermentation. Glycolysis is the chemical breakdown of glucose to lactic acid. Alcoholic fermentation is identical to glycolysis except for the final step. In alcoholic fermentation, pyruvic acid is broken down into ethanol and carbon dioxide.

Q11. Enzymes catalyzing in the link together of two compounds are ________.
    (A) Lyases
    (B) Isomerases
    (C) Hydrolases
    (D) Ligases   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Ligases catalyze the linking together of 2 compounds, e.g., enzymes that catalyze joining of C-O, C-S, C-N, P-O, etc. bonds.

Q12. The protein portion of an enzyme is called:
    (A) Prosthetic group
    (B) Cofactors
    (C) Apoenzyme   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Co-enzyme
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Apoenzyme: The polypeptide or protein part of the enzyme is called the apoenzyme and may be inactive in its original synthesized structure. The inactive form of the apoenzyme is known as a proenzyme or zymogen.

Q13. Nicotinamide can be synthesized in the human body from _______.
    (A) Fructose
    (B) Tryptophan   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Lactose
    (D) Tyrosine
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Tryptophan is an amino acid needed for normal growth in infants and for nitrogen balance in adults. Nicotinamide can be synthesized in the human body from tryptophan.

Q14. An important site for the formation of glycoproteins and glycolipids is:
    (A) Golgi apparatus   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Plastids
    (C) Vacuoles
    (D) Lysosomes
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Synthesis of glycoproteins and glycolipids take place in Golgi apparatus inside the cell. Golgi apparatus is located near the nucleus of the cell.

Q15. Most abundant mineral in body fluids are:
    (A) Na^+ and Cl^-   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Ca^2+ and O^2
    (C) Mg^2+ and I^-
    (D) Na^+ and Mg^2+
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Most abundant mineral in body fluids is Na^+ and Cl^- ions. These ions are responsible for the generation of impulses and its transfer through neuron cells.

# Cell Cycle and Cell Division  (5 tests)

========================================================================
Cell Cycle And Cell Division Test-01  (id 3384) [FREE]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Cell Cycle and Cell Division
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. Plants show mitotic divisions in ________.
    (A) Diploid cells
    (B) Haploid cells
    (C) Haploid cells and diploid cells   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Somatic cells
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The plants can show mitotic divisions in both haploid and diploid cells due to the alternation of generations in the life cycle.

Q2. What is the average cell cycle span for a mammalian cell?
    (A) 48 hours
    (B) 4 hours
    (C) 12 hours
    (D) 24 hours   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: All the phases of the cell cycle in the mammalian cell are completed in 24 hours.

Q3. The number of chromosomes and the amount of DNA are changed in:
    (A) Anaphase and S phase   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Interphase and S phase
    (C) Dilution and D phase
    (D) Metaphase and M phase
    Answer: A
    Explanation: S phase marks the period during which DNA synthesis or replication takes place. During this time the amount of DNA per cell doubles. If the initial amount of DNA is denoted as 2C then it increases to 4C and even in anaphase, the chromosome numbers are changed.

Q4. In yeast, the cell cycle is progressed through:
    (A) 60 minutes
    (B) 90 minutes   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 20 minutes
    (D) 30 minutes
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Yeast can progress through the cell cycle in only about 90 minutes due to its simple organisation.

Q5. M phase represents:
    (A) Mitosis phase   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Metaphase
    (C) Meiosis I phase
    (D) Meiosis phase
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The M Phase represents the phase when the actual cell division or mitosis occurs/starts during the cell cycle.

Q6. How many chromosomes are present in each cell of onion root tip?
    (A) 3 chromosomes
    (B) 4 chromosomes
    (C) 2 chromosomes
    (D) 16 chromosomes   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Onion root tip cells have 16 chromosomes in each cell, the same as the number of chromosomes in somatic cells.

Q7. In animal cells, during G2 phase:
    (A) DNA are synthesized
    (B) Spindle fibres are formed
    (C) Middle lamellae are formed
    (D) Proteins are synthesized   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: During the G2 phase, proteins and RNA are synthesised in preparation for mitosis while cell growth continues.

Q8. The resting phase is otherwise called as______.
    (A) Metaphase
    (B) Telophase
    (C) Interphase   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Prophase
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The interphase though called the resting phase is the time during which the cell is preparing for division by undergoing cell growth in an orderly manner. No divisional activities occur during this phase. Hence the name.

Q9. In animal cells, the mitotic division is seen in:
    (A) Haploid somatic cells
    (B) Diploid somatic cells   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Haploid cells
    (D) Diploid cells
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In animals, mitotic cell division is only seen in the diploid somatic cell since mitosis produces cells with the same number of chromosomes as that of parents.

Q10. In which stage, the cells remain metabolically active but do not proliferate?
    (A) S-phase
    (B) G2-phase
    (C) G_o-phase   <-- CORRECT
    (D) G1-phase
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In the G_o stage, the cells are in a metabolically active state but do not divide unless there are some abnormal genes which reverse the same. This stage is also called the quiescent stage. Examples of human nerve cells.

Q11. S phase marks:
    (A) Chromosome condensation
    (B) DNA replication and chromosome duplication   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Cytoplasmic growth
    (D) It carries out normal metabolism
    Answer: B
    Explanation: S phase marks the phase of DNA replication and chromosome duplication. In this phase increase in the amount of DNA takes place. No synthesis of proteins or RNA takes place.

Q12. Which step proceeds reformation of the nuclear envelope during M-phase of the cell cycle?
 Decondenstion of chromosomes with the appearance of the nuclear lamina
 Transcription from chromosomes and reassemble of the nuclear lamina
 Formation of contractile ring and phragmoplast
 Formation of contractile ring and transcription
    (A) (A)   <-- CORRECT
    (B) (D)
    (C) (B)
    (D) (C)
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Before the completion of Mitosis reappearance of the nuclear membrane takes place along with the formation of nucleolus so that the cells become separate entities after cytokinesis but having the same chromosome number as parent cells.

Q13. The stage of inactivation of cell cycle due to non-availability of mitogens and energy-rich compounds is called:
    (A) S-phase
    (B) Interphase
    (C) M-phase
    (D) Quiescent phase   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: It is the stage of the cell cycle during which the cells remain metabolically active and do not divide due to the absence of mitogens and energy-producing compounds.

Q14. Karyokinesis is the:
    (A) Division of chromosome   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Equational division
    (C) Mitosis division
    (D) Division of cytoplasm
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Cell division consists of karyokinesis and cytokinesis. During karyokinesis division of chromosomes takes place and during cytokinesis division of cytoplasm takes place. Ultimately the cell divides into two halves.

Q15. Each chromosome consists of ________ chromatid.
    (A) two   <-- CORRECT
    (B) eight
    (C) four
    (D) one
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The resulting two identical copies of DNA are connected to each other at the centromere. Each copy is called a chromatid. A chromosome, before cell division is formed of one chromatid while it is formed of two chromatids after cell division.

Cell Cycle And Cell Division Test-02  (id 3385) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Cell Cycle and Cell Division
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. Plant Cytokinesis differ from animals Cytokinesis in having ______.
    (A) Macrofilament
    (B) Midbody
    (C) Microfilament
    (D) Cell plate   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In plants, cytokinesis or division of cytoplasm occurs due to cell plate formed out of deposition of materials along the equatorial region of the cell but in animals, cytokinesis occurs due to the formation of the cleavage furrow in the middle cell membrane.

Q2. Various phases of the cell cycle are controlled by proteins:
    (A) Hormones and CDKs
    (B) Cytokines and Cyclins
    (C) Cyclins and CDKs   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Cycline and CDKs can modify various protein substrates involved in cell cycle progression. Cancer results due to mutations of these proteins leading to uncontrolled cell divisions.

Q3. Which phase of M-stage is called as an invisible phase?
    (A) S-phase   <-- CORRECT
    (B) G0-phase
    (C) G1-phase
    (D) G2-phase
    Answer: A
    Explanation: S-phase of M-stage is called an invisible phase of cell cycle because during this phase synthesis of DNA takes place which is not visible to the naked eye. There is an only imbalance of the Nucleoplasmic ratio.

Q4. The multinucleate condition arises when Cytokinesis does not follow karyokinesis, this type of cell is called as _____.
    (A) Prototype
    (B) Holotype
    (C) Uninuleate
    (D) Coenocytes   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Karyokinesis is followed by cytokinesis but some times cytokinesis is not followed by karyokinesis which leads to the establishment of multinucleate condition. This type of cells is called as coenocytes.

Q5. The mechanism of distributing centriole pairs to the daughter cells is called:
    (A) Haplontic division
    (B) Equational division
    (C) Reductional division
    (D) Astral division   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The mechanism of distributing chromosomes to the daughter cells is called astral division. This kind of division occurs in animal cells.

Q6. Dinoflagellates possess condensed chromosomes even in interphase, their nucleus is called:
    (A) Cytokaryone
    (B) Polykaryone
    (C) Mesokaryon   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Heterokaryon
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Dinoflagellates are unicellular protists. They possess condensed chromosomes even during interphase. Their nucleus is called as mesokaryon.

Q7. Division of nucleus without being followed by cytokinesis results into:
    (A) Multinucleate condition   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Phargmoplast
    (C) Polyploidy
    (D) Uninucleate condition
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The division of nucleus or karyokinesis without being followed by cytokinesis results in an increase in the content of the nucleus, a condition known as a multinucleate condition.

Q8. Which of the following phases in mitosis is in the correct order?
    (A) Anaphase, telophase, metaphase, prophase
    (B) Prophase, metaphase, anaphase, telophase   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Prophase, telophase, metaphase, anaphase
    (D) Metaphase, prophase, anaphase, telophase
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Mitosis. A four-stage process that creates two identical cells from one original cell.
 Prophase. The first and longest stage of mitosis.
 Metaphase. The second stage of mitosis.
 Anaphase. The third stage of mitosis.
 Telophase. The fourth and last stage of mitosis.

Q9. In the metaphase stage, the chromosomes are made up of:
    (A) Two non-sister chromatids
    (B) Two sister chromatids   <-- CORRECT
    (C) One sister and two non-sister chromatids
    (D) One sister chromatid
    Answer: B
    Explanation: At the metaphase stage, the chromosome is made up of two sister chromatids formed due to longitudinal splitting of the chromatids, which are held together by the centromere.

Q10. The nuclear structures disappear during ______.
    (A) Telophase
    (B) Anaphase
    (C) Metaphase
    (D) Prophase   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Prophase

Q11. During zygotene, stage chromosomes start pairing together and the process is called:
    (A) Crossing over
    (B) Recombination
    (C) Fertilisation
    (D) Synapsis   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: During the zygotene stage, the homologous chromosomes start pairing together and this process of association is called synapsis. The paired homologous chromosomes are called bivalents.

Q12. The complex formed by a pair of synapsed homologous chromosomes is called :
    (A) Haploid
    (B) Diploid
    (C) bivalent.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Chaismata
    Answer: C
    Explanation: During zygotene stage chromosomes start pairing together and this process of association is called synapsis. Such paired chromosomes are called homologous chromosomes. Electron micrographs of this stage indicate that chromosome synapsis is accompanied by the formation of complex structure called synaptonemal complex. The complex formed by a pair of synapsed homologous chromosomes is called a bivalent or a tetrad.

Q13. At the end of meiosis II, how many cells are formed?
    (A) Four haploid cells   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Four diploid cells
    (C) Two haploid cells
    (D) Two diploid cells
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Four haploid cells are formed at the end of meiosis II. It is the reductional division resulting in a halving of chromosome number in daughter cells.

Q14. The plane of alignment of the chromosome at metaphase is referred to as:
    (A) Metaphase/Metaphasic plate   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Cell plate
    (C) Cytokinesis
    (D) Kinetochore
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The plane of alignment of the chromosomes at metaphase is referred to as the metaphase plate. This stage is also called a tetrad stage.

Q15. In which stage of mitosis, the number and shape of the chromosome can be observed?
    (A) Prophase
    (B) Telophase
    (C) Metaphase   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Anaphase
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The metaphase is characterized by all the chromosomes coming to lie at the equator with one chromatid of each chromosome connected by its kinetochore to spindle fibres from one pole and its sister chromatid connected by its kinetochore to spindle fibres from the opposite pole.

Cell Cycle And Cell Division Test-03  (id 3386) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Cell Cycle and Cell Division
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. Cell growth results in disturbing the ratio between:
    (A) Cytoplasm-chromosome ratio
    (B) Nucleo-cytoplasmic ratio   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Nucleus - chromosome ratio
    (D) Cytoplasm-spindle fibre ratio
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Cell growth results in disturbing the ratio between the nucleus and the cytoplasm. It, therefore, becomes essential for the cell to divide to restore the nucleo-cytoplasmic ratio. The cell becomes stable when the N/C ratio is 1.

Q2. In some lower plants and social insects, the haploid cells are divide by _______.
    (A) Meiosis
    (B) Cytokinesis
    (C) Mitosis   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Karyokinesis
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Mitosis is called equational division. Since the parent cells are haploid so mitosis will lead to the restoration of chromosome number in haploid cells.

Q3. M - phase undergoes:
    (A) Cytokinesis
    (B) Equational division   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Reductional division
    (D) Diakinesis
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Since in mitosis the number of chromosomes in the parent and progeny cells is the same, it is also called an equational division.

Q4. In plant cells, the new cell wall begins by the:
    (A) Centromere
    (B) Chromatid
    (C) Cell cycle
    (D) Cell plate   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In-plant cells, wall formation starts in the centre of the cell and grows outward to meet the existing lateral walls. The formation of the new cell wall begins with the formation of a simple precursor, called the cell plate which hardens to give rise to the middle lamella.

Q5. In between, two walls of adjacent cells are seen:
    (A) Cytoplasm
    (B) Middle lamellae   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Plasma membrane
    (D) Cell wall
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The middle lamella cements the tertiary walls of two adjacent plant cells. It is formed out of materials of the cell plate.

Q6. Astral body is formed of________.
    (A) Microfilaments
    (B) Microvilli
    (C) Intermediate filaments
    (D) Microtubules   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The astral body is formed of microtubules. Astral bodies are produced by centriolar division prior to the start off during cell division and attach with the centromere of the chromosome during.

Q7. Plant mitosis is generally controlled by_______.
    (A) Genetic make-up
    (B) Cytokinins   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Auxin
    (D) Cytochrome
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In the plant cell, mitosis cell division is generally controlled by cytokinin hormone. It increases the rate of cell division leading to increased cell production. Auxin is also required for cell division in the plant.

Q8. During mitosis ER and nucleolus begin to disappear at:
    (A) Early metaphase
    (B) Late prophase   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Late metaphase
    (D) Early prophase
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Late prophase

Q9. In animal cells, Cytokinesis takes place by furrow deepening centripetally and formation of two daughter cells. This method is known as:
    (A) Cleavage Cytokinesis   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Phragmoplast
    (C) Cell plate formation
    (D) klinokinesis
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In animal cell, cytokinesis takes place by furrow which appears at the margins of the plasma membrane and gradually deepens towards the central part of the cell. Ultimately the furrow divides the cell into two halves. This method of cytokinesis is known as cleavage cytokinesis.

Q10. An alkaloid widely used in plant breeding for doubling the chromosome number also known as mitotic poison is ______.
    (A) Nicotinamide
    (B) Alcidine
    (C) Auxine
    (D) Colchicine   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Colchicine is an alkaloid used in plant breeding for doubling of chromosomes by inhibiting cytokinesis. It is also called as mitotic poison. It is extracted from the bark of plant belonging to the genus Colchicum.

Q11. The material used for the study of mitotic cell division in the classroom is:
    (A) Onion and broad bean root tips   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Testes of grasshopper
    (C) Young anthers from unopened of onion
    (D) All of these
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The most common material used for the study of mitosis cell division in the classroom is onion root and broad bean root tip. They can be grown quickly and in all seasons. Also, they are easier to handle with and divisional stages are completed quickly.

Q12. A grown-up cell divides when the maximum size is attained and which disturb the ________.
    (A) Chromosome-cytoplasm ratio
    (B) Enzyme-Hormone ratio
    (C) Chromosome-Hormone ratio
    (D) Kern-plasma ratio   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: A disturbance in the nucleoplasmic ratio will cause the cell to divide and attain stable ration which is 1. If it is less or more than 1 the cell becomes unstable and divides again.

Q13. Which type of cell division helps in regeneration?
    (A) Meiotic
    (B) Amitosis
    (C) Mitosis   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Meiosis
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Regeneration is the ability of an organism to regain its lost body parts. Regeneration is achieved by mitotic cell division to maintain the same number of chromosomes in the cell.

Q14. In meiosis:
    (A) Second division is reductional
    (B) First division is reductional   <-- CORRECT
    (C) First division is equational
    (D) Second division is equational
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Meiosis cell division consists of two phases. The first phase is called meiosis I during which the number of chromosomes reduces to half the number in parent cells. In meiosis II chromosome number remain the same.

Q15. The stage connecting meiosis I and meiosis II is __________.
    (A) Anaphase I
    (B) Interphase I
    (C) Interphase II
    (D) Interkinesis   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Interkinesis is the stage connecting meiosis I and meiosis II cell division. It is a brief period between two stages. No DNA synthesis occurs during this period. The cell undergoes preparation for the next divisional stages.

Cell Cycle And Cell Division Test-04  (id 3387) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Cell Cycle and Cell Division
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. Chromosome appeared beaded during ______.
    (A) Diakinesis
    (B) Leptotene   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Diplotene
    (D) Panchytene
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Chromosome appeared beaded during leptotene stage of the prophase of meiosis I due to the distinct appearance of nucleosomes. Chromatin materials start condensing after that stage.

Q2. Which stage is marked by terminalization of chiasmata?
    (A) Zygotene
    (B) Diplotene
    (C) Panchytene
    (D) Diakinesis   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Chiasmata is formed due to crossing over. During diakinesis of prophase, I of meiosis terminalization of chiasmata takes place which indicates the end of crossing over and separation of the non-sister chromatids.

Q3. Which phase of meiosis in an animal cell is shown in the figure given below?
    (A) Diakinesis   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Leptotene
    (C) Interphase
    (D) Zygotene
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In the diakinesis phase of prophase of meiosis, I terminalisation of chismata takes place which is visualized in the picture.

Q4. Crossing over results in an exchange of genetic material, which occurs between:
    (A) Bivalents
    (B) Non-homologous chromosome
    (C) Homologous chromosomes   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Sister chromatids
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Crossing over is the exchange of genetic material between non-sister chromatids of two homologous chromosomes involved in the pairing process.

Q5. Sexual reproduction involves the fusion of special types of cells called gametes, produced by ______.
    (A) Equational division
    (B) Mitosis
    (C) Meiosis   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Amitosis
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Meiosis cell division is involved in gametes formation as gametes contain half the number of chromosomes that a normal cell diploid cell contains. Gametes fuse to produce a diploid zygote.

Q6. Small disc-like structures that occur in the centromere are________.
    (A) Microtubules
    (B) Centriole
    (C) Kinetochore   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Nucleolus
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Small disc-shaped structures at the surface of the centromeres are called kinetochores. These structures serve as the sites of attachment of spindle fibres (formed by the spindle fibres) to the chromosomes.

Q7. Arrange the order of events taking place in anaphase II stage of meiosis:
 Metaphase plate splits
 Each chromosome moves away from equatorial plane
 Centromeres split and chromatids separate
 Chromatids move to opposite poles
    (A) C, A, D, B
    (B) B, D, A, C
    (C) D, C, B, A
    (D) A, B, C, D   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: During anaphase stage, metaphase plate splits and each chromosome moves away from equatorial plane splitting the centromere and separate chromatids which move to opposite poles.

Q8. Which one is not a significance of meiotic cell division?
    (A) Number of chromosomes remain same   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Formation of spores and gametes
    (C) Number of chromosome reduced to half
    (D) New recombination of genes
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Meiosis cell division results in halving of chromosome number in daughter cells, recombination of genes and formation of spores and gametes.

Q9. In telophase I, which of the following event takes place?
 Reappearance of nuclear membrane and nucleolus.
 Nuclear membrane disappears.
 Nuclear membrane and nucleolus disappear.
 Nucleolus disappears.
    (A) (C)
    (B) (B)
    (C) (A)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (D)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In telophase I, the nuclear membrane and nucleolus reappear indicating the process of completion of nuclear division. Meiosis II is similar to mitosis.

Q10. Synapsis occurs between:
    (A) Spindle fibres and centromeres
    (B) Ribosome and m-RNA
    (C) Two homologous chromosomes   <-- CORRECT
    (D) A male and female gametes
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Synapsis occurs between two homologous chromosome during zygotene phase of prophase of meiosis I due to presence of a synaptonemal complex between homologous chromosomes.

Q11. Diplotene stage can last for months or years. Dinoflagellates possess condensed chromosomes even in interphase, their nucleus is called_______.
    (A) Cytokaryon
    (B) Mesokaryon   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Heterokaryon
    (D) Polykaryon
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In oocytes of some vertebrates, diplotene can last for months or years. Such a nucleus showing arrested diplotene stage is called mesokaryotic nucleus.

Q12. Inter kinesis is followed by which type of cell division that helps in regeneration?
    (A) Prophase II Mitosis   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Prophase I Meiosis
    (C) Meiotic Mitosis
    (D) Amitosis Meiosis
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The stage between the two meiotic divisions is called interkinesis and is generally short-lived. Interkinesis is followed by prophase II, much simpler prophase than prophase I.

Q13. Crossing over occurs during
    (A) Zygotene
    (B) Pachytene   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Leptotene
    (D) Diplotene
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Crossing over is the exchange of chromosomes segments between non-sister chromatids of homologous pair. It brings about gene recombination and produces genetic variation. Pachytene is the third stage of the prophase of meiosis during which the homologous chromosomes become short and thick and divide into four distinct chromatids.

Q14. A cell divides every minute. It will fill a 100 ml beaker in one hour. How much time would it take to fill 50 ml beaker?
    (A) 30 minutes
    (B) 15 minutes
    (C) 58 minutes
    (D) 59 minutes   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: If a cell divides every minute, the number of cells gets doubled at the end of each minute. If a 100 ml beaker is filled in one hour, it will take 59 minutes to fill a 50 ml beaker.

Q15. A plant X has 2n = 8 chromosomes, how many chromosomes are present in daughter cells after meiosis II.
    (A) 8 chromosomes
    (B) 2 chromosomes
    (C) 4 chromosomes   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 16 chromosomes
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The number of chromosomes reduces to half at the end of meiosis cell division. If the plant has 2n = 8 chromosome the number of chromosomes present in daughter cells after meiosis II is 4 only.

Cell Cycle And Cell Division Test-05  (id 3388) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Cell Cycle and Cell Division
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. The transition period between M-phase I and M-phase II in without DNA replication?
    (A) Interkinesis   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Transition period
    (C) Interstage
    (D) Interphase
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The transition period between M-phase of Meiosis I and M-phase II during which no replication of DNA occurs is called as interkinesis. The cell undergoes preparation for the next round of division.

Q2. Crossing over results the exchange of genetic material, which occurs between:
    (A) Sister chromatids
    (B) Non-sister chromosomes
    (C) Homologous chromosomes   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Non-homologous chromosome
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Crossing over results in the exchange of genetic material between two homologous chromosomes during meiosis I of cell division.

Q3. Who started first that new cells are formed from the division of pre-existing cells?
    (A) Strasburger
    (B) Farmer and Moore
    (C) Rudolph Virchow   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Winiwater
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Rudolph Virchow was the first scientist who stated that new cells are formed from the division of pre-existing cells. It is a part of cell theory postulated by Virchow in 1855.

Q4. Two similar chromosomes of each type present in diploid cells are called as:
    (A) Sister chromosome
    (B) Paternal chromosome
    (C) Homologous chromosomes   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Maternal chromosome
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A homologous chromosome is two similar chromosomes of each type present in diploid cells. During meiosis homologous chromosomes separate from each other. In homologous pair, one chromosome is from mother while the other is from father.

Q5. Astral bodies are formed of______.
    (A) Microfilaments
    (B) Microtubules   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Intermediate filaments
    (D) Microvilli
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The astral body is formed of protein microtubules. Astral bodies are produced by centriole during cell division and attach with the centromere of the chromosome.

Q6. Human ________ did not divide after birth.
    (A) Heart cells
    (B) Blood cells
    (C) All of these
    (D) Nerve cells   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Human nerve cells do not divide after birth. These cells remain in the Go phase throughout their life. In G_o phase cells do not actually divide but undergo preparations for further division.

Q7. In diploid cells, each homologous chromosome consists of:
    (A) Two sister chromatids
    (B) A pair of paternal chromosomes
    (C) A pair of maternal chromosomes
    (D) Paternal and maternal chromosomes   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In Diploid cells, each homologous chromosome consists of one paternal and one maternal chromosome that fuses together during fertilization of gametes. These chromosomes are called homologous chromosomes.

Q8. Polyploidy is the property of:
    (A) Maintaining the genetic materials
    (B) Increasing the number of chromosome sets   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Increasing the size of chromosomes
    (D) Decreasing the number of chromosome sets
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Polyploidy is the condition in which more than one set of chromosomes is present in one cell. It is the property of increasing the number of chromosome sets of the cell and results due to the failure of the segregation of non-sister chromatids after crossing over.

Q9. Lampbrush chromosome where two homologous chromosomes with several chiasmata with several loops in the chromatic region are found in ______.
    (A) Skin cells
    (B) Bean inflorescence
    (C) Hair cells
    (D) Egg yolks   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Egg yolk contains a lampbrush chromosome where two homologous chromosomes with several chiasmata with several loops in the chromatic region are found. They are also called giant chromosomes.

Q10. Number of chromosome and amount of DNA content per cell change during:
    (A) Telophase and M-phase
    (B) Anaphase and S-phase   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Interphase and G1 phase
    (D) Metaphase and S-phase
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The number of chromosome changes during anaphase of meiosis I and the amount of DNA content increases during S-phase of the cell cycle. This is reflected in the disturbance of the nucleocytoplasmic ratio.

Q11. The number of chromosomes and the amount of DNA are changed in:
    (A) Dilution and D phase
    (B) Metaphase and M phase
    (C) Interphase and S phase
    (D) Anaphase and S phase   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: S phase marks the period during which DNA synthesis or replication takes place. During this time the amount of DNA per cell doubles. If the initial amount of DNA is denoted as 2C then it increases to 4C and even in anaphase, the chromosome numbers are changed.

Q12. Each chromosome consists of ________ chromatid.
    (A) four
    (B) one
    (C) eight
    (D) two   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The resulting two identical copies of DNA are connected to each other at the centromere. Each copy is called a chromatid. A chromosome, before cell division is formed of one chromatid while it is formed of two chromatids after cell division.

Q13. In the metaphase stage, the chromosomes are made up of:
    (A) One sister chromatid
    (B) Two sister chromatids   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Two non-sister chromatids
    (D) One sister and two non-sister chromatids
    Answer: B
    Explanation: At the metaphase stage, the chromosome is made up of two sister chromatids formed due to longitudinal splitting of the chromatids, which are held together by the centromere.

Q14. In plant cells, the new cell wall begins by the:
    (A) Chromatid
    (B) Cell plate   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Centromere
    (D) Cell cycle
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In-plant cells, wall formation starts in the centre of the cell and grows outward to meet the existing lateral walls. The formation of the new cell wall begins with the formation of a simple precursor, called the cell plate which hardens to give rise to the middle lamella.

Q15. Crossing over results in an exchange of genetic material, which occurs between:
    (A) Non-homologous chromosome
    (B) Sister chromatids
    (C) Bivalents
    (D) Homologous chromosomes   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Crossing over is the exchange of genetic material between non-sister chromatids of two homologous chromosomes involved in the pairing process.

Photosynthesis In Plants Test-01  (id 3400) [FREE]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Photosynthesis in Higher Plants
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
