Q1. The chief pigment associated in the process of photosynthesis is:
    (A) Chlorophyll m
    (B) Chlorophyll a   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Chlorophyll c
    (D) Chlorophyll b
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Chlorophyll-a is the chief pigment associated with photosynthesis because, in the blue and red regions of the spectrum, there is maximum absorption by chlorophyll-a. It also shows a higher rate of photosynthesis.

Q2. The essential role of air in the growth of green plants is given by:
    (A) Julis von sach
    (B) Joseph Priestly   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Cornelius van niel
    (D) Engelmann
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Joseph Priestley (1733-1804) in 1770 performed a series of experiments that revealed the essential role of air in the growth of green plants.

Q3. The site in chloroplast which is responsible for trapping for light energy is:
    (A) Stromal lamellae
    (B) Stroma
    (C) Grana   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Ribosomes
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The grana are responsible for trapping the light energy and converting it into ATP and NADPH during the light reaction of photosynthesis.

Q4. Photosynthesis mainly take place in:
    (A) Flowers
    (B) Roots
    (C) Leaves   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Stem
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Photosynthesis takes place only in the green parts of the plants, mainly the leaves.

Q5. Photosynthesis is maximum in:
    (A) Red light   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Very high light
    (C) Green light
    (D) Continuous light
    Answer: A
    Explanation: There is maximum absorption by chlorophyll a, in the red region and so there is a higher rate of photosynthesis.

Q6. In Bacterial photosynthesis, hydrogen donor is:
    (A) O_2
    (B) H_2O
    (C) H_2S   <-- CORRECT
    (D) CO_2
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In green plants, H_2O is the hydrogen donor and is oxidised to O_2. Some organisms do not release O_2 during photosynthesis. When H_2S, instead is the hydrogen donor for purple and green sulphur bacteria, the ‘oxidation’ product is sulphur or sulphate depending on the organism.

Q7. Solarisation is:
    (A) Effect of solar light
    (B) Formation of chlorophyll
    (C) Destruction of chlorophyll   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Utilisation of sunlight
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Solarisation is the inhibition of photosynthesis at very high light intensities due to photooxidation of certain compounds and the destruction of chlorophyll molecules.

Q8. The substances that have the ability to absorb light at different specific wavelength are:
    (A) Proteins
    (B) Enzymes
    (C) Pigments   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Carbohydrates
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Pigments are substances that have an ability to absorb light, at specific wavelengths. The chlorophyll-a pigment absorbs lights of different wavelengths.

Q9. The splitting of water molecule take place inside:
    (A) Outer membrane of thylakoid
    (B) Lumen of thylakoid
    (C) Stroma
    (D) Inner membrane of thylakoid   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Splitting of the water molecule takes place on the inner side of the membrane, the protons or hydrogen ions that are produced by the splitting of water accumulate within the lumen of the thylakoids.

Q10. PGA as the first CO_2 fixation product was discovered in photosynthesis of:
    (A) Algae   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Gymnosperm
    (C) Bryophytes
    (D) Angiosperm
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The pathway of photosynthesis was discovered by Melvin Calvin after the experiment on single-celled algae. The first stable product of the C_3 cycle is a three-carbon compound called PGA (phosphoglyceric acid).

Q11. Melvin Calvin use the radioactive ^14C in:
    (A) All of these
    (B) Plant photosynthesis
    (C) Bacterial photosynthesis
    (D) Algal photosynthesis   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The use of radioactive C-14 by him in algal photosynthesis studies led to the discovery that the first CO_2 fixation product was a 3-carbon organic acid.

Q12. Accessory pigments protect plants from:
    (A) Photosystem
    (B) Photo-oxidation   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Photosynthesis
    (D) Photorespiration
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Other thylakoid pigments like chlorophyll b, xanthophylls, and carotenoids, which are called accessory pigments, also absorb light and transfer the energy to chlorophyll a. Indeed, they not only enable a wider range of wavelengths of incoming light to be utilized for photosynthesis but also protect chlorophyll from photo-oxidation.

Q13. The portion of ATPase enzyme that protrudes on the outer surface of the thylakoid membrane on the side faces of the stroma _______.
    (A) ATP
    (B) F_0 of the ATPase
    (C) NADH
    (D) F_1 of the ATPase   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The ATPase enzyme consists of two parts: one called the F_0 is embedded in the membrane and forms a transmembrane channel that carries out facilitated diffusion of protons across the membrane. The other portion is called F_1 and protrudes on the outer surface of the thylakoid membrane on the side that faces the stroma.

Q14. Which form of carbon is absorbed by the hydrophytes through their general body surface?
    (A) Bicarbonates   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Calcium hydrogen carbonate
    (C) Hydrogen carbonates
    (D) Carbonates
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Hydrophytes are those plants that grow in water. Hydrophytes can absorb bicarbonates through their general body surface.

Q15. Name the photosynthetic pigment which can be converted to Vitamin A.
    (A) Beta-carotenes   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Beta-corticoids
    (C) Alpha-carotenes
    (D) Alpha-corticoids
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The photosynthetic pigment Beta-carotenes can be converted to Vitamin A. Carrot contain a large number of carotenes that can be converted into vitamin A.

Photosynthesis In Plants Test-02  (id 3401) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Photosynthesis in Higher Plants
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. What does C_6H_12O_6 represent in plant photosynthesis?
    (A) Sucrose
    (B) Starch
    (C) Glucose   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ATP
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The key features of plant photosynthesis were known, namely, that plants could use light energy to make carbohydrates C_6H_12O_6 from CO_2 and water, where C_6H_12O_6 represents glucose.

Q2. Name the central element present in chlorophyll.
    (A) Nitrogen
    (B) Carbon
    (C) Magnesium (Mg)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Iron
    Answer: C
    Explanation: As chlorophyll is a complex compound, Magnesium(Mg) is found in the centre of the structure of this compound.

Q3. Paper chromatography is a technique to separate__________.
    (A) Proteins
    (B) Leaf pigments   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Enzymes
    (D) Carbohydrates
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Separation of leaf pigments of any green plant through paper chromatography. Chromatographic separation of the leaf pigments shows that the colour that we see in leaves is not due to a single pigment but due to four pigments: Chlorophyll a (bright or blue-green in the chromatogram), chlorophyll b (yellow-green), xanthophylls (yellow) and carotenoids.

Q4. The substances like ATP carry energy in_______.
    (A) NAD
    (B) NADH
    (C) Chemical bonds   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ADP
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Living organisms have the capability of extracting energy from oxidizable substances and store this in the form of bond energy. Special substances like ATP, carry this energy in their chemical bonds.

Q5. Stroma in the chloroplasts of higher plants contain
    (A) Chlorophyll
    (B) Ribosomes
    (C) Light dependent reaction enzyme
    (D) Light independent reaction enzyme   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In the stroma, enzymatic reactions incorporate CO_2 into the plant leading to the synthesis of sugar, which are not directly light driven but are dependent on the products of light reactions (ATP and NADPH). Hence, to distinguish the latter they are called, by convention, as dark reactions. However, this should not be construed to mean that they occur in darkness or that they are not light-dependent.

Q6. In cells, ATP is synthesized in _________ and ________.
    (A) mitochondria and chloroplast   <-- CORRECT
    (B) cell wall and mitochondria
    (C) chloroplast and cell wall
    (D) cytoplasm and mitochondria
    Answer: A
    Explanation: ATP is synthesized by cells (in mitochondria and chloroplasts) is named phosphorylation.

Q7. Calvin cycle is discovered by:
    (A) Cornelius van neil
    (B) Melvin Calvin   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Hatch and Slack
    (D) Blackmann
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The work of Melvin Calvin is the discovery, the first CO_2 fixation product was a 3-carbon organic acid. He also contributed to working out the complete biosynthetic pathway; hence it was called the Calvin cycle.

Q8. Hill reaction requires:
    (A) Presence of Ferricyanide   <-- CORRECT
    (B) High attitude
    (C) Total darkness
    (D) Absence of water
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The light-dependent transfer of electrons by chloroplasts in photosynthesis that results in the cleavage of water molecule and liberation of oxygen is called Hill reaction. Hill reaction required ferricyanide.

Q9. In PSI, the chlorophyll-a has an absorption peak at _________.
    (A) 780nm
    (B) 700nm   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 680nm
    (D) 800nm
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In PS I the reaction centre chlorophyll-a has an absorption peak at 700 nm, hence is called P700.

Q10. The splitting of water molecules is associated with:
    (A) Non-cyclic phosphorylation
    (B) PS I
    (C) Cyclic phosphorylation
    (D) PS II   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: This is achieved by electrons available due to the splitting of water. The splitting of water is associated with the PSII; water is split into H+, [O], and electrons.

Q11. Light-harvesting complexes are made up of:
    (A) Hundreds of carbohydrates
    (B) Hundreds of enzymes
    (C) Hundreds of proteins
    (D) Hundreds of pigments   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Light-harvesting complexes (LHC) within the Photosystem I (PS I) and Photosystem II (PS II). These are named in the sequence of their discovery, and not in the sequence in which they function during the light reaction. The LHC is made up of hundreds of pigment molecules.

Q12. The single chlorophyll molecule forms a:
    (A) Primary acceptor
    (B) Reaction centre   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Antennae
    (D) Photon
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The single chlorophyll a molecule forms the reaction centre. The reaction centre is different in both the photosystems. In PS I the reaction centre is chlorophyll-a.

Q13. Which wavelength is inactive in PS I?
    (A) 690 nm
    (B) 550 nm
    (C) 680 nm
    (D) 780 nm   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Photosystem is light-reactive centre to capture solar energy. Photosystem I is active below the wavelength of light below 780 nm. While photosystem II is active above 780 nm.

Q14. The process of synthesis of ATP from ADP in the presence of light are:
    (A) Photophosphorylation   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Cyclic photophosphorylation
    (C) Non cyclic photophosphorylation
    (D) Chemiosmotic hypothesis
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The process of which ATP is synthesized by cells (in mitochondria and chloroplasts) is named phosphorylation. Photophosphorylation is the synthesis of ATP from ADP and inorganic phosphate in the presence of light.

Q15. Which range of wavelength (in nm) is called photosynthetically active radiation (PAR)?
    (A) 100 - 390
    (B) 400-700   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 390 - 430
    (D) 760 – 100,00
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The wavelength of light in which photosynthesis light reaction can occur is called PAR ( photosynthetically active radiation) which is 400-700 nm in most of the plants.

Photosynthesis In Plants Test-03  (id 3402) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Photosynthesis in Higher Plants
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. Each photosystem has all the pigments forming light-harvesting system also called as:
    (A) Z-scheme
    (B) Antennae   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Cytochromes
    (D) Reaction centre
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Each photosystem has all the pigments (except one molecule of chlorophyll a) forming a light-harvesting system also called antennae. These pigments help to make photosynthesis more efficient by absorbing different wavelengths of light.

Q2. Carotenes protect plants from:
    (A) Photosynthesis
    (B) Photorespiration
    (C) Photo-oxidation   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Desiccation
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Carotene is present in chloroplast along with chlorophyll pigment. This pigment protects the plants from photo-oxidation during photosynthesis at a higher intensity of light.

Q3. The excitation of electrons, finally down-hill to NADP^+ causing it to be reduced to NSFPH_2^+ is called as:
    (A) Redox potential
    (B) ATP
    (C) Z scheme   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Cytochromes
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Excitation of electrons, transfer to another accepter, and finally, down-hill to NADP^+ causing it to be reduced to NADPH + H^+ is called the Z scheme.

Q4. Which is the most effective wavelength of light for photosynthesis?
    (A) Yellow
    (B) Green
    (C) Red   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Violet
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Certain red and blue wavelengths of light are the most effective in photosynthesis because they have exactly the right amount of energy to energize, or excite, chlorophyll electrons and boost them out of their orbits to a higher energy level.

Q5. Electrons from excited chlorophyll molecules of photosystem II to photosystem I transferred and finally convert:
    (A) NAD to NADH   <-- CORRECT
    (B) NADH to NAD
    (C) PGA to NAD
    (D) ATP to NADH
    Answer: A
    Explanation: After absorbing light, electrons are excited and transferred through PS II and PS I and finally to NAD forming NADH.

Q6. Which of the following stages of Calvin cycle are in the correct order?
    (A) Carboxylation, regeneration, reduction
    (B) Carboxylation, reduction, regeneration   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Regeneration, reduction, carboxylation
    (D) Regeneration, carboxylation, reduction
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The Calvin cycle can be described under three stages: carboxylation, reduction, and regeneration. Pathway operated in a cyclic manner.

Q7. Electrons from excited chlorophyll molecules of photosystem II are accepted first by:
    (A) Cytochrome b
    (B) Quinone   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Cytochrome f
    (D) Ferredoxin
    Answer: B
    Explanation: During photophosphorylation, electron released during photolysis of water passes through the electron transport chain. The electron from excited chlorophyll molecules of Photosystem II is accepted first by quinone.

Q8. On excitation, the electrons picked up by an electron acceptor is passed to _______.
    (A) photons
    (B) reaction centre
    (C) anntenae
    (D) cytochromes   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Electrons become excited and jump into an orbit farther from the atomic nucleus. These electrons are picked up by an electron acceptor which passes them to an electrons transport of cytochrome.

Q9. The first product of photosynthesis is sugar and it is converted to ________.
    (A) Starch   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Ammonia
    (C) Protein
    (D) Glycogen
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Photosynthesis is the process by which plants, some bacteria, and some protistans use the energy from sunlight to produce glucose from carbon dioxide and water. The glucose is used in respiration, or converted into starch and stored.

Q10. Light reaction otherwise called as:
    (A) Carboxylation
    (B) Regeneration
    (C) Photochemical phase   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Biosynthetic phase
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Light reactions or the ‘Photochemical’ phase include light absorption, water splitting, oxygen release, and the formation of high-energy chemical intermediates, ATP, and NADPH. Several complexes are involved in the process.

Q11. Chloroplast stroma contains:
    (A) Light dependent reaction enzyme
    (B) Light independent reaction enzyme   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Chlorophyll
    (D) Ribosomes
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Chloroplast contains stroma and grana. Stroma is involved in light-independent reaction enzymes for the synthesis of glucose molecules using the product of the light reaction.

Q12. Carbon dioxide is fixed in:
    (A) Light reaction
    (B) Aerobic respiration
    (C) Anaerobic respiration
    (D) Dark reaction   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Photosynthesis occurs in two steps- light reaction and dark reaction. During light reaction, ATP, and NADPH molecules are formed and in dark reaction carbon dioxide is fixed.

Q13. Scientist awarded noble prize in 1960 for tracing the path of carbon is
    (A) Hatch
    (B) Calvin   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Huber
    (D) Blackmann
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Melvin Calvin awarded noble prize in 1960 for tracing the path of carbon during photosynthesis. The cycle of event is named after him as Calvin cycle.

Q14. Photorespiration in C_3 plants begins from:
    (A) Glycine
    (B) Glycerate
    (C) Phosphoglycerate
    (D) Phosphoglycolate   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Photorespiration in C_3 plants starts with Phosphoglycolate as a primary acceptor in the presence of RUBP enzyme to form a two-carbon compound and a three-carbon compound.

Q15. C_3 plants respond to higher CO_2 concentration leads to:
    (A) Death of plant
    (B) Lower productivity
    (C) Poor yield
    (D) Higher productivity   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The fact that C_3 plants respond to higher CO_2 concentration by showing increased rates of photosynthesis leading to higher productivity. They are allowed to grow in a carbon dioxide enriched atmosphere that leads to higher yields.

Photosynthesis In Plants Test-04  (id 3403) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Photosynthesis in Higher Plants
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. In ${C_3}$ pathway, the bundle sheath cells are lack of an enzyme called
    (A) ATP synthetase
    (B) PEP carboxylase   <-- CORRECT
    (C) RuBisCo
    (D) PGA
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The $C{O_2}$ released in the bundle sheath cells enters the ${C_3}$ or the Calvin pathway, a pathway common to all plants. The bundle sheath cells are rich in an enzyme Ribulose bisphosphate carboxylase-oxygenase (RuBisCO), but lack PEPcase.

Q2. In photosynthesis photolysis of water is used in:
    (A) Reduction of CO_2
    (B) Reduction of NADP^+   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Oxidation of FAD
    (D) Oxidation of NADP
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Breaking down of water molecules in the presence of sunlight during photosynthesis is called photolysis of water. During photolysis of water reduction of NADP^+ into NADPH takes place.

Q3. Who proved that oxygen evolved in photosynthesis comes from water?
    (A) Hatch and Slack
    (B) Von Mayer
    (C) Ruben, Hassid, and Kamen   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Melvin Calvin
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Ruben, Hassid and Kamen proved that Oxygen evolved during photosynthesis comes from water and not from carbon dioxide. For this, they used water with heavy isotope of oxygen, ^18O.

Q4. First transitory biochemical produced in reaction between CO_2 and RuBP is:
    (A) PGA
    (B) DiHAP
    (C) 2-carboxy 3-keto 1,5-biphosphoribotol   <-- CORRECT
    (D) PGAL
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The first intermediate product produced in the C_3 cycle of photosynthesis in the presence of RUBP enzyme is 2-carboxy 3-keto 1,5-biphosphoribotol which changes into two molecules of PGA.

Q5. The number of Oxygen molecules released per photon or quantum of light absorbed is called
    (A) Quantum number
    (B) Net yield
    (C) Quantum yield   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Quantosome
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Quantum yield is the number of Oxygen molecules released per photon or quantum of light. During the light reaction of photosynthesis, oxygen molecules are released during photolysis.

Q6. Energy obtained from the light reaction is transferred to the dark reaction in the form of:
    (A) Chlorophyll
    (B) ATP   <-- CORRECT
    (C) ADP
    (D) RuBP
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The energy produced during light reaction is transferred to a dark reaction in the form of ATP to fix the carbon dioxide in the form of glucose.

Q7. In sugarcane, CO_2 is fixed in malic acid with the help of enzyme _____.
    (A) PEP carboxylase   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Fructose phosphotase
    (C) RuBP carboxylase
    (D) Ribulose phosphate kinase
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In C_4 plants, Carbon dioxide is fixed in malic acid with the help of enzyme phosphoenolpyruvate (PEP). Malic acid is a four-carbon compound that later changes into oxaloacetic acid.

Q8. Which one has Kranz anatomy?
    (A) Wheat
    (B) Potato
    (C) Rice
    (D) Maize   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In the leaves of C_4 plants such as maize, sorghum we can observe the Kranz anatomy.

Q9. The C_4 pathway is otherwise called as:
    (A) Cyclic phosphorylation
    (B) Hatch and slack pathway   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Calvin pathway
    (D) Non cyclic phosphorylation
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The presence of the bundle sheath would help you identify the C_4 plants. This pathway that has been named the Hatch and Slack Pathway, is again a cyclic process.

Q10. Chloroplast dimorphism is a characteristic feature of ________.
    (A) C_4 plants   <-- CORRECT
    (B) C_3 plants
    (C) Only in algae
    (D) All plants
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Chloroplast dimorphism is a characteristic feature of C_4 plants. These plants contain two kinds of chloroplast in their leaves, bundles sheath cells contain chloroplast in which grana is absent and mesophyll cells without stroma.

Q11. What is the site of the formation of glycoxylate from glycolate?
    (A) Mitochondria of palisade cells
    (B) Peroxisomes of mesophyll cells   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Peroxisomes of palisade cells
    (D) Mitochondria of mesophyll cells
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Mesophyll cells contain peroxisomes where the formation of glyoxylate is formed from glycolate during the Hatch and Slack cycle of carbon fixation.

Q12. C_4 pathway is seen in:
    (A) Temperate plants
    (B) Deciduous plants
    (C) Evergreen plants
    (D) Dry tropical plants   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Plants that are adapted to dry tropical regions have the C_4 pathway Though these plants have the C_4 oxaloacetic acid as the first CO_2 fixation product they use the C_3 pathway or the Calvin cycle as the main biosynthetic pathway.

Q13. Pigment of PS-I occurs in:
    (A) Stromal
    (B) Stromal thylakoids and non-appressed parts of granal thylakoids   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Appressed parts of granal thylakoids
    (D) Both Appressed parts of granal thylakoids and Stromal thylakoids
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The pigment of Photosystem I occurs in stromal thylakoids and non-appressed parts of granal thylakoids. PS-I absorbs light of a wavelength of less than 780 nm.

Q14. The enzyme required in early CO_2 fixation in C_4 cycle is:
    (A) PEP carboxylase   <-- CORRECT
    (B) RuBP oxygenase
    (C) PGA dehydrogenase
    (D) RuBP carboxylase
    Answer: A
    Explanation: During the fixation of carbon dioxide in the C_4 cycle, the enzyme required is PEP carboxylase. These enzymes become active only when the concentration of carbon dioxide gas more.

Q15. The C_4 plants show saturation at about ______.
    (A) 400$\mu l$L^-1
    (B) 450$\mu l$L^-1
    (C) 360$\mu l$L^-1   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 500$\mu l$L^-1
    Answer: C
    Explanation: It is important to note is that the C_4 plants show saturation at about 360$\mu l$L^-1 while C_3 responds to increased CO_2 concentration and saturation is seen only beyond 450 μlL-1. Thus, the current availability of CO_2 levels is limiting to C_3 plants.

Photosynthesis In Plants Test-05  (id 3404) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Photosynthesis in Higher Plants
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. The C_4 plants show higher rate of photosynthesis in:
    (A) High temperature   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Low temperature
    (C) Absence of temperature
    (D) Optimum temperature
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The C_4 plants respond to higher temperatures and show a higher rate of photosynthesis while C_3 plants have a much lower temperature optimum.

Q2. The number of ATP molecules required to synthesize one molecule of glucose by C_4 pathways is _____.
    (A) 36 ATP
    (B) 24 ATP
    (C) 30 ATP   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 12 ATP
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The synthesis of glucose molecules during photosynthesis involves the utilization of ATP molecules. In C_4 plants, 30 ATP molecules are required to fix one molecule of glucose.

Q3. Most abundant enzyme in the world is:
    (A) PEP carboxylase
    (B) RuBisCo   <-- CORRECT
    (C) RuBp
    (D) ATPase
    Answer: B
    Explanation: RuBisCO is the most abundant enzyme in the world and is characterized by the fact that its active site can bind to both CO_2 and O_2 hence the name.

Q4. Which of the following occurs in dark reaction of photosynthesis?
    (A) Formation of ATP
    (B) Release of H_2
    (C) Synthesis of PGAL   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Release of O_2
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Photosynthesis consists of light reaction and dark reaction. During light reaction, ATP molecules are formed along with H_2 and O_2 . Synthesis of PGAL occurs during dark reaction.

Q5. The response of the different organism to environment rhythms of light and darkness is called:
    (A) Phototaxis
    (B) Photoperiodism   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Phototropism
    (D) Vernalization
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Photoperiodism is the response of the different organisms to environmental change of light and dark periods of light. In plants, flowering takes place after a certain period of light.

Q6. Photorespiration does not occur in:
    (A) C_3 plants
    (B) Bacteria
    (C) C_4 plants   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Algae
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In the photorespiratory pathway, there is no synthesis of ATP or NADPH. Therefore, photorespiration is a wasteful process. In C_4 plants photorespiration does not occur. This is because they have a mechanism that increases the concentration of CO_2 at the enzyme site.

Q7. Dark fixation of CO_2 in CAM plants is called ossification because it produces:
    (A) Malic acid   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Oxaloacetic acid
    (C) Tartaric acid
    (D) Formic acid
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The dark reaction of Carbon dioxide fixation in CAM plants is called ossification because it produces Malic acid. These plants open their stomata during the night to prevent transpiration.

Q8. The law of limiting factors is given by:
    (A) Sachs
    (B) Blackmann   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Priestly
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Blackman proposed the law of limiting factors in 1905. According to this law, when a process depends on a number of factors, its rate is limited by the pace of the slowest factor. Blackman's law of limiting factors determines the rate of photosynthesis.

Q9. Succulents carry out photosynthesis ________.
    (A) C_3 pathway
    (B) CAM pathway   <-- CORRECT
    (C) C_4 pathway
    (D) CO_2 pathway
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Succulents plants have stomata sunken deeply in leaf epidermis to prevent loss of water by transpiration. These plants open their stomata at night and follow the CAM pathway for the fixation of carbon dioxide.

Q10. Which one of the following is not an internal factor that influences the rate of photosynthesis?
    (A) Hormones
    (B) Chlorophyll
    (C) Mesophyll cells
    (D) Carbondioxide   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The plant factors include the orientation of leaves, mesophyll cells and chloroplasts, and the amount of chlorophyll. The external factors would include the availability of sunlight temperature, CO_2 concentration, and water. As a plant photosynthesizes, all these factors will simultaneously affect its rate.

Q11. As compared to sun plants, plants adapted to low light intensity possess:
    (A) High rate of CO_2 fixation
    (B) Larger photosynthetic unit   <-- CORRECT
    (C) More extended root system
    (D) Spiny leaves
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The plants adapted to low light intensity for photosynthesis contain a larger amount of photosynthetic units as compared to sun plants.

Q12. Half leaf experiment is performed to prove ________ is required for photosynthesis.
    (A) CO_2   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Light
    (C) Chlorophyll
    (D) Oxygen
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Moll's half leaf experiment is done to show that carbon dioxide is necessary for photosynthesis to occur. In this experiment Moll (inventor of an experiment) divided the leaf into two half portion one inside the bottle and another outside. The one inside the bottle did not show photosynthesis due to a lack of carbon dioxide. After testing leaf present inside the bottle for starch, it is proved that it does not contain starch and hence, photosynthesis did not occur in this leaf. The leaf which was outside the bottle shows the presence of starch indicating the occurrence of photosynthesis in it.

Q13. Of the total solar radiation, the proportion of PAR is:
    (A) More than 80%
    (B) About 60%
    (C) Less than 50%   <-- CORRECT
    (D) About 70%
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Solar radiation consists of light of different wavelengths ranging from ultraviolet to infrared. A small portion of these light is useful for photosynthesis called PAR or photosynthetically active radiation which comprises less than 50% of total radiation.

Q14. Passage of light rays in between the chloroplasts of palisade parenchyma cells to spongy parenchyma is known as:
    (A) Sieve Effect   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Hydro Effect
    (C) Light Effect
    (D) Salt Effect
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The passage of light rays in between the chloroplast of palisade parenchyma cells to spongy parenchyma is known as the Sieve effect because the light that falls on chloroplast will be absorbed and reflected back. the light that passes between the chloroplast will reach the spongy parenchyma.

Q15. Which one is not an internal factor that influences the rate of photosynthesis?
    (A) Chlorophyll
    (B) Leaf anatomy
    (C) Hormones
    (D) Carbon dioxide   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The rate of photosynthesis is influenced by a number of factors like chlorophyll, leaf anatomy, hormones, water availability, etc. Carbon dioxide is not an internal factor that influences the rate of photosynthesis.

Respiration In Plants Test-01  (id 3405) [FREE]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Respiration in Plants
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. An organism which depends on the dead and decaying organic matter is__________.
    (A) Saprophytes   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Autotrophs
    (C) Carnivores
    (D) Herbivorous
    Answer: A
    Explanation: A saprophyte or saprotroph is an organism that gets its energy from dead and decaying organic matter. This may be decaying pieces of plants or animals. This means that saprophytes are heterotrophs. They are consumers in the food chain.

Q2. In plants, the gaseous exchange takes place in:
    (A) Stomata
    (B) Stomata and Root   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Stems
    (D) Root
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Plants, unlike animals, have no special systems for breathing or gaseous exchange. Stomata and lenticels allow gaseous exchange by diffusion.

Q3. Respiration is:
    (A) Both anabolic and catabolic
    (B) Amphibolic process
    (C) Catabolic process   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Anabolic process
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Catabolism is the process of break down any large substance into smaller ones. In respiration, glucose is broken down into carbon dioxide and water molecules. Thus it is referred to as a catabolic reaction.

Q4. Pasteur effect can be studied in case of ________.
    (A) Sccharomyces   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Nostoc
    (C) Pinnularia
    (D) Penicillium
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Reduction in consumption of respiratory substrate when the mode of respiration is changed from aerobic to anaerobic is called pasture effect. It is studied in the case of Saccharomyces.

Q5. Glycolysis occurs in:
    (A) Mitochondria
    (B) Chloroplast
    (C) Cell membrane
    (D) Cytoplasm   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Glycolysis means the splitting of glucose. The first step of the process occurs in the cytoplasm of the cell and yields a small amount of energy (measured in units of ATP) and two molecules of pyruvate. The other steps occur in the mitochondria. It is an ongoing process as your cells have a constant need for energy.

Q6. Glycolysis is also known as:
    (A) TCA cycle
    (B) EMP pathway   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Photophosphorylation
    (D) Calvin cycle
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The scheme of glycolysis was given by Gustav Embden, Otto Meyerhof, and J. Parnas, and is often referred to as the EMP pathway.

Q7. The complete combustion of glucose produces:
    (A) Pyurvic acid
    (B) Ethanol
    (C) Lactic acid
    (D) Carbon dioxide and oxygen   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The complete combustion of glucose, which produces carbon dioxide and water as end products, yields energy most of which is given out as heat.

Q8. Respiratory Quotient for the reaction C_57H_107O_6 + 80O_2$\rightarrow$ 57CO_2 + 52H_2O is:
    (A) 0.071
    (B) 0.71   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 1.71
    (D) 1.7
    Answer: B
    Explanation: RQ is equal to the number of carbon dioxide molecules produced divided by the number of oxygen molecules used during respiration. Here, RQ = $\frac{57}{80}$ = 0.71.

Q9. What is the final product of Glycolysis?
    (A) Pyruvic acid   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Glucose
    (C) Acetyl CoA
    (D) Malic acid
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Glycolysis involves the breaking down of sugar (generally glucose, although fructose and other sugars may be used) into more manageable compounds in order to produce energy. The net end products of glycolysis are two Pyruvate, two NADH, and two ATP.

Q10. How many net ATP are produced in Glycolysis?
    (A) 2 ATP   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 8 ATP
    (C) 36 ATP
    (D) 16 ATP
    Answer: A
    Explanation: At the end of glycolysis pathway, 2 net ATP molecules at step 6 and step 9 are produced.

Q11. The enzyme which converts glucose into glucose -6- phosphate is _______.
    (A) Invertase
    (B) Dehydrogenase
    (C) Succinyl CoA
    (D) Hexokinase   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Hexokinase is an enzyme that phosphorylates hexoses (six-carbon sugars), forming hexose phosphate. In most organisms, glucose is the most important substrate of hexokinases, and glucose-6-phosphate is the most important product.

Q12. How many step reactions are involved in glycolysis?
    (A) 12
    (B) 8
    (C) 10   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 9
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Glycolysis is a series of reactions and extracts energy from glucose by splitting it into two three-carbon molecules called pyruvates. Glycolysis is an ancient metabolic pathway, meaning that it evolved long ago, and it is found in the great majority of organisms alive today. Glycolysis has ten steps.

Q13. The partial breakdown of glucose takes place in __________.
    (A) Fermentation   <-- CORRECT
    (B) ETS cycle
    (C) Respiration
    (D) TCA cycle
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Fermentation is an anaerobic breakdown of carbohydrates in which an organic molecule is the final electron acceptor. It does not involve an electron transport system. Furthermore, it is a partial breakdown of glucose giving a little energy, 2 net ATPs per glucose by the way of substrate-level phosphorylation.

Q14. Which one is incorrect about Glycolysis?
    (A) No carbon dioxide is evolved
    (B) It occurs inside the cytoplasm
    (C) It is a cyclic pathway   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Oxygen is not required for Glycolysis
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Glycolysis is not a cyclic pathway and carbon dioxide gas is not released during this cycle. Oxygen is not required for Glycolysis process. Glycolysis occurs in the cytoplasm of the cell.

Q15. During cellular respiration, pyruvic acid is reduced to lactic acid in the presence of:
    (A) Lactate dehydrogenase   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Pyruvate dehydrogenase
    (C) Dehydrogenase
    (D) NADH dehydrogenase
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Lactate dehydrogenase (LDH) is an enzyme that catalyzes the conversion of lactate to pyruvate. When oxygen is inadequate for cellular respiration. This is an important step in energy production in cells. Many different types of cells in the body contain this enzyme. Some of the organs relatively rich in LDH are the heart, kidney, liver, and muscle.

Respiration In Plants Test-02  (id 3406) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Respiration in Plants
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. Energy is stored in the form of _______.
    (A) FAD
    (B) ATP   <-- CORRECT
    (C) NADH
    (D) ADP
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Cells store energy in a molecule called adenosine triphosphate (abbreviated as ATP). The adenosine molecule has three phosphate groups attached to it (triphosphate means three phosphates) which are held together by high energy bonds. If one of these bonds is broken, a great amount of energy is released which can be used in an endergonic reaction.

Q2. Glycolysis is the conversion of:
    (A) Glucose to pyruvic acid   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Glucose to fructose
    (C) Glucose to citric acid
    (D) Glucose to malic acid
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Glycolysis is the metabolic pathway that converts glucose C_6H_12O_6, into pyruvate, CH_3COCOO^− + H^+. The free energy released in this process is used to form the high-energy molecules ATP (adenosine triphosphate) and NADH (reduced nicotinamide adenine dinucleotide).

Q3. In animal cells, the first stage of glucose breaks down is _________.
    (A) Kreb cycle
    (B) Oxidative phosphorylation
    (C) ETS cycle
    (D) Glycolysis   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In animal cells, like muscles during exercise, when oxygen is inadequate for cellular respiration pyruvic acid is reduced to lactic acid by lactate dehydrogenase. The reducing agent is NADH^+ and H^+ which is oxidized to NAD^+ in both the processes.

Q4. ${F_0} - {F_1}$ particles participate in the synthesis of
    (A) NADPH
    (B) $FAD{H_2}$
    (C) ADP
    (D) ATP   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: F0−F1 particles participate in the synthesis of ATP from ADP in the inner wall of mitochondria with the help of enzymes during oxidative phosphorylation.

Q5. Which one is not a preparatory phase or energy spending phase of Glycolysis?
    (A) Synthesis of fructose 6-phosphate
    (B) Phosphorylation of glucose
    (C) Formation of Pyruvate   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Isomerisation of DiHAP
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Formation of pyruvate is not a preparatory phase or energy spending phase of Glycolysis. In this phase, one ATP molecule is released.

Q6. Anaerobic respiration of yeast produces_______.
    (A) Citric acid
    (B) Ethanol   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Malic acid
    (D) Pyurvic acid
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Anaerobic respiration in some microorganisms such as yeast produces ethanol and carbon dioxide, as opposed to lactic acid. Glucose is achieved under anaerobic conditions by sets of reactions. It can be summarised by the following equation: 
glucose $\to $ ethanol + carbon dioxide (+ energy released).

Q7. At the end of the citric acid cycle, most of the energy is transferred to:
    (A) Citric acid
    (B) NADH and FADH_2   <-- CORRECT
    (C) ATP
    (D) Oxaloacetic acid
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Citric acid cycle or C_3 cycle start with pyruvate and leads to complete oxidation of glucose to carbon dioxide and energy in form of ATP, NADH, and FADH_2. At the end of the citric acid cycle, most of the energy is transferred to NADH and FADH_2.

Q8. In eukaryotic organisms, aerobic respiration takes place in the presence of ______.
    (A) Lactic acid
    (B) Oxygen   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Carbon dioxide
    (D) Ethanol
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Aerobic means “with air”. This type of respiration needs oxygen for it to occur so it is called aerobic respiration. The word equation for aerobic respiration is:
Glucose + Oxygen $\to$ Carbon dioxide + Water + Energy
The chemical equation is:
C_6H_12O_6 + 6O_2 $\to$ 6CO_2 + 6H_2O + 2900 kJ/mol.

Q9. Electron transport system takes place in:
    (A) Cristae
    (B) Matrix
    (C) Mitochondrial space
    (D) Inner mitochondrial membrane   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The metabolic pathway through which the electron passes from one carrier to another is called the ETS and it is present in the inner mitochondrial membrane.

Q10. Arrange the following in descending order based upon the number of carbon atoms in the Kreb cycle:
 $\alpha$ - ketoglutaric acid
 citric acid
 Acetyl co A
 Succinic acid
    (A) A, D, B, C
    (B) B, C, D, A
    (C) B, A, D, C   <-- CORRECT
    (D) A, B, C, D
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In the Kerb cycle citric acid consists of 6C atoms, $\alpha$- ketoglutaric acid consists of 5C atoms, succinic acid consists of 4C atoms, and Acetyl co A consists of 2C atoms,

Q11. Which compound consists of 5 carbon atoms?
    (A) α –Ketoglutaric acid   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Malic acid
    (C) Oxalo acetic acid
    (D) Citric acid
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Alpha-ketoglutaric acid is an important biological compound and is a key intermediate in the Krebs cycle. Alpha-ketoglutaric acid occurs naturally within cells.
One of its functions is to combine with ammonia to form glutamic acid and then glutamine. Another function is to combine with nitrogen released in the cell, therefore preventing nitrogen overload.

Q12. In the electron transport system, the two copper centres are found in:
    (A) Cytochrome c oxidase   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Pyruvate dehydrogenase
    (C) NADH dehydrogenase
    (D) Ubiquinone
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The enzyme cytochrome c oxidase or Complex IV is a large transmembrane protein complex found in bacteria and the mitochondrion of eukaryotes. The complex contains two hemes, a cytochrome a and cytochrome a_3, and two copper centres, the Cu_A and Cu_B centres. The cytochrome a_3 and Cu_​​​B form a binuclear centre that is the site of oxygen reduction.

Q13. The complex V is also known as:
    (A) ADP
    (B) NAD
    (C) F_oF_1-ATPase   <-- CORRECT
    (D) FAD
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Complex V or ATP synthase can be separated into 2 parts:
F_o - the portion embedded in the inner mitochondrial membrane and F_1-ATPase - the portion projecting into the matrix of the mitochondrion.
This is why the intact ATP synthase is also called the F_oF_1-ATPase.

Q14. The cytochrome c moves in between:
    (A) Complex I and II
    (B) Complex III and IV   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Complex II and III
    (D) Complex I and IV
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Cytochrome c is a small protein attached to the outer surface of the inner membrane and acts as a mobile carrier for the transfer of electrons between complex III and IV.

Q15. In the electron transport system, the oxidation of one molecule of NADH produces:
    (A) 4 molecules of ATP
    (B) 3 molecules of ATP   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 1 molecule of ATP
    (D) 2 molecules of ATP
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Oxidation of one molecule of NADH gives rise to 3 molecules of ATP, while that of one molecule of FADH_2 produces 2 molecules of ATP.

Respiration In Plants Test-03  (id 3407) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Respiration in Plants
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. The TCA cycle starts with ______.
    (A) Dehydrogenation
    (B) Condensation   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Phosphorylation
    (D) Decarboxylation
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The TCA cycle starts with the condensation of acetyl group with oxaloacetic acid (OAA) and water to yield citric acid.

Q2. Aerobic respiration is common in:
    (A) Prokaryotes
    (B) Higher organisms   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Unicellular eukaryotes
    (D) Yeast
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Aerobic respiration is the process that leads to complete oxidation of organic substances in the presence of oxygen and releases carbon dioxide, water, and a large amount of energy present in the substrate. This type of respiration is most common in higher organisms.

Q3. In Kreb cycle, isocitric acid is converted into $\alpha$ - keto glutaric acid by:
    (A) Carboxylation
    (B) Condensation
    (C) Dehydration
    (D) Decarboxylation   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Citrate is first isomerized to isocitrate and then followed by decarboxylation, leading to the formation of $\alpha$ - ketoglutaric acid.

Q4. In Kreb cycle conversion of succinyl-CoA to succinic acid by_____.
    (A) ADP
    (B) GDP
    (C) GTP   <-- CORRECT
    (D) NADH
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Conversion of Succinyl-CoA to Succinate: Succinyl-CoA, like acetyl-CoA, has a strongly negative free energy of hydrolysis of its thioester bond In the next step of the citric acid cycle, the energy released in the breakage of this bond is used to drive the synthesis of a phosphoanhydride bond in either GTP or ATP, and succinate is also formed in the process. The enzyme that catalyzes this reversible reaction is called either succinyl-CoA synthetase or succinic thiokinase.

Q5. Two molecules of pyruvate are completely degraded in the Krebs cycle to form _______.
    (A) 2ATP, 8NADH_2, and 2FADH_2   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 2ATP, 6NADH_2, and 2FADH_2
    (C) 4ATP, 12NADH_2, and 4FADH_2
    (D) 8ATP, 8NADH_2, and 2FADH_2
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In the Kreb cycle glucose has been broken down to release carbon dioxide and eight molecules of NADH_2; two of FADH_2 have been synthesized besides just two molecules of ATP.

Q6. Fermentation is ________.
    (A) Anaerobic respiration   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Incomplete oxidation
    (C) Aerobic respiration
    (D) Excretory process
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Fermentation is the process of anaerobic respiration in which incomplete oxidation leads to the formation of ethanol in the absence of oxygen. Fermentation occurs in yeast.

Q7. Number of glucose molecule required to produce 38 ATP under anaerobic condition is_____.
    (A) 38
    (B) 19   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 2
    (D) 4
    Answer: B
    Explanation: During anaerobic respiration, only two molecules of ATP are produced by each molecule of glucose. So, 19 glucose molecules are required to produce 38 ATP molecules.

Q8. Cellular respiration first takes place in ________.
    (A) Endoplasmic reticulum
    (B) Golgi bodies
    (C) Cytoplasm   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Lysosomes
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Cellular respiration takes place in two steps- Glycolysis and Kreb’s cycle. Glycolysis occurs in the cytoplasm of cells and Kreb’s cycle in mitochondria. So, the first step of respiration takes place in the cytoplasm.

Q9. Lactic acid is formed by the process of:
    (A) Nitrogen fixation
    (B) Kreb’s cycle
    (C) Incomplete oxidation   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Glycolysis
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Lactic acid is formed in muscle cells by the process of incomplete oxidation of glucose due to lack of sufficient oxygen.

Q10. In mitochondria, protein accumulates in:
    (A) Matrix
    (B) Outer membrane
    (C) Intermembrane space   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Inner membrane
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In mitochondria, protein accumulate in intermembrane space between two layers of mitochondria.

Q11. Energy releasing enzymatically controlled catabolic process which involves step-wise oxidative breakdown of organic substance inside living cells is called:
    (A) Cellular respiration   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Decarboxylation
    (C) Anaerobic respiration
    (D) Fermentation
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Cellular respiration is a set of metabolic reactions and processes that take place in the cells of organisms to convert biochemical energy from nutrients into adenosine triphosphate (ATP), and then release waste products.

Q12. Two Synonyms are
    (A) Tricarboxylic acid cycle and urea cycle
    (B) Krebs cycle and calvin cycle
    (C) Tricarboxylic acid cycle and citric acid cycle   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Citric acid cycle and calvin cycle
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Tricarboxylic acid cycle and citric acid cycle are two synonyms as both represent same cycle occurring during respiration process.

Q13. The net gain of ATP molecules per hexose during aerobic respiration is _______.
    (A) 18
    (B) 12
    (C) 30
    (D) 36   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Each glucose (hexose) during complete oxidation or aerobic respiration produces net 36 ATP molecules, which is produced in the form of NADPH and FADH. Each NADPH produce 3 ATP and FADH two ATP molecules.

Q14. Krebs cycle is both catabolic and anabolic as it provides ________.
    (A) ATP is released as well as utilised
    (B) A number of final products
    (C) Produce energy as well as use energy
    (D) A number of intermediates   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Kreb’s cycle is both catabolic and anabolic because it provides a number of intermediates which are the product of catabolism as well as anabolism.

Q15. Lactic acid produced in muscle is sent to ________ to regenerate glucose.
    (A) Kidney
    (B) Pancreases
    (C) Lungs
    (D) Liver   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Lactic acid is produced in muscle during insufficient oxygen in muscle cells. Lactic acid produced in muscle is sent to regenerate glucose during rest in the presence of sufficient oxygen.

Respiration In Plants Test-04  (id 3408) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Respiration in Plants
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. During anaerobic respiration, less energy is produced than aerobic respiration because:
    (A) Glucose is not available
    (B) It takes place in inert medium
    (C) Incomplete oxidation of glucose takes place   <-- CORRECT
    (D) It takes place is micrograms
    Answer: C
    Explanation: During anaerobic respiration, incomplete oxidation of glucose takes place but during aerobic respiration complete oxidation of glucose occurs in which less energy is produced.

Q2. The dough kept overnight in warm place becomes soft and spongy due to _______.
    (A) Cohesion
    (B) Absorption of CO_2
    (C) Osmosis
    (D) Fermentation   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Fermentation is a kind of anaerobic respiration in the absence of oxygen to produce ethanol and carbon dioxide gas. The dough kept overnight in warm place becomes soft and spongy due to carbon dioxide gas released during fermentation.

Q3. When and where anaerobic respiration does occur in man and yeast?
    (A) Bone in man and yeast in normal condition
    (B) Muscle in man and yeast in adverse condition
    (C) Muscle in man and salt solution in yeast
    (D) Muscle in man and submergence in sugary solution in yeast   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Anaerobic respiration in man occurs in muscle cells during sudden activity in cells to form lactic acid. In yeast anaerobic respiration occurs in the absence of oxygen to form ethanol.

Q4. Acetyl CoA combines with oxaloacetate in the presence of condensing enzyme citrate synthetase to form a 6-C compound called _______.
    (A) Tartaric acid
    (B) Citric acid   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Pyruvic acid
    (D) Malic acid
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Acetyl CoA combines with oxaloacetate in presence of enzyme citrate synthetase to form 6-C compound called citric acid during Kreb’s cycle.

Q5. Two molecules of pyruvate are completely degraded in the Krebs cycle to form:
    (A) 4ATP, 12NADH_2 and 4FADH_2
    (B) 2ATP, 8NADH_2, 2FADH_2   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 8ATP, 8NADH_2 and 2FADH_2
    (D) 2ATP, 6NADH_2 and 2FADH_2
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Two molecules of pyruvate are produced during Glycolysis from one molecule of glucose. When these molecules of pyruvate completely degraded in Kreb’s cycle it forms 2 ATP, 8NADH_2, 2FADH_2 molecules.

Q6. The correct sequential order of pathway is:
    (A) ETS cycle, TCA cycle, glycolysis
    (B) Glycolysis, TCA cycle, ETS cycle   <-- CORRECT
    (C) TCA cycle, Glycolysis, ETS cycle
    (D) Glycolysis, ETScycle, TCA cycle
    Answer: B
    Explanation: There is a sequential, orderly pathway functioning, with one substrate forming the next and with glycolysis, TCA cycle and ETS pathway following one after another.

Q7. Oxidative phosphorylation is:
    (A) Production of ATP by chemiosmosis   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Citric acid production of ATP
    (C) Alcoholic fermentation
    (D) Anaerobic production of ATP
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Oxidative phosphorylation is a process in which ATP is produced by chemiosmosis in the inner wall of mitochondria called cristae.

Q8. During which stage in the complete oxidation of glucose is the greatest number of ATP formed from ADP?
    (A) Electron transport chain   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Krebs cycle
    (C) Glycolysis
    (D) During conversion of pyruvic acid to Acetyl Co A
    Answer: A
    Explanation: During electron transport chain stage of respiration of complete oxidation of glucose, the greatest number of ATP is formed from ADP in the inner wall of mitochondria.

Q9. FAD^+ is produced during the conversion of:
    (A) Isocitric acid Oxalosuccinic acid
    (B) Citric acid to isocitric acid
    (C) Fumaric acid to Malic acid
    (D) Succinic acid to Fumaric acid   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: During the citric acid cycle, Succinic acid is converted into Fumaric acid during which FAD^+ molecules is produced that produce 2 ATP molecules.

Q10. Which process makes direct use of oxygen?
    (A) Glycolysis
    (B) Krebs cycle
    (C) Fermentation
    (D) Electron transport   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Electron transport process makes direct use of oxygen to produce ATP molecules in the respiration process.

Q11. Chemiosmotic theory of ATP synthesis in chloroplast and mitochondria is based on:
    (A) Accumulation of Na^+ ions
    (B) Membrane potential
    (C) Accumulation of K^+ ions
    (D) Proton gradient   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Synthesis of ATP during photosynthesis and respiration in chloroplast and mitochondria respectively is based explained by chemiosmotic theory. This theory is based on a protein gradient between the inner and outer membrane to form ATP from ADP and phosphate ions.

Q12. The electrochemical potential gradient created across the membrane due to high H^+ concentration on one side is called:
    (A) Energy movement force
    (B) Proton motive force   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Electromotive force
    (D) Electron movement force
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The electrochemical potential gradient created across the membrane due to high hydrogen ion H^+ concentration on the outer side of the membrane of mitochondria is called the proton motive force.

Q13. Mitochondria is called power house of the cell because
    (A) Enzyme of Krebs cycle and the cytochromes are found   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Mitochondria contain ATP
    (C) Mitochondria have double membrane
    (D) Mitochondria are found in all kinds of cells
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Mitochondria are called the powerhouse of the cell because it contains enzymes and cytochrome for cellular respiration during which energy is released in form of ATP.

Q14. Respiratory Quotient is more than one in case the substrate is:
    (A) Fats
    (B) Proteins
    (C) Organic acids   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Glucose
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Respiratory Quotient is the ratio of the number of carbon dioxide molecules produced to the number of oxygen molecules used during respiration. RQ is more than one in case the substrate is organic acids.

Q15. Which is the most common respiratory substrate?
    (A) Fats
    (B) Carbohydrates   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Amino acids
    (D) Organic acids
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The compounds that are oxidized during this process are known as respiratory substrates. Usually, carbohydrates are oxidized to release energy, but proteins, fats, and even organic acids can be used as respiratory substances in some plants.

Respiration In Plants Test-05  (id 3409) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Respiration in Plants
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. The enzyme that interconnects the glycolysis and Kreb cycle is:
    (A) NADH
    (B) NADP
    (C) Oxalo acetic acid
    (D) Acetyl-CoA   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The two molecules of pyruvic acid (produced from one glucose molecule during glycolysis). The acetyl CoA then enters a cyclic pathway, tricarboxylic acid cycle, more commonly called as Krebs’ cycle. Thus, acetyl-CoA is interconnecting between two cyclic pathways.

Q2. The respiratory ratio of protein is _________.
    (A) 0.8   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 1.0
    (C) 0.7
    (D) 0.2
    Answer: A
    Explanation: When proteins are respiratory substrates the ratio would be about 0.8. Due to the complexity of the various ways in which different amino acids can be metabolized, no single RQ can be assigned to the oxidation of protein in the diet; however, 0.8 is a frequently utilized estimate.

Q3. The respiratory pathway (Kreb’s cycle) is involved in both anabolism and catabolism because it provides _________.
    (A) Produce energy as well as use energy
    (B) A number of final products
    (C) ATP is released as well as utilised
    (D) A number of intermediates   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: During the breakdown and synthesis of protein too, respiratory intermediates form the link. Breaking down processes within the living organism is catabolism, and synthesis is anabolism. Because the respiratory pathway (Kreb’s cycle) is involved in both anabolism and catabolism, it would hence be better to consider the respiratory pathway.

Q4. The respiratory quotient (RQ) is defined as:
    (A) The volume of O_2 evolved / Volume of CO_2 consumed
    (B) The volume of CO_2 evolved / Volume of O_2 consumed   <-- CORRECT
    (C) The volume of CO_2 consumed/ Volume of O_2 evolved
    (D) The volume of O_2 consumed/ Volume of CO_2 evolved
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The ratio of the volume of carbon dioxide evolved to the volume of oxygen consumed in respiration is called the respiratory quotient(RQ) or respiratory ratio.

Q5. The respiratory quotient depends upon:
    (A) ATP
    (B) NADH
    (C) Respiratory products
    (D) Respiratory substrates   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The respiratory quotient depends on the type of respiratory substrate used during the act of respiration. Additionally, the respiratory quotient is a dimensionless number used in the calculations of the basal metabolic rate or BMR when estimated from the carbon dioxide production.

Q6. Glycerol would enter the amphibolic pathway after being converted into
    (A) Glucose
    (B) Acetyl co A
    (C) PGAL (Glyceraldehyde 3-phosphate)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Fatty acids
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Fats would need to be broken down into glycerol and fatty acids first. If fatty acids were to be respired they would first be degraded to acetyl CoA and enter the pathway. Glycerol would enter the pathway after being converted to PGAL. The proteins would be degraded by proteases and the individual amino acids (after deamination) depending on their structure would enter the pathway at some stage within the Krebs’ cycle or even as pyruvate or acetyl CoA.

Q7. Which one is known as the energy currency of the living cells?
    (A) GTP
    (B) ATP   <-- CORRECT
    (C) UTP
    (D) ADP
    Answer: B
    Explanation: ATP is known as the energy currency of living cells because the energy produced during respiration is stored in the form of ATP, which can be utilized for performing different activities.

Q8. The most common respiratory substrate is _______.
    (A) Protein
    (B) Fat
    (C) Organic acid
    (D) Glucose   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The most common respiratory substrate is glucose. Glucose gets oxidized completely to produce carbon dioxide and water along with ATP molecules.

Q9. Respiratory quotient (R.Q) is less than unity in the case of_____.
    (A) Glucose
    (B) Organic acid
    (C) Protein   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Starch
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The respiratory quotient is the ratio of the volume of carbon dioxide produced to the volume of oxygen consumed in respiration over a period of time. Its value can be one, zero, more than 1 or less than one. RQ is less than one when respiration is aerobic but the respiratory substrate is either fat or protein.

Q10. Before combining with oxaloacetate, pyruvate is changed into:
    (A) Succinic acid
    (B) Citric acid
    (C) Malic acid
    (D) Acetyl Co A   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Pyruvate produced during Glycolysis is changed into Acetyl CoA for Kreb’s cycle to proceed further to combine with oxaloacetate molecule, a six-carbon compound.

Q11. Reduction in consumption of respiratory substrate when the mode of respiration is changed from aerobic to anaerobic is called:
    (A) Krebs Effect
    (B) Substrate Effect
    (C) London Effect
    (D) Pasteur Effect   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: A slowing or complete cessation of alcoholic fermentation in the presence of oxygen; first observed by L. Pasteur in 1857. The effect also occurs in animals and plant tissues, where O_2 inhibits anaerobic glycolysis.

Q12. If both fatty acids and carbohydrates are available to muscles, which one is consumed first in respiration?
    (A) Fatty acids
    (B) Carbohydrates   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Both Carbohydrates and Fatty acids
    (D) Minerals
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Carbohydrates are the chief respiratory material. Starch and sucrose are the most important respiratory substrate. The reserve carbohydrates like starch are first transformed into simple carbohydrates. Then they are consumed in respiration. Fats: Fats are respiratory substrate in oily seeds. Fats are first converted into sugars. Then they are used in the respiratory process.

Q13. Metabolism of one palmitic acid molecules yields_______.
    (A) 36 ATP
    (B) 136 ATP
    (C) 129   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 56 ATP
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Energy Yield of Palmitic Acid (16C):
8 Acetyl-CoA (1 for each round + the remaining from the last two carbons) 7 FADH_2 7 NADH.
Each Acetyl-CoA yields 12 ATPs, thus 8 Acetyl-CoA will yield 96 ATPs. Each FADH_2 yields 2 ATPs while each NADH yields 3 ATPs
8 Acetyl-CoA $\times$ 12 = 96 ATPs
7 FADH_2 $\times$ 2 = 14 ATPs
7 NADH $\times$ 3 = 21 ATPs
The total energy yield is 131 ATPs, but the activation of the fatty acid (step 1) requires 2 ATPs so the net yield of energy is 129 ATPs for a molecule of palmitic acid (16 carbon).

Q14. Which of the following pair act as ETC poison?
    (A) 2:4 Dinitrophenol and alcohol
    (B) Cyanide and FAD
    (C) Cyanide and Antimycin   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Antimycin and aldehyde
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Cyanide and antimycin act as ETC (electron transport chain) poison to prevent the synthesis of ATP that leads to starvation of energy and leads to death.

Q15. Which compound is the terminal electron acceptor in aerobic respiration?
    (A) Carbon dioxide
    (B) Ethanol
    (C) Hydrogen
    (D) Oxygen   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In the electron transport chain, electron passes through different acceptor of electron and produce ATP. The terminal electron acceptor in aerobic respiration is Oxygen.

Plant Growth And Development Test-01  (id 3410) [FREE]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Plant Growth and Development
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. How many cells per hour does a single maize root apical meristem can give?
    (A) 1,750
    (B) 1,75,000
    (C) 17,500   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 175
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Growth is measured by a variety of parameters some of which are: increase in fresh weight, dry weight, length, area, volume, and cell number. One single maize root apical meristem can give rise to more than 17,500 new cells per hour, whereas cells in watermelon may increase in size by up to 3,50,000 times. In the former, growth is expressed as an increase in cell number; the latter expresses growth as an increase in the size of the cell.

Q2. The process of de-specialization of differentiated cells so that they become undifferentiated and meristematic is called ________.
    (A) Development
    (B) ReDifferentiation
    (C) Differentiation
    (D) Dedifferentiation   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The process of de-specialization of differentiated cells so that they become undifferen­tiated and able to divide is known as dedifferentiation. It involves the activation of certain genes that not only reverse differentiation but also stimulate cell division. Cork cambium, wound cambium and inter-fascicular vascular cambium are always produced through dedifferentia­tion.

Q3. The undifferentiated mass of parenchymatous cells are called:
    (A) Cytokinesis
    (B) Cambium
    (C) Callus   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Carotenoids
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Plant callus is a growing mass of unorganized plant parenchyma cells. In living plants, callus cells are those cells that cover a plant wound.

Q4. The correct sequence leading to the growth curve:
    (A) stationary, log, lag phases
    (B) lag, log, stationary phases   <-- CORRECT
    (C) log, lag, stationary phases
    (D) lag, stationary, log phases
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The initial growth is slow (lag phase), and it increases rapidly thereafter - at an exponential rate (log or exponential phase). Here, both the progeny cells following mitotic cell division retain the ability to divide and continue to do so. However, with limited nutrient supply, the growth slows down leading to a stationary phase.

Q5. Auxins are generally produced in:
    (A) Phloem
    (B) Root and shoot tips   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Leaves
    (D) Xylem
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Auxins promote stem elongation, inhibit the growth of lateral buds (maintains apical dominance). They are produced in the stem, buds, and root tips. Example, Indole Acetic Acid (IA). Auxin is a plant hormone produced in the stem tip that promotes cell elongation.

Q6. The differentiated cells have lost the capacity to divide can regain the capacity of the division under certain conditions called _______.
    (A) Dedifferentiation   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Maturation
    (C) Re differentiation
    (D) Differentiation
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The living differentiated cells that have lost the capacity to divide can regain the capacity of the division under certain conditions. This phenomenon is termed as dedifferentiation.

Q7. Measurement and the comparison of total growth per unit time is called _________.
    (A) Relative growth rate
    (B) Arithmetic growth rate
    (C) Absolute growth rate   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Geometric growth rate
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The absolute growth rate refers to the measurement and comparison of total growth per unit time. Thus, Absolute growth = Growth in a given time period. Relative growth rate refers to the growth of a particular system per unit time, expressed on a common basis.

Q8. Which of the following events are arranged in the correct order?
    (A) Growth, development, differentiation
    (B) Growth, differentiation, development   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Development, differentiation, growth
    (D) Differentiation, growth, development
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Growth, differentiation, and development are very closely related events in the life of a plant. Broadly, development is considered as the sum of growth and differentiation.

Q9. All changes that an organism goes through during its life cycle is called _________.
    (A) Development   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Maturation
    (C) Differentiation
    (D) Elongation
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Development is a term that includes all changes that an organism goes through during its life cycle from germination of the seed to senescence.

Q10. The phenomenon of heterophylly is an example of _______.
    (A) Development
    (B) Redifferentiation
    (C) Senescence
    (D) Plasticity   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Plants follow different pathways in response to the environment or phases of life to form different kinds of structures. This ability is called plasticity. This phenomenon of heterophylly is an example of plasticity.

Q11. Auxanometer is used to measure
    (A) Leaf number
    (B) Pest population
    (C) Growth in breadth
    (D) Growth in length   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: An auxanometer (Gr. auxain, "to grow" + metron, "measure") is an apparatus for measuring increase or rate of growth in plants.
In case of an arc-auxanometer (see picture), there is a wire fixed with the plant apex on one end and a dead-weight on the other.

Q12. Maximum growth occurs in:
    (A) Stationary phase
    (B) Leg phase
    (C) Exponential phase   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Senescent phase
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In growth curve, maximum growth occurs in the exponential phase of the sigmoid curve. During these periods cells divide mitotically to increase the length and girth of the plant.

Q13. Which growth is also called apparent growth?
    (A) Irreversible increase in mass or volume   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Reversible decrease in mass and volume
    (C) Reversible increase in mass and volume
    (D) Irreversible decrease in mass and volume
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Irreversible increase in mass or volume of plant part is called apparent growth. Apparent growth is permanent and cannot be reversed back as it occurs due to increase in cell number.

Q14. The S-shaped graph produced on plotting growth against time is called _________.
    (A) Relative growth curve
    (B) Arithmetic growth line
    (C) Sigmoid growth curve   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Geometric line
    Answer: C
    Explanation: S-Shaped growth curve (Sigmoid growth curve) A pattern of growth in which, in a new environment, the population density of an organism increases slowly initially, in a positive acceleration phase; then increases rapidly approaching an exponential growth rate, but then declines in a negative acceleration phase until at zero growth rate the population stabilizes. This slowing of the rate of growth reflects increasing environmental resistance which becomes proportionately more important at higher population densities. This type of population growth is termed ‘density-dependent’.

Q15. The point at which exponential phase ends and decelerating phase begins is called
    (A) Compensation point
    (B) Inflexion point   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Saturation point
    (D) Relaxation point
    Answer: B
    Explanation: An inflection point is a point on a curve at which the sign of the curvature (i.e., the concavity) changes. Inflection points may be stationary points, but are not local maxima or local minima.
For example, for the curve plotted given, the red point is an inflection point.

Plant Growth And Development Test-02  (id 3411) [PAID]

Q1. Which of the following areas in the higher plants take part in the formation of new cells?
    (A) Meristems   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Parenchyma
    (C) Permanent tissue
    (D) Collenchyma
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The tissues that have the ability of cell division located in a specific area are called meristem. They are located at stem and root tips, nodes of the stem, and intercalary region.

Q2. Permanent and irreversible increase in dry weight, size, and mass, the volume of cell, organ, or organism is called ________.
    (A) Differentiation
    (B) Development
    (C) Regeneration
    (D) Growth   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Growth is defined as a permanent or irreversible increase in dry weight, size, mass, or volume of a cell, organ, or organism. Growth in living beings is intrinsic or internal.

Q3. In dicotyledonous plants, the girth of the stem and root increase due to ________.
    (A) Primary growth
    (B) Development
    (C) Differentiation
    (D) Secondary growth   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Secondary growth is the result of the activity of the two lateral meristems, the cork cambium, and vascular cambium. Arising from lateral meristems, secondary growth increases the girth of the plant root or stem, rather than its length.

Q4. Mathematically arithmetic growth is expressed as ________.
    (A) L_t = L_0 + rt   <-- CORRECT
    (B) L_t = L_0.rt
    (C) L_t = $\frac{L_0}{rt}$
    (D) L_t = L_0 - rt
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Arithmetic growth is represented by L_t = L_0 + rt where L_t is final growth, L_0 is the initial size and r_t is the rate of growth and time respectively.

Q5. It is the testing of biological activity like growth response of a substance by employing a living material like plant or plant part.
    (A) Autopsy
    (B) Fractionalisation
    (C) Separation
    (D) Bioassay   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Testing of biological activity like the growth response of a substance by employing a living material like a plant or plant part is called bioassay. It is used to know the effect of the substance on plant growth.

Q6. Exponential growth is dependent on:
    (A) Initial size, nutrient availability and time interval
    (B) Initial size, rate of growth and time interval   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Plant type, initial size and time interval
    (D) Initial size, rate of growth and season
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Exponential growth is dependent on initial size, rate of growth, and time interval. L_t = L_0 + rt.

Q7. Which one is not a phase of Growth?
    (A) Formative phase
    (B) Linear phase   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Phase of maturation
    (D) Phase of enlargement
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Growth phase consists of leg phase, exponential phase and stable phase. It does not consist of linear phase.

Q8. The graphical representation of the total growth against time is called _________.
    (A) Growth curve   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Growth phase
    (C) Growth graph
    (D) Growth table
    Answer: A
    Explanation: A growth curve is an empirical model of the evolution of a quantity over time or a graphical representation of how a particular quantity increases over time. Growth curves are used in statistics to determine the type of growth pattern of the quantity - be it linear, exponential or cubic. It is also known as Sigmoid curve.

Q9. If W_1 is the final size, W_0 is initial size, r is the growth rate and t is a time of growth than Exponential growth is represented by:
    (A) W_1 = W_0 - e^rt
    (B) W_1 = W_0.e^rt2
    (C) W_1 = W_0.e_2^rt
    (D) W_1 = W_0.e^rt   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Exponential growth is represented by initial size and growth rate and time. If W_1 is the final size, W_0 is the initial size, r is the growth rate and t is the time of growth than exponential growth is W_1 = W_0.e^rt

Q10. Natural cytokinins are synthesized in:
    (A) Stem
    (B) Root apices   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Seeds
    (D) Leaf
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Natural cytokinins are synthesised in regions where rapid cell division occurs, for example, root apices.

Q11. Which one prevents premature fall of fruit?
    (A) Ethylene
    (B) Zeatin
    (C) NAA   <-- CORRECT
    (D) GA1
    Answer: C
    Explanation: They help to prevent fruit and leaf drop at early stages but promote the abscission of older mature leaves and fruits.

Q12. Which hormone is responsible for seed dormancy?
    (A) Auxin
    (B) ABA   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Gibberellin
    (D) Cytokinin
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Abscisic acid encourages fruit to drop and leaves to fall. When the plant is low on water abscisic acid closes the stomata, pores in the leaves. It encourages both seeds and plants to go dormant. The hormone induces seeds to produce proteins to store when the seeds are dormant.

Q13. Auxin was isolated from tips of coleoptiles of oat seedlings by:
    (A) Miller
    (B) Went   <-- CORRECT
    (C) E.Kurosawa
    (D) Skoog
    Answer: B
    Explanation: F. W. Went isolated auxins (1926) from tips of coleoptiles of oat seedlings. Isolation of auxins from tips of coleoptiles of oat seedlings is based upon. Avena coleoptile curvature test. The result will be differential growth and formation of curvature. Degree of curvature is almost proportional to the concentration of auxin.

Q14. Auxins are mostly produced in:
    (A) Root
    (B) Meristematic region   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Leaf buds
    (D) Shoot
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Auxins are generally produced in growing apices of shoot and root. These two regions are the meristematic cells that are actively taken part in cell division.

Q15. Natural auxins among the following are:
    (A) NAA and 2, 4 D
    (B) IBA and NAA
    (C) IAA and IBA   <-- CORRECT
    (D) IAA and 2, 4 D
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Auxins like IAA and indole butyric acid (IBA) have been isolated from plants. (naturally). NAA (naphthalene acetic acid) and 2, 4-D (2, 4-dichlorophenoxyacetic) are synthetic auxins.

Plant Growth And Development Test-03  (id 3412) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Plant Growth and Development
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
