Q1. Abscisic acid is also known as:
    (A) Cell hormone
    (B) Ripening hormone
    (C) Stress hormone   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Shoot hormone
    Answer: C
    Explanation: ABA stimulates the closure of stomata in the epidermis and increases the tolerance of plants to various kinds of stresses. Therefore, it is also called the stress hormone.

Q2. In rosette plants, bolting is due to:
    (A) Gibberellins   <-- CORRECT
    (B) ABA
    (C) Cytokinins
    (D) Auxins
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Gibberellins also promote bolting (internode elongation just prior to flowering) in beet, cabbages, and many plants with rosette habit.

Q3. Which plant hormone is named anti-ageing hormone?
    (A) Gibberellins
    (B) Ethylene
    (C) Cytokinin   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Abscisic acid
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A unique role of cytokinins is to produce anti-ageing effects on some plant parts. Cytokinins actually provide a younger, healthier look in plants. By adding this hormone to cut flowers, florists are able to slow down the ageing process, providing us with prettier flowers for longer.

Q4. In higher plants, the growing apical bud inhibits the growth of the lateral buds. This phenomenon is called _______.
    (A) Apical dominance   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Differentiation
    (C) Decapitation
    (D) Dormancy
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Apical dominance is the phenomenon whereby the main, central stem of the plant is dominant over (i.e., grows more strongly than) other side stems; on a branch, the main stem of the branch is further dominant over its own side branchlets.

Q5. Growth regulator ethylene is used for:
    (A) Producing seedless fruits
    (B) Increasing the size of fruit
    (C) Speeding up of ripening of fruits   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Slowing down the ripening of fruits
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Ethylene is highly effective in fruit ripening. It enhances the respiration rate during the ripening of the fruits.

Q6. Which of the following gibberellic acid is used for malting process in the brewing industry?
    (A) GA
    (B) GA_1
    (C) GA_2
    (D) GA_3   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: GA_3 is used to speed up the malting process in the brewing industry.

Q7. Which of the following hormone is used to kill dicotyledonous weeds?
    (A) Gibberellin
    (B) ABA
    (C) 2,4 D   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Cytokinin
    Answer: C
    Explanation: 2, 4 D (2,4-Dichlorophenoxyacetic acid) are widely used as herbicides. It is widely used to kill dicotyledonous weeds, does not affect mature monocotyledonous plants.

Q8. Parthenocarpy can be induced to develop seedless fruit by application of:
    (A) IBA and cytokinin
    (B) Zeatin and IAA
    (C) IAA and IBA   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Ethylene and gibberellins
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Auxins (IAA, IBA) also induce parthenocarpy, (Seed fewer fruits) e.g., in tomatoes.

Q9. Identify the cytokinin given below.
    (A) Kinetin   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Zeatin
    (C) IMA
    (D) IAA
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Cytokinin is of different types. The cytokinin shown above is of kinetin which promotes cell division. It was isolated by Miller and Skoog from autoclaved herring sperm DNA.

Q10. Plant growth regulator that is used in delay in leaf senescence is_______.
    (A) Cytokinin   <-- CORRECT
    (B) ABA
    (C) Ethylene
    (D) Auxin
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Cytokinins help overcome apical dominance. They promote nutrient mobilization which helps in the delay of leaf senescence.

Q11. Kinetin was identified by:
    (A) E.kurosawa
    (B) F.skoog
    (C) Francis Darwin
    (D) Skoog and miller   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The discovery of Kinetin is comparatively more recent. Its credit goes to Miller et al (1955) who were working in Prof. Skoog’s laboratory at the University of Wisconsin on the growth of tobacco pith callus in culture and wanted it to grow indefinitely.

Q12. A farmer grows cucumber plants in his field. He wants to increase the number of female flowers in them. Which plant hormones can be applied to achieve this?
    (A) Auxins
    (B) Gibberellins
    (C) Ethylene   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Abscisic acid
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Ethylene promotes female flowers in cucumbers thereby increasing the yield.

Q13. Ethylene is a:
    (A) Adenine derivatives
    (B) Gaseous hormone   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Carotenoids
    (D) Terpenes
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Ethylene is a simple gaseous hormone. It is synthesized in large amounts by tissues undergoing senescence and ripening fruits.

Q14. The most commonly used compound as a source of ethylene
    (A) Ethephon   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Kinetin
    (C) IBA
    (D) Zeatin
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The most widely used compound as a source of ethylene is ethephon. Ethephon in an aqueous solution is readily absorbed and transported within the plant and releases ethylene slowly.

Q15. How many numbers of gibberellins are distributed in different organisms?
    (A) More than 150
    (B) More than 10
    (C) More than 100   <-- CORRECT
    (D) More than 200
    Answer: C
    Explanation: There are more than 100 gibberellins reported from widely different organisms such as fungi and higher plants. They are denoted as GA1, GA2, GA3, and so on.

Plant Growth And Development Test-04  (id 3413) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Plant Growth and Development
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. Phytochrome is sensitive to:
    (A) Red and far-red light   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Yellow light
    (C) Blue light
    (D) Green light
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Phytochrome is a photoreceptor and a pigment that plants, and some bacteria and fungi, use to detect light. It is sensitive to light in the red and far-red regions of the visible spectrum.

Q2. Antiauxin used in picking cotton bolls is______.
    (A) TIBA   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Ethylene
    (C) NNA
    (D) 2,4-D
    Answer: A
    Explanation: TIBA (2,3,5 Triidobenzoic acid) acts as antiauxin that inhibits root and shoots formation. TIBA is used as an antiauxin in picking cotton bolls.

Q3. Which pair of hormones promotes femaleness in flowers?
    (A) Ethylene and ABA
    (B) Ethylene and cytokinins
    (C) Auxin and ethylene   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Auxin and abscisic acid
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Flower Sex Conversions:
 Gibberellins (GA_3) promote maleness
 Ethylene and auxins promote femaleness

Q4. What would be expected to happen if a rotten fruit gets mixed with unripe fruits?
    (A) Unripe fruits have no effect
    (B) Rot the unripe fruits
    (C) Slow down the ripening of unripe fruits
    (D) Increasing to ripen of unripe fruits   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Rotten fruit produces ethylene gas that hastens the ripening of unripe fruits. So, if a rotten fruit gets mixed with unripe fruits the remaining unripe get ripen faster.

Q5. If GA3 is applied to the rice seedlings, the plant will show:
    (A) Dwarfing
    (B) Delayed ripening
    (C) Extra elongation   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Early flowering
    Answer: C
    Explanation: GA3 is gibberellin that helps in the elongation of the stem of the plant. If the GA3 plant hormone is applied to the rice seedling the plant will show extra elongation of the plant body.

Q6. You forget to add Cytokinin the culture medium, there will be very little growth as Cytokinin is essential for:
    (A) Cell division and cell differentiation   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Cell maturation and cell expansion
    (C) Cell differentiation and cell elongation
    (D) Cell division and cell elongation
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Cytokinin is added to the culture medium to induce cell division and cell differentiation. If cytokine is not added to the culture medium, there will be very little growth in culture.

Q7. A student culture a callus from the tobacco pith in sterilized minimal nutritive medium but add more Cytokinin than Auxin. What would develop first from callus?
    (A) Roots
    (B) Shoots   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Leaves
    (D) Buds
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Shoots

Q8. In the wheat field, some broad-leaved weeds were seen by a farmer, which plant hormone would you suggest getting rid of the same?
    (A) 2 : 4-D and 2 : 4 :5 T   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 2 : 6-D and 2 : 2 :5 T
    (C) 2 : 5-D and 2 : 5 :5 T
    (D) 2 : 2-D and 2 : 4 :6 T
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Plant hormone 2 : 4-D and 2 : 4 : 5 T have ability to kills the weeds in the crop field. Weeds are unwanted plants that grow along with crop plants and compete with the crop for nutrient and water.

Q9. Auxin precursor for IAA is:
    (A) Aspartic acid
    (B) Buteric acid
    (C) Tryptophan   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Alanine
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The major precursor of Auxin is most likely the amino acid Tryptophan. However, the tryptophan is possibly derived from the shikimic acid pathway. Numerous enzymes would be utilized for Auxin alone. the ultimate precursor depends on how far you want to follow the production back.

Q10. Photoperiodism stimulus is perceived by
    (A) Leaves   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Meristem
    (C) Flower
    (D) Buds
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The response of plants to periods of day/night is termed photoperiodism. The site of perception of light/dark duration is the leaves.

Q11. Flowering in short-day plants is stimulated by:
    (A) Short day and short night
    (B) Short nights
    (C) Short day and uninterrupted long nights   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Short day and interrupted long nights
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Short-day (i.e.long-night) plants flower as days grow shorter (and nights grow longer) after 21 June in the northern hemisphere, which is during summer or fall. Short-day plants flower when the night lengths exceed their critical photoperiod. They cannot flower under short nights or if a pulse of artificial light is shone on the plant for several minutes during the night; they require a continuous period of darkness before floral development can begin.

Q12. Vernalisation takes place in response to:
    (A) Humidity
    (B) High light intensity
    (C) High temperature
    (D) Low temperature   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: There are plants for which flowering is either quantitatively or qualitatively dependent on exposure to low temperature. This phenomenon is termed vernalization.

Q13. A process of shortening of the juvenile or vegetative phase and hastening flowering by a previous cold treatment is
    (A) Shortening
    (B) Photoperiodic
    (C) Cold and hot treatment
    (D) Vernalization   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Vernalization is the induction of a plant's flowering process by exposure to the prolonged cold of winter, or by an artificial equivalent.

Q14. Short day plants are also called long night plant because they require a continuous:
    (A) Critical light period
    (B) Critical dark period   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Uninterrupted season period
    (D) Interrupted night period
    Answer: B
    Explanation: A plant that requires a long period of darkness, is termed a "short day" (long night) plant. Short-day plants form flowers only when day length is less than about 12 hours. Many spring and fall flowering plants are short-day plants.

Q15. Photoperiodism was discovered by:
    (A) F.F.Blackman
    (B) W.Went
    (C) Garner and Allard   <-- CORRECT
    (D) F.E.Fritsch
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In 1920, W. W. Garner and H. A. Allard published their discoveries on photoperiodism and felt it was the length of daylight that was critical, but it was later discovered that the length of the night was the controlling factor.

Digestion And Absorption Test-01  (id 3414) [FREE]

Q1. The teeth occur in human beings are:
    (A) diphyodont, homodont and acrodont
    (B) monophyodont, homodont and thecodont
    (C) monophyodont, heterodont and acrodont
    (D) diphyodont, heterodont and thecodont   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Each tooth is embedded in a socket of a jaw bone called thecodont. The human being forms two sets of teeth during their life temporary milk or deciduous teeth replaced by a set of permanent or adult teeth called diphyodont. An adult human has 32 permanent teeth which are of four different types called heterodont.

Q2. Complete the following reaction:
 Maltose - Maltase $\rightarrow$ Glucose + i
 Lactose - Lactase $\rightarrow$ Glucose + ii
 Sucrose - Sucrase $\rightarrow$ Glucose + iii
    (A) i - glucose
 ii - galactose
 iii - fructose   <-- CORRECT
    (B) i-mannose
 ii-glucose
 iii-galactose
    (C) i-fructose
 ii-galactose
 iii-glucose
    (D) i-galactose
 ii-glucose
 iii-fructose
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Maltose in presence of maltase produces two molecules of glucose. Lactose in the presence of lactase produces glucose and galactose. Sucrose in the presence of sucrose produces glucose and fructose.

Q3. Which of the following is not a part of the colon?
    (A) Longitudinal colon   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Ascending colon
    (C) Transverse colon
    (D) Pelvic colon
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The colon is divided into three parts - an ascending, a transverse and a descending part.

Q4. Brunner’s gland is:
    (A) Gastro-intestinal sphincter
    (B) Sub-mucosal gland   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Hepatic-pancreatic duct
    (D) Gastric gland
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Brunner’s glands are submucosal mucin secreting glands localized predominantly in the duodenal bulb and proximal duodenum, decreasing progressively in size and number in the distal portions. Sub-mucosal glands (Brunner’s glands) provide the alkaline medium.

Q5. Match the cells and their secretions:
 Cell Type
 Secretion
 a) Goblet cell
 i) succusentericus
 b) Oxyntic cells
 ii) mucus
 c) Chief cells
 iii) acid
 d) Intestinal gland cells
 iv) pepsinogen
    (A) a) - ii
 b) - iii
 c) - i
 d) - iv
    (B) a) - ii 
 b) - iii 
 c) - iv
 d) - i   <-- CORRECT
    (C) a) - ii
 b) - i
 c) - iv
 d) - iii
    (D) a) - iv
 b) - i
 c) - ii
 d) - iii
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The intestinal mucosal epithelium has goblet cells which secrete mucus. The secretions of the brush border cells of the mucosa along with the secretions of the goblet cells constitute the intestinal juice or succusentericus. The peptic or chief cells which secrete the proenzyme pepsinogen. The parietal or oxyntic cells secrete HCl acid.

Q6. The part which is common passage for both digestive and respiratory tracts :
    (A) Pharynx   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Trachea
    (C) Oesophagus
    (D) Larynx
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In humans, the pharynx is part of the digestive system and also of the conducting zone of the respiratory system. The oesophagus and the trachea (windpipe) open into the pharynx.

Q7. All are digestive glands except:
    (A) Thyroid gland   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Pancreas
    (C) Liver
    (D) Salivary gland
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The thyroid is part of the endocrine system, which is made up of glands that produce, store, and release hormones into the bloodstream so the hormones can reach the body's cells. The thyroid gland uses iodine from the foods you eat to make two main hormones: Triiodothyronine (T_3) Thyroxine (T_4).

Q8. ________ from pharynx is conveyed into the oesophagus by ________.
    (A) Chyme, degluition
    (B) Bolus, deglutition   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Bolus, regurgition
    (D) Chyme, regurgition
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The bolus is conveyed into the pharynx and then into the oesophagus by swallowing or deglutition.

Q9. The bile duct and the pancreatic duct open together into the duodenum as:
    (A) Duct of liver
    (B) Cystic duct
    (C) Hepatic duct
    (D) Hepato-pancreatic duct   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The bile duct and the pancreatic duct open together into the duodenum as the common hepato-pancreatic duct which is guarded by a sphincter called the sphincter of Oddi.

Q10. Digestion can be defined as:
    (A) Intake and direct cellular utilisation of biomacromolecules present in food
    (B) Breakdown of simple molecules into absorbable forms
    (C) Reduction of food molecules to produce energy
    (D) Breakdown of complex molecules into absorbable forms   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Digestion is the breakdown of large insoluble food molecules into small water-soluble food molecules so that they can be absorbed into the watery blood plasma. In certain organisms, these smaller substances are absorbed through the small intestine into the bloodstream.

Q11. Which among the following is not in the wall of the alimentary canal?
    (A) Mucosa
    (B) Sub-serosa   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Sub-mucosa
    (D) Serosa
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The wall of the alimentary canal from the oesophagus to rectum possesses four layers namely serosa, muscularis, sub-mucosa and mucosa.

Q12. Which layer of alimentary canal forms villi?
    (A) Mucosa   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Muscularis
    (C) Sub-mucosa
    (D) Serosa
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Mucosa layer forms irregular folds (rugae) in the stomach and small finger-like foldings called villi in the small intestine.

Q13. Read the following statements:
 Opening of the hepato-pancreatic duct into jejunum is guarded by Sphincter of Oddi.
 Duodenum receives bile-pancreatic duct.
    (A) Statement B is wrong and A is correct
    (B) Statement B is correct and A is wrong   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Both statements are wrong
    (D) Both statements are correct
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Duodenum receives bile from the pancreatic duct. Bile contains bile juice that contains bile salt used for emulsification of fat. Sphincter of Oddi is not present between hepatic-pancreatic duct into the jejunum.

Q14. The dental formula for human deciduous and permanent set are 212/212 and 2123/2123. So the deciduous set lacks:
    (A) Molars
    (B) Incisors
    (C) Canines
    (D) Premolars   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Arrangement of teeth in each half of the upper and lower jaw in the order I, C, P, M, is represented by a dental formula which in human is 2123/2123. 212/212 lacks premolar.

Q15. Match the following:
 Nutrient
 Absorbable Forms
 (i) Carbohydrate
 (a) Amino acids
 (ii) Nucleic acid
 (b) Monosaccharides
 (iii) Proteins
 (c) Sugar and bases
 (iv) Lipids
 (d) Fatty acids and glycerol
    (A) (i) - (b), (ii) - (c), (iii) - (d), (iv) - (a)
    (B) (i) - (d), (ii) - (a), (iii) - (b), (iv) - (c)
    (C) (i) - (b), (ii) - (c), (iii) - (a), (iv) - (d)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (i) - (b), (ii) - (a), (iii) - (d), (iv) - (c)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Carbohydrate is converted into monosaccharides, the nucleic acid is converted into sugar and bases by nucleosidases, proteins are converted into amino acids by dipeptidases and lipids are converted into fatty acids and glycerol by lipases.

Digestion And Absorption Test-02  (id 3415) [PAID]

Q1. Which layer of the alimentary canal is formed of loose connective tissues?
    (A) Mucosa
    (B) Sub-mucosa   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Serosa
    (D) Muscularis
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The submucosa consists of a dense and irregular layer of loose connective tissue with blood vessels, lymphatics, and nerves branching into the mucosa and muscular layer. It contains the submucous plexus, an enteric nervous plexus, situated on the inner surface of the muscular layer.

Q2. The enzyme which hydrolyzes the starch is_______.
    (A) Carboxypeptidase
    (B) Amylase   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Lysozyme
    (D) Lipases
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The enzymes that break down or hydrolyze starch into the constituent sugars are known as amylases. Alpha-amylases are found in plants and in animals. Human saliva is rich in amylase, and the pancreas also secretes the enzyme.

Q3. What should be filled in to replace the question mark in the following sequence:
?$\to$Trypsinogen $\to$Trypsin
    (A) Carboxypeptidase
    (B) Tryptokinase
    (C) Enterokinase   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Intestinal Protease
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Trypsinogen is activated by an enzyme, enterokinase, secreted by the intestinal mucosa into active trypsin.

Q4. The arrows represent :[upward to downward]
    (A) Pancreas and pancreatic duct
    (B) Gall bladder and cystic duct   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Gall bladder and common bile duct
    (D) Liver and hepatic duct
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The figure shows the muscular sac called the gall bladder. The duct of gall bladder (cystic duct) along with the hepatic duct from the liver forms the common bile duct.

Q5. The secretions released into small intestine are:
    (A) Bile and intestinal juices
    (B) Pancreatic and intestinal juices
    (C) Bile, pancreatic and intestinal juices   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Bile and pancreatic juices
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The bile, pancreatic juice, and intestinal juice are the secretions released into the small intestine.

Q6. Which layer of alimentary canal forms crypts in between the base of villi?
    (A) Mucosa   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Muscularis
    (C) Sub-mucosa
    (D) Serosa
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Mucosa forms gastric glands in the stomach and crypts in between the bases of villi in the intestine (crypts of Lieberkuhn).

Q7. The optimum pH meant for hydrolyzing starch is______.
    (A) 5.4
    (B) 6.8   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 8.6
    (D) 4.5
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Amylase is an enzyme that catalyses the hydrolysis of starch into sugars. Amylase is present in the saliva of humans and some other mammals, where it begins the chemical process of digestion. it is a major digestive enzyme, and its optimum pH is 6.8

Q8. An active form of which enzyme hydrolyses milk protein in the stomach?
    (A) Rennin
    (B) Trypsin
    (C) Pepsin   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Chymotrypsin
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Chymosin, known also as rennin, is a proteolytic enzyme related to pepsin that synthesized by chief cells in the stomach of some animals. Its role in digestion is to curdle or coagulate milk in the stomach, a process of considerable importance in the very young animal.

Q9. The correct sequence of layers in the gut wall from inside to outside is :
    (A) Submucosa →Mucosa → Muscularis → Serosa
    (B) Muscularis →Mucosa → Submucosa → Serosa
    (C) Mucosa → Submucosa → Muscularis → Serosa   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Mucosa → Muscularis → Submucosa → Serosa
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Serosa is the outermost layer while mucosa is the innermost layer. The layer next to mucosa is the sub-mucosa containing nerves, blood, and lymph vessels. Muscularisis found between sub-mucosa and serosa.

Q10. One of the gut hormones which is often referred to as the hunger hormone since it works as a strong stimulant for appetite and feeding is:
    (A) Secretin
    (B) Ghrelin   <-- CORRECT
    (C) GLP-1
    (D) Gastrin
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Ghrelin the hunger hormone is a peptide hormone produced by ghrelinergic cells in the gastrointestinal tract which function as a neuropeptide in the central nervous system. It stimulates appetite and feeding.

Q11. Numerous folds present on the inner surface of the stomach are called rugae. Another part of the digestive tract which contains rugae is______.
    (A) Tongue
    (B) Saliva
    (C) Palate   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Teeth
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Numerous folds present on the inner surface of the stomach are called rugae. They are a series of ridges produced by the folding of the wall of an organ. Another part of the digestive tract which contains rugae is the palate, the top part of the inside mouth.

Q12. Which of the following is not secreted from its source in the form of a Zymogen?
    (A) Angiotensin
    (B) Carboxypeptidase
    (C) Chymotrypsin
    (D) Amylase   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Zymogen is an inactive enzyme precursor that requires a biochemical change to become active. The amylase enzyme is not released from its source in the form of a proenzyme or zymogen.

Q13. Which of the following is not a part of the human alimentary canal?
    (A) Jejunum
    (B) Duodenum
    (C) Ilium   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Colon
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The Ilium is the uppermost and largest bone of the pelvis invertebrates. Duodenum jejunum and colon are parts of the human alimentary canal but ileum is not a part of this system.

Q14. The correct sequence of lipid digestion in alimentary canal is :
    (A) lipid → micelles → chylomicrons → emulsified globules
    (B) lipid → micelles → emulsified globules → chylomicrons
    (C) lipid → emulsified globules → chylomicrons → micelles
    (D) lipid → emulsified globules → micelles → chylomicrons   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Digestion of (lipid) fat begins in small intestine by secretion of bile juice that contains bile salts. Bile salt emulsify the lipids into globules that is further simplified into micelles and chylomicrons.

Q15. In elephant and walrus, projecting tusks are:
    (A) Premolars and canines respectively
    (B) Molars and incisors respectively
    (C) Incisors and canines respectively   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Canines and incisors respectively
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The projecting tusk of elephant and walrus are incisors and canines respectively. These teeth are not used for chewing food.

Digestion And Absorption Test-03  (id 3416) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Digestion and Absorption (FA ONLY)

Q1. Which of the following statement is/ are incorrect for the Enteric nervous system:
 neurons of Myentric plexus regulates glandular secretions in the GI tract.
 neurons of Meissner’s plexus regulates peristaltic waves.
    (A) i is incorrect
    (B) i and ii are incorrect   <-- CORRECT
    (C) ii is correct and i is incorrect
    (D) i is correct and ii is incorrect
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The inner plexus is the main control for GI secretion and local blood flow. The myenteric plexus is principally responsible for the peristaltic movement of the bowels. It extends throughout the entire length of the gut as a linear chain of interconnected neurons.
The Meissner or submucosal plexus regulates the configuration of the luminal surface, controls glandular secretions, alters electrolyte and water transport, and regulates local blood flow.

Q2. Every cell contains DNA and when we consume plant/animal material, the DNA which reaches our digestive tract is digested by:
    (A) Enzymes present in bile juice and gastric juice
    (B) Enzymes present in bile juice and succusentericus
    (C) Enzymes present in pancreatic juice and succus entericus   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Enzymes present in pancreatic juice and gastric juice
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Food material consists of plant or animal cells. Each cell contains DNA in the nucleus. Digestion of DNA takes place in the small intestine by the action of enzyme succus entricus.

Q3. The process by which small electrolytes are absorbed:
    (A) Active transport
    (B) Facilitated transport
    (C) Passive transport
    (D) Simple diffusion   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Small amounts of monosaccharides like glucose, amino acids, and some of the electrolytes like chloride ions are generally absorbed by simple diffusion.

Q4. That part of alimentary canal which is responsible for absorption of water, simple sugars, and alcohol:
    (A) Mouth
    (B) Small intestine   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Large intestine
    (D) Stomach
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Absorption in different parts of the digestive system: 
 The small intestine is the primary site for the absorption of water, simple sugars (like glucose), and alcohol into the bloodstream.
 The stomach absorbs very little, though alcohol and some drugs can be absorbed here.
 The large intestine primarily absorbs water and electrolytes, but not simple sugars or alcohol.
 The mouth is involved in digestion but does not play a significant role in absorption.

Q5. Select which one is correctly matched pair:
    (A) Glucose - absorbed by passive transport that doesn’t need energy
    (B) Amino acids - transported by simple diffusion that doesn’t need energy
    (C) Fructose - transported by facilitated diffusion that doesn’t need energy   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Galactose - absorbed by active transport that doesn’t need energy
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Some of the substances like fructose and some amino acids are absorbed with the help of the carrier ions like sodium ions. This mechanism is called facilitated transport.

Q6. Absorption of food takes place in stomach as well as intestine but villi are present in intestine only because:
    (A) The stomach is already provided with microvilli
    (B) Intestine receives better blood supply than other parts of the alimentary canal
    (C) Food is converted into absorbable form within the intestine   <-- CORRECT
    (D) The stomach is not much provided with microvilli
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Villi increase the surface area thereby increasing the absorption of food. The villi also contain lymph vessels for absorbing the products of fat-digestion. From the bloodstream, the absorbed food is finally delivered to each and every cell of the body. The mucosal walls of the stomach form irregular fold known as rugae. These help in increasing the surface area to volume ratio of the expanding stomach.

Q7. Absorption of fats takes place through:
    (A) Blood capillaries
    (B) Lymphatic ducts   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Intestinal mucosa
    (D) Intestinal villi
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Lymph is the extracellular fluid that constitutes the lymphatic system in the human body. The absorption of fats takes place through lymphatic ducts. As fats cannot be carried through narrow capillaries.

Q8. Trans fats:
 they are found in most processed and fast foods for eg. French fries.
 they help food stay fresh for a long time.
 they are a much better type of fat than saturated fats.
    (A) All of these
    (B) Only i and iii are correct
    (C) Only i is the correct statement
    (D) Only i and ii are correct   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Trans fats are hydrogenated fats which make the oil more solid. They are found in most processed and fast foods. They help food stay fresh for a long time.

Q9. Read the following statements:
 In ruminants, cellulose digesting bacteria are present in the digestive system.
 Such digestion by microbial activity is called Anaerobic digestion.
 Camels are ruminants lacking the omasum chamber.
    (A) All of these   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Statement (i) and (ii) are correct
    (C) Statement (i) and (iii) are correct
    (D) Only statement (i) is correct
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In ruminants like cows, buffalos, cellulose digesting bacteria are present in the digestive system that release cellulose enzymes.
 Anaerobic digestion is a collection of processes by which microorganisms break down biodegradable material in the absence of oxygen.
 Camel is a pseudo ruminant as it has only 3 chambers instead of 4.

Q10. If an imaginary food contains 5 grams of protein, 4 grams of fat and 10 grams of carbohydrates. Now calculate total calories it would provide ( given 1g protein = 4 calories, 1g fat = 10 calories, 1g carbohydrates = 4 calories):
    (A) 96 calories
    (B) 50 calories
    (C) 100 calories   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 90 calories
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Five gram of protein will produce 5 $\times $ 4 = 20 calories, 4 g of fat = 4 $\times $ 10 = 40 calories and 10 g of carbohydrates = 10 $\times $ 4 = 40 calories. So total energy produced is equal to 20 + 40 + 40 = 100 calories.

Q11. Correct sequence of layers in gut wall from inside to outside is:
    (A) Submucosa →Mucosa → Muscularis → Serosa
    (B) Mucosa → Muscularis → Submucosa → Serosa
    (C) Mucosa → Submucosa → Muscularis → Serosa   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Muscularis →Mucosa → Submucosa → Serosa
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The wall of the alimentary canal is made of four layers performing different functions. The innermost layer is called mucosa followed by submucosa,muscularis and serosa. These layers are made of different kind of tissues to perform a different function.

Q12. The reflex action of vomiting is controlled by ______.
    (A) Pons varoli
    (B) Cerebrum
    (C) Cerebellum
    (D) Medulla   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Vomiting is believed to be controlled by two distinct brain centres - the vomiting centre and the chemoreceptor trigger zone - both located in the medulla oblongata. The vomiting centre initiates and controls the act of emesis, which involves a series of contractions of the smooth muscles lining the digestive tract.

Q13. Which digestive disorder reduces the absorption of food?
    (A) Vomitting
    (B) Constipation
    (C) Diarrhoea   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Indigestion
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The abnormal frequency of bowel movement and increased liquidity of the fecal discharge reduces the absorption of food leading to diarrhoea.

Q14. Which one is a mismatched pair?
    (A) Diarrhoea - less enzyme secretion   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Indigestion - food poisoning
    (C) Vomiting - antiperistalsis
    (D) Jaundice - deposition of bile pigments
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The abnormal frequency of bowel movement and increased liquidity of the faecal discharge is known as diarrhoea.

Digestion And Absorption Test-04  (id 3417) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Digestion and Absorption (FA ONLY)

Q1. Match the following:
 Digestive Disorder
 Cause
 (a) Constipation
 (i) gallstones
 (b) Jaundice
 (ii) reflex action anxiety
 (c) Indigestion
 (iii) intentional ischemia
 (d) Vomiting
 (iv) irregular bowel movements
    (A) (a) - (iii), (b) - (iv), (c) - (ii), (d) - (i)
    (B) (a) - (iv), (b) - (i), (c) - (ii), (d) - (iii)   <-- CORRECT
    (C) (a) - (ii), (b) - (i), (c) - (iv), (d) - (iii)
    (D) (a) - (ii), (b) - (iii), (c) - (ii), (d) - (iv)
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The causes of indigestion are inadequate enzyme secretion, anxiety, food poisoning, overeating, and spicy food. In constipation, the bowel movements occur irregularly. In jaundice, the deposition of bile pigments results in gall stones. A reflex action is controlled by the vomiting centre in the medulla.

Q2. Malnutrition covers:
    (A) Only overnutrition
    (B) All the diseases which infants suffer from
    (C) Only undernutrition
    (D) Both undernutrition and overnutrition   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Malnutrition is the condition of having less than the required amount of food or more than the required amount of food. Both conditions are harmful to health. So, malnutrition covers both undernutrition and overnutrition.

Q3. Bacteria responsible for chronic gastritis is:
    (A) Helicobacter pylori   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Salmonella enterica
    (C) Haemophilusducreyi
    (D) Lactobacillus casei
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Chronic gastritis involves swelling or inflammation of the stomach lining. Helicobacter pylori colonize the stomach and induce chronic gastritis, a long-lasting inflammation of the stomach.

Q4. Regurgitation is more common in infants than in adults. The reason will be:
    (A) Pyloric sphincter is much less effective in infants
    (B) Excessive acid formation and secretion in the stomach of infants
    (C) Cardiac sphincter is much less effective in infants   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Peristaltic waves are not strong enough in infants
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Regurgitation is the expulsion of material from the pharynx, or esophagus, usually characterized by the presence of undigested food or blood. Regurgitation is used by a number of species to feed their young. Regurgitation is more common in infants than adults because the cardiac sphincter is much less effective in infants.

Q5. ________ from pharynx is conveyed into oesophagus by ________.
    (A) Chyme, degluition
    (B) Bolus, deglutition   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Chyme, regurgition
    (D) Bolus, regurgition
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Bolus from pharynx is passed into the oesophagus by deglutition. The bolus is the semisolid chewed food mixed with saliva in the mouth. The food from pharynx passed to the oesophagus by swallowing.

Q6. Read the following statements about CCK:
 This hormone stimulates gastrointestinal motility and pancreatic endocrine function.
 This hormone stimulates release of bile from the gall bladder.
    (A) Both are wrong
    (B) Statement ii is correct and i is wrong   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Statement ii is wrong and i is correct
    (D) Both are correct
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Cholecystokinin, previously called pancreozymins, is synthesized and secreted by enteroendocrine cells in the duodenum, the first segment of the small intestine.
Its presence causes the release of digestive enzymes and bile from the pancreas and gallbladder, respectively, and also acts as a hunger suppressant.

Q7. People who are lactose intolerant:
 Cannot digest food with lactose in them.
 They need to take a calcium supplement.
    (A) Statement ii is correct and i is wrong
    (B) Statement ii is wrong and i is correct
    (C) Both are correct   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Both are wrong
    Answer: C
    Explanation: People who are lactose intolerant cannot digest food with lactose in them and these people need to take a calcium supplement which is naturally present along with lactose in milk.

Q8. Liver stores extra glycogen but once storage limit is reached then extra carbohydrate will be:
    (A) Converted into protein
    (B) Excreted out from body
    (C) Metabolised to form vitamins
    (D) Converted into fat   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Glycogen is the form in which the body stores glucose. The liver can only store about 100 g of glucose in the form of glycogen. The muscles also store glycogen. Muscles can store approximately 500 g of glycogen. Because of the limited storage areas, any carbohydrates that are consumed beyond the storage capacity are converted to and stored as fat. There is practically no limit on how many calories the body can store as fat.

Q9. In Reema’s body, substances in bile harden forming stone in the gall bladder. What can be the possible treatment?
    (A) Dissolving the stone with Surgery
    (B) Removing only stone from gall bladder by surgery
    (C) Removal of gall bladder   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Dissolving the stone with medicinal treatment
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The substance in bile hardens to form stone in the gall bladder. It is difficult to remove stone surgically and by lithotripsy. So, in most cases, the gall bladder is removed surgically.

Q10. Which of the following is a mismatched pair?
    (A) frog - acrodont teeth
    (B) spiny anteater - teeth absent
    (C) humans - diastema present   <-- CORRECT
    (D) rabbit - rootless teeth
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Diastema is the gap between teeth. Generally, a diastema is not present in human beings. Rabbit has rootless teeth and frogs are acrodont as same teeth remain throughout their life.

Q11. Blood vessels of the alimentary canal:
 provide nourishment to the cells of the alimentary canal.
 absorb digested fat molecules from the stomach and intestine.
    (A) Both are correct
    (B) Statement i is wrong and ii is correct
    (C) Statement i is correct and ii is wrong   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Both are wrong
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Blood vessels of the alimentary canal provide nourishment to the cells of the alimentary canal but do not absorb digested fat molecules from the stomach and intestine.

Q12. Out of the following which one doesn’t provide any calories?
    (A) Fats
    (B) Proteins
    (C) Vitamins   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Alcohol
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Fats, protein, and alcohol on oxidation produce energy along with other products but vitamins are not oxidized to release energy to us. They act as protective food to protect us from the disease.

Q13. Match the cells and their secretions:
 Cell Type
 Secretion
 (a) Goblet cell
 (i) succus entericus
 (b) Oxyntic cells
 (ii) mucus
 (c) Chief cells
 (iii) acid
 (d) Intestinal gland cells
 (iv) pepsinogen
    (A) (a) - (iv), (b) - (i), (c) - (ii), (d) - (iii)
    (B) (a) - (ii), (b) - (iii), (c) - (iv), (d) - (i)   <-- CORRECT
    (C) (a) - (ii), (b) - (iii), (c) - (i), (d) - (iv)
    (D) (a) - (ii), (b) - (i), (c) - (iv), (d) - (iii)
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Mucus is secreted by Goblet cell, pepsinogen is released from Chief cells, Hydrochloric acid is released by Oxyntic cells and succus entericus enzymes are released from intestinal gland cells.

Q14. Match the following:
 GI hormone
 Function
 (a) Enterocrinin
 (i) stimulates gastric juice secretion
 (b) Duocrinin
 (ii) inhibits gastric juice secretion
 (c) Gastrin
 (iii) stimulates secretory activity of brunner’s glands
 (d) Enterogasterone
 (iv) stimulates secretory activity of crypts of lieberkuhn
    (A) (a) - (iv), (b) - (iii), (c) - (i), (d) - (ii)   <-- CORRECT
    (B) (a) - (ii), (b) - (iii), (c) - (i), (d) - (iv)
    (C) (a) - (ii), (b) - (i), (c) - (iv), (d) - (iii)
    (D) (a) - (iv), (b) - (i), (c) - (ii), (d) - (iii)
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Gastrointestinal hormone Enterocrinin stimulates secretory activity of crypts of Lieberkuhn. Duocrinin stimulates the secretory activity of Brunner’s glands. Gastrin stimulates gastric juice secretion. Enterogasterone inhibits gastric juice secretion.

Q15. Parodontax toothpaste launched a few months ago that helps to prevent periodontal disease which are caused by microbe named:
    (A) Tannerella forsythia gingivalis
    (B) Porphyromonas gingivalis   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Entamoeba gingivalis
    (D) Escherichia gingivalis
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Porphyromonas gingivalis is a Gram-negative oral anaerobe that is involved in the pathogenesis of periodontitis, an inflammatory disease that destroys the tissues supporting the tooth which eventually may lead to tooth loss. Paodontax toothpaste help to prevent periodontal disease.

Breathing And Exchange Of Gases Test-01   (id 3418) [FREE]

Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. Tracheal tube divides into right and left bronchi at the level of:
    (A) 5th thoracic vertebra   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 6th thoracic vertebra
    (C) 7th thoracic vertebra
    (D) 4th thoracic vertebra
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The trachea divides at the level of 5th thoracic vertebra into a right and left primary bronchi.

Q2. Vital capacity of our lungs include all of the following except:
    (A) RV   <-- CORRECT
    (B) IRV
    (C) ERV
    (D) TV
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Vital capacity includes ERV, TV, and IRV or the maximum volume of air a person can breathe out after a forced inspiration.

Q3. Skin is the only respiratory organ in:
    (A) Ranatigrina
    (B) Larvae of mosquitoes
    (C) Peripatus
    (D) Hirudinaria granulosa   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: There are no special respiratory organs in Hirudinaria. In addition to its primary role as a protective covering, the skin also serves a respiratory function. It is provided with a rich supply of haemocoelomic fluid in an extensive system of capillaries and capillary loops, which penetrate into the spaces between the inner ends of the epidermal cells.

Q4. The pharynx is the common passage for food and air but still, food does not enter into the windpipe due to the presence of _______.
    (A) Frenulum
    (B) Epiglottis   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Glottis
    (D) Valve of windpipe
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The epiglottis is a leaf-shaped flap of cartilage located behind the tongue, at the top of the larynx, or voice box. The main function of the epiglottis is to seal off the windpipe during eating, so that food is not accidentally inhaled.

Q5. The value of TV is about 500 ml for an average adult human male but only some parts of it enter the lung alveoli and the rest of it fills the respiratory passage. What should be the distribution ratio for alveolar volume /respiratory passage volume?
    (A) 7:3   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 3:7
    (C) 2:3
    (D) 1:1
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Tidal volume (TV) = volume moved in one breath. Normal = 500 ml
 About 70% of TV reaches alveoli (350 ml) Only this amount is involved in gas exchange
 30% in airways =respiratory passage (anatomical dead space)
So ratio = 350:150 = 7:3

Q6. It is known that exposure to carbon monoxide is harmful to animals because
    (A) it increases O_2 transport.
    (B) it increases CO_2 transport
    (C) it reduces CO_2 transport
    (D) it reduces O_2 transport   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Carbon monoxide poisoning occurs after enough inhalation of carbon monoxide (CO). Carbon monoxide binds with haemoglobin to form carboxyhaemoglobin because of which oxygen is not released to the tissues.

Q7. Ram suffers punctures in his chest cavity without any damage to the lungs in an accident. It results in:
    (A) No effect in breathing
    (B) Rapid increase in breathing rate
    (C) Reduction in breathing rate
    (D) Cessation of breathing   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Haemopneumothorax is a medical term describing the combination of two conditions: pneumothorax, or air in the chest cavity, and hemothorax (also called haemothorax), or blood in the chest cavity. A hemothorax, pneumothorax, or both can occur if the chest wall is punctured. Because of the punctured chest wall, the lungs cannot expand, the pressure in the lungs never drops and no air is pulled into the bronchi. Respiration is not possible.

Q8. Which one of the following is the wrong statement with respect to the functions of the respiratory system?
    (A) Diffusion of gases
    (B) Cleans up the air   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Warms up the air
    (D) Humidifies the air
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The function of the respiratory system does not deal with the cleaning up of the air.

Q9. Match the following:
 Respiratory volume
 Value (in ml)
 (a) RV
 (i) 1000 - 1100
 (b) ERV
 (ii) 6000 - 8000
 (c) TV
 (iii) 2500 - 3000
 (d) IRV
 (iv) 1100 - 1200
    (A) (a) - (iii), (b) - (iv), (c) - (ii), (d) - (i)
    (B) (a) - (ii), (b) - (iii), (c) - (i), (d)- (iv)
    (C) (a) - (ii), (b) - (i), (c) - (iv), (d) - (iii)
    (D) (a) - (iv), (b) - (i), (c) - (ii), (d) - (iii)   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: TV is approx. 500 mL., i.e., a healthy man can inspire or expire approximately 6000 to 8000mL of air per minute. IRV averages 2500mL to 3000 mL. ERV averages 1000mL to 1100 mL. RV averages 1100 mL to 1200 mL.

Q10. Respiration in insects is direct due to exchange of gases:
    (A) Directly with coelomic fluid
    (B) By tracheal tubes directly with haemocoel which then exchanges with tissues   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Directly with the air in tubes
    (D) Directly with the air outside through body surface
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Insects have spiracles on their exoskeletons to allow air to enter the trachea. In insects, the tracheal tubes primarily deliver oxygen directly into the insects' tissues. The spiracles can be opened and closed in an efficient manner to reduce water loss. This is done by contracting closer muscles surrounding the spiracle.

Q11. If TLC is 5500ml, IRV is 2950ml, ERV is 900ml and TV is 500ml then what will be the value of RV?
    (A) 1200ml
    (B) 1150ml   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 1100ml
    (D) 2550ml
    Answer: B
    Explanation: RV = TLC - IRV - ERV - TV
substitute the values
RV = 5500 - 2950 - 900 - 500 = 1150ml.

Q12. The correct sequence of respiration is:
 Breathing in oxygen.
 Transportation of gases by the blood.
 Diffusion of gases between blood and tissues.
 Diffusion of gases across the alveolar membrane.
 Using oxygen and releasing carbon dioxide.
    (A) (i), (iii), (iv), (ii), (v)
    (B) (i), (iv), (ii), (iii), (v)   <-- CORRECT
    (C) (i), (ii), (iv), (iii), (v)
    (D) (i), (ii), (iii), (iv), (v)
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Respiration involves breathing or pulmonary ventilation by which atmospheric air is drawn in. Diffusion of gases across the alveolar membrane, Transport of gases by the blood, Diffusion of gases between blood and tissues. The utilization of oxygen by the cells.

Q13. Match the following:
 Animal
 Respiratory Organ
 (a) Nereis
 (i) Book Lungs
 (b) Limulus
 (ii) Book Gills
 (c) Palaemon
 (iii) General Body Surface
 (d) Palamnaeus
 (iv) Parapodia
 (e) Dugesia
 (v) Gills
    (A) (a) - (i), (b) - (iii), (c) - (v), (d) - (ii), (e) - (iv)
    (B) (a) - (v), (b) - (iv), (c) - (iii), (d) - (i), (e) - (ii)
    (C) (a) - (iv), (b) - (ii), (c) - (v), (d) - (i), (e) - (iii)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (a) - (ii), (b) - (i), (c) - (iv), (d) - (iii), (e) - (v)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The respiratory organ of Nereis is parapodia, Limulus is book gills, Palamnaeus is the book lungs and the respiratory organ of Dugesia is general body surface. Palaemon respire through gills.

Q14. Those bronchioles which divide into alveolar ducts are called as:
    (A) Tertiary bronchioles
    (B) Respiratory bronchioles   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Secondary bronchioles
    (D) Primary bronchioles
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Terminal bronchioles give rise to respiratory bronchioles that ultimately lead to the alveoli. The exchange of gases takes place in alveoli with blood vessels.

Q15. Which part of our respiratory system doesn’t need ciliated epithelium and thus have non-ciliated walls?
    (A) Nasal chamber
    (B) Bronchioles
    (C) Trachea
    (D) Alveoli   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The respiratory system does not need ciliated epithelium and thus have non-ciliated walls such as alveoli. Alveoli are the balloon-like structure at which the exchange of gases takes place.

Breathing And Exchange Of Gases Test-02  (id 3419) [PAID]

Q1. After a forceful expiration:
    (A) Gaseous exchange continues uninterrupted   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Diaphragm and intercostals increase respiratory surface area
    (C) Gaseous exchange is interrupted
    (D) Lungs becomes empty so exchange stops for a while
    Answer: A
    Explanation: After a forceful expiration, the gaseous exchange continues uninterrupted because there is always a residual volume of air that continues the diffusion of gases.

Q2. What is the difference between the two given below diagrams:
    (A) (i)alveoli of pneumoconiosis patient, (ii) healthy alveoli
    (B) (i)alveoli of asthma patient, (ii)alveoli of pneumoconiosis patient
    (C) (i)alveoli of bronchitis patient, (ii)alveoli of asthma patient
    (D) (i)healthy alveoli, (ii)alveoli of an emphysema patient   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Figure (i) represents the alveoli of healthy person and figure (ii) is the alveoli of emphysema patient. The wall of alveoli is get damaged in figure (ii) to reduce the surface area for exchange of gases.

Q3. First step in the process of inspiration is:
    (A) Relaxation of sternum
    (B) Increase in volume of thoracic cavity
    (C) Relaxation of diaphragm
    (D) Contraction of diaphragm   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Inspiration is the process of intake of oxygen from the surrounding. This is achieved by increasing the volume of the thoracic cavity. The contraction of the diaphragm relaxes the sternum that increases the thoracic cavity.

Q4. The gaseous exchange portion of the human respiratory tract includes :
    (A) alveoli, bronchioles, trachea and nasal chambers
    (B) alveoli and alveolar ducts   <-- CORRECT
    (C) alveoli and bronchioles
    (D) alveoli, bronchioles and trachea
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Alveolar ducts are tiny ducts that connect the respiratory bronchioles to alveolar sacs, each of which contains a collection of alveoli (small mucus-lined pouches made of flattened epithelial cells). They are tiny end ducts of the branching airways that fill the lungs.

Q5. Air breathing animals lose a large amount of precious water from their respiratory surface through:
    (A) Evaporation   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Secretion
    (C) Diffusion
    (D) dispersal
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Water is released in the atmosphere along with expired air during the respiratory cycle. Air-breathing animals lose a large amount of precious water from their respiratory surface through evaporation.

Q6. Which of the following pair of factors are considered favourable for the formation of oxyhaemoglobin?
    (A) High H^+ concentration and high pO_2
    (B) Low pCO_2 and low temperature   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Low pO_2 and low H^+ concentration
    (D) Low H^+ concentration and high pCO_2
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In the alveoli, where there is high pO_2, low pCO_2, lesser H^+ concentration, and lower temperature, the factors are all favourable for the formation of oxyhaemoglobin.

Q7. Read the following statements:
 Pressure contributed by and individual gas in a mixture of gases is called its partial pressure.
 pCO_2 in alveolar air is 45 mm Hg and in venous blood is 40 mm Hg.
    (A) Both statement (i) and (ii) are incorrect
    (B) Statement (i) is wrong and (ii) is correct
    (C) Statement (i) is correct and (ii) is wrong   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Both statement (i) and (ii) are correct
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In a mixture of gases, each gas has a partial pressure which is the hypothetical pressure of that gas if it alone occupied the entire volume of the original mixture at the same temperature. The total pressure of an ideal gas mixture is the sum of the partial pressures of each individual gas in the mixture.
 The pCO_2 in alveolar air is 40 mm Hg and in venous blood is 45 mm Hg.

Q8. The principle of exchange of gases at the lungs is:
    (A) Conditioning and facilitated transport
    (B) Both diffusion and filtration
    (C) Diffusion   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Filtration
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The main function of the respiratory system is the gaseous exchange. This refers to the process of Oxygen and Carbon Dioxide moving between the lungs and blood. Diffusion occurs when molecules move from an area of high concentration (of that molecule) to an area of low concentration. This occurs during the gaseous exchange as the blood in the capillaries surrounding the alveoli has a lower oxygen concentration of Oxygen than the air in the alveoli which has just been inhaled.

Q9. Read the following statements:
 The affinity of Hb for CO is 200 to 250 times more than its affinity for oxygen therefore CO competes with oxygen for binding to Hb.
 The result of this binding is a shift of oxygen-hemoglobin dissociation curve to the left and its alteration to a more hyperbolic shape.
    (A) Statement (i) is incorrect and (ii) is correct
    (B) Both statement (i) and (ii) are correct   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Statement (i) is correct and (ii) is incorrect
    (D) Both statement (i) and (ii) are incorrect
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The affinity of Haemoglobin is 200 to 250 times more than that of Oxygen, therefore, CO competes with oxygen for binding to Hb. Due to this binding a shift of oxygen-hemoglobin dissociation curve to left and its alteration to a more hyperbolic shape.

Q10. Expiration will take place when there is:
 Positive intrapulmonary pressure
 Negative intrapulmonary pressure
 Less pressure within lungs as compared to atmospheric pressure
    (A) (B)
    (B) (A)   <-- CORRECT
    (C) (C)
    (D) (B) and (C)
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Expiration is the release of carbon dioxide-rich air from the thoracic cavity. When the volume of air decreases and pressure increase the air from the chest moves out. This kind of pressure is called positive intrapulmonary pressure.

Q11. RBCs and muscle cells carry out anaerobic respiration, but:
 RBCs are permanently anaerobic and muscle cells are temporarily anaerobic.
 RBCs are temporarily anaerobic and muscle cells are permanently anaerobic.
 Muscle cells lack mitochondria.
    (A) Only statement (ii) and (iii) are correct
    (B) Only statement (ii) is correct
    (C) Only statement (i) is correct   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Only statement (iii) is correct
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Red blood cells and muscle cells carry out anaerobic respiration but RBC’s are permanently anaerobic and muscle cells are temporarily anaerobic in nature.

Q12. Water breathing is more problematic than air-breathing because:
 Water is 800 times denser and hence holds much more oxygen than air does.
 Since oxygen dissolved in water diffuses far more slowly than air therefore, the large quantity of water is required to be passed over the gills.
    (A) Both statements (i) and (ii) are wrong
    (B) Statement (i) is wrong and (ii) is correct   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Statement (ii) is wrong and (i) is correct
    (D) Both statements (i) and (ii) are correct
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Water breathing is more problematic than air-breathing because oxygen dissolved in water diffuses far more slowly than air therefore, a large quantity of water is required to be passed over the gills.

Q13. Read the following about blood pigments:
 Hemoglobin is the pigment present in our blood and is an iron-containing protein.
 Haemocyanin is the pigment present in the blood of Palaemon and is copper-containing protein.
 Haemocyanin is much more efficient than haemoglobin.
    (A) Statement (iii) is correct
    (B) Statement (i) is correct
    (C) Statement (i) and (ii) are correct   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Statement (ii) and (iii) are correct
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Haemoglobin is the pigment present in our blood and is iron-containing protein. Haemocyanin is the pigment present in the blood of Palaemon and is copper-containing protein.

Q14. The given graph shows $ {O_2}$ consumption and ventilation during exercise so we can infer from this graph :
During exercise, oxygen consumption rate in our body increases.
Neural stimulus allows abdominal muscles, which are a kind of smooth muscle to contract to facilitate ventilation while exercising.
Increase in ventilation during exercise prevents large changes in the partial pressure of $ {O_2}$ or $ C{O_2}$
The overall impact is the breathing rate increases.
    (A) all the above statements are correct.
    (B) the only (i) and (iii) are correct.
    (C) only (i) and (ii) are correct.
    (D) the only (i),(iii) and (iv) are correct.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: During exercise Oxygen consumption and ventilation changes drastically. Oxygen consumption rate in our body increases during exercise. Increase in ventilation during exercise prevents a large change in the partial pressure of O_2 and CO_2 to increase breathing rate.

Q15. The exchange of gases in:
 The alveoli that lower the pO_2 of blood and raise its pCO_2 is external respiration.
 The tissues that lower the pCO_2 of blood and raise its pO_2 is internal respiration.
    (A) Both statements (i) and (ii) are incorrect   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Both statements (i) and (ii) are correct
    (C) Statement (ii) is incorrect and (i) is correct
    (D) Statement (i) is incorrect and (ii) is correct
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In the alveoli, there is high pO_2, low pCO_2, lesser H^+ concentration, and lower temperature.

Breathing And Exchange Of Gases Test-03  (id 3420) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Breathing and Exchange of Gases
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. Which of the following is not correctly matched?
    (A) Cutaneous respiration = Breathing via skin
    (B) TLC = VC + RV
    (C) Respiration = Physiochemical process
    (D) Inspired air = Alveolar air   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Respiration is a physiological process. Total lung capacity (TLC) includes vital capacity (VC) and residual volume. Cutaneous respiration is breathing via the skin.

Q2. Read the following statements:
 Every 100 ml of deoxygenated blood delivers about 4 ml of CO_2 to the alveoli.
 30% - 40% of CO_2 is transported to the alveoli as carbamino-hemoglobin.
 At the respiratory surface, CO_2 diffuses from venous blood into alveolar spaces.
    (A) Statement (iii) is correct
    (B) Statement (i) and (ii) are correct
    (C) Statement (i) and (iii) are correct   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Statement (i) is incorrect
    Answer: C
    Explanation: 20 - 25% of CO_2 is transported to the alveoli as carbamino-hemoglobin.

Q3. The condition favourable for dissociation of oxygen from oxyhemoglobin in the tissues is:
    (A) Low pO_2, high pCO_2, low H^+ concentration, and higher temperature
    (B) High pO_2, low pCO_2, high H^+ concentration, and lower temperature
    (C) High pO_2, low pCO_2, low H^+ concentration, and lower temperature
    (D) Low pO_2, high pCO_2, high H^+ concentration, and higher temperature   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In tissues, low pO_2, high pCO_2, high H^+ concentration, and higher temperature exist, the conditions are favourable for dissociation of oxygen from the oxyhaemoglobin.

Q4. The solubility of carbon dioxide is:
    (A) 10 - 15 times higher than that of oxygen
    (B) 20 - 25 times lower than that of oxygen
    (C) 10 - 15 times lower than that of oxygen
    (D) 20 - 25 times higher than that of oxygen   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The solubility of carbon dioxide is 20-25 times higher than that of oxygen, the amount of carbon dioxide that can diffuse through the diffusion membrane per unit difference in partial pressure is much higher compared to that of oxygen.

Q5. The major factor which affects binding related to the partial pressure of carbon dioxide is______.
    (A) CO_2
    (B) pCO_2   <-- CORRECT
    (C) O_2
    (D) pO_2
    Answer: B
    Explanation: pCO_2

Q6. 70% of carbon dioxide is transported as bicarbonate by the enzyme_______.
    (A) Carbonates
    (B) Carbonic anhydrase   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Carbonic hydrase
    (D) Carbaminase
    Answer: B
    Explanation: An enzyme present in red blood cells, carbonic anhydrase, aids in the conversion of carbon dioxide to carbonic acid and bicarbonate ions. When red blood cells reach the lungs, the same enzyme helps to convert the bicarbonate ions back to carbon dioxide, which we breathe out. It transports nearly 70% of carbon dioxide as bicarbonate.

Q7. The regulatory centres for respiration are located in:
    (A) Medulla oblongata and pons   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Cerebellum and medulla oblongata
    (C) Diencephalon and pons
    (D) Pons and cerebellum
    Answer: A
    Explanation: A specialized centre present in the medulla region of the brain called respiratory rhythm centre is primarily responsible for this regulation. In the pons region of the brain called pneumotaxic centre can moderate the functions of the respiratory rhythm centre.

Q8. In CNS, regulation of respiratory rhythm during normal breathing is largely dependent upon:
    (A) Carbon dioxide concentration   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Oxyhemoglobin concentration
    (C) Oxygen concentration
    (D) RBCs in the body
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In the central nervous system, regulation of respiratory rhythm during normal breathing is dependent upon the concentration of carbon dioxide gas in the air.

Q9. Name the unlabelled parts of a given flow chart:
    (A) carbondioxide, inspiratory centre and diaphragm
    (B) oxygen, inspiratory centre and expiratory centre
    (C) stretch, expiratory centre and inspiratory centre   <-- CORRECT
    (D) carbondioxide, pneumotoxiccentre and spinal cord
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The flow chart of respiratory mechanism labeled as stretch, expiratory centre and inspiratory centre respiratory. It is controlled by the medulla and pons of hind brain.

Q10. The specialized centre which can reduce the inspiratory duration upon stimulation is_________.
    (A) Medullary inspiratory centre
    (B) Apneusticcentre
    (C) Pneumotaxic centre   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Chemosensitivecentre
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The pneumotaxic centre can moderate the functions of the respiratory rhythm centre. A neural signal from this centre can reduce the duration of inspiration and thereby alter the respiratory rate.

Q11. Loud snoring and labored breathing are symptoms of:
    (A) Bronchitis
    (B) Obstructive sleep apnea   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Peripheral sleep apnea
    (D) Central sleep apnea
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Loud snoring and labored breathing are the symptoms of obstructive sleep apnea. Obstructive sleep apnea is a sleep disorder in which breathing is briefly and repeatedly interrupted.

Q12. A film of ________ lines lung alveoli that lowers ________ of the alveoli and makes breathing ________.
    (A) cuticle, inflating, difficult
    (B) pleuron, surface tension, easier
    (C) cuticle, bacterial inflammation, difficult
    (D) lecithin, surface tension, easier   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: A thin film of lecithin lines lung alveoli that lowers the surface tension of the alveoli and makes breathing easier. The lining also reduces the friction of alveoli to avoid its damage.

Q13. Habit of Cigarette smoking can lead to:
    (A) Loss of cilia lining the respiratory tract
    (B) Emphysema
    (C) Coughing
    (D) All of these   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The habit of cigarette smoking can lead to coughing, emphysema, and loss of cilia lining the respiratory tract. It contains nicotine that breaks the wall of alveoli to reduce the respiratory surface.

Q14. Read the following:
 During chloride shift, the chloride ions diffuse from RBC’s into the blood plasma.
 The chloride shift helps to maintain ionic balance and chemical neutrality.
 The chloride shift occurs during the transport of CO_2.
    (A) Only statement (iii) is correct
    (B) All of these
    (C) Only statement (ii) and (iii) are correct   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Only statement (i) and (ii) are correct
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Chloride shift is a process that occurs in a cardiovascular system and refers to the exchange of bicarbonate and chloride across the membrane of red blood cells. The chloride shift helps to maintain ionic balance and chemical neutrality.

Q15. Insect of the family Chironomidae like Chironomous larvae are also known as bloodworms since:
    (A) They have only blood
    (B) They contain haemocyanin as their respiratory pigment
    (C) They contain haemoglobin as their respiratory pigment   <-- CORRECT
    (D) They are blood parasites
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Insects of family Chironomidae eg. Chironomus commonly known as the harlequin fly is a species of the non-biting midge. Their larvae are known by the common name of blood worm due to their red colouration. The red colouration is because they contain haemoglobin as their respiratory pigment.

Q1. Which of the following blood components play a major role in blood coagulation?
    (A) Lymphocytes
    (B) Thrombocytes   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Fibrinocytes
    (D) Granulocytes
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Platelets also called thrombocytes are cell fragments produced from megakaryocytes. Platelets can release a variety of substances most of which are involved in the coagulation or clotting of blood.

Q2. The pre-hypertension blood pressure value is a measurement between:
    (A) 120/80 and 139/89   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 100/70 and 120/80
    (C) 139/89 and 140/90
    (D) 120/80 and 140/90
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Hypertension or high blood pressure is a condition where blood pressure increases substantially. The pre-hypertension blood pressure value is between 120/80 and 139/89.

Q3. Where (a) is a neutrophil, identify the other four WBCs?
    (A) basophil, eosinophil, lymphocyte and monocyte
    (B) eosinophil, basophil, lymphocyte and monocyte
    (C) lymphocyte, eosinophil, monocyte and basophil
    (D) monocyte, basophil, lymphocyte and eosinophil   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: There are two main categories of WBCs – granulocytes and agranulocytes. Neutrophils, eosinophils and basophils are different types of granulocytes, while lymphocytes and monocytes are the agranulocytes.

Q4. Rh incompatibility develops when :
    (A) foetus is Rh+ve and mother is Rh-ve   <-- CORRECT
    (B) foetus is Rh-ve and mother is Rh+ve
    (C) foetus is Rh+ve and mother is Rh+ve
    (D) foetus is Rh-ve and father is Rh-ve
    Answer: A
    Explanation: A special case of Rh incompatibility (mismatching) has been observed between the Rh-ve blood of a pregnant mother with Rh+ve blood of the foetus.

Q5. The middle man of our body is:
    (A) Blood
    (B) Heart
    (C) Kidney
    (D) Lymph   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Lymph is the extracellular fluid that contains WBC’s and plasma. Lymph flows in the lymphatic system and finally drains into veins. Lymph is called as the middle man of our body.

Q6. Correct order for increasing number of corpuscles in our blood is:
    (A) Erythrocytes < Platelets < Leucocytes
    (B) WBCs < Platelets < Erythrocytes   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Lymphocytes < RBCs < Platelets
    (D) Thrombocytes < Leucocytes < RBCs
    Answer: B
    Explanation: WBCs are relatively lesser in number which averages 6000-8000 mm^-3 of blood. A healthy adult man has, on an average, 5 million to 5.5 million of RBCs mm-3 of blood. Blood normally contains 1,500,00-3,500,00 platelets mm^-^3.

Q7. Among mammals, the nucleus is absent in:
    (A) WBCs and platelets
    (B) Only RBCs
    (C) Mature RBCs and platelets   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Lymphocytes and RBCs
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The absence of a nucleus is an adaptation of the red blood cell for its role. It allows the red blood cell to contain more hemoglobin and, therefore, carry more oxygen molecules. Platelets are devoid of the nucleus in most of the mammals.

Q8. Blood plasma proteins:
 decrease in their level causes excessive absorption of water from tissues into the blood.
 they maintain osmotic pressure.
    (A) Both statement (i) and (ii) are incorrect
    (B) Statement (i) is incorrect and (ii) is correct   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Both statement (i) and (ii) are correct
    (D) Statement (i) is correct and (ii) is incorrect
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Fibrinogen, globulins, and albumins are the major proteins. The albumins help in osmotic balance.

Q9. Manoj has AB blood group, so he will have the following antibodies in his blood plasma:
    (A) A antibody
    (B) No antibodies are present   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Both A and B antibodies
    (D) B antibody
    Answer: B
    Explanation: AB blood group does not have any antibodies in plasma. That's why AB blood group is a universal recipient.

Q10. Lymph will transport:
    (A) Digested carbohydrates
    (B) Digested proteins
    (C) Digested fats   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Oxyhemoglobin
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Fats are absorbed through lymph in the lacteals present in the intestinal villi.

Q11. In our blood:
 Granulocytes which constitute the maximum percentage of total leucocytes are neutrophils.
 An elevated number of neutrophils in blood indicates an acute infection such as appendicitis.
    (A) Statement (i) is incorrect and (ii) is correct
    (B) Statement (i) is correct and (ii) is incorrect
    (C) Statement (i) and (ii) are incorrect
    (D) Statement (i) and (ii) are correct   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In human blood, granulocytes and agranulocytes types of leucocytes are present. Neutrophils constitute the maximum percentage of total WBCs. A sharp increase in the number of neutrophils in the blood indicates an acute infection such as appendicitis.

Q12. The following pie chart shows four components of blood plasma represented from first to fourth Qtr and the correct sequence will be:
    (A) proteins, water, inorganic salts and other materials
    (B) water, proteins, lipids and other materials
    (C) water, proteins, inorganic salts and other materials   <-- CORRECT
    (D) water, proteins, dissolved gases and other materials
    Answer: C
    Explanation: 90-92 per cent of plasma is water and proteins contribute 6-8 per cent of it. Plasma also contains small amounts of minerals and other materials such as glucose, amino acids, lipids, etc., arealso present in the plasma.

Q13. When blood clot starts contracting, a pale yellow fluid starts oozing out. Its name and composition are:
    (A) Serum = plasma - [fibrinogen + blood corpuscles]   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Serum = dissolved fibrin - [plasma + blood corpuscles]
    (C) Sera = blood corpuscles - [thrombin + fibrin]
    (D) Serum = plasma - [thrombin + blood corpuscles]
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Plasma without the clotting factors is called serum. The clotting factors include fibrinogen and blood corpuscles.

Q14. Ramesh has Rh antigen and Anti-A as well as Anti-B antibodies in his blood. During blood transfusion, he can receive blood from:
    (A) Person with AB negative blood group
    (B) Person with O negative blood group
    (C) Person with AB positive blood group
    (D) Person with O positive blood group   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Since he has both antibodies A and Band have Rh antigen and hence has O+ blood group. So, he can receive blood from the O-positive blood group.

Q15. Which of the following represent examples of extracellular fluids?
    (A) Tissue fluid
    (B) Blood plasma
    (C) Blood
    (D) Both tissue fluid and blood plasma   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Tissue fluid (lymph) and blood plasma represent the extracellular fluids. Lymph flows in lymphatic vessels and plasma in arteries and veins along with RBC, WBC, and platelets.
