Q1. The specialized patch of modified heart muscles from where contraction initiates, is/are:
    (A) Pacemaker of heart   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Both SAN and AVN together
    (C) ECG
    (D) Pacesetter of heart
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The nodal musculature has the ability to generate action potentials without any external stimuli. The number of action potentials that could be generated in a minute varies at different parts of the nodal system. The SAN can generate the maximum number of action potentials and is responsible for initiating and maintaining the rhythmic contractile activity of the heart. Therefore, it is called the pacemaker.

Q2. The incorrect statement about the human heart is:
    (A) It is myogenic
    (B) It is four chambered
    (C) Wall of left ventricle is thickest
    (D) It is derived from endoderm   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Human being is triploblastic. The different organs are evolved from different layers of foetus. Human heart is derived from mesoderm.

Q3. The layer of heart pericardium which checks it's overstretching and overfilling as well as also protects the heart from mechanical injury is:
    (A) Fibrous pericardium   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Serous pericardium
    (C) Parietal pericardium
    (D) Visceral pericardium
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The pericardium is a protective covering of the heart. The pericardium is made of different layers to perform different functions. The layer of heart pericardium which checks it's overstretching and overfilling as well as protects the heart from mechanical injury is the fibrous pericardium.

Q4. Which of the following is correctly matched?
    (A) QRS wave = ventricular repolarisation
    (B) P wave = atrial relaxation
    (C) T wave = ventricular relaxation   <-- CORRECT
    (D) P wave = atrial repolarisation
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The T-wave represents the return of the ventricles from excited to a normal state.

Q5. Read the following:
 Blood vessels include arteries and veins. Arteries carry blood from the heart to body parts and veins bring back blood from body parts to the heart.
 The blood vessel which carry blood from the heart to lungs is a pulmonary artery and it carries oxygenated blood.
    (A) Statement (i) and (ii) are correct
    (B) Statement (ii) is incorrect and (i) is correct   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Statement (ii) is correct and (i) is incorrect
    (D) Statement (i) and (ii) are incorrect
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Blood vessels include arteries and veins. Arteries carry blood from the heart to body parts and veins bring back blood from body parts to the heart. The pulmonary artery carries deoxygenated blood.

Q6. Which of the following statements doesn’t hold true for blood clotting cascade?
 Ruptured platelets release thromboplastin.
 Prothrombinis converted into thrombin in the presence of vitamin K and Na^+ions.
 Fibrinogen is converted into fibrin through enzymatic action of thrombin in the presence of Ca^++ions.
 Fibrin makes clot via process of polymerisation.
    (A) only statement (i) and (iv) are wrong
    (B) only statement (iv) is wrong
    (C) only statement (ii) and (iii) are wrong   <-- CORRECT
    (D) all statements are wrong
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Ruptured platelets release thromboplastin. Fibrinogen present in blood plasma is converted into fibrin through enzymatic action of thrombin. Fibrin makes clot via process of polymerisation.

Q7. Read the following:
 The instrument used for recording the heart’s electrical events is named electrocardiogram.
 In any ECG the part of the baseline between any two deflections is called an interval.
 Abnormality in the working of heart changes the wave pattern of ECG.
    (A) Statement (i) and (iii) are correct
    (B) All of these
    (C) Statement (ii) and (iii) are correct   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Statement (iii) is correct
    Answer: C
    Explanation: ECG is a graphical representation of the electrical activity of the heart during a cardiac cycle.

Q8. The mass of tissue seen in the left corner of the right atrium close to the atri-ventricular septum is_____.
    (A) AVN   <-- CORRECT
    (B) SAN
    (C) Bundle of His
    (D) Purkinje fibres
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Atrioventricular Node or AV node is a compact half oval mass of myogenic fibres which lies in the posterior septal wall of the right atrium near the opening of the coronary sinus. It receives an impulse from the SA node and transmits it to ventricles.

Q9. Look at the following ECGs:
    (A) (ii) ECG is abnormal while (i) is a normal ECG
    (B) (ii) represents enlargement of atrium and (i) represents enlargement of ventricles
    (C) both (i) and (ii) represent myocardial infarction   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (i) represents enlargement of atrium and (ii) represents enlargement of ventricles
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Both electro cardiogram (ECG) represents myocardial infarction in which heart do not receive the sufficient oxygen due to blockage of coronary artery.

Q10. Blood pressure is expressed as the ratio of systolic over diastolic pressure. The difference between systolic and diastolic pressure is called pulse pressure. What will be its value for a normal healthy adult?
    (A) 40 mm Hg   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 30 mm Hg
    (C) 70 mm Hg
    (D) 50 mm Hg
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Pulse pressure is the difference between the systolic and diastolic pressure readings. It is measured in millimeters of mercury (mmHg). It represents the force that the heart generates each time it contracts. If resting blood pressure is (systolic-diastolic) 120-80 millimeters of mercury (mmHg), the pulse pressure is 40.

Q11. In the human heart:
 The valve between the right atrium and right ventricle is tricuspid while the valve between the left atrium and left ventricle is the mitral valve.
 Openings of the right and the left ventricles into the pulmonary artery and the aorta are guarded by semilunar valves.
 ‘Lub’ the first sound which is low pitched is caused by the closure of semilunar valves while ‘Dub’ the second sound which is high pitched is caused by the closure of bicuspid and tricuspid valves.
    (A) Statement (iii) is correct
    (B) Statement (ii) and (iii) are correct
    (C) Statement (i) and (ii) are correct   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Statement (ii) is correct
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The first heart sound (lub) is associated with the closure of the tricuspid and bicuspid valves whereas the second heart sound (dub) is associated with the closure of the semilunar valves.

Q12. Each cardiac cycle takes 0.8 seconds to occur. Calculate how many cardiac cycles occur in 4 minutes?
    (A) 75
    (B) 400
    (C) 300   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 250
    Answer: C
    Explanation: 4 min = 240 sec. Therefore, 240/0.8 = 300 cardiac cycles.

Q13. In the given ECGs:
    (A) the P waves in both ECGs show changes due to rigorous exercise
    (B) the abnormal P wave in both ECGs represent atrial hypertrophy   <-- CORRECT
    (C) the abnormal P wave in both ECGs represent atrial hypotrophy
    (D) the abnormal P wave in both ECGs represent ventricular hypertrophy
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The ECGs shown above shows the abnormal P wave in both ECGs represents atrial hypertrophy or atrial enlargement.

Q14. The left atrium receives deoxygenated blood in:
    (A) Humans
    (B) Lizards   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Monkey
    (D) Pigeons
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Deoxygenated blood from body parts reaches the left atrium of lizards but in human beings left atrium receives the oxygenated blood.

Q15. Read the following statements:
 When the heart is not pumping blood sufficient to meet the need of the body then this state is called a heart attack.
 When the heart stops beating due to the irreversible death of cells then this state is called heart failure.
    (A) Both Statement (i) and (ii) are incorrect   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Both Statement (i) and (ii) are correct
    (C) Statement (i) is incorrect and (ii) is correct
    (D) Statement (i) is correct and (ii) is incorrect
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The state when the heart is not pumping blood sufficient to meet the need of the body then this state is called heart failure. When the heart muscles are suddenly damaged due to inadequate blood supply is called a heart attack.

Q1. In the systemic circulation, blood vessel that carries blood from the intestine to liver is named:
    (A) Hepatic portal arch
    (B) Casanova
    (C) Hepatic portal vein   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Hepatic portal artery
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The hepatic portal vein carries blood from intestine to the liver before it is delivered to the systemic circulation.

Q2. The cardiovascular centre is located in:
    (A) Cerebrum
    (B) Cerebellum
    (C) Medulla oblongata   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Pons
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The cardiovascular centre is a part of the human brain responsible for the regulation of the rate at which the heart beats through the nervous and endocrine systems. It is found in the medulla oblongata.

Q3. Prothrombin plays a crucial role in blood coagulation and vitamin K is considered essential for blood clotting, now read the following:
 Vitamin K is necessary for the synthesis of prothrombin in the liver.
 Vitamin K is necessary for the synthesis of prothrombin in the bone marrow.
 Vitamin K is necessary for the conversion of prothrombin into active thrombin.
    (A) Both statements (i) and (iii) are correct
    (B) Statement (ii) is correct
    (C) Both statements (ii) and (iii) are correct
    (D) Statement (i) is correct   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Prothrombin plays a crucial role in blood coagulation and vitamin K is essential for blood clotting. Vitamin K is necessary for the synthesis of prothrombin in the liver.

Q4. Mayank stood still for a long time and he felt swelling of feet. What would you suggest to him?
    (A) Drink a cup of tea
    (B) Keep on standing and do some shoulder exercise
    (C) Ask for some medicine to cure his swelling of feet
    (D) Jerk or wriggle his legs to restart circulation   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: During long hours of standing still swelling of feet is observe due to the accumulation of blood in the lower limb due to the gravitation effect. This can be corrected by a jerk or wriggle of legs to restart circulation properly.

Q5. Angina pectoris is very often mistaken for:
    (A) Chest pain
    (B) Severe headache
    (C) Indigestion   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Apnea
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Angina pectoris is the sensation of chest pain, pressure, or squeezing or pain in the centre of the chest. These symptoms are often mistaken by indigestion.

Q6. The list of risk factors associated with hypertension doesn’t include:
    (A) Hypoglycaemia and diabetes insipidus   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Birth control pills
    (C) Hyperglycemia and diabetes mellitus
    (D) Vitamin D deficiency
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Hypertension can cause a number of effects on the functioning of different vital functions but hypertension does not associate with hypoglycemia and diabetes insipidus.

Q7. Match the following:
 (a) Atherosclerosis
 (i) Hypotension
 (b) Haemorrhage
 (ii) High blood pressure
 (c) Heparin
 (iii) Abnormal increase in RBC count
 (d) Polycythemia
 (iv) Anticoagulant
    (A) (a) - (iii), (b) - (iv), (c) - (ii), (d) - (i)
    (B) (a) - (i), (b) - (iii), (c) - (iv), (d) - (ii)
    (C) (a) - (ii), (b) - (i), (c) - (iv), (d) - (iii)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (a) - (iv), (b) - (i), (c) - (ii), (d) - (iii)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Atherosclerosis leads to high blood pressure, haemorrhage causes hypotension, heparin is used as an anticoagulant and polycythemia causes an abnormal increase in RBC count.

Q8. When a person suffers from chest pain:
 the reason for this suffering is decreased blood flow and simultaneously lowered oxygen supply to an area of the heart.
 deprived of oxygen, myocardium opts for alternative pathways i.e. anaerobic respiration and its byproduct ethanol causes the pain.
    (A) Both statement (i) and (ii) are incorrect
    (B) Both statement (i) and (ii) are correct
    (C) Statement (i) is correct and (ii) is incorrect   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Statement (i) is incorrect and (ii) is correct
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Statement (i) is correct and (ii) is incorrect

Q9. As Soham, ages with chronic CAD the lumen of his coronary artery may get nearly completely obstructed Result is flow of blood to heart tissue is restricted such that the tissue receives an inadequate supply of oxygen-rich blood and this condition is diagnosed as:
    (A) Myocardial infarction
    (B) Heart failure
    (C) Hypertension
    (D) Myocardial ischemia   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In case of chronic CAD, the lumen of coronary artery may get nearly completely obstructed that results into restricted flow of blood to heart. The tissue receives inadequate bloods called myocardial ischemia.

Q10. Meghna suffers from allergic asthma. After a blood test, her leucocyte count displayed an abnormal increase in the number of:
    (A) Eosinophils   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Neutrophils
    (C) Basophils
    (D) Monocytes
    Answer: A
    Explanation: An absolute eosinophil count is a blood test that measures the number of white blood cells called eosinophils. Eosinophils become active when you have certain allergic diseases infections and other medical conditions.

Q11. For a healthy individual, calculate stroke volume for him if other values are; heartbeat per minute = 72 and cardiac output is 5 litre?
    (A) 0.05
    (B) 0.09
    (C) 0.06   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 0.08
    Answer: C
    Explanation: E Stroke volume of a healthy individual can be calculated by dividing cardiac output by a number of heartbeat per minute. So stroke volume = 5/72 = 0.0694.

Q12. Sarla is on a protein-deficient diet. As a result, her plasma proteins content is reduced. She may develop symptom like:
    (A) Swellings of hands and feet   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Diabetes
    (C) Reduced oxygen supply to tissues
    (D) High blood pressure
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Consuming a protein-deficient diet for longer duration may result in a reduction in protein plasma reduction. The symptoms that appear on the body include swelling of hands and feet.

Q13. Match the following:
 (a) Waller
 (i) rhesus antigen
 (b) Landsteiner
 (ii) first ECG
 (c) de castello and Steini
 (iii) A, B and O blood group
 (d) Landsteiner and Weiner
 (iv) AB blood group
    (A) (a) - (iii), (b) - (i), (c) - (ii), (d) - (iv)
    (B) (a) - (ii), (b) - (iii), (c) - (iv), (d) - (i)   <-- CORRECT
    (C) (a)- (iv), (b) - (i), (c) - (ii), (d) - (iii)
    (D) (a) - (i), (b) - (iii), (c) - (iv), (d) - (ii)
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Waller performed first ECG. Landsteiner and Weiner discovered rhesus antigen (Rh). De castello and Steini shows the AB blood grouping and Landsteiner A, B, O blood grouping.

Q14. Which of the following is a mismatched pair?
    (A) Fishes $\Rightarrow $ Venous heart and two accessory chambers
    (B) Mammals $\Rightarrow $ complete double circulation and no accessory chambers
    (C) Amphibians $\Rightarrow $ Arteriovenous heart and two accessory chambers
    (D) Reptiles $\Rightarrow $ Arteriovenous heart and three accessory chambers   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Amphibians have arteriovenous heart and two accessory chambers. Fishes have two-chambered venous heart and two accessory chambers. In mammals, complete double circulation with a four-chambered heart without any accessory chambers.

Q15. Match the following:
 Animal
 Circulation method
 (a) Paramecium
 (i) water canal system
 (b) Pila
 (ii) cyclosis
 (c) Scypha
 (iii) blood flowing through vessels
 (d) Pheretima
 (iv) blood passing through sinuses
    (A) (a) - (ii), (b) - (iv), (c) - (i), (d) - (iii)   <-- CORRECT
    (B) (a) - (iv), (b) - (i), (c) - (ii), (d) - (iii)
    (C) (a) - (i), (b) - (iii), (c) - (iv), (d) - (ii)
    (D) (a) - (iii), (b) - (iv), (c) - (ii), (d) - (i)
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In Paramecium oxygen is carried by cyclosis, in Pila blood passing through sinuses carries oxygen, in Scypha water canal system is present, and in Pheretima (earthworm) respiration is carried by blood flowing through vessels.

# Excretory Products and their Elimination  (3 tests)

========================================================================
Excretory Products And Their Elimination Test-01  (id 3424) [FREE]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Excretory Products and their Elimination
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. Blood enters glomerular capillaries through ________ arteriole & leaves through ________ arteriole.
    (A) distributing, collecting
    (B) afferent, efferent   <-- CORRECT
    (C) radial, collecting
    (D) efferent, afferent
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The blood plasma is filtered through the capillaries of the glomerulus into the capsule. The Bowman's capsule empties the filtrate into the proximal tubule that is also part of the duct system of the nephron. A glomerulus receives its blood supply from an afferent arteriole of the renal circulation.

Q2. A renal corpuscle is:
    (A) Nephron
    (B) Malpighian tubule
    (C) Malpighian body   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Bowman’s capsule
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Renal corpuscle, also called malpighian body, filtration unit of vertebrate nephrons, functional units of the kidney. It consists of a knot of capillaries (glomerulus) surrounded by a double-walled capsule (Bowman's capsule) that opens into a tubule.

Q3. Homeostasis in the body is largely maintained by:
    (A) Egestion and Osmoregulation
    (B) Excretion and Osmoregulation   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Osmoregulation, Excretion, and Egestion
    (D) Excretion and Egestion
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Homeostasis is the maintenance of constant body temperature. It is mainly maintained by excretion and osmoregulation, which is the function of the kidney.

Q4. The urinary bladder is absent in:
    (A) Kangaroos
    (B) Camels
    (C) Snakes   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Monkey
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Urinary bladder is absent in snake and bird because the urine of these is semi-solid consisting mainly of uric acid. The primary function of the urinary bladder is to store urine in mammals. The urinary bladder cannot store semi-solid urine.

Q5. Ascending limb of Henle’s loop is not permeable for:
    (A) K^+
    (B) Cl^-
    (C) Na^+
    (D) H_2O   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Ascending limb of Henle’s is not permeable to water. The descending limb is although permeable to water. Countercurrent exchange takes place between the loop of Henle’s and arteries surrounding it.

Q6. The physiological unit of a kidney is:
    (A) Juxtaglomerular apparatus
    (B) Proximal convoluted tubule
    (C) Distal convoluted tubule
    (D) Uriniferous tubule   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Nephrons are the physical unit or functional unit of the kidney. Millions of nephrons are present in each kidney but a physiological unit of the kidney is uriniferous tubules.

Q7. The adult human kidney is metanephric. So, first embryonic tubules formed in vertebrates during embryonic development are:
    (A) Mesonephric
    (B) Metanephric
    (C) Amphinephric
    (D) Pronephric   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The adult human kidney is metanephric, the third and final excretory organ that develops in a vertebrate embryo. First embryonic tubules formed in vertebrates during embryonic development are pronephric.

Q8. Urinary bladder helps to:
    (A) Stores urine for reabsorbing water from it
    (B) Concentrate urea in urine
    (C) Detoxify excess urine
    (D) Void urine when desired   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The urinary bladder is a hollow elastic organ that functions as the body's urine storage tank. Urine produced by the kidneys flows through the ureters to the urinary bladder, where is it stored before passing into the urethra and exiting the body.

Q9. The part of a nephron which adds some material to the filtrate is:
    (A) Loop of Henle
    (B) Bowman’s capsule
    (C) Proximal convoluted tubule
    (D) Distal convoluted tubule   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Each nephron consists of Bowman’s cup, tubules, and loops of Henle’s. The filtration of blood occurs in glomerulus cells present in Bowman’s cup. Some materials are added to the initial filtrate in the distal convoluted tubule.

Q10. In the human kidney:
 the outer zone is called the medulla and inner zone is called the cortex.
 cortex extends between medullary pyramids as renal columns of Bellini.
    (A) Statement (ii) is wrong and (i) is correct
    (B) Statement (ii) is correct and (i) is incorrect
    (C) Both statements (i) and (ii) are incorrect   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Both statements (i) and (ii) are correct
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Inside the kidney, there are two zones, an outer cortex, and an inner medulla. The cortex extends in between the medullary pyramids as renal columns called columns of Bertini.

Q11. Vasa recta is absent or reduced in:
    (A) Bowman’s capsule
    (B) Juxtamedullary nephrons
    (C) PCT
    (D) Cortical nephrons   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The efferent arteriole emerging from the glomerulus forms a fine capillary network around the renal tubule called the peritubular capillaries. A minute vessel of this network runs parallel to Henle’s loop forming a ‘U’ shaped vasa recta. Vasa recta are absent or highly reduced in cortical nephrons.

Q12. Towards the centre of the inner concave surface of the kidney is a notch called:
    (A) Hilum   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Calyces
    (C) Medulla
    (D) Cortex
    Answer: A
    Explanation: On the medial margin of the kidney is a concave region called the renal hilum. The renal hilum is the entrance to the renal sinus. Structures such as the renal veins, artery, nerves, and lymphatic vessels are located in the renal hilum.

Q13. Label the following in diagram
    (A) Parenchyma cells
    (B) Podocytes   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Proximal cells
    (D) Pituicytes
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The diagram shown above is Malpighian body or renal corpuscles. The marked part in this is called Podocytes or visceral epithelial cells in Bowman’s capsule in the kidney that warp around capillaries of the glomerules.

Q14. In the human excretory system:
 Kidneys and ureters are paired structures but the urinary bladder is single.
 Kidneys are situated between the levels of the last thoracic and third lumbar vertebra.
    (A) Statement (i) is correct and (ii) is incorrect
    (B) Both statements (i) and (ii) are incorrect
    (C) Both statements (i) and (ii) are correct   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Statement (ii) is incorrect and (i) is correct
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The excretory system in humans consists of a pair of kidneys, one pair of ureters, a urinary bladder, and a urethra. Kidneys are reddish-brown, bean-shaped structures situated between the levels of the last thoracic and third lumbar vertebra close to the dorsal inner wall of the abdominal cavity.

Q15. In the following diagram what are 7,9 & 10 :
    (A) ureter, hilum and medulla
    (B) hilum, pelvis and medulla
    (C) pelvis, hilum and calyx   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ureter, pelvis and calyx
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Towards the centre of the innerconcave surface of the kidney is a notchcalled hilum through which ureter, bloodvessels and nerves enter. Inner to the hilumis a broad funnel shaped space called therenal pelvis with projections called calyces. The medulla is divided into a few conical masses projecting into the calyces. Thus, 7, 9, and 10 are pelvis, hilum and calyx respectively.

Excretory Products And Their Elimination Test-02  (id 3425) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Excretory Products and their Elimination
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. Blood enters glomerular capillaries through ________ arteriole and leaves through ________ arteriole.
    (A) distributing, collecting
    (B) afferent, efferent   <-- CORRECT
    (C) radial, collecting
    (D) efferent, afferent
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Bowman cup contains glomerular capillaries to filter the blood. Blood enters the glomerular capillaries through afferent arteriole and leaves through the efferent arteriole.

Q2. pH of urine under healthy conditions is:
    (A) Slightly acidic   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Highly alkaline
    (C) Slightly alkaline
    (D) Neutral
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The pH of urine under healthy conditions is slightly less than 7 so, slightly acidic in nature.

Q3. Which of the following is not a part of glomerular filtrate?
    (A) Globulins   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Inorganic salts
    (C) Creatinine
    (D) Glucose
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Glomerular filtrate contains glucose, inorganic salts, and creatinine but it does not contain globulins protein.

Q4. The epithelial cells of Bowman’s capsule are called:
    (A) Podocytes   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Calyces
    (C) Filtration slits
    (D) Slit pores
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Podocytes are cells in the Bowman's capsule in the kidneys that wrap around capillaries of the glomerulus. The Bowman's capsule filters the blood, retaining large molecules such as proteins while smaller molecules such as water, salts, and sugars are filtered as the first step in the formation of urine.

Q5. Conditional reabsorption of sodium ions and water takes place in_______.
    (A) PCT
    (B) DCT   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Collecting duct
    (D) Henle’s loop
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Distal Convoluted Tubule (DCT): Conditional reabsorption of Na^+ and water takes place in this segment. DCT is also capable of reabsorption of HCO_3^- and selective secretion of hydrogen and potassium ions and NH_3 to maintain the pH and sodium-potassium balance in the blood.

Q6. The filtration fraction is the ratio of GFR to RPF where both the values are in ml/min and FF is expressed in percentage. Calculate FF for a normal adult human being, if RPF= 600ml/min:
    (A) 10.38%
    (B) 2.08%
    (C) 20.83%   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 20.73%
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Filtration fraction is the ratio of glomerular filtration rate (GFR) to the renal plasma flow (RPF). GFR of a normal human is 120 ml/min. so,
FF = ${GFR\over RPF} \times 100$
= ${120\over 600} \times 100$ = 20%.

Q7. During urine formation, the tubular cells secrete ________ into the filtrate.
    (A) only ammonia
    (B) hydrogen ions and potassium ions
    (C) potassium ions and ammonia
    (D) hydrogen ions, potassium ions and ammonia   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The substances that are secreted into the tubular fluid (for removal from the body) include:
 Potassium ions (K+),
 Hydrogen ions (H+),
 Ammonium ions (NH_4+),
 Creatinine,
 Urea,
 Some hormones,
 and some drugs (e.g. penicillin).

Q8. Counter current mechanism:
 It operates in all vertebrates.
 It produces hypertonic urine.
    (A) Statement (i) is correct and (ii) is incorrect
    (B) Statement (i) is incorrect and (ii) is correct   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Both statement (i) and (ii) are incorrect
    (D) Both statements (i) and (ii) are correct
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Countercurrent mechanism operates in mammals but not in all vertebrates. Due to the countercurrent mechanism, it produces hypertonic urine, highly concentrated.

Q9. Read the following statements about urine formation:
 Ultrafiltration doesn’t need any energy expenditure by kidney cells.
 Selective reabsorption of glucose, water, urea, hormones, amino acids, etc takes place through passive transport.
 PCT cells have many microvilli along with few mitochondria since most of the nutrients are absorbed passively.
    (A) Statement (ii) is correct
    (B) Statement (i) is correct   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Statement (ii) and (iii) are correct
    (D) All of these
    Answer: B
    Explanation: During urine formation, ultrafiltration takes place in which energy is not required by cells of the kidney. Selective reabsorption of glucose, water, salt, etc. occurs actively and proximal convoluted tubules (PCT) do not have microvilli.

Q10. If in glomerular capillaries, pressure of blood is 75 mm Hg, osmotic pressure of plasma proteins is 30 mm Hg, and hydrostatic pressure of fluid in renal tubule is 25 mm Hg then net force or the filtration pressure will be calculated as :
    (A) 75 – [ 30 + 20 ] mm Hg   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 75 – [ 30 – 20 ] mm Hg
    (C) 75 + [ 30+20 ] mm Hg
    (D) 75 + [ 30 – 20 ] mm Hg
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Net force of filtration pressure is equal to the blood pressure of glomerular capillaries minus sum of the osmotic pressure of plasma and hydrostatic pressure of fluid in renal tubule. So, filtration pressure = 75 – [ 30 + 20 ] mm Hg.

Q11. The hormone with enzymatic action which catalyses the conversion of angiotensinogen into angiotensin is:
    (A) ANF
    (B) Renin   <-- CORRECT
    (C) JFA
    (D) Aldosterone
    Answer: B
    Explanation: A fall in glomerular blood flow/glomerular blood pressure/GFR can activate the JG cells to release renin which converts angiotensinogen in the blood to angiotensin I and further to angiotensin II.

Q12. Vasopressin is a hormone involved in the regulation of urine formation. It is secreted from:
    (A) Kidney JGA
    (B) Neurohypophysis   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Hypothalamus
    (D) Adenohypohysis
    Answer: B
    Explanation: An excessive loss of fluid from the body can activate receptors that stimulate the hypothalamus to release antidiuretic hormone (ADH) or vasopressin from the neurohypophysis.

Q13. Select the mismatched pair of the following:
    (A) Cortical Nephron - About 25% of total nephrons
    (B) Glomerular Filtration Rate - 180 litres per day
    (C) Lungs removes CO_2 - 180L/day   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Juxtamedullary Nephron - About 15% of total nephrons
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A cortical nephron is about 25% of total nephrons. The glomerular filtration rate is 180 litre per day. Juxtamedullary nephron makes about 15% of total nephrons but the lung does not remove 180 L of carbon dioxide per day.

Q14. What are the unlabeled a, b & c in the given flow chart?
    (A) renin, adrenal cortex, sodium retention   <-- CORRECT
    (B) rennin, adrenal cortex, sodium retention
    (C) renin, adrenal medulla, potassium retention
    (D) rennin,adrenal medulla, sodium chloride retention
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Renin convert angiotensin I to angiotensin II which activates adrenal cortex to release aldosterone. Aldosterone helps to reabsorption of sodium and water from DCT.

Q15. Read the following statements about renal threshold:
 The renal threshold of glucose is 180 mg/100ml of blood.
 If the blood level of glucose exceeds 180mg, it leads to diabetes insipidus.
 If the blood level of glucose exceeds 180mg, it leads to diabetes mellitus.
    (A) Statement (i) and (ii) are correct
    (B) Statement (i) and (iii) are correct   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Statement (ii) is correct
    (D) Statement (i) is correct
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The renal threshold is the state when glucose is present in urine. The renal threshold of glucose is 180 mg/100 ml of blood. If the blood glucose level exceeds 180 mg, it leads to diabetes insipidus.

Excretory Products And Their Elimination Test-03  (id 3426) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Excretory Products and their Elimination
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. During micturition, the muscles of urinary bladder, and urethral sphincters will:
    (A) Relax and contract respectively
    (B) Contract and relax respectively   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Keep expanding
    (D) Show fatigue
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The CNS passes on motor messages to initiate the contraction of smooth muscles of the bladder and simultaneous relaxation of the urethral sphincter causing the release of urine.

Q2. In the following pictorial representation of Kreb’s Hensleit cycle, find out 1,2& 3?
    (A) ornithine, arginine and citrulline
    (B) citrulline, arginine and ornithine   <-- CORRECT
    (C) ornithine, citrulline and arginine
    (D) arginine, citrulline and ornithine
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Kreb’s Hensleit cycle is the sequence of chemical reaction occurring primarily in the liver that results in the production of urea. In this cycle ammonia is fist converted into citrulline along with carbon dioxide that change into arginine and finally into ornithine.

Q3. Read the following:
 Infants and toddlers are often under the habit of bed wetting since micturition is a reflex process.
 Adults and grown-up children can control this reflex process, voluntarily to some extent.
    (A) Statement (i) is correct and (ii) is incorrect
    (B) Statement (i) is incorrect and (ii) is correct
    (C) Both statements (i) and (ii) are incorrect
    (D) Both statement (i) and (ii) are correct   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The process of release of urine is called micturition and the neural mechanism causing it is called the micturition reflex. Adults and grown-up children can control the reflex process of micturition voluntarily to some extent.

Q4. All of the following organs help in excretion except:
    (A) Lungs
    (B) Heart   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Liver
    (D) Skin
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The lungs help in the excretion of carbon dioxide, the liver help in the excretion of the toxic substance, and the skin help in the removal of extra salts along with sweat. The heart is the organ that pumps the blood in the body.

Q5. Urea cycle operates in:
    (A) Sweat glands and sebaceous glands
    (B) Skin cells
    (C) Lungs
    (D) Liver   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Urea cycles operate in the liver, where ammonia is converted into urea. Sometimes urea cycle also occurs in the kidney.

Q6. Read the following:
 Avian kidneys have very short loops of Henle.
 Birds are unable to make urine as hypotonic as mammals can.
    (A) Statement (ii) is correct and (i) is incorrect
    (B) Both statements (i) and (ii) are correct
    (C) Both statements (i) and (ii) are incorrect
    (D) Statement (ii) is incorrect and (i) is correct   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Avian kidneys have very short loops of Henle’s. Loops of Henle’s used in the concentration of urine. Birds make urine highly hypotonic.

Q7. If kidney tissues are supplied with blood low in oxygen then:
    (A) Both tubular reabsorption and ultrafiltration stops   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Tubular reabsorption stops
    (C) Both tubular reabsorption and ultrafiltration continue normally
    (D) Ultrafiltration stops
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Both tubular reabsorption and ultrafiltration stops

Q8. Diabetes insipidus is caused due to:
    (A) Increased secretion of ADH
    (B) Hypotension
    (C) Impaired urea cycle
    (D) Reduced secretion of ADH   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Diabetes insipidus is a rate variety of diabetes characterized by excessive thrust and excretion of a large amount of urine. It is caused due to reduced secretion of antidiuretic hormone (ADH) or vasopressin hormone.

Q9. Rahul is anaemic and a few days ago suffered from massive haemorrhage. Now, what problems he may face:
    (A) All of these   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Accumulation of waste products in body
    (C) Very low blood pressure
    (D) No glomerular filteration
    Answer: A
    Explanation: If the anaemic person suffered from massive haemorrhage, the problem he may face includes very low blood pressure, accumulation of wastes products in the body, and no glomerular filtration in the kidney.

Q10. Reema is on dialysis and she is unable to conceive due to high levels of waste products in her body fluids. Her doctor can suggest her ________.
    (A) Kidney transplant   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Laser therapy
    (C) Operation of damaged kidney
    (D) More frequent hemodialysis
    Answer: A
    Explanation: When both kidneys of a person get damaged and not able to filter the blood, dialysis is used to remove nitrogenous wastes. High wastes accumulation is unable a woman to conceive. The ultimate solution to this problem is a kidney transplant.

Q11. People with chronic kidney disease are usually affected by anaemia. It happens because a damaged kidney doesn’t secrete sufficient:
    (A) Angiotensin II
    (B) Erythropoietin   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Angiotensin I
    (D) Atrial natriuretic factor
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The person suffering from chronic kidney disease are usually affected by anaemia. The damaged kidney is not able to secrete sufficient erythropoietin in the blood that helps in the absorption of iron.

Q12. Match the kidney disorders and its symptoms:
 (a) Ketosis
 (i) frequent thirst
 (b) Polydipsia
 (ii) blood in urine
 (c) Alkaptonuria
 (iii) acetoacetic acid in urine
 (d) Haematuria
 (iv) homogentisic acid in urine
    (A) (a) - (iv), (b) - (i), (c) - (iii), (d) - (ii)
    (B) (a) - (iv), (b) - (ii), (c) - (iv), (d) - (i)
    (C) (a) - (iii), (b) - (i), (c) - (iv), (d) - (ii)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (a) - (iii), (b) - (ii), (c) - (iv), (d) - (i)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Ketosis is the presence of acetoacetic acid in the urine, polydipsia is the condition of frequent thirst, alkaptonuria is the presence of homogentisic acid in urine and haematuria is the presence of blood in the urine.

Q13. Dev consumes a large amount of alcohol and the result is polyuria and dehydration due to:
    (A) Increase in the level of vasopressin
    (B) Decrease in the level of vasopressin   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Decrease in the level of ANF
    (D) Decrease in the level of aldosterone
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Polyuria is usually the result of drinking excessive amounts of fluids (polydipsia), particularly water and fluids that contain caffeine or alcohol. A person suffering from polyuria may develop excessive production of urea and suffer from dehydration due to a decrease in the level of antidiuretic hormone or vasopressin.

Q14. Which one of the following is correct with reference to haemodialysis?
    (A) Anti-heparin is added prior to haemodialysis.
    (B) It absorbs and resends excess of ions.
    (C) The dialysis unit has a coiled semi permeable cellophane tube.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Nitrogenous wastes are removed by active transport
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In haemodialysis, blood drained from a convenient artery is pumped into a dialysing unit after adding an anticoagulant like heparin. The unit contains a coiled cellophane tube surrounded by a fluid (dialysing fluid) having the same composition as that of plasma except for the nitrogenous wastes. The porous cellophane membrane of the tube allows the passage of molecules based on concentration gradient. As nitrogenous wastes are absent in the dialysing fluid, these substances freely move out, thereby clearing the blood. The cleared blood is pumped back to the body through a vein after adding anti-heparin to it.

Q15. Match the following:
 Animal
 Excretory organ
 (a) Dugesia
 (i) body surface
 (b) Palaemon
 (ii) malpighian tubules
 (c) Palamnaeus
 (iii) protonephridia
 (d) Sea anemone
 (iv) green glands
    (A) (a) - (i), (b) - (iii), (c) - (iv), (d) - (ii)
    (B) (a) - (iv), (b) - (ii), (c) - (i), (d) - (iii)
    (C) (a) - (ii), (b) - (i), (c) - (iii), (d) - (iv)
    (D) (a) - (iii), (b) - (iv), (c) - (ii), (d) - (i)   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Excretory system of Dugesia is protonephridia, Palaemon is a body surface, Palamnaeus is malpighian tubules and that of Sea anemone is body surface.

# Locomotion and Movement  (3 tests)

Locomotion And Movement Test-01  (id 3427) [FREE]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Locomotion and Movement
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. Actin filaments are found in all eukaryotic cells but reportedly absent in:
    (A) Human sperms
    (B) Fish sperms
    (C) Nematode sperms   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Camel sperms
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Actin filament help in the contraction and relaxation of muscles. Actin filament is found in all eukaryotic cells but it is absent in nematode sperms.

Q2. Study of muscles is called:
    (A) Musclogy
    (B) Mycology
    (C) Sarcology
    (D) Myology   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Myology is the study of the muscular system, including the study of the structure, function, and diseases of muscle.

Q3. The correct organization of skeletal muscle is:
    (A) fascicles $ \to $ muscle fibres $ \to $ myofilaments $ \to $ sarcomere   <-- CORRECT
    (B) muscle bundles $ \to $ myofibrils $ \to $ muscle cells $ \to $ sarcomere
    (C) fascia $ \to $ muscle cells $ \to $ myofibrils $ \to $ sarcomere
    (D) muscle bundles $ \to $ muscle cells $ \to $ muscle fibres $ \to $ sarcomere
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Each organized skeletal muscle in our body is made of a number of muscle bundles or fascicles held together by a common collagenous connective tissue layer called fascia. Each muscle bundle contains a number of muscle fibers. A characteristic feature of the muscle fiber is the presence of a large number of parallelly arranged filaments in the sarcoplasm called myofilaments or myofibrils. The portion of the myofibril between two successive ‘Z’ lines is considered as the functional unit of contraction and is called a sarcomere.

Q4. Discovery of actin is credited to_______.
    (A) Straub   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Halliburton
    (C) John Kendren
    (D) Pollard and Korn
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Actin and myosin filaments are responsible for the contraction and relaxation of the muscle. The discovery of actin is credited to Straub.

Q5. Muscles are attached to bones via:
    (A) Tendon   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Joints
    (C) Ligament
    (D) Screw
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Muscles are attached to bones by tendons and bones are attached to another bone by ligaments. Tendon and ligaments are types of connective tissue.

Q6. A functional G-actin molecule in its free state is bound to:
    (A) Magnesium ion and ATP   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Mangnese ion and ATP
    (C) Sodium ion and ATP
    (D) Calcium ion and ATP
    Answer: A
    Explanation: A functional G-actin molecule in its free state is bound to magnesium ion and ATP. The G-actin molecule forms a bridge between the muscle fibres for sliding.

Q7. A meromyosin molecule doesn’t contain:
    (A) Tail
    (B) Arm
    (C) Trunk   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Head
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Each meromyosin has two important parts, a globular head with a short arm and a tail.

Q8. The property which doesn’t belong to muscle fibres is:
    (A) Excitability
    (B) Elasticity
    (C) Contractility
    (D) Conductivity   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Muscle fibres have properties of excitability, elasticity, and contractility but conductivity is not present in muscle fibers. These fibres help in the movement of different body parts.

Q9. Myoglobin is found to be:
 highly abundant in muscles of whales and seals.
 exhibiting cooperative binding of oxygen.
 allowing organisms to hold their breath longer underwater.
    (A) Statement (i) and (iii) are correct   <-- CORRECT
    (B) All of these
    (C) Statement (ii) is correct
    (D) Statement (i) and (ii) are correct
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Myoglobin is found to be highly abundant in muscles of whales and seals. Myoglobin being oxygen and iron-binding protein allowing organisms to hold their breath longer underwater.

Q10. Polymerisation of actin monomers involves ATP hydrolysis as shown in the following figure: [choose the correct one]
    (A) 
    (B)    <-- CORRECT
    (C) 
    (D) 
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Each ‘F’ actin is a polymer of monomeric ‘G’ (Globular) actins.

Q11. Look at the following figure of myofibrils
figure (1), (2), (3), (4) : showing ?
    (A) (1) & (2) represent relaxed state while (3) & (4) represent breaking of cross bridge
    (B) (1) & (2) represent relaxed state while (3) & (4) represent cross bridge formation   <-- CORRECT
    (C) (1) & (2) represent contracted state while (3) & (4) represent breaking of cross bridge
    (D) (1) & (2) represent contracted state while (3) & (4) represent cross bridge formation
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Myofibrils are present in muscles fibers which are parallelly arranged filaments in sarcoplasm. Figure 1 and 2 present relaxed state while figure 3 and 4 represents cross bridge formation.

Q12. Look at the following figure of movement of the thin filaments
The label x, y, and z are respectively
    (A) H zone, A band and I band
    (B) I band, A band, H zone
    (C) H zone, I band, A band   <-- CORRECT
    (D) I band, H zone, A band
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The label x is H-zone, y is I band and z is A band.

Q13. The correct result of ATPase activity that occurs during muscle contraction is :
    (A)    <-- CORRECT
    (B) 
    (C) 
    (D) 
    Answer: A
    Explanation: ATPase enzyme acts on myosin to act on ATP to convert into ADP. The activated myosin combine with actin for contraction.

Q14. Read the following statements about muscle contraction in humans:
 chemical energy is converted into mechanical energy during muscle contraction and the chemical is a neurotransmitter.
 neurotransmitter acetylcholine at the motor end plate converts electrical energy into mechanical energy.
 in a contracted muscle, volume remains the same.
 a contracted muscle becomes shorter and thicker.
    (A) Statement (i) and (iv) are correct
    (B) Statement (iv) is correct
    (C) Statement (ii), (iii) and (iv) are correct
    (D) Statement (i), (iii) and (iv) are correct   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The chemical energy is converted into mechanical energy during muscle contraction and the chemical is a neurotransmitter. In a contracted muscle, volume remains the same and a contracted muscle becomes shorter and thicker.

Q15. Which of the following statements is/are incorrect about sliding filament theory of muscle contraction?
    (A) During contraction, Z lines come closer together.
    (B) During the contraction width of the H zone decreases.
    (C) During contraction width of I and A bands remain the same.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) During contraction width of I and A bands remain the same and During contraction width of H zone decreases.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: During contraction, the ‘I’ bands get reduced, whereas the ‘A’ bands retain the length.

Q1. What do the following figure represent in (i),(ii) and (iii)?
    (A) H-line, myosin myofilaments, Z-line
    (B) Z-line, myosin myofilaments, M-line
    (C) M-line, actomyosinmyofilaments, Z-line   <-- CORRECT
    (D) M-line, actin myofilaments, Z-lines
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The figure represents muscle fibres marked
 as M-line,
 as actomyosin myofilaments and
 Represents Z-line.

Q2. From the following figure infer:
(a) = ?, (b) = ? and (c) = ?
    (A) staircase effect, tetanus and summation
    (B) single muscle twitch, staircase effect and tetanus
    (C) staircase effect, summation and tetanus   <-- CORRECT
    (D) summation, recruitment and tetanus
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Myograms is a diagnostic test of health and functionality of a person’s muscle. In the given myograms,
 shows staircase effect,
 shows summation and
 shows tetanus that leads to fatigue.

Q3. Myoglobin was the first protein to have its three-dimensional structure revealed. Ravi was diagnosed with myoglobin in his bloodstream. This had occurred due to:
    (A) Myasthenia gravis
    (B) Arthritis
    (C) Muscle injury   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Conversion of Hb into Mb
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Myoglobin is an iron and oxygen-binding protein found in the muscle tissue of mammals. The presence of myoglobin in the bloodstream may be due to muscle injury of Ravi due to accident or sudden jerk.

Q4. The vertebral formula of human is:
    (A) C_7T_12L_5S_(5)C_(4)   <-- CORRECT
    (B) C_8T_12L_4S_(5)C_(6)
    (C) C_6T_12L_6S_(5)C_(4)
    (D) C_7T_11L_5S_(7)C_(4)
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The vertebral column is differentiated into cervical (7), thoracic (12), lumbar (5), sacral (5-fused) and coccygeal (4-fused) regions starting from the skull.

Q5. At the base of skull, a large hole is present which allows brain to continue with the spinal cord. That hole is called :
    (A) Vertebral foramen
    (B) Foramen magnum   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Foramen ovale
    (D) Obturator foramen
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Foramen Magnum is the largest foramen situated on the base of the skull through which multiple structures pass including the Spinal Cord. It acts as a passage between the cranial vault and the base of the skull.

Q6. Axial skeleton consists of:
    (A) 70 bones
    (B) 65 bones
    (C) 22 bones
    (D) 80 bones   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The axial skeleton is the part of the skeleton that consists of the bones of the head and trunk of a vertebrate. In the human skeleton, it consists of 80 bones and is composed of six parts; the skull bones, the ossicles of the middle ear, the hyoid bone, the rib cage, the sternum, and the vertebral column.

Q7. Match the following:
 Vertebra
 No.of bones feature
 (a) Cervical
 (i) 5
 (b) Coccyx
 (ii) 4
 (c) Thoracic
 (iii) 12
 (d) Lumbar
 (iv) 7
    (A) (a) - (ii), (b) - (iii), (c) - (i), (d) - (iv)
    (B) (a) - (i), (b) - (iii), (c) - (iv), (d) - (ii)
    (C) (a) - (iv), (b) - (ii), (c) - (iii), (d) - (ii)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (a) - (iv), (b) - (ii), (c) - (i), (d) - (iii)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The vertebral column usually consists of 33 vertebrae: 24 presacral vertebrae (7 cervical, 12 thoracic, and 5 lumbar) followed by the sacrum (5 fused sacral vertebrae) and the coccyx (4 frequently fused coccygeal vertebrae).

Q8. Which of the following is not a part of hip bone?
    (A) Pubis
    (B) Tibia   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Ilium
    (D) Ischium
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Hip bone or pelvic girdle consists of two coxal bones. Each coxal bone is formed by the fusion of three bones- ilium, ischium, and pubis.

Q9. Which of the following is not a part of coxal bone?
    (A) Ilium
    (B) Pubis
    (C) Ischium
    (D) Acromion   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The coxal bone (hip bone, pelvic bone) is a large, flattened, irregularly shaped bone, constricted in the center and expanded above and below. It consists of three parts, the ilium, ischium, and pubis, which are distinct from each other in the young subject but are fused in the adult.

Q10. Match the following:
 Animal
 Type of skeleton
 (a) Sphyrna
 (i) exoskeleton
 (b) Pediculus
 (ii) hydrostatic skeleton
 (c) Asterias
 (iii) cartilaginous skeleton
 (d) Metridium
 (iv) endoskeleton
    (A) (a) - (iv), (b) - (ii), (c) - (i), (d) - (iii)
    (B) (a) - (i), (b) - (iii), (c) - (iv), (d) - (ii)
    (C) (a) - (iii), (b) - (i), (c) - (iv), (d) - (ii)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (a) - (ii), (b) - (iii), (c) - (i), (d) - (iv)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Different kinds of skeleton systems are found in different organisms. Sphyma contains a cartilaginous skeleton. Pediculus contains an exoskeleton. Asterias contain endoskeleton and Metridium contains a hydrostatic skeleton.

Q11. The upright posture in humans is facilitated by:
    (A) Radius and ulna
    (B) Massive hindlimb bones making broad feet
    (C) Only pelvis
    (D) Massive hind limb bones making broad feet and pelvis   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The upright posture in humans is facilitated by massive hind limbs bones that make broad feet and pelvis to withhold the weight of whole body.

Q12. Each pectoral girdle:
 it has 2 pairs of bones, a pair of the clavicle and a pair of scapula.
 scapula contains the expanded process and glenoid cavity, the latter is for the articulation of the head of humerus.
    (A) Both statements (i) and (ii) are correct
    (B) Statement (i) is correct and (ii) is incorrect
    (C) Statement (i) is incorrect and (ii) is correctt
    (D) Both statements (i) and (ii) are incorrect   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Both statements (i) and (ii) are incorrect

Q13. Match the following:
 (a) Hipbone
 (i) patella
 (b) Kneebone
 (ii) clavicle
 (c) Collarbone
 (iii) suture
 (d) Immovable joint
 (iv) innominate
    (A) (a) - (iv), (b) - (i), (c) - (ii), (d) - (iii)   <-- CORRECT
    (B) (a) - (iv), (b) - (ii), (c) - (iii), (d) - (i)
    (C) (a) - (ii), (b) - (iii), (c) - (i), (d) - (iv)
    (D) (a) - (iii), (b) - (ii), (c) - (iv), (d) - (ii)
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Hip bone is called as innominate bone, the knee bone is called as patella, collarbone is called as clavicle and immovable joint is called a suture.

Q14. Select the correctly matched pair:
    (A) 9th and 10th pair of ribs → false ribs
    (B) 9th and 10th pair of ribs $\to $ true ribs
    (C) 11th and 12th pair of ribs → floating ribs   <-- CORRECT
    (D) First eight pair of ribs → true ribs
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The last 2 pairs i.e., 11th and 12th of ribs are not connected ventrally and are, therefore, called floating ribs.

Q15. In a woman, the pelvis is larger and has a broader front than a man. It is:
    (A) An adaptation for sexual dimorphism
    (B) Responsible for problems during the menstrual cycle
    (C) An adaptation for gestation and parturition   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Evolutionary error
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In a woman, the pelvis is larger and has a broader front than a man. It is an adaptation for gestation and parturition during pregnancy.

Q1. Read the following statements:
 Cartilaginous joint is often called symphysis and eg. joints between adjacent vertebrae.
 The joint between atlas and axis vertebrae in man is a cartilaginous joint.
    (A) Both statements (i) and (ii) are incorrect
    (B) Both statements (i) and (ii) are correct
    (C) Statement (ii) is incorrect and (i) is correct   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Statement (ii) is correct and (i) is incorrect
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The joint between the adjacent vertebrae in the vertebral column is caritilaginous joint.

Q2. Read the following:
 The synovial joints are characterized by the presence of a fluid-filled synovial cavity between the articulating surfaces of the two bones.
 The saddle is a type of synovial joint.
    (A) Statement (i) is correct and (ii) is incorrect
    (B) Both statements (i) and (ii) are correct   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Statement (ii) is incorrect and (i) is correct
    (D) Both statements (i) and (ii) are incorrect
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Synovial joints are characterized by the presence of a fluid-filled synovial cavity between the articulating surfaces of the two bones. A saddle joint is a synovial joint where one of the bones forming the joint is shaped like a saddle with the other bone resting on it like a rider on a horse. Saddle joint (between carpal and metacarpal of thumb).

Q3. The following X-ray shows:
    (A) a person with muscular dystrophy
    (B) a person with bone cancer
    (C) a person with osteoporosis in his knee
    (D) a person with gout in his knee   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The X-ray of knee shows gout in the knee. Gout is a kind of arthritis. It can cause an attack of sudden burning pain, stiffness and swelling in joint.

Q4. The joint present between the carpals is
    (A) Ball and socket joint
    (B) Pivot joint
    (C) Gliding joint   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Saddle joint
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Many gliding joints are formed in the appendicular skeleton between the carpal bones of the wrist; between the carpals and the metacarpals of the palm; between the tarsal bones of the ankle; and between the tarsals and the metatarsals of the foot.

Q5. Match the following:
(a) Fibrous joint
(i) 
(b) Hinge joint
(ii) 
(c) Ball and socket joint
(iii) 
(d) Ellipsoid joint
(iv)
    (A) - ii
 - i

 - iii
 - i
 - ii
    (C) - ii
 - iv
 - iii
 - i
    (D) - iii
 - i
 - iv
 - ii
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Fibrous joint is present in skull bone, hinge joint is present in knee, ball and socket joint is present in shoulder and forelimb and ellipsoid joint is present in wrist of human beings.

Q6. Read the following statements and view carefully the figure:
Osteoporosis is an age-related disorder characterised by decreased bone mass. Osteoarthritis is shown in the following figure.
The above figure shows gouty arthritis which is caused by inflammation of joints.
Decreased levels of estrogen is a common cause for increased chances of fractures.
Inflammation of joints is caused by decreased levels of calcium ions in body fluids.
    (A) only statement (ii) is correct.
    (B) only statement (ii) and (iv) are correct.
    (C) only statement (i) and (iii) are correct.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) only statement (iv) is correct.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Osteoporosis is an age-related disorder characterised by decreased bone mass. It is mainly caused by decreased level of estrogen in blood. Osteoporosis may leads to increased chances of fracture.

Q7. In the following two graphs:
 the first graph shows: twitch $ \to $ summation $ \to $ etanus $ \to $ fatigue.
 the second graph shows incomplete and complete tetanus.
    (A) Statement (ii) is wrong and (i) is correct.
    (B) both statements are wrong.
    (C) Statement (i) is correct and (ii) is wrong.
    (D) both statements are correct.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Graph 1 shows muscle fibre tension with time. Which occurs in order as: twitch $ \to $ summation $ \to $ tetanus $ \to $ fatigue.
Graph 2 shows complete and incomplete tetanus. Tetanus is also known as lockjaw, which is a infection characterized by muscle spasm.

Q8. Aging will be characterised by:
    (A) Increased muscle fat
    (B) Decreased muscle size
    (C) Increased muscle protein
    (D) Decreased muscle size and increased muscle fat   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Aging will be characterized by decreased muscle size and increased muscle fat. With aging muscle loose its contractile and elasticity nature. Fats are deposited in muscle fibres the further decrease contracting ability.

Q9. Muscular dystrophy is a genetic disorder:
 It is genetically inherited.
 Some people get affected by MD due to the mutated dystrophin gene and nutritional defects at the pre-natal age.
 Predominantly males are affected by DMD although females can be carriers of it.
 Dystrophin is a protein found in tendons.
    (A) Statement (i) and (iii) are correct
    (B) Statement (i), (ii) and (iii) are correct   <-- CORRECT
    (C) All of these
    (D) Statement (i) is correct
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Muscular dystrophy is a genetic disorder and genetically inherited. It may also occur due to mutated dystrophin gene and nutritional defects at the pre-natal age. Males are more affected by MD although females can be carriers of it.

Q10. Read the following about joint replacement therapy :
 Artificial joints are made from a similar material that makes our bones.
 Metal or plastic is used to prepare an artificial joint.
 The following figure shows a dysfunctional joint in the knee.
 Above figure shows an artificial joint in the knee.
    (A) only statement (ii) and (iv) are correct.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) only statement (i) and (iv) are correct.
    (C) only statement (i) and (iii) are correct.
    (D) only statement (iv) is correct.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Artificial joints are made up of metal and plastic. The figure shown above shows artificial joint in the knee.

Q11. Sachin suffers from hypoparathyroidism. This can lead him to:
    (A) Hypercalcemia and tetany
    (B) Hypoglycemia and tetany
    (C) Hypocalcemia and tetany   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Hypoglycemia and arthritis
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Hypoparathyroidism is the condition in which the body secretes abnormally low level of parathyroid hormone. This deficiency may lead to hypocalcemia and tetany.

Q12. Which disorder is caused due to wild contractions in muscles?
    (A) Muscular dystrophy
    (B) Tetany   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Arthritis
    (D) Gout
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Tetany is caused due to rapid spasms (wild contractions) in muscle due to low Ca^++ in body fluid.

Q13. During vigorous exercise:
 Lactic acid accumulates in muscle cells to meet its energy needs immediately.
 Lactic acid is formed by anaerobic respiration hence oxygen consumption by muscles is reduced.
 This reduction in oxygen consumption is called oxygen debt of muscle.
    (A) Statement (i) is correct
    (B) Statement (i) and (ii) are correct   <-- CORRECT
    (C) All of these
    (D) Statement (ii) and (iii) are correct
    Answer: B
    Explanation: During vigorous exercise, lactic acid accumulates in muscles cells to meet the energy requirement of muscle cell. Lactic acid is formed due to insufficient availability of oxygen.

Q14. Myasthenia gravis leads to fatigue and weakness. It is not:
    (A) Neuromuscular disease
    (B) Causing paralysis of respiratory muscles
    (C) Affecting heart muscles   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Autoimmune disorder
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Myasthenia gravis is an autoimmune disorder affecting neuromuscular junction leading to fatigue, weakening, and paralysis of skeletal muscle.

Q15. A 5-year-old girl Sita and her grandmother together met an accident. Her grandmother got her leg fractured but Sita didn’t suffer from any fractures:
 At a young age, bones are more flexible and contain lots of organic matter.
 Sita has a more powerful immune system than her grandmother.
 In old people bones become hard and brittle.
    (A) All of these
    (B) Statement (iii) is correct
    (C) Statement (i) and (iii) are correct   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Statement (ii) is correct
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Generally, bones are flexible at a young age and become hard and brittle at old age.

Neural Control And Coordination Test-01   (id 3430) [FREE]

Q1. Nissl’s granules are absent in:
    (A) Cyton
    (B) Dendrite
    (C) Axon   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Perikaryon
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Nissl’s grains are mainly present in cyton and dendrite. These granules are rough endoplasmic reticulum with rosettes of the free ribosome, the site for protein synthesis. It is absent in the axon.

Q2. In the prosencephalon, first, and second ventricles open into the third ventricle by:
    (A) Foramen of Monro   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Foramen of Magnum
    (C) Foramen of Ovale
    (D) Foramen of Magnidae
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In prosencephalon, the first and second ventricles open into third ventricles by foramen of Monro. It is the opening that connects the left and right sides of the lateral ventricle in the brain.

Q3. The property which doesn’t belong to nerve fibres is:
    (A) Only contractility
    (B) Only elasticity
    (C) Both elasticity and contractility   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Conductivity and excitability
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Nerve fibres are specialized to transmit impulses from one part of the body to others. Nerve fibres do not show the property of elasticity and contractility.

Q4. Hypothalamus helps to maintain homeostasis by controlling hunger, thirst, blood pressure, temperature feelings, etc. So it is an important link between:
    (A) Nervous system and circulatory system
    (B) Nervous system and respiratory system
    (C) Nervous system and endocrine system   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Nervous system and digestive system
    Answer: C
    Explanation: One of the most important functions of the hypothalamus is to link the nervous system to the endocrine system via the pituitary gland (hypophysis). The hypothalamus is located below the thalamus and is part of the limbic system.

Q5. Brain stem is the support system of brain and is the collective name for:
    (A) Cerebrum, mesencephalon, diencephalon, and medulla
    (B) Medulla, pons, midbrain, and diencephalon   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Prosencephalon, mesencephalon, pons, and medulla
    (D) Hypothalamus, diencephalon, cerebellum and pons
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The brainstem (or brain stem) is the posterior part of the brain, adjoining and structurally continuous with the spinal cord. In the human brain, the brainstem includes the midbrain, the pons, and the medulla oblongata. Sometimes the diencephalon, the caudal part of the forebrain, is included.

Q6. Match the following :
 Column A
 Column B
 a) Unipolar nerves
 i) Nerve cells of retina
 b) Mixed nerves
 ii) Nerve cells of cerebral cortex
 c) bipolar nerves
 iii) Nerves of embryonic stage
 d) Multipolar nerves
 iv) All the spinal nerves
    (A) a)-iii, b)-iv, c)-ii, d)-i
    (B) a)-iii, b)-iv, c)-i, d)-ii   <-- CORRECT
    (C) a)-i, b)-iii, c)-iv, d)-ii
    (D) a)-iv, b)-ii, c)-i, d)-iii
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Unipolar nerves are present in nerves of embryonic stage. Mixed nerves are found in all the spinal nerves. Bipolar nerves are present in nerve cells of retina. Multipolarnerves are present in nerve cells of cerebral cortex.

Q7. Match the following:
 Column A
 Column B
 (a) Motor Neuron
 (i) carry impulse away from cyton
 (b) Axon
 (ii) carry impulse from receptor to CNS
 (c) Afferent Neuron
 (iii) carry impulse towards cyton
 (d) Dendrite
 (iv) carry impulse from CNS to effector
    (A) (a) - (iv), (b) - (ii), (c) - (i), (d) - (iii)
    (B) (a) - (i), (b) - (iii), (c) - (iv), (d) - (ii)
    (C) (a) - (iv), (b) - (i), (c) - (ii), (d) - (iii)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (a) - (ii), (b) - (iii), (c) - (i), (d) - (iv)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Motor neurons carry impulse from CNS to the effector. Axon carries the impulse away from cyton. Afferent neuron carries impulse from receptor to CNS and dendrite carry impulse towards cyton.

Q8. Complete the following hierarchical chart showing parts of the nervous system :
    (A) 10 , 33
    (B) 12, 31   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 11, 21
    (D) 8, 30
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The human nervous system consists of the central nervous system and peripheral nervous system. The peripheral nervous system includes 12 pairs of cranial nerves emerging from the brain and 31 pairs of spinal nerves arising from a spinal nerve.

Q9. In the following figure a synapse is shown :
i & ii (from up to down)
is a presynaptic membrane and
is a postsynaptic membrane.
synaptic vesicles are in postsynaptic knob.
neurotransmitter receptors are located on the postsynaptic membrane
    (A) only (i) is correct.
    (B) only (ii) and (iii) are correct.
    (C) only (ii) is correct.
    (D) only (i) and (iii) are correct.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The synapse is formed by the membranes of apre-synaptic neuron and a post-synaptic neuron, which may or may not be separated by a gap called synaptic cleft. The neurotransmitter receptors are located on the postsynaptic membrane.

Q10. Due to refractory period, a nerve fibre in human body on an average transmits about:
    (A) Only 6000 impulses per second
    (B) Only 100 impulses per second
    (C) Only 10,000 impulses per second
    (D) Only 1000 impulses per second   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The refractory period is the time taken to nerve become ready to conduct other impulses. Due to this refractory period, a nerve fibre in the human body on average transmits about 1000 impulses per second.

Q11. Read the following about the surface of cerebral hemispheres:
 Is made up of the pia mater.
 Is greatly convoluted and called the cerebral cortex.
    (A) Both statements (i) and (ii) are incorrect
    (B) Both statements (i) and (ii) are correct
    (C) Statement (i) is incorrect and (ii) is correct   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Statement (i) is correct and (ii) is incorrect
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The layer of cells which covers the cerebral hemisphere is called the cerebral cortex and is thrown into prominent folds.

Q12. The autonomic nervous system or ANS:
 Is truly autonomic i.e. independent of the CNS.
 Is also known as the VNS.
 Transmit impulse from CNS to involuntary organs and smooth muscles.
    (A) Statement (iii) is correct
    (B) All of these
    (C) Statement (i) and (iii) are correct
    (D) Statement (ii) and (iii) are correct   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The autonomic nervous system or ANS is the division of the peripheral nervous system that influences the function of internal organs. ANS is also known as VNS. These nerves transmit impulse from CNS to involuntary organs and smooth muscles.

Q13. Label the arrows in the given diagram of the brain from top to bottom :
    (A) occipital lobe,pons,medulla
    (B) cerebellum, pons, medulla   <-- CORRECT
    (C) cerebrum, pons, medulla
    (D) temporal lobe,cerebellum,medulla
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The part of the human brain shown above has marked as cerebellum, pons and medulla oblongata of the hindbrain.

Q14. The band of nerve fibers that joins the two cerebral hemisphere in mammals is:
    (A) Corpora quadrigemina
    (B) Corpora bigemina
    (C) Corpus callosum   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Cruracerebri
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The corpus callosum (CC) is the largest of the commissural fibres, linking the cerebral cortex of the left and right cerebral hemisphere.

Q15. Vermis is a portion of:
    (A) Medulla oblongata
    (B) Cerebellum   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Pons
    (D) Cerebrum
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The cerebral vermis is located in the medial, cortico-nuclear zone of the cerebellum. It is constricted between the lobe of the cerebellum.

Neural Control And Coordination Test-02  (id 3431) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Neural Control and Coordination

Q1. Part of brain that acts as relay centre to receive and transmit general sensations except smell:
    (A) Midbrain
    (B) Thalamus   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Epithalamus
    (D) Hypothalamus
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Thalamus is the part of the brain that acts as a relay centre to receive and transmit general sensations except for the smell. Thalamus is located in the forebrain superior to the midbrain.

Q2. Brain cavities are filled with CSF. In subarachnoid space, the CSF plays the following roles:
    (A) Acts as a shock proof cushion   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Changes pressure inside cranium in coordination with blood pressure
    (C) Plays a role in night vision
    (D) Keeps brain and spinal cord dry to prevent infection
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Brain cavities are filled with cerebrospinal fluid (CSF). In subarachnoid space, the CSF acts as a shockproof cushion to prevent injury in case of an accident.

Q3. In Pavlov’s conditioned reflex experiment find the correct matches :
 Column A
 Column B
 a) conditioned stimulus
 i) salivation in response to food
 b) conditioned response
 ii) food itself
 c) unconditioned stimulus
 iii)sound of the bell
 d) unconditioned response
 iv) salivation in response to bell
    (A) a)-ii, b)-iii, c)-i, d)-iv
    (B) a)-iii, b)-iv, c)-ii, d)-i   <-- CORRECT
    (C) a)-iv, b)-ii, c)-i, d)-iii
    (D) a)-i, b)-iii, c)-iv, d)-ii
    Answer: B
    Explanation: There are different kinds of stimulus that is received by different receptors in our body. Hearing of sound of bell is conditioned stimulus and salivation in response to bell is conditioned response. Food itself is conditioned stimulus and salivation in response to food is unconditioned response.

Q4. In the following identify from up to down :
    (A) receptor,effector,greymatter,white matter   <-- CORRECT
    (B) receptor,effector,whitematter,grey matter
    (C) effector,receptor,greymatter,white matter
    (D) effector,receptor,whitematter,grey matter
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The reflex pathway comprises at least one afferent neuron (receptor) and one efferent (effector excitor) neuron appropriately arranged in a series. The (iii) and (iv) shows gray and white matter.

Q5. A region on retina of the human eye which is free from rods and cones is:
    (A) Yellow spot
    (B) Fovea
    (C) Black spot
    (D) Optic nerves   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The optic nerves leave the eye and the retinal blood vessels enter it at a point medial to and slightly above the posterior pole of the eyeball. Photoreceptor cells are not present in that region and hence it is called the blind spot.

Q6. The vestibular apparatus is composed of:
    (A) Semicircular canals and otolith organ   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Semicircular canals and macula
    (C) Crista ampullaris and otolith organ
    (D) Crista ampullaris and macula
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The vestibular apparatus is composed of three semicircular canals and the otolith organ consisting of the saccule and utricle.

Q7. The space within cochlea called scala media is filled with_______.
    (A) Labyrinth
    (B) Epilymph
    (C) Endolymph   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Perilymph
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Cochlear duct or scala media has endolymph and high potassium ion concentration that the stereocilia of the hair cells protrude into helicotrema.

Q8. Blood vessels are found to be present in which region of an eye?
    (A) Pupil
    (B) Blind spot
    (C) Cornea
    (D) Choroid   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The middle layer, choroid contains many blood vessels and looks bluish in colour.

Q9. Sneha ceased to get the smell of a perfume applied to her clothes but her friend Reema who passed by complimented her for the noticeable fragrance. This is an example of:
    (A) Reflex action
    (B) Conditioned response
    (C) Hypnotism
    (D) Sensory reception   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The sensory organs detect all types of changes in the environment and send appropriate signals to the CNS, where all the inputs are processed and analysed.

Q10. Among photoreceptors, cones are responsible for the bright light vision and them also:
 give colour vision because they contain 3 different pigments.
 pigments are sensitive to red, green, and yellow lights.
 pigments are sensitive to red, green, and blue lights.
 individual cone cell contains all the three pigments in it.
    (A) Statement (i), (iii) and (iv) are correct
    (B) Statement (i) and (iii) are correct   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Statement (i), (ii) and (iv) are correct
    (D) Statement (i) and (iv) are correct
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In the human eye, there are three types of cones which possess their own characteristic photopigments that respond to red, green, and blue lights. The sensations of different colours are produced by various combinations of these cones and their photopigments.

Q11. Select the correct terms for labels
    (A) Retina, sclera, cornea
    (B) Sclera, lens and pupil
    (C) Cornea, sclera and pupil
    (D) Sclera, pupil and iris   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The external layer is composed of a dense connective tissue and is called the sclera. The ciliary body itself continues forward to form a pigmented and opaque structure called the iris which is the visible coloured portion of the eye. In front of the lens, the aperture surrounded by the iris is called the pupil.

Q12. In the diagram below, 1 and 2 are
    (A) External auditory canal and Eustachian tube
    (B) Cochlear nerve and external auditory canal
    (C) Cochlear nerve and Eustachian tube
    (D) Eustachian tube and External auditory canal   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The outer ear consists of the pinna and external auditory meatus or canal. A Eustachian tube connects the middle ear cavity with the pharynx.

Q13. The human internal ear is:
    (A) Ectodermal in origin   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Mesodermal in origin
    (C) Comprising of ear pinna
    (D) Endodermal in origin
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The human body is triploblastic in nature, ectoderm, mesoderm, and endoderm. These three layers of the embryo form the different organs of human beings. The human internal ear is ectodermal in origin.

Q14. The correctly matched pair is:
    (A) Birds $\to $ both nocturnal and diurnal vision
    (B) Crayfishes $\to $ monochrome vision
    (C) Cats $\to $ binocular vision   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Sharks $\to $ colour vision
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Cats have binocular vision that is cat can use two eyes together. This kind of vision helps in-depth measurement and analysis of the image formed on the retina.

Q15. In the prosencephalon, first, and second ventricles open into the third ventricle by:
    (A) Foramen of Magnidae
    (B) Foramen of Monro   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Foramen of Magnum
    (D) Foramen of Ovale
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In prosencephalon, the first and second ventricles open into third ventricles by foramen of Monro. It is the opening that connects the left and right sides of the lateral ventricle in the brain.
