Q1. Part of brain that acts as relay centre to receive and transmit general sensations except smell:
    (A) Hypothalamus
    (B) Thalamus   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Midbrain
    (D) Epithalamus
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Thalamus is the part of the brain that acts as a relay centre to receive and transmit general sensations except for the smell. Thalamus is located in the forebrain superior to the midbrain.

Q2. Among the following correct matches for ear parts and functions are:
 (a) Cristae
 (i) responsible for lubrication and protection
 (b) Cerumen
 (ii) responsible for dynamic equilibrium
 (c) Organ of Corti
 (iii) responsible for static equilibrium
 (d) Maculae
 (iv) responsible for hearing
    (A) (a) - (iv), (b) - (ii), (c) - (i), (d) - (iii)
    (B) (a) - (iii), (b) - (iv), (c) - (ii), (d) - (i)
    (C) (a) - (ii), (b) - (i), (c) - (iv), (d) - (iii)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (a) - (i), (b) - (iii), (c) - (iv), (d) - (ii)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The cristae present in the internal ear is responsible for dynamic equilibrium. Cerumen is responsible for lubrication and protection. The organ of Corti is responsible for hearing and maculae is responsible for the static equilibrium of the body.

Q3. Gustatoreceptors are responsible for the sense of:
    (A) Touch
    (B) Pressure
    (C) Taste   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Pain
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Gustatoreceptors are responsible for the sense of taste. Gustatory receptors are located inside taste buds on the tongue.

Q4. In the process of eye donation, a particular part of a dead man’s eye is stored and grafted on another person’s eye to restore vision. That donated part of an eye is:
    (A) Cornea   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Retina
    (C) Lens
    (D) Sclera
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The eye donation process involves grafting of the cornea of a dead man’s eye, which is stored and grafted on another person’s eye to restore vision.

Q5. Read the following about neurohypophysis:
 Neurohypophysis secretes neurohormones.
 Oxytocin and ADH are synthesized in the neurohypophysis.
    (A) Both statements (i) and (ii) are correct
    (B) Statement (ii) is correct and (i) is incorrect
    (C) Both statements (i) and (ii) are incorrect
    (D) Statement (ii) is incorrect and (i) is correct   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Neurohyphysis secretes neurohormones, which is a posterior gland, itself is a neural projection from the hypothalamus. Neurohypophyis secretes vasopressin and oxytocin hormone.

Q6. Match the following:
 (a) Hypophysis
 (i) Sense organs
 (b) Modulator
 (ii) Pituitary
 (c) Receptor
 (iii) Brain and spinal cord
 (d) Effector
 (iv) Muscles and glands
    (A) (a) - (iii), (b) - (iv), (c) - (ii), (d) - (i)
    (B) (a) - (i), (b) - (iii), (c) - (iv), (d) - (ii)
    (C) (a) - (ii), (b) - (iii), (c) - (i), (d) - (iv)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (a) - (iv), (b) - (ii), (c) - (i), (d) - (iii)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The hypophysis is a part of the pituitary gland. The modulator is present in the brain and spinal cord. The receptor is located in sense organs. Effectors are muscles and glands that bring about movement.

Q7. Find out the mismatched pair:
    (A) smell area → frontal lobe
    (B) general sensory area → parietal lobe
    (C) speech area → parietal lobe   <-- CORRECT
    (D) visual area → occipital lobe
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Different parts of the human brain have a specialized area for different receptors. Visual area is located in the occipital lobe. A general sensory area is located in the parietal lobe, the smell area is located in the frontal area. Speech area is not located in the parietal lobe.

Q8. Reticular activating system (RAC) of the brain:
 It works as a bridge to connect the lower brain to the upper brain.
 It helps us to focus on the important things and evade the useless things.
    (A) Statement (i) is incorrect and (ii) is correct
    (B) Statement (i) is correct and (ii) is incorrect
    (C) Both statements (i) and (ii) are correct   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Both statements (i) and (ii) are incorrect
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The reticular activating system (RAC) of the brain works as a bridge to connect the lower brain to the upper brain. It helps to focus on the important things and evade useless things.

Q9. The choroid layer in the human eye:
 darkens the cavity of the eyeball to prevent internal reflection of light.
 its blood vessels nourish the retina.
 it regulates the shape of the eye lens.
    (A) Only (i) and (ii) are correct   <-- CORRECT
    (B) All of these
    (C) Only (ii) is correct
    (D) Only (i) and (iii) are correct
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The choroid layer in the human eye darkens the cavity of the eyeball to prevent internal reflection of light. The blood vessels of the choroid layer nourish the retina. The shape of the eye lens is changed by ciliary muscles.

Q10. Read the following:
 In the human iris, the contraction of sphincter muscles widens the pupil in dim light to let in more light.
 The amount of pigment in the ciliary body of eye provides an eye with its characteristic colour.
    (A) Statement (i) is incorrect and (ii) is correct
    (B) Statement (i) is correct and (ii) is incorrect
    (C) Both statements (i) and (ii) are incorrect   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Both statements (i) and (ii) are correct
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Human eyes contain iris that is responsible for changing the size of the pupil to allow or prevent the amount of light entering the eyeball. Cons cells present in the retina are responsible for colour perception.

Q11. While crying, tears come out of eyes but some watery fluid comes out of the nose as well. This fluid is:
    (A) Excessive secretion of Pituitary glands
    (B) Excessive secretion of mucus glands
    (C) Excessive secretion of lacrimal glands   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Excessive secretion of sebaceous glands
    Answer: C
    Explanation: While crying, tears come out of eyes. Sometimes water fluid also comes out of the nose as well. This water fluid coming out of the nose is due to excessive secretion of lacrimal glands.

Q12. Read the following:
 insects have taste receptors on their feet.
 crickets have ears on the legs.
 snakes are highly sensitive to airborne sounds.
 frogs have colour vision.
    (A) Only (ii), (iii) and (iv) are correct
    (B) Only (i), (ii) and (iv) are correct   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Only (iii) and (iv) are correct
    (D) Only (i) and (iii) are correct
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Insects have taste receptors on their feet. These receptors are located in different regions to get the stimulus more accurately. Crickets have ears on the legs and frogs have colour vision.

Q13. Mohan lacks one or more type of cone cells in the retina of his eye. So he will suffer from:
    (A) Cataract
    (B) Colour blindness   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Squint
    (D) Night blindness
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Colour perception of the human eye is due to the presence of cones in their retina. If one or more kinds of cones is missing from the retina of the eye, the person suffers from a genetic disease called colour blindness.

Q14. Match the ear part and their shapes :
 (a) Stapes
 (i) anvil shaped
 (b) External auditory canal
 (ii) hammer-shaped
 (c) Malleus
 (iii) S-shaped
 (d) Incus
 (iv) stir-up shaped
    (A) (a) - (iv), (b) - (ii), (c) - (i), (d) - (iii)
    (B) (a) - (i), (b) - (iii), (c) - (iv), (d) - (ii)
    (C) (a) - (iii), (b) - (iv), (c) - (ii), (d) - (i)
    (D) (a) - (iv), (b) - (iii), (c) - (ii), (d) - (i)   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: There are three different kinds of bone present in the middle ear of human beings to amplify the sound received by the ear. Stapes are stir-up shaped, the external auditory canal is S-shaped, Malleus is hammer-shaped and the incus is anvil-shaped.

Q15. Ramesh is suffering from cough and cold. However his taste receptors are working quite well, yet his food do not give him characteristic flavour and is thus less enjoyable because:
    (A) Smell also plays a role in tasting food   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Impaired signals of taste are sent due to the spread of viral infection in brain lobes
    (C) His mood is not good
    (D) Infected smell receptor cells secrete toxins which inhibit the proper working of taste receptors
    Answer: A
    Explanation: During cough and cold, taste buds work properly but olfactory receptors present in the nose are badly affected. Due to these foods become less enjoyable as smell play a role in tasting food.

Chemical Coordination Test-01  (id 3432) [FREE]

Q1. Which of the following is not a mixed/composite gland?
    (A) Pancreas
    (B) Ovary
    (C) Pineal   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Testis
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A gland that contains both exocrine and endocrine portions is called a mixed or composite gland. These glands secrete both hormones and enzymes. The pineal gland is an example of an endocrine gland.

Q2. By chemical nature, hormones are never:
    (A) Steroids
    (B) Proteins
    (C) Monosaccharide derivatives   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Amino acid derivatives
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Hormones are generally protein components having amino acids as well as steroids. Hormones are generally not monosaccharide derivatives in nature.

Q3. Glucocorticoids regulate the metabolism of:
    (A) Proteins and carbohydrates
    (B) Fats and carbohydrates
    (C) Carbohydrates
    (D) Carbohydrates, lipids, and proteins   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The name glucocorticoid (glucose + cortex + steroid) is composed of its role in the regulation of glucose metabolism, synthesis in the adrenal cortex, and its steroidal structure. The principal glucocorticoid hormone is cortisol, which regulates the metabolism of proteins, carbohydrates, and lipids.

Q4. The hormone secreted by pars intermedia of hypophysis is:
    (A) ACTH
    (B) TSH
    (C) GH
    (D) MSH   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The hormone secreted by pars intermedia of hypophysis is melanocyte-stimulating hormones (MSH). MSH is a peptide hormone also known as melanotropins.

Q5. Adrenal medulla consists of a cluster of ________ nerves and those cells are also known as ________ cells.
    (A) sympathetic, paraffin
    (B) parasympathetic, follicular
    (C) parasympathetic, clear
    (D) sympathetic, chromaffin   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The adrenal medulla consists of a cluster of sympathetic nerves and those cells are also known as chromaffin cells. The adrenal medulla is part of the adrenal gland located at the center of the adrenal gland.

Q6. Process of parturition is facilitated by:
    (A) Gonadotropins
    (B) Relaxin and Oxytocin   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Oxytocin
    (D) Relaxin
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The process of parturition begins after the completion of the gestation period. The muscles present in the uterus start contracting due to the release of hormone Relaxin and Oxytocin.

Q7. The largest endocrine gland (only) is:
    (A) Testis
    (B) Pituitary
    (C) Pancreas
    (D) Thyroid   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The thyroid is the largest endocrine gland present in the human body. This gland release thyroxin hormone that helps in the metabolism of carbohydrates, fats, and proteins.

Q8. Match the following :
 Hormone
 Nature
 a) Parathormone
 i) Polypeptide
 b) Oxytocin
 ii) Amino acid Derivative
 c) Sex hormone
 iii) Peptide
 d) Norepinephrine
 iv) Steroid
    (A) a)-i, b)-iii, c)-iv, d)-ii   <-- CORRECT
    (B) a)-ii, b)-iii, c)-iv, d)-i
    (C) a)-iii, b)-iv, c)-ii, d)-i
    (D) a)-iii, b)-ii, c)-i, d)-iv
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Parathormoneis a polypeptide hormone. Oxytocin is peptide hormone. Sex hormone is a steroid hormone and Norepinephrine is a amino acid derivative.

Q9. Old people usually exhibit weaker immune power due to degeneration of:
    (A) Thymus gland   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Hypothalamus
    (C) Pineal gland
    (D) Parathyroid gland
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The thymus gland produces a hormone called thymosin which stimulates the T-cells. T-cells help in producing antibodies in the bodies. In older people, weaker immune power is due to the degeneration of the thymus gland.

Q10. Thyroid gland do not secrete______.
    (A) Calcitonin
    (B) T_4
    (C) T_3
    (D) Melatonin   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The melatonin hormone is secreted by Pineal Gland.

Q11. The hormone causing release of milk after the birth of young one is:
    (A) Relaxin
    (B) Prolactin
    (C) Progesterone
    (D) Oxytocin   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Mammary glands start releasing milk after parturition. The hormone causing the release of milk after the birth of the young one is Oxytocin.

Q12. Thermostat for the body is:
    (A) Pineal
    (B) Hypothalamus   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Pituitary
    (D) Adrenal
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The body keeps its core temperature constant at about 37^oC by physiological adjustment controlled by Hypothalamus, the so-called thermostat center.

Q13. A hormone which acts on the hypothalamus to decrease food intake, stimulate satiety, and increase energy output is:
    (A) Growth hormone
    (B) Secretin
    (C) Leptin   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Gastrin
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Leptin hormone acts on the hypothalamus to decrease food intake, stimulate satiety, and increase energy output. Leptin hormone is made by adipose cells.

Q14. Match the following :
 Hormone
 Target tissue/cell
 a) Follicle stimulating hormone
 i) liver
 b) Luteinising hormone
 ii) kidney tubule
 c) Cortisol
 iii)sertoli cells
 d) Aldosterone
 iv) interstitial cells
    (A) a)-iv, b)-iii, c)-i, d)-ii
    (B) a)-iii, b)-ii, c)-i, d)-iv
    (C) a)-iii, b)-iv, c)-i, d)-ii   <-- CORRECT
    (D) a)-iv, b)-iii, c)-ii, d)-i
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Follicle stimulating hormone acts on sertoli cells. Luteinsing hormone acts on interstitial cells. Cortisol cells acts on liver and Aldosterone hormone acts on kidney tubule.

Q15. Read the following:
 The major pineal hormone is melatonin.
 In normal human beings, melatonin secretion increases in light and decreases in dark.
 Abnormally high levels of melatonin in children cause delayed sexual development.
    (A) All of these
    (B) Statement (i) is correct
    (C) Statement (i) and (iii) are correct   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Statement (i) and (ii) are correct
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Melatonin is a hormone secreted by the pineal gland in the brain. It helps to regulate other hormones and maintains the body circadian rhythm. Abnormally high levels of melatonin in children cause delayed sexual development.

Chemical Coordination Test-02  (id 3433) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Biology > Chemical Coordination and Integration
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. Insulin is ________ hormone.
    (A) Catabolic
    (B) Glycogenolytic
    (C) Anabolic   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Neuro
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Insulin is an anabolic hormone because this hormone helps in the conversion of glucose into glycogen.

Q2. Which of the following hormones will stimulate gluconeogenesis?
    (A) Mineralocorticoids and Glucagon
    (B) Mineralocorticoids and Insulin
    (C) Glucocorticoids and Insulin
    (D) Glucocorticoids and Glucagon   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Glucocorticoids stimulate gluconeogenesis. Similarly, glucagon also stimulates the process of gluconeogenesis which also contributes to hyperglycemia.

Q3. Shekhar is 3 years old and he lives in hilly areas. He has swollen neck:
 He is suffering from goitre caused due to iodine deficiency which may lead to cretinism.
 Goitre may lead him to myxoedema and Grave’s disease in the future.
    (A) Both statements (i) and (ii) are incorrect
    (B) Statement (ii) is correct and (i) is incorrect
    (C) Both statements (i) and (ii) are correct
    (D) Statement (ii) is incorrect and (i) is correct   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The persons living in hilly areas generally suffer from goiter disease. Goiter is caused due to iodine deficiency which may lead to cretinism. Goiter never leads to myxedema or hypothyroidism.

Q4. A chemical acts slowly, requiring hours to take effect. It may pass in and out of many cells in which they have no effect. When they find appropriate receptors in their target cell they bind to it. Chemical is:
    (A) Aldosterone   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Somatotropin
    (C) Adrenaline
    (D) Oxytocin
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Aldosterone hormone is a chemical that acts slowly, requires hours to take effect. It may pass in and out of many cells in which they have no effect. When they find appropriate receptors in their target cell they bind to it to bring about changes.

Q5. Match the following:
 Hormone
 Synonym
 (a) Adrenaline
 (i) birth hormone
 (b) Oxytocin
 (ii) moulting hormone
 (c) Ecdysone
 (iii) luteotropic hormone
 (d) Prolactin
 (iv) fight or flight hormone
    (A) (a) - (iii), (b) - (iv), (c) - (ii), (d) - (i)
    (B) (a) - (iv), (b) - (iii), (c) - (i), (d) - (ii)
    (C) (a) - (iv), (b) - (i), (c) - (ii), (d) - (iii)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (a) - (iv), (b) - (iii), (c) - (ii), (d) - (i)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Adrenaline hormone is called fight and flight hormone. Oxytocin is called the birth hormone. Ecdysone is called moulting hormone and prolactin is called a luteotropic hormone.

Q6. A dwarf person showing stunted growth and mental retardation both is a result of hyposecretion of:
    (A) Growth hormone
    (B) Thymosin and melatonin
    (C) Parathyroid hormone
    (D) Thyroid hormone   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Hypothyroidism causes defective development and maturation of the growing baby leading to stunted growth (cretinism), mental retardation, low intelligence quotient, abnormal skin, deaf-mutism, etc.

Q7. Match the names of organ having isolated endocrine cells with hormone secreted by those cells :
 Organ
 Hormone
 a) Kidney
 i) angiotensin
 b) Liver
 ii) Erythropoietin
 c) Gastro-intestinal Tract
 iii) ANF
 d) Heart
 iv) CCK
    (A) a)-i, b)-ii, c)-iv, d)-iii
    (B) a)-ii, b)-i, c)-iv, d)-iii   <-- CORRECT
    (C) a)-ii, b)-i, c)-iii, d)-iv
    (D) a)-i, b)-ii, c)-iii, d)-iv
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The atrial wall of our heart secretes a very important peptide hormone called ANF.
Angiotensin I is produced by the action of renin (an enzyme produced by the kidneys) on a protein called angiotensinogen, which is formed by the liver.
The juxtaglomerular cells of kidney produce a peptide hormone called erythropoietin.
The gastro-intestinal tract secrete peptide hormone called CCK.

Q8. Match the following:
 Column A
 Column B
 (a) PTH
 (i) Mineralocorticoid
 (b) Cortisol
 (ii) Inhibiting hormone
 (c) Aldosterone
 (iii) Collip’s hormone
 (d) Somatostatin
 (iv) Glucocorticoid
    (A) (a) - (iv), (b) - (iii), (c) - (ii), (d) - (i)
    (B) (a) - (i), (b) - (iii), (c) - (iv), (d) - (ii)
    (C) (a) - (iv), (b) - (ii), (c) - (i), (d) - (iii)
    (D) (a) - (iii), (b) - (iv), (c) - (i), (d) - (ii)   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Pituitary thyroid hormone is also called as collip’s hormone. Cortisol is called a glucocorticoid hormone. Aldosterone is called as mineralocorticoid and somatostatin is called an inhibiting hormone.

Q9. The Prolactin inhibiting neurohormone is:
    (A) Acetylcholine
    (B) Serotonin
    (C) Dopamine   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Catecholamine
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The Prolactin inhibiting neurohormone is dopamine. Dopamine is a neurotransmitter that helps control the brain’s reward and pleasure centers.

Q10. Pituitary dwarfs will not show:
    (A) Mental retardation   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Inhibited growth of long bones
    (C) Normal intelligence
    (D) Stunted growth
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The pituitary dwarf hormone will show normal intelligence, stunning growth, and inhibited the growth of long bones. Pituitary dwarfs will no show mental retardation.

Q11. Read the following statements about gestational diabetes:
 It must be controlled to protect the baby’s growth and development.
 It puts women at risk for developing Type - 1 diabetes.
    (A) Both statements (i) and (ii) are incorrect
    (B) Statement (ii) is correct and (i) is incorrect
    (C) Both statements (i) and (ii) are correct
    (D) Statement (ii) is incorrect and (i) is correct   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Gestational diabetes develops during pregnancy. It must be controlled to protect the baby’s growth and development. This kind of diabetes never leads to develop type-1 diabetes.

Q12. Oral contraceptive pills contain estrogen and progesterone, that prevent:
    (A) All of these
    (B) release of a secondary oocyte from the ovary.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) formation of new ovarian follicles.
    (D) implantation of a fertilized egg in the uterus.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The oral contraceptive pill contains estrogen and progesterone that prevents the release of a secondary oocyte from the ovary. The secondary oocyte develops into a female egg or ovum. The use of these pills prevents the ovum formation.

Q13. To exert their effect on the target cell, water-soluble hormones will need to bind with ______.
    (A) Plasma proteins
    (B) Cytosolic receptors
    (C) Nuclear receptors
    (D) Cell membrane-bound receptors   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Hormones are released in trace amounts from endocrine glands and to exert their effect on the target cell, water-soluble hormones will need to bind with cell membrane-bound receptors.

Q14. During the adolescence phase, Sunil’s body became abnormally large due to the excessive growth of bones of his lower jaw and limbs. This abnormality is called:
    (A) Addison’s disease
    (B) Gigantism
    (C) Acromegaly   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Exopthalamic goitre
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Acromegaly is the abnormal growth of the hands, feet, and face caused by overproduction of growth hormone by the pituitary gland.

Q15. Which of the following is not matched correctly?
    (A) Adrenal medulla $ \to $ derived from ectoderm
    (B) Thyroid and Parathyroid $ \to $ derived from ectoderm
    (C) Gonads $ \to $ derived from mesoderm
    (D) Adrenal cortex $ \to $ derived from ectoderm   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The adrenal cortex is mesodermal in origin. The adrenal medulla is derived from ectoderm, gonads are derived from mesoderm, thyroid, and parathyroids derived ectoderm.

Chemical Coordination Test-03  (id 3434) [PAID]

Q1. The following slide is of Transverse section of the thyroid gland and it shows [from left to right] :
    (A) C-cells, colloid containing T3&T4, parafollicular cells
    (B) follicular epithelium, colloid containing thyroglobulin, clear cells   <-- CORRECT
    (C) parafollicular cells, colloid containing thyroxine&TCT, follicular epithelium
    (D) epithelium, colloid containing T4&TCT, parafollicular cells
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Transverse section of thyroid gland shows mark (1) as follicular epithelium, mark (2) as colloid containingthyroglobuin and mark (3) as clear cells.

Q2. Following conversion in forward and backward directions is regulated as :
$(i) \to \ \Leftrightarrow \ \leftarrow (ii)$
Blood calcium Bone calcium
    (A) is PTH and
 is TCT
    (B) is Ca++ and
 is phosphorus
    (C) is epinephrine and
 is norepinephrine
    (D) is TCT and
 is PTH   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Thyrocalcitonin (TCT) influence the metabolism of calcium inside the body. Parathyroid hormone (PTH) absorption of calcium in bone.

Q3. To exert their effect on the target cell, water-soluble hormones will need to bind with:
    (A) Cytosolic receptors
    (B) Cell membrane-bound receptors   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Plasma proteins
    (D) Nuclear receptors
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Hormone receptors present on the cell membrane of the target cells are called membrane-bound receptors and the receptors present inside the target cell are called intracellular receptors, mostly nuclear receptors (present in the nucleus). Binding of a hormone to its receptor leads to the formation of a hormone-receptor complex.

Q4. Secretion of aldosterone is stimulated by:
 the decrease in sodium ion concentration in the plasma.
 the decrease in potassium ion concentration in the plasma.
 the decrease in the volume of blood.
    (A) Statement (i) and (iii) are correct   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Statement (i) and (ii) are correct
    (C) All of these
    (D) Statement (ii) and (iii) are correct
    Answer: A
    Explanation: If decreased blood pressure is detected, the adrenal gland is stimulated by these stretch receptors to release aldosterone, which increases sodium reabsorption from the urine, sweat, and the gut. This causes increased osmolarity in the extracellular fluid, which will eventually return blood pressure toward normal.

Q5. Read the following statements about suprarenal glands:
 A suprarenal gland represents two endocrine glands arranged in one organ.
 It’s outer region secretes steroid hormones.
 Also known as a gland of emergency.
    (A) Statement (i) is correct
    (B) All of these   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Statement (ii) and (iii) are correct
    (D) Statement (i) and (iii) are correct
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The adrenal glands (also known as suprarenal glands) are endocrine glands that produce a variety of hormones including adrenaline and the steroids aldosterone and cortisol. They are found above the kidneys. Also Known as the emergency gland of the body. This is because it produces a hormone called ADRENALIN which prepares our body from emergencies.

Q6. A person accidentally got his adrenal gland injured. He died and reports will probably reveal that death was caused due to:
    (A) Loss of both adrenal medulla function and adrenal cortex function
    (B) Loss of adrenal cortex function   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Loss of adrenal medulla function
    (D) Insulin shock
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The adrenal cortex is situated along the perimeter of the adrenal gland. The adrenal cortex mediates the stress response through the production of aldosterone and cortisol. If a person got injured his adrenal gland may die due to loss of stress response which will be revealed in the report.

Q7. Which of the following scientists won the Nobel prize for discovering second messengers?
    (A) Martin Rodbell
    (B) Alfred G. Gilman
    (C) Robert Huxley
    (D) Wilbur Sutherland   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Second messengers are molecules that relay signals received at receptors on the cell surface to trigger physiological changes.
The Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine 1971 was awarded to Earl W. Sutherland, Jr. "for his discoveries concerning the mechanisms of the action of hormones".

Q8. Which of the following gas is found to work as a second messenger?
    (A) NO_2
    (B) SO_2
    (C) NO   <-- CORRECT
    (D) N_2O
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Second messengers are molecules that relay signals received at receptors on the cell surface to trigger physiological changes. Nitrogen oxide (NO) acts as a second messenger.

Q9. Read the following statements:
 the endocrine system corrects the imbalance originally detected by the nervous system.
 nerve cells and endocrine cells exist side by side in the adrenal gland and pituitary.
    (A) Both statements (i) and (ii) are incorrect
    (B) Both statements (i) and (ii) are correct   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Statement (i) is incorrect and (ii) is correct
    (D) Statement (i) is correct and (ii) is incorrect
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The endocrine system corrects the imbalance originally detected by the nervous system. Nerve cells and endocrine cells exist side by side in the adrenal gland and pituitary gland.

Q10. Glucose will be lost in the urine of patients suffering from:
    (A) Diabetes mellitus   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Low blood pressure
    (C) Diabetes insipidus
    (D) Both diabetes mellitus and diabetes insipidus
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Glucose will be lost in the urine of patients suffering from diabetes mellitus. It is a chronic lifelong condition that affects our body ability to use the energy found in the blood.

Q11. The correct matched pair out of the following is:
    (A) PTH $ \to $ hypocalcemic
    (B) Type 2 diabetes $ \to $ insulin dependent diabetes
    (C) Glucagon $ \to $ hyperglycemic   <-- CORRECT
    (D) TSH $ \to $ neurohormone
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Glucagon hormone released from the pancreas increase the sugar level in blood in case deficiency of glucose. Parathyroid hormone is not hypocalcemia and TSH is not a neurohormone.

Q12. Tanay is diagnosed with a tumor in his parathyroid. He will show out of the following symptoms:
 excretion of calcium in urine
 osteoporosis
 tetany
 deposition of calcium in kidney tubules
    (A) Only (ii) and (iii)
    (B) Only (i) and (ii)
    (C) Only (ii) and (iv)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Only (i) and (iii)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Parathyroid hormone is released from parathyroid glands that regulate calcium ions in the body. The person suffering from a tumor of parathyroid shows symptoms of osteoporosis and deposition of calcium in kidney tubules.

Q13. Some girls develop male secondary sexual characters like beard, moustaches, hoarse voice, etc. This is called ________.
    (A) Eunuchoidism
    (B) Gonadotropin excessism
    (C) Adrenal virilism   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Cushions syndrome
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Development of secondary sexual characters like beard, moustaches, hoarse voice, etc. in girls is called adrenal virilism. This occurs due to the excessive secretion of the adrenaline hormone.

Q14. Match the following :
 Disease 
 Hormone source responsible
 a) Cushion syndrome
 i) hyposecretions from pars nervosa
 b) Diabetes mellitus
 ii) hyposecretion of mineralocorticoids
 c) Diabetes insipidus
 iii) hyposecretion of glucocorticoids
 d) Addison’s disease
 iv) hyposecretion from beta cells of pancreas
    (A) a)-iii, b)-iv, c)-i, d)-ii   <-- CORRECT
    (B) a)-ii, b)-iii, c)-iv, d)-i
    (C) a)-iii, b)-ii, c)-i, d)-iv
    (D) a)-ii, b)-i, c)-iv, d)-iii
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Cushing’s syndrome occurs hypo-secretion of glucocorticoids hormone. Diabetes mellitus is due to hypo-secretion of beta cells of pancreas. Diabetes insipidus is due to hypo-secretion form pars nervosa and Addison’s disease is due to hypo-secretion of mineral corticoids.

Q15. Girls blind from birth attain puberty earlier than normal due to:
    (A) Non inhibition of growth hormone by melatonin
    (B) Stimulation of gonadotropins by thymosin
    (C) Ovaries of inborn blind girls is quite different from other girls
    (D) Non-inhibition of gonad by melatonin   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The pineal gland releases Melatonin (a hormone) which is responsible for inhibiting the Luteinising hormone and Follicle Stimulating Hormone that brings about puberty. Melatonin is secreted more in absence of light. In normal humans, it is more released at night when it is released more. In blind girls, light is absorbed more at day whose effect continues at night. Hence, Melatonin is secreted less and LH and FSH are not inhibited more, and puberty is experienced early.
